**312.2.d.** When the turn is in a [[#closed state|Closed State]], they are the next [[#player|Player ]]in [[#turn order|Turn Order]], and the player with [[#priority|Priority ]]passes. 

#### rule 312.3
**312.3.** When a player is granted [[#priority|Priority, ]]it is either created if no player has it or taken from the player with [[#priority|Priority. ]]

### rule 313
**313.** At any given time, up to one player has [[#focus|Focus. ]]

#### rule 313.1
**313.1.** [[#focus|Focus ]]is the permission to take appropriately timed [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions ]]when the turn is in a [[#showdown open state|Showdown Open State.  ]]See [[##rule 307|rule 307.]] [[#states of the turn|States of the Turn]] for more information. 

#### rule 313.1.a
**313.1.a.** The player with [[#focus|Focus ]]must obey any additional restrictions on which [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions ]]may be performed.  Example: A player with [[#focus|Focus ]]may not play spells or activate abilities that don't have the [[#action|Action ]]or [[#reaction|Reaction ]]keywords. 

#### rule 313.2
**313.2.** A player who gains [[#focus|Focus ]]also gains [[#priority|Priority. ]]

#### rule 313.3
**313.3.** A player who passes [[#priority|Priority ]]retains [[#focus|Focus. ]]

#### rule 313.4
**313.4.** A player may not make discretionary actions with [[#focus|Focus ]]unless they also possess [[#priority|Priority. ]]

#### rule 313.5
**313.5.** If the turn is in a [[#neutral state|Neutral State]], no player has [[#focus|Focus. ]]

### rule 314
**314.** Phases of the Turn 

### rule 315
**315.** [[#start of turn|Start of Turn ]]

#### rule 315.1
**315.1.** Awaken Phase 

#### rule 315.1.a
**315.1.a.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding]]: 

#### rule 315.1.b
**315.1.b.** 1. The [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]readies all [[#game object|Game Objects ]]they control that are able to be readied.  See [[##rule 415|rule 415.]] [[#ready|Ready]] for more information. 

#### rule 315.2
**315.2.** Beginning Phase 

#### rule 315.2.a
**315.2.a.** Beginning Step 

#### rule 315.2.a.1
**315.2.a.1.** At the start of Beginning Phase game effects take place. 

#### rule 315.2.b
**315.2.b.** Scoring Step 

#### rule 315.2.b.1
**315.2.b.1.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding]]: 

#### rule 315.2.b.2
**315.2.b.2.** 1. The [[#turn player|Turn Player Holds ]]all [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]they [[#control|Control]]. See [[##rule 462|rule 462.]] [[#scoring|Scoring]] for more information. 

#### rule 315.2.b.3
**315.2.b.3.** Reminder: In [[#modes of play|Modes of Play ]]with [[#teams|Teams]], [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]held by a Teammate of the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]during this phase are [[#disqualiﬁed|disqualiﬁed ]]from being scored this turn by the [[#turn player|Turn Player. ]]

#### rule 315.3
**315.3.** Channel Phase 

#### rule 315.3.a
**315.3.a.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding]]: 

#### rule 315.3.b
**315.3.b.** 1. The [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]channels 2 runes from their [[#rune deck|Rune Deck.  ]]See [[##rule 430|rule 430.]] [[#channeled|Channel]] for more information. 

#### rule 315.3.b.1
**315.3.b.1.** If there are fewer than 2 runes in the [[#rune deck|Rune Deck, ]]they channel as many as possible. 

#### rule 315.4
**315.4.** Draw Phase 

#### rule 315.4.a
**315.4.a.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding]]: 

#### rule 315.4.b
**315.4.b.** 1. The [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]draws 1. 

#### rule 315.4.b.1
**315.4.b.1.** If there are no cards remaining in their [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]to draw, the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]has been [[#burned out|Burned Out]].  See [[##rule 431|rule 431.]] [[#burn out|Burn Out]] for more information. 

#### rule 315.4.b.2
**315.4.b.2.** After completing the [[#burn out|Burn Out ]]the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]still [[#drawn|Draws 1. ]]

#### rule 315.4.c
**315.4.c.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding: ]]

#### rule 315.4.d
**315.4.d.** 1. Each player's [[#rune pool|Rune Pool ]]empties. Any unspent [[#energy|Energy ]]and [[#power|Power ]]are lost. See [[##rule 164|rule 164.]] [[#rune pool|Rune Pools]] for more information. 

### rule 316
**316.** [[#main phase|Main Phase ]]

#### rule 316.1
**316.1.** When all steps of the [[#start of turn|Start of Turn ]]have been completed, the [[#main phase|Main Phase ]]begins. 

#### rule 316.2
**316.2.** The [[#main phase|Main Phase ]]has no deﬁned structure. 

#### rule 316.2.a
**316.2.a.** A player may take any number of [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions ]]they are able to perform during this phase.  See [[##rule 410.1|rule 410.1.]] [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions]] for more information. 

#### rule 316.2.b
**316.2.b.** This is denoted as a [[#neutral open|Neutral Open State]], and only the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]has the ability to play spells or activate abilities.  See [[##rule 307|rule 307.]] [[#states of the turn|States of the Turn]] for more information. 

#### rule 316.2.b.1
**316.2.b.1.** In [[#modes of play|Modes of Play ]]with teammates, the [[#turn player|Turn Player's ]]teammates may play spells and activate abilities, including ones without [[#action|Action ]]or [[#reaction|Reaction. ]]They can only do so when the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]invites them to do so with their own [[#priority|Priority. ]]

#### rule 316.3
**316.3.** As a result of a player taking [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions]], one or more structured phases may occur. 

#### rule 316.4
**316.4.** [[#combat|Combat ]]

#### rule 316.4.a
**316.4.a.** A [[#combat|Combat ]]occurs as a result of [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by opposing players being present at the same [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld]]. 

#### rule 316.4.b
**316.4.b.** This could be the result of a [[#standard move standard action|Standard Move Standard Action]], a [[#spells|Spell]], or other [[#game effects|Game Effect. ]]

#### rule 316.4.c
**316.4.c.** The source effect does not change the structure or flow of [[#combat|Combat ]]once initiated. 

#### rule 316.4.d
**316.4.d.** A [[#combat|Combat ]]can only occur between two players.  See [[##rule 454|rule 454.]] [[#combat|Combat]] for more information. 

#### rule 316.4.e
**316.4.e.** Play proceeds following the steps of combat.  See [[##rule 458|rule 458.]] [[#steps of combat|The Steps of Combat]] for more information. 

#### rule 316.4.f
**316.4.f.** Combat will also include a [[#showdown|Showdown. ]]

#### rule 316.5
**316.5.** [[#showdown|Showdowns ]]

#### rule 316.5.a
**316.5.a.** A [[#showdown|Showdown ]]occurs when a [[#combat|Combat ]]occurs. 

#### rule 316.5.a.1
**316.5.a.1.** Showdowns that occur as a result of Combat are a [[#sub-phase|Sub-Phase ]]of [[#combat|Combat. ]]

#### rule 316.5.b
**316.5.b.** A [[#showdown|Showdown ]]is marked as [[#state|Staged ]]at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]when the [[#contested|Contested ]]status is applied to a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]with no current controller. 

#### rule 316.5.b.1
**316.5.b.1.** Showdowns that occur as a result of a player moving to an empty [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]are a stand-alone [[#phases|Phase ]]and do not create a [[#combat|Combat. ]]

#### rule 316.5.b.1.a
**316.5.b.1.a.** These [[#showdown|Showdowns ]]are called [[#non-combat showdown|Non-Combat Showdowns]]. During the proceedings of a [[#non-combat showdown|Non-Combat Showdown]], units controlled by a different player may become present at the Battleﬁeld where the [[#showdown|Showdown ]]is ongoing. This will cause the [[#showdown|Showdown ]]to become a [[#combat showdown|Combat Showdown. ]]

#### rule 316.5.c
**316.5.c.** A [[#showdown|Showdown ]]is a structured [[#window of opportunity|Window of Opportunity ]]where [[#player|Players ]]may play cards and activate abilities with [[#action|Action ]]or [[#reaction|Reaction. ]]See [[##rule 341|rule 341.]] [[#showdown|Showdowns]] for more information. 

#### rule 316.6
**316.6.** When a player has no more [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions ]]they wish to execute, they must indicate they are ending their turn. 

#### rule 316.6.a
**316.6.a.** This ends the [[#main phase|Main Phase. ]]

#### rule 316.6.b
**316.6.b.** Play proceeds to the [[#ending phase|Ending Phase. ]]

### rule 317
**317.** Ending Phase 

#### rule 317.1
**317.1.** Ending Step 

#### rule 317.1.a
**317.1.a.** At the end of the turn [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]take place. 

#### rule 317.1.b
**317.1.b.** Speciﬁc game effects and abilities will reference this timing and phase as necessary. 

#### rule 317.2
**317.2.** Expiration Step 

#### rule 317.2.a
**317.2.a.** Invoke an Ending [[#special cleanup|Special Cleanup.  ]]See [[##rule 318|rule 318.]] [[#cleanup|Cleanups]] for more information. 

#### rule 317.2.b
**317.2.b.** Insert “2c. [[#healed|Heal ]]all [[#unit|Units]].” 

#### rule 317.2.c
**317.2.c.** Insert “2d. All ‘this turn’ effects expire simultaneously.” 

#### rule 317.2.d
**317.2.d.** Insert “2e. Each player’s [[#rune pool|Rune Pool ]]empties. Any unspent [[#energy|Energy ]]and [[#power|Power ]]are lost.” 

#### rule 317.2.e
**317.2.e.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding]]: 

#### rule 317.2.f
**317.2.f.** 1. If any items underwent the FEPR process, return to the start of the Expiration Step 

#### rule 317.3
**317.3.** The next player with their [[#turn order|Turn ]]queued becomes the [[#turn player|Turn Player. ]]

### rule 318
**318.** [[#cleanup|Cleanups ]]

### rule 319
**319.** A [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]will be made an [[#outstanding|Outstanding Task ]]at the following times: 

#### rule 319.1
**319.1.** After the game transitions to or from an [[#open state|Open ]]or [[#closed state|Closed ]]state 

#### rule 319.2
**319.2.** After the game transitions between [[#phases|Phases, ]]unless speciﬁed otherwise 

#### rule 319.3
**319.3.** After a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]is added to the [[#chain|Chain ]]

#### rule 319.4
**319.4.** After a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]becomes a [[#legal item|Legal Item ]]on the [[#chain|Chain ]]

#### rule 319.5
**319.5.** After a [[#chain|Chain Item ]]is removed from the [[#chain|Chain ]]for any reason 

#### rule 319.6
**319.6.** After any number of [[#game object|Game Objects ]]enter or leave the Board 

#### rule 319.7
**319.7.** After the status of any number of [[#game object|Game Objects ]]changes for any reason 

#### rule 319.8
**319.8.** After a [[#move|Move ]]is completed 

### rule 320
**320.** While a [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]is occurring, [[#chain|Chain Items ]]cannot be [[#resolving|Resolved. ]]

#### rule 320.1
**320.1.** New [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]can be added, but [[#legal item|Legal Items ]]cannot be executed and [[#priority|Priority ]]and [[#focus|Focus ]]are not passed or awarded. 

### rule 321
**321.** Similarly, while [[#chain|Chain Items ]]are [[#resolving|Resolving]], a [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]cannot occur. 

#### rule 321.1
**321.1.** If an event occurs during the [[#resolution|Resolution ]]of a [[#chain|Chain Item ]]that qualiﬁes for a [[#cleanup|Cleanup]], that [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]will be made an [[#outstanding|Outstanding Task. ]]

### rule 322
**322.** If an event occurs during a [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]that qualiﬁes for a [[#cleanup|Cleanup, ]]another [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]will occur immediately after the ﬁrst completes, repeating until a [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]occurs with no new change in the game’s state. 

#### rule 322.1
**322.1.** These new [[#cleanup|Cleanups ]]are themselves [[#outstanding|Outstanding Tasks. ]]

### rule 323
**323.** When a [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]occurs, the following [[#task|Tasks ]]become [[#outstanding|Outstanding ]]in the order described: 

#### rule 323.1
**323.1.** 1.  If a player has points greater than or equal to the [[#victory score|Victory Score, ]]and more points than any opponent, that player wins. 

#### rule 323.2
**323.2.** 2. Assign or Remove the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]or [[#defender|Defender ]]designation from [[#unit|Units ]]as needed if there is a [[#combat|Combat ]]in progress 

#### rule 323.2.a
**323.2.a.** If there are [[#unit|Units ]]present at the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]the [[#combat|Combat ]]is taking place at, but do not have a designation, they gain the same designation as their [[#control|Controller ]]now 

#### rule 323.2.b
**323.2.b.** If there are [[#unit|Units ]]present at the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]the [[#combat|Combat ]]is taking place at, but have the opposite designation of their controller, they lose that designation, and gain the same designation as their controller now 

#### rule 323.2.c
**323.2.c.** If there are [[#unit|Units ]]at locations other than the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that the [[#combat|Combat ]]is taking place at, but have either [[#attacker|Attacker ]]or [[#defender|Defender ]]designations, they lose those designations now 

#### rule 323.3
**323.3.** 3. Handle outstanding board state 

#### rule 323.4
**323.4.** 3a. All [[#unit|Units ]]that have non-zero [[#damage|Damage ]]marked on them equalling or exceeding their [[#might|Might ]]that have [[#deathknell|Deathknell ]]abilities will trigger their [[#deathknell|Deathknell ]]ability now, making note of their current location, attributes, and other information relevant to add the trigger as a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]See [[##rule 808]] [[#deathknell|Deathknell]] for more information. 

#### rule 323.5
**323.5.** 3b. All [[#unit|Units ]]that have non-zero [[#damage|Damage ]]marked on them equalling or exceeding their [[#might|Might ]]are killed and placed in their owners' [[#trashes|Trash. ]]

#### rule 323.6
**323.6.** 4. If the turn is in an [[#open state, battleﬁelds|Open State, Battleﬁelds ]]with no [[#unit|Units ]]occupying them and no [[#showdown|Showdown ]]or [[#combat|Combat ]]ongoing become [[#uncontrolled|Uncontrolled. ]]

#### rule 323.7
**323.7.** 5. Recall all [[#unattached|Unattached ]]non-[[#unit|Unit Gear ]]at [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds, ]]and all [[#permanents|Permanents ]]and [[#rune|Runes ]]in [[#bases|Bases ]]other than their controller’s. Remove all [[#hide|Hidden ]]cards from all [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's [[#trashes|Trash. ]]

#### rule 323.8
**323.8.** 6. Mark a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]as [[#state|Staged ]]at each [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that [[#contested|Contested ]]was applied to. 

#### rule 323.8.a
**323.8.a.** The [[#showdown|Showdown ]]remains [[#state|Staged ]]at each [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that is [[#contested|Contested ]]and has units present controlled by the player that applied [[#contested|Contested. ]]

#### rule 323.9
**323.9.** 7. Mark a [[#combat|Combat ]]as [[#state|Staged ]]at each [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that [[#contested|Contested ]]was applied to that have Units present controlled by opposing players.  

#### rule 323.9.a
**323.9.a.** The [[#combat|Combat ]]remains [[#state|Staged ]]at that [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]as long as there are [[#unit|Units ]]present from two opposing players there. 

#### rule 323.10
**323.10.** 7a. If Units of two opposing players are no longer present at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that has a [[#combat staged|Combat Staged ]]before it has opened, the [[#combat|Combat ]]will cease being [[#state|Staged ]]

#### rule 323.11
**323.11.** 8. If the current state is a [[#neutral open|Neutral Open State ]]and one or more [[#showdown|Showdowns ]]are [[#state|Staged]], the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]chooses one of those [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds. ]]A [[#showdown|Showdown ]]begins there. 

#### rule 323.12
**323.12.** 8a. If a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]and [[#combat|Combat ]]are staged at the same [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]and the turn player chooses to initiate the [[#showdown|Showdown ]]there, the [[#showdown|Showdown ]]will open as a [[#combat showdown|Combat Showdown. ]]

#### rule 323.13
**323.13.** 9. If the current state is a [[#neutral open|Neutral Open State ]]and [[#combat|Combat ]]is [[#state|Staged ]]at one or more [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]], the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]chooses one of those [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]]. [[#combat|Combat ]]begins there. 

#### rule 323.14
**323.14.** 9a. If the current state is [[#showdown open state|Showdown Open State ]]and [[#combat|Combat ]]is [[#state|Staged ]]at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]where there is a [[#non-combat showdown|Non-Combat Showdown ]]ongoing, that [[#showdown|Showdown ]]becomes a [[#combat showdown|Combat Showdown.  ]]

### rule 324
**324.** [[#special cleanup|Special Cleanups ]]are [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]steps invoked at speciﬁc times that have additional steps not present in a normal [[#cleanup|Cleanup. ]]

#### rule 324.1
**324.1.** When a [[#special cleanup|Special Cleanup ]]is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a [[#combat cleanup|Combat Cleanup ]]is invoked, the [[#combat|Combat ]]section deﬁnes what steps are added to the [[#cleanup|Cleanup. ]]See [[##rule 461|rule 461.]] [[#resolution|The Resolution Step]] for more information. Example: When an [[#end of turn cleanup|End of Turn Cleanup ]]is invoked, the [[#end of turn phase|End of Turn Phase ]]subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the [[#cleanup|Cleanup. ]]See [[##rule 317|rule 317.]] [[#ending phase|The Ending Phase]] for more information. 

#### rule 324.2
**324.2.** If events during a [[#special cleanup require|Special Cleanup require ]]another [[#cleanup|Cleanup, ]]a normal [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]is invoked, not another iteration of the [[#special cleanup|Special Cleanup]]. 

### rule 325
**325.** [[#chains and showdowns|Chains and Showdowns ]]

### rule 326
**326.** Players can act during the following [[#windows of opportunity|Windows of Opportunity ]]that occur during the course of regular play: 

#### rule 326.1
**326.1.** During a [[#chain|Chain ]]

#### rule 326.2
**326.2.** During a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]

### rule 327
**327.** Chains 

### rule 328
**328.** The [[#chain|Chain ]]is a [[#non-board zones|Non-Board Zone ]]that temporarily exists whenever a card is played or an ability is activated. 

#### rule 328.1
**328.1.** Cards are placed here as part of the process of being played. 

#### rule 328.2
**328.2.** Abilities are queued here as part of the process of resolving.  See [[##rule 360|rule 360.]] [[#abilities|Abilities]] for more information. 

### rule 329
**329.** Cards and abilities added to the chain are added as [[#pending chain items|Pending Chain Items ]]that become Finalized [[#chain|Chain Items. ]]

#### rule 329.1
**329.1.** [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]are on the Chain. 

#### rule 329.2
**329.2.** [[#chain|Chain Items ]]are [[#pending item|Pending ]]until the “Check Legality” step of playing a card.  See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 329.3
**329.3.** When a [[#pending chain items|Pending Chain Item ]]is no longer [[#pending item|Pending ]]it is ﬁnalized and becomes a Finalized [[#chain|Chain Item]]. 

### rule 330
**330.** The [[#chain|Chain ]]exists as long as a [[#chain|Chain Item ]]is on it. 

#### rule 330.1
**330.1.** Only one [[#chain|Chain ]]can exist at a time. 

#### rule 330.2
**330.2.** If a card would begin to be played while a [[#chain|Chain ]]already exists, it is placed on the existing [[#chain|Chain. ]]

### rule 331
**331.** The [[#state|State ]]of the [[#turn order|Turn ]]is partially determined by whether or not the [[#chain|Chain ]]currently exists. 

#### rule 331.1
**331.1.** The turn is said to be in a [[#closed state|Closed State ]]if a [[#chain|Chain ]]exists. 

#### rule 331.1.a
**331.1.a.** Cards of all Categories, by default, cannot be played during a [[#closed state|Closed State. ]]

#### rule 331.1.b
**331.1.b.** Card abilities, by default, cannot be played during a [[#closed state|Closed State. ]]

#### rule 331.2
**331.2.** The turn is said to be in an [[#open state|Open State ]]if no [[#chain|Chain ]]exists. 

### rule 332
**332.** Steps of Resolving Chain Items 

### rule 333
**333.** Whenever a card or token is played or an ability is activated or triggered, a [[#chain|Chain ]]is created. 

#### rule 333.1
**333.1.** The player that created the chain becomes the ﬁrst player with [[#priority|Priority. ]]

### rule 334
**334.** A [[#task|Task ]]is one or more steps or processes that one or more [[#player|Players ]]must perform before continuing with any other actions. 

#### rule 334.1
**334.1.** [[#task|Tasks ]]include, but are not limited to: [[#cleanup|Cleanups]], the actions performed during the [[#start of turn process|Start of Turn Process]], throughout [[#combat|Combat ]]in its various steps, and the actions performed during the [[#end of turn  process|End of Turn  Process. ]]See [[##rule 318|rule 318.]] [[#cleanup|Cleanups]] for more information on Cleanups See [[##rule 315|rule 315.]] [[#start of turn|Start of Turn]] for more information on the Start of Turn process See [[##rule 454|rule 454.]] [[#combat|Combat]] for more information on the steps of Combat See [[##rule 317|rule 317.]] [[#ending phase|Ending Phase]] for more information.  

### rule 335
**335.** Whenever a [[#player|Player ]]takes one or more actions that incur [[#task|Tasks ]]they should refer to the process of [[#hot fepr: h|HOT FEPR: H]]andle [[#calm|O]]utstanding [[#tags|T]]asks; then [[#fury|F]]inalize, [[#calm|E]]xecute, [[#play|P]]ass, [[#rune|R]]esolve. 

#### rule 335.1
**335.1.** In the course of Handling Outstanding Tasks, [[#chain|Chain Items ]]may be added to the [[#chain|Chain]]. They will remain there until the [[#task|Tasks ]]are complete.  

#### rule 335.2
**335.2.** When all Outstanding [[#task|Tasks ]]are completed, all pending [[#chain|Chain Items ]]will subsequently be processed by the [[#fepr|FEPR ]]process.  

#### rule 335.2.a
**335.2.a.** During the FEPR process, new Tasks may be incurred. Pause the process and complete the necessary Tasks before continuing. 

#### rule 335.3
**335.3.** If there are no Outstanding [[#task|Tasks]], no pending [[#chain|Chain Items]], and it is the [[#main phase|Main Phase, ]]the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]receives priority. If there are no Outstanding [[#task|Tasks]], no pending items, and it is any other phase of the turn, proceed to the next substep, step, phase, or turn. 

### rule 336
**336.** When there are no outstanding [[#task|Tasks ]]and there are pending [[#chain|Chain Items ]]on the [[#chain|Chain]], players should refer to the [[#fepr|FEPR ]]process to proceed. 

#### rule 336.1
**336.1.** In the sequence of resolving [[#fepr|FEPR ]]more [[#chain|Chain Items ]]may become [[#pending chain items|Pending Chain Items]]. These will be processed by the same [[#fepr|FEPR ]]process that produced them. 

### rule 337
**337.** [[#step 1: finalize|Step 1: Finalize ]]

#### rule 337.1
**337.1.** If one or more Items are [[#pending item|Pending]], their controllers must complete the steps of [[#playing|Playing ]]those [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]until they are [[#finalized items|Finalized Items ]]or leave the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 337.1.a
**337.1.a.** This process does not pass [[#priority|Priority. ]]

#### rule 337.1.b
**337.1.b.** Each Item is [[#finalized items|Finalized ]]in the order it was appended to the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 337.1.c
**337.1.c.** [[#units, gear|Units, Gear, ]]and abilities that [[#added|Add ]]resources resolve immediately when [[#finalized items|Finalized ]]and do not progress to Step 2: Execute.  See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 337.1.c.1
**337.1.c.1.** If the [[#chain|Chain ]]is empty, play proceeds in an [[#open state|Open State. ]]

#### rule 337.1.c.1.a
**337.1.c.1.a.** If this occurs during a [[#showdown|Showdown]], the next player in turn order gains [[#focus|Focus]]. 

#### rule 337.1.c.2
**337.1.c.2.** If the [[#chain|Chain ]]is not empty and there are one or more [[#pending item|Pending Items]], repeat Step 1. 

#### rule 337.1.c.3
**337.1.c.3.** If the [[#chain|Chain ]]is not empty and there are no [[#pending item|Pending Items]], the controller of the newest item on the chain gains [[#priority|Priority ]]and becomes the [[#active player|Active Player. ]]Proceed to Step 2: Execute. 

### rule 338
**338.** [[#step 2: execute|Step 2: Execute ]]

#### rule 338.1
**338.1.** The player with [[#priority|Priority ]]may do any the following: 

#### rule 338.1.a
**338.1.a.** [[#play|Play ]]a [[#card|Card ]]that is [[#legally timed|legally timed. ]]

#### rule 338.1.a.1
**338.1.a.1.** [[#card|Cards]], by default, cannot be played during a [[#closed state|Closed State. ]]

#### rule 338.1.a.2
**338.1.a.2.** A [[#legally timed|Legally Timed Card ]]would be a [[#card|Card ]]with [[#reaction|Reaction ]]or a card that will have [[#reaction|Reaction ]]when played under appropriate circumstances. 

#### rule 338.1.a.3
**338.1.a.3.** Other exceptions may be created during regular play. 

#### rule 338.1.a.4
**338.1.a.4.** The card will be added to the chain as a [[#pending item|Pending Item]], following the steps of playing a card. 

#### rule 338.1.a.5
**338.1.a.5.** This can be an additional card to the item that [[#started|Started ]]the [[#chain|Chain ]]in the case of the ﬁrst player with [[#priority|Priority ]]after creating the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 338.1.a.6
**338.1.a.6.** Whether a [[#card|Card ]]is legally timed is evaluated during the “Check Legality” step of [[#playing a card|Playing a Card.  ]]See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 338.1.a.7
**338.1.a.7.** Playing a card will create one or more [[#pending item|Pending Items]]. Return to Step 1: Finalize. 

#### rule 338.1.b
**338.1.b.** [[#activate abilities|Activate Abilities ]]of [[#game object|Game Objects ]]that are [[#legally timed|legally timed.  ]]See [[##rule 398|rule 398.]] [[#playing or activating abilities|Playing or Activating Abilities]] for more information. 

#### rule 338.1.b.1
**338.1.b.1.** All rules for [[#legally timed|legally timed ]]cards apply to [[#legally timed|legally timed ]]abilities. 

#### rule 338.1.b.2
**338.1.b.2.** Activating abilities will create one or more [[#pending item|Pending Items]]. Return to Step 1: Finalize. 

#### rule 338.1.c
**338.1.c.** [[#pass priority|Pass Priority ]]

#### rule 338.1.c.1
**338.1.c.1.** The player with [[#priority|Priority ]]passes [[#priority|Priority ]]to the next [[#player|Player ]]in [[#turn order|Turn Order. ]]Proceed to Step 3: Pass. 

### rule 339
**339.** [[#step 3: pass|Step 3: Pass ]]

#### rule 339.1
**339.1.** If all players have passed [[#priority|Priority ]]without adding any items to the [[#chain|Chain]], proceed to Step 4: Resolve. 

#### rule 339.2
**339.2.** Otherwise, the player with [[#priority|Priority ]]passes [[#priority|Priority ]]to the next [[#player|Player ]]in [[#turn order|Turn Order. ]]Return to Step 3: Execute. 

### rule 340
**340.** [[#step 4: resolve|Step 4: Resolve ]]

#### rule 340.1
**340.1.** The newest item on the [[#chain|Chain ]]resolves. Execute its game effects in their entirety. See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information on resolving spells.  See [[##rule 398|rule 398.]] [[#playing or activating abilities|Playing or Activating Abilities]] for more information on resolving abilities. 

#### rule 340.2
**340.2.** If the [[#chain|Chain ]]is empty, play proceeds in an [[#open state|Open State. ]]

#### rule 340.2.a
**340.2.a.** If this occurs during a [[#showdown|Showdown]], focus passes to the next player in turn order. 

#### rule 340.3
**340.3.** If the [[#chain|Chain ]]is not empty and there are one or more [[#pending item|Pending Items]], return to Step 1: Finalize. 

#### rule 340.4
**340.4.** If the [[#chain|Chain ]]is not empty and there are no [[#pending item|Pending Items]], the controller of the newest item on the chain gains [[#priority|Priority]]. Return to Step 2: Execute. 

### rule 341
**341.** [[#showdown|Showdowns ]]

### rule 342
**342.** A [[#showdown|Showdown ]]is a [[#window of opportunity|Window of Opportunity ]]in which [[#player|Players ]]have an [[#open state|Open State ]]in which they may play [[#spells|Spells ]]in an alternating fashion. 

#### rule 342.1
**342.1.** Each spell played this way creates a [[#chain|Chain ]]as normal. 

### rule 343
**343.** The [[#state|State ]]of the turn is partially determined by whether or not a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]or [[#combat|Combat ]]is in progress. 

#### rule 343.1
**343.1.** The turn is said to be in a [[#showdown|Showdown State ]]if a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]or [[#combat|Combat ]]is in progress. 

#### rule 343.1.a
**343.1.a.** Cards of all Categories, by default, cannot be played during a [[#showdown|Showdown State. ]]

#### rule 343.1.b
**343.1.b.** Card abilities, by default, cannot be played during a [[#showdown|Showdown State. ]]

#### rule 343.2
**343.2.** The turn is said to be in a [[#neutral state|Neutral State ]]if no [[#showdown|Showdown ]]or [[#combat|Combat ]]is in progress. 

### rule 344
**344.** A [[#showdown|Showdown ]]begins when [[#control|Control ]]of a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]is [[#contested|Contested ]]and the turn is in a [[#neutral open|Neutral Open State. ]]

#### rule 344.1
**344.1.** If [[#control|Control ]]of a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]is [[#contested|Contested ]]between two players, then a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]will be opened as the ﬁrst step of [[#combat|Combat.  ]]See [[##rule 454|rule 454.]] [[#combat|Combat]] for more information. 

#### rule 344.2
**344.2.** If [[#control|Control ]]of a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]is [[#contested|Contested ]]and the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]in question is uncontrolled when it becomes [[#contested|Contested]], a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]is opened during the [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]at the end of the action that caused the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]to become [[#contested|Contested. ]]

### rule 345
**345.** As a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]begins, the player who applied [[#contested|Contested ]]status to the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]gains [[#focus|Focus. ]]

### rule 346
**346.** When the last item on the chain resolves and the turn returns to an [[#open state|Open State ]]during a [[#showdown|Showdown]], [[#focus|Focus ]]passes, and the next [[#player|Player ]]gains both [[#focus|Focus ]]and [[#priority|Priority. ]]

#### rule 346.1
**346.1.** Focus will not pass in this way if the chain opened as a result of a triggered ability being added to the chain, nor if it opened as a result of an [[#added|Add ]]ability being added to the chain. Example: the Initial Chain opens as a result of triggered abilities being added to the chain, so when the last item on the Initial Chain resolves and the turn returns to an Open State, Focus will not pass. 

### rule 347
**347.** During a [[#showdown|Showdown]], the player with [[#focus|Focus ]]may do one of the following: 

#### rule 347.1
**347.1.** [[#play|Play ]]a card that is [[#legally timed|legally timed. ]]

#### rule 347.1.a
**347.1.a.** The card will start a [[#chain|Chain ]]as normal. 

#### rule 347.2
**347.2.** [[#activate abilities|Activate Abilities ]]of [[#game object|Game Objects ]]that are [[#legally timed|legally timed.  ]]See [[##rule 360|rule 360.]] [[#abilities|Abilities]] for more information. 

#### rule 347.3
**347.3.** Pass. 

#### rule 347.3.a
**347.3.a.** If all [[#player|Players ]]have passed once in sequence, the [[#showdown|Showdown ]]ends. 

#### rule 347.3.a.1
**347.3.a.1.** Perform a [[#cleanup|Cleanup. ]]

#### rule 347.4
**347.4.** Otherwise, [[#focus|Focus ]]passes to the next [[#player|Player ]]in [[#turn order|Turn Order. ]]

### rule 348
**348.** If all players pass [[#focus|Focus ]]without playing a spell or activating an ability, then the [[#showdown|Showdown ]]Closes. 

#### rule 348.1
**348.1.** If it is a [[#combat showdown|Combat Showdown, ]]proceed with the remaining steps of [[#combat|Combat ]]to resolve the phase.  See [[##rule 458|rule 458.]] [[#steps of combat|The Steps of Combat]] for more information. 

#### rule 348.2
**348.2.** If it is a [[#non-combat showdown|Non-Combat Showdown, ]]do the following: 

#### rule 348.2.a
**348.2.a.** If only one player’s Units remain at the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld]], and if that player does not already Control the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld]], that player establishes Control over the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld]]. See [[##rule 185|rule 185.]] [[#control|Control]] for more information on [[#control|Control]].  See [[##rule 464.1|rule 464.1.]]for more information on [[#conquering|Conquering]]. 

#### rule 348.2.a.1
**348.2.a.1.** This results in a Conquer if that player has not yet scored that [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]this turn. 

### rule 349
**349.** [[#playing cards|Playing Cards ]]

### rule 350
**350.** Playing a card is the act of a player utilizing their cards. 

#### rule 350.1
**350.1.** A card is [[#played|Played ]]when it has ﬁnished this process in its entirety. 

#### rule 350.2
**350.2.** Tokens are not cards, but can still be [[#played|Played.  ]]See [[##rule 176|rule 176.]] [[#token|Tokens]] for more information. 

### rule 351
**351.** Cards have different behaviors when played. 

#### rule 351.1
**351.1.** [[#permanents|Permanents ]]become [[#game object|Game Objects ]]when [[#played|Played. ]]

#### rule 351.2
**351.2.** [[#spells|Spells ]]create game effects that are executed, then the card is placed in the trash when [[#played|Played. ]]

### rule 352
**352.** Cards have different states during the process of being played. 

#### rule 352.1
**352.1.** When initially being played cards are [[#pending item|Pending, ]]as [[#pending chain items|Pending Chain Items. ]]

#### rule 352.2
**352.2.** Near the end of the process cards will cease being [[#pending item|Pending ]]and become [[#finalized chain items|Finalized Chain Items]]. 

### rule 353
**353.** [[#process of play|The Process of Play ]]

### rule 354
**354.** 1. Remove the card from the zone you are playing it from and put it onto the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 354.1
**354.1.** This [[#closes the state|Closes the State.  ]]See [[##rule 307|rule 307.]] [[#states of the turn|States of the Turn]] for more information. 

#### rule 354.2
**354.2.** This item becomes [[#pending item|Pending, ]]awaiting the ﬁnalization process (steps 2 - 5) 

#### rule 354.3
**354.3.** If another Card Effect or ability is currently resolving, continue resolving it before proceeding with any further steps of this process. 

#### rule 354.4
**354.4.** If there are Tasks outstanding or currently being handled, ﬁnish those Tasks before continuing this process. See [[##rule 334|rule 334.]]for more information on Tasks. 

### rule 355
**355.** 2. Make relevant choices. 

#### rule 355.1
**355.1.** If the card is a spell, or has an effect that speciﬁes a choice "As I am played," those choices are made now. 

#### rule 355.2
**355.2.** For [[#unit|Units]], choose a valid [[#location|Location ]]where that [[#unit|Unit ]]will be placed upon being [[#played|Played. ]]

#### rule 355.2.a
**355.2.a.** By default, [[#valid|Valid ]]locations include the controller’s [[#bases|Base ]]or a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]the controller controls. 

#### rule 355.2.b
**355.2.b.** Some [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]may grant players permission to play [[#unit|Units ]]to locations that are not normally [[#valid|Valid]]. Such locations become [[#valid|Valid ]]for the purposes of [[#playing|Playing ]]the [[#unit|Unit. ]]

#### rule 355.3
**355.3.** For [[#spells|Spells ]]and [[#abilities|Abilities ]]with a bulleted list of modes to choose from, make the appropriate choices now. 

#### rule 355.4
**355.4.** For [[#spells|Spells ]]and [[#abilities|Abilities ]]that [[#move|Move ]]one or more [[#unit|Units]], choose a valid [[#location|Location ]]as the [[#move destination|Move Destination ]]for each [[#move|Move ]]that will be performed. 

#### rule 355.4.a
**355.4.a.** A valid [[#location|Location ]]is one other than the [[#unit|Units’ ]]current [[#location|Location ]]where they are allowed to be present. 

#### rule 355.5
**355.5.** If a card requires you to speciﬁcally choose one or more [[#game object|Game Objects]], that choice is made now. 

#### rule 355.5.a
**355.5.a.** This does not include cards that affect one or more [[#game object|Game Objects ]]based on criteria.  Example: "Stun a unit at a battleﬁeld" is a [[#choice|Choice.  ]]Example: "Kill all gear" is not a [[#choice|Choice. ]]

#### rule 355.5.b
**355.5.b.** This does not include making choices for [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]of permanents, even if those abilities trigger when the permanent is played.  Example: A unit with a triggered ability that says "When I'm played, kill a unit" does not require you to choose a target as it's played. The target will be chosen when the ability triggers.  See [[##rule 382|rule 382.]] [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities]] for more information. 

#### rule 355.6
**355.6.** [[#targeting|Targeting ]]

#### rule 355.7
**355.7.** When a card [[#chooses|Chooses ]]one or more speciﬁc [[#game object|Game Objects ]]to affect, it is [[#targeting|Targeted ]]unless indicated otherwise by the rules in this section. 

#### rule 355.8
**355.8.** In order to put a spell or ability on the chain, valid choices must be made for all targets. 

#### rule 355.9
**355.9.** A target is a valid choice if it meets all of the following requirements: 

#### rule 355.9.a
**355.9.a.** It is a permanent or rune on the board, a spell or ability on the chain, a player or zone, or speciﬁed explicitly or implicitly as being in some other zone.  e.g., “Kill a unit” targets a unit on the board.  e.g., “Recycle a unit from your trash” targets a unit card in your trash. 

#### rule 355.9.a.1
**355.9.a.1.** “Unit,” “gear,” and “rune” refer to objects on the Board unless speciﬁed otherwise. 

#### rule 355.9.a.2
**355.9.a.2.** “Spell” and “ability” refer to objects on the Chain unless speciﬁed otherwise. 

#### rule 355.9.a.3
**355.9.a.3.** “Facedown card” refers to a card in a Facedown Zone unless speciﬁed otherwise. 

#### rule 355.9.a.4
**355.9.a.4.** “Legend” refers to a legend in the Legend Zone. 

#### rule 355.9.a.5
**355.9.a.5.** “Chosen Champion” and “unit in the Champion Zone” refer to a unit in the Champion Zone unless speciﬁed otherwise. 

#### rule 355.9.b
**355.9.b.** It meets all targeting restrictions.  e.g., A unit is a valid target for a spell that refers to a “unit at a battleﬁeld,” “enemy unit,” “unit you control,” or “unit with Might 4 or greater” only if it meets the appropriate criteria. 

#### rule 355.9.c
**355.9.c.** It is not the spell or ability itself.  e.g., A spell that says “Counter a spell” cannot target itself.  e.g., An ability of a permanent can target that permanent, because abilities and their sources are separate objects. 

#### rule 355.10
**355.10.** A game object, player, or zone mentioned in the text of a spell, activated ability, or triggered ability is a target UNLESS any of the following are true: 

#### rule 355.10.a
**355.10.a.** It is in a zone whose information status is not Public.  e.g., “Ready a legend” targets a legend, because the Legend Zone is Public.  e.g., “Return a unit from your trash to your hand” targets a unit card in your trash, because your trash is Public.  e.g., “You may play a unit from your hand, ignoring its costs” does not target a unit card in your hand, because your hand is not a public zone. 

#### rule 355.10.a.1
**355.10.a.1.** Public zones are Battleﬁeld Zones, Bases, Trashes, Legend Zones, Champion Zones, and Facedown Zones. 

#### rule 355.10.b
**355.10.b.** It is included only as part of a targeting restriction for another choice.  e.g., “Kill a unit at a battleﬁeld” targets a unit, but not a battleﬁeld, because the units are targets and “at a battleﬁeld” is a restriction.  e.g., “Kill all units at a battleﬁeld” targets a battleﬁeld, but not any units. 

#### rule 355.10.c
**355.10.c.** It is included only as part of a cost, trigger condition, or replacement effect.  e.g., “As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit” doesn’t target anything.  e.g., “When a friendly unit dies, kill a gear” targets a gear, but not a friendly unit.  e.g., “When you play me, the next time a friendly unit would die this turn, return it to your hand instead” doesn’t target anything. The replacement effect applies when any friendly unit dies.  e.g., “Choose a friendly unit. The next time it would die this turn, return it to your hand instead” targets a friendly unit, because “choose a friendly unit” is not part of the replacement effect. 

#### rule 355.10.c.1
**355.10.c.1.** This includes costs within instructions, identiﬁed by phrases like “[do X] to [do Y].” The cost within that instruction is “[do X].”  e.g., “When I hold, you may kill another friendly unit here to draw 1” does not target anything.  e.g., “When you play me, you may spend a buff to move a friendly unit” targets the friendly unit, but not the buff. 

#### rule 355.10.d
**355.10.d.** It is programmatically selected based on its characteristics rather than chosen by the spell or ability’s controller.  e.g., “Kill all units at a battleﬁeld” targets a battleﬁeld, but does not target any units.  e.g., “Kill all units at battleﬁelds” doesn’t target anything.  e.g., “Destroy a unit. Its controller draws 2 cards” targets the unit, but not its controller.  e.g., “Ready your legend” doesn’t target anything, because you can only have one legend. e.g., “Ready a friendly legend” targets a legend, because in a 2v2 game there are two friendly legends.  e.g., “Recycle all cards in your trash” doesn’t target anything, because it affects all cards and you only have one trash. 

#### rule 355.10.d.1
**355.10.d.1.** This exception applies solely to objects for which no choice is ever possible. 

#### rule 355.10.d.2
**355.10.d.2.** This exception does not apply to objects that are the only valid choice at the moment a spell or ability is placed on the chain, but which would require a choice under other circumstances.  e.g., “Kill a unit at a battleﬁeld” always targets a unit, even if that unit is the only unit currently at a battleﬁeld. 

#### rule 355.10.e
**355.10.e.** It is part of a set of objects chosen in whole or in part by other players.  e.g., “Each player kills a unit they control” does not target. Each player, including the one who played the spell, chooses a unit to kill as the spell or ability resolves. 

#### rule 355.10.f
**355.10.f.** It is identiﬁed in an instruction that a player “must” complete.  e.g., “You must recycle one of your runes” doesn’t target anything. You choose from among your runes as the spell or ability resolves.  e.g., “Recycle a rune you control” targets a rune. You choose a rune you control as you put the spell or ability on the chain. 

#### rule 355.11
**355.11.** Some cards identify a group of [[#targeting|Targets ]]with [[#targeting requirements|Targeting Requirements ]]that must be met by the group as a whole. 

#### rule 355.11.a
**355.11.a.** As they’re ﬁnalized on the chain, such cards can choose any group of valid targets that collectively fulﬁll the targeting restriction. 

#### rule 355.11.b
**355.11.b.** If the group of targets no longer collectively fulﬁll the targeting restriction as the spell or ability resolves, that spell or ability’s controller can choose a subset of the original targets that fulﬁlls the targeting requirement for the spell or ability to affect.  Example: A player plays Fox-Fire, a spell that says in part “Kill any number of units at a battleﬁeld with total Might 4 or less.” That player chooses four 1 [M] Recruit tokens at a single battleﬁeld. As a Reaction, another player gives two of those Recruits +1 [M], so the Recruits’ Mights are 1, 1, 2, and 2. Then Fox-Fire resolves. The Recruits no longer have total Might 4 or less, so Fox-Fire’s controller must choose a legal subset of the original targets to affect. They could choose to kill the two 2 [M] Recruits, or the two 1 [M] Recruits plus one 2 [M] Recruit. The units they choose are Fox-Fire’s remaining legal targets. They can’t choose to affect units at the same battleﬁeld that weren’t initially chosen as targets. They can, however, choose to affect units that were initially chosen as targets that left the chosen battleﬁeld before Fox-Fire resolved as long as those units are all located at the same battleﬁeld. 

#### rule 355.12
**355.12.** If a spell speciﬁes that a player may perform a [[#game actions|Game Action ]]on some number of [[#game object|Game Objects]], then all choices are considered targeted and chosen independently of the decision to perform the [[#game actions|Game Action. ]]

#### rule 355.13
**355.13.** If a card speciﬁes that a player chooses “any number” or “up to” some number of [[#game object|Game Objects ]]to be affected, they may choose any number of available targets, including zero. If they choose zero, the spell or ability can be played without any targets. 

#### rule 355.14
**355.14.** [[#splitting|Splitting ]]

#### rule 355.14.a
**355.14.a.** If a card speciﬁes that an amount of damage may be split among some number of [[#unit|Units]], then each [[#unit|Unit ]]chosen is [[#targeting|Targeted. ]]

#### rule 355.14.b
**355.14.b.** The [[#targeting|Targets ]]are chosen when the spell or ability is ﬁnalized on the chain. 

#### rule 355.14.c
**355.14.c.** A number of [[#targeting|Targets ]]can only be chosen up to, and not exceeding, the initial amount of damage available when the spell is played. Example: A player playing a spell that instructs them to "Split 5 damage" may only choose up to 5 units, but may choose fewer. 

#### rule 355.14.d
**355.14.d.** Each [[#targeting|Target ]]is valid, and contributes to [[#chosen|Chosen ]]triggers individually. 

#### rule 355.14.e
**355.14.e.** The choice of how much damage is divided across the split is not decided until the resolution of the spell or ability. 

#### rule 355.14.f
**355.14.f.** Each [[#targeting|Target ]]must receive a valid amount of damage. 

#### rule 355.14.g
**355.14.g.** Valid damage is a positive integer amount, greater than or equal to 1 damage. See [[##rule 417|rule 417.]] [[#decks|Deal]] for more information. 

#### rule 355.14.h
**355.14.h.** If, at resolution of the spell or effect, there are more [[#targeting|Targets ]]than available damage to divide, then the player who controls the effect dealing damage determines which [[#targeting|Targets ]]cease being [[#targeting|Targets. ]]

#### rule 355.14.i
**355.14.i.** Any costs that were paid, or effects that were triggered as a result of those [[#game object|Game Objects ]]being chosen as [[#targeting|Targets ]]remain in effect, paid, or otherwise triggered. 

#### rule 355.15
**355.15.** These choices cannot be changed after this step. 

#### rule 355.16
**355.16.** A player may not make choices during this step that will deterministically result in illegal choices or actions later in this process unless they have no choice.  Example: A player plays a card which reads “as an additional cost to play this, kill the unit you control with the most Might. Give a friendly unit +[M] equal to the killed unit’s Might this turn. Predict 2.” They cannot choose to target their unit with the highest Might during this step of ﬁnalization. 

#### rule 355.17
**355.17.** If a spell or ability requires one or more players to make choices that are not outlined in this section, they are made on resolution. 

### rule 356
**356.** 3. Determine Total Cost. 

#### rule 356.1
**356.1.** Apply base cost modiﬁcations in any order. 

#### rule 356.1.a
**356.1.a.** If an ability or instruction allows you to play a card “for [Cost]”, replace the card’s [[#base cost(s)|Base Costs ]]with [Cost]. 

#### rule 356.1.b
**356.1.b.** If an ability or instruction allows you to "ignore" one or more of a card's costs, set the appropriate [[#base cost(s)|Base Cost(s) ]]of the card to zero. 

#### rule 356.1.b.1
**356.1.b.1.** If a card allows a player to play a card "ignoring its cost," its base [[#energy|Energy cost ]]and base [[#power|Power cost ]]are set to zero. 

#### rule 356.1.b.2
**356.1.b.2.** If a card instructs a player to play a card "ignoring its Energy cost" or "ignoring its Power cost," only the appropriate cost is set to zero, and the remaining cost still applies. 

#### rule 356.1.b.3
**356.1.b.3.** Further additional costs and/or cost increases applied in subsequent steps may raise the card's [[#total cost|Total Cost ]]above zero.  Example: Legion Rearguard is a Fury unit that costs 2 Energy and 0 Power and has Accelerate. A player plays Legion Rearguard and is instructed to ignore its costs, but chooses to pay the Accelerate cost. They ignore Legion Rearguard's [[#base cost(s)|Base Cost ]]of 2 Energy, but the optional additional cost of 1 Energy and 1 Fury Power is added to its [[#total cost|Total Cost ]]and must be paid. 

#### rule 356.2
**356.2.** Apply additional costs in any order. 

#### rule 356.2.a
**356.2.a.** [[#mandatory additional costs|Mandatory Additional Costs ]]

#### rule 356.2.a.1
**356.2.a.1.** Some [[#additional costs|Additional Costs ]]speciﬁed by [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities ]]on the card being played or another card are [[#mandatory|Mandatory]], and must be paid to complete playing the card. They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and don't include the word "may."  Example: A unit has the passive ability "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." To play that unit, a player must kill a friendly unit.  See [[##rule 363|rule 363.]] [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities]] for more information. 

#### rule 356.2.a.2
**356.2.a.2.** The cost imposed by the [[#deflect|Deflect ]]keyword is a [[#mandatory additional costs|Mandatory Additional Cost.  ]]See [[##rule 809|rule 809.]] [[#deflect|Deflect]] for more information. 

#### rule 356.2.b
**356.2.b.** [[#optional additional costs|Optional Additional Costs ]]

#### rule 356.2.b.1
**356.2.b.1.** Some [[#optional costs|Optional Costs ]]speciﬁed by [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities ]]on the card being played or another card are [[#non-mandatory|Non-Mandatory]], and must be paid only if the player made the choice to pay them in [[#step 2|step 2. ]]They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and the word "may."  Example: A unit has the ability "As you play me, you may discard 1 as an additional cost. If you do, reduce my cost by [2]." While playing the unit, its controller declares their intention to pay the additional cost in [[#step 2|step 2]], applies that additional cost in [[##rule 356.2]], applies the discount granted by paying that cost in [[##rule 356.4]], and discards a card to pay that additional cost in [[##rule 357.2|rule 357.2.]]See [[##rule 363|rule 363.]] [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities]] for more information. 

#### rule 356.3
**356.3.** Apply cost increases. 

#### rule 356.4
**356.4.** Apply discounts. 

#### rule 356.4.a
**356.4.a.** Discounts may be applied by the card being played or by any other card or effect. 

#### rule 356.4.b
**356.4.b.** Discounts may say that cards "cost [amount] less" or that one or more of their costs are "reduced by [amount]." 

#### rule 356.4.c
**356.4.c.** Discounts that only apply to a component of the cost will be applied when that component is added to the cost of the spell and before any other discounts.  Example: Ezreal, Prodigy reads “optional additional costs you pay cost [1] or [A] less.” When playing a Frigid Touch and choosing to pay the additional cost in step 2, as soon as the additional cost is added to the cost of the spell, Ezreal, Prodigy’s discount is applied to it. 

#### rule 356.4.c.1
**356.4.c.1.** Discounts that apply to a given component of a spell’s cost may be applied in any order to that component. 

#### rule 356.4.d
**356.4.d.** Discounts that apply to the total cost of a spell and not any one component of the cost must be applied after any discount that applies only to a component of the cost. 

#### rule 356.4.d.1
**356.4.d.1.** These discounts may be applied in any order as long as they are applied after component discounts. 

#### rule 356.4.e
**356.4.e.** If a discount applies a minimum cost, that minimum applies only to that discount.  Example: Eager Apprentice says "While I'm at a battleﬁeld, the Energy costs for spells you play is reduced by [1], to a minimum of [1]." A player who controls Eager Apprentice and a unit with 7 Might plays Sky Splitter, a spell that costs 8 Energy and says "This spell's Energy cost is reduced by the highest Might among units you control." That player can choose to apply Eager Apprentice's discount ﬁrst, reducing Sky Splitter's Energy cost to 7, then apply Sky Splitter's discount, reducing its Energy cost to 0. If they applied these discounts in the other order, Sky Splitter's Energy cost would be 1. 

#### rule 356.4.f
**356.4.f.** Discounts can reduce additional costs, including to 0. 

#### rule 356.4.f.1
**356.4.f.1.** An optional additional cost was "paid" if the player made the decision to pay it. It doesn't matter how much the player actually paid. Example: Clockwork Keeper is a unit that costs 2 Energy and 0 Power and says "As you play me, you may pay [C] as an additional cost. If you do, draw 1." A player controls a card that says "Units you play cost [A] less." That player plays Clockwork Keeper and chooses to pay the optional additional cost of [C]. They will draw a card, even though the optional additional cost was reduced to 0. 

#### rule 356.5
**356.5.** Energy and Power costs can't be reduced below 0. 

#### rule 356.6
**356.6.** [[#cost|Costs ]]may be Energy costs, Power costs, or non-standard costs. Example: A card reads "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." Killing a friendly unit is an additional cost to play that card. 

### rule 357
**357.** 4. Pay the card's costs. 

#### rule 357.1
**357.1.** In total, pay the combined [[#energy|Energy ]]cost (if any) and [[#power|Power ]]cost (if any). 

#### rule 357.1.a
**357.1.a.** During this step, the card's controller can use activated abilities with the [[#reaction|Reaction ]]tag that [[#added|Add ]]resources to add [[#energy|Energy ]]and [[#power|Power ]]to pay the card's costs.  See [[##rule 164|rule 164.]] [[#rune pool|Rune Pools]] and [[##rule 429|rule 429.]] [[#added|Add]] for more information. 

#### rule 357.2
**357.2.** In addition, pay any non-standard [[#cost|Cost ]]summed in [[#step 3: pass|step 3 ]]in any order. 

#### rule 357.2.a
**357.2.a.** Costs that are replaced with other events by replacement effects are still considered paid.  Example: A player plays Cruel Patron, which says "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." They also control Zhonya’s Hourglass, which says “If a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Heal that unit, exhaust it, and recall it.” They choose to kill a friendly unit during [[#step 3: pass|step 3, ]]but as they pay the cost in [[#step 4|step 4, ]]Zhonya’s Hourglass replaces that unit’s death. The cost is considered paid, and the player can continue playing Cruel Patron. 

#### rule 357.3
**357.3.** A player may not pay costs during this step that will deterministically result in illegal choices or actions later in this process unless they have no choice.  Example:  A player plays a card which reads “as an additional cost to play this, you may kill a friendly unit. Give a friendly unit +2 [M] this turn. If you paid the cost, give that unit +7 [M] this turn instead” If they chose to pay the cost, they must choose to kill a unit other than the targeted unit unless they have no choice. 

### rule 358
**358.** 5. Check legality. 

#### rule 358.1
**358.1.** Check that all chosen targets are legal. 

#### rule 358.2
**358.2.** Ensure that the outcome of the effect of this card being played would not create an illegal state.  Example: Check that a spell's execution does not create a state where a Battleﬁeld has [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by 3 different players. 

#### rule 358.3
**358.3.** Ensure that the card has the appropriate permissions to be played at this timing. Example: If the state is Showdown Closed and the card was the one that Closed the state, ensure that it has [Action] or [Reaction]. Example: If the state is Closed and the card wasn’t the one that Closed the state, ensure that it has [Reaction]. 

#### rule 358.4
**358.4.** If the card, if continued to be played, would create an illegal state, or if a choice or action at this state is illegal, the actions taken in this process are undone and the action is cancelled. 

### rule 359
**359.** 6. Finish ﬁnalizing this card and proceed with the card's category of [[#play|Play. ]]

#### rule 359.1
**359.1.** This card is no longer [[#pending item|Pending]]. 

#### rule 359.2
**359.2.** A [[#permanents|Permanent ]]leaves the [[#chain|Chain ]]and becomes a [[#game object|Game Object. ]]

#### rule 359.2.a
**359.2.a.** Any passive abilities become active. 

#### rule 359.2.b
**359.2.b.** Execute all rules text on the card, from top to bottom. 

#### rule 359.2.c
**359.2.c.** If it is a [[#unit|Unit]], it enters [[#board exhausted|the Board exhausted ]]at the [[#location|Location ]]that was chosen. 

#### rule 359.2.d
**359.2.d.** If it is a [[#gear|Gear, ]]it enters [[#board|the Board Ready ]]at the player's [[#bases|Base. ]]

#### rule 359.3
**359.3.** A [[#spells|Spell ]]lingers on the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 359.3.a
**359.3.a.** This card becomes a Finalized [[#chain|Chain Item. ]]

#### rule 359.3.b
**359.3.b.** If there are other [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]on the Chain, then the controller of those [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]completes Steps 2 through 5 of Playing Cards for those items before continuing.  See [[##rule 327|rule 327.]] [[#chain|Chains]] for more information. 

#### rule 359.3.c
**359.3.c.** Other players have an opportunity to play [[#reaction|Reactions ]]before the resolution of spells.  See [[##rule 327|rule 327.]] [[#chain|Chains]] for more information. 

#### rule 359.3.d
**359.3.d.** Otherwise, execute the game effect of the spell, from top to bottom of the rules text of the card and then place the card in the [[#trashes|Trash ]]of the owning player. 

#### rule 359.3.e
**359.3.e.** Handling illegal and impossible instructions 

#### rule 359.3.e.1
**359.3.e.1.** The spell resolves even if some or all of its targets are illegal. 

#### rule 359.3.e.2
**359.3.e.2.** A target is illegal as the spell resolves if it no longer meets the targeting requirements of the spell, or if it has changed [[#zones|Zones ]]to or from a [[#non-board zones|Non-Board Zone. ]]

#### rule 359.3.e.3
**359.3.e.3.** If a target ceases to meet the targeting requirements while the spell is on the chain, then meets them again, it's a legal target.  Example: A spell targets "a unit at a battleﬁeld." A player reacts with a spell that moves the unit to base, then another player reacts with a spell that moves it back to that battleﬁeld, then the original spell resolves. The unit is a legal target. 

#### rule 359.3.e.4
**359.3.e.4.** If a target changes [[#zones|Zones ]]to or from a [[#non-board zones|Non-Board Zone ]]and then returns to its original zone, it is no longer a legal target, because it's not treated as the same object.  Examples:  An enemy unit at a battleﬁeld is no longer a legal target if it is no longer an enemy, no longer a unit, or no longer at a battleﬁeld.  A unit with 3 or less Might is no longer a legal target if it is no longer a unit or if its Might is greater than 3.  Something that's exhausted is no longer a legal target if it is no longer exhausted. (It can't stop being "something.")  A spell that's played from hidden can normally only target its own battleﬁeld or something at that battleﬁeld. A target for such a spell may cease to be a legal target if it moves from the battleﬁeld where that spell was played, even if the spell has no location targeting requirement otherwise. 

#### rule 359.3.e.5
**359.3.e.5.** If any of the spell's targets are no longer legal, those targets are unaffected by the spell as it resolves.  Example: A player plays Void Seeker, a spell that says "Deal 4 to a unit at a battleﬁeld. Draw 1." The unit's controller uses a Reaction to move the unit to their base. Since the unit is no longer a legal target, it is not dealt any damage. Void Seeker's controller still draws 1. 

#### rule 359.3.e.6
**359.3.e.6.** Instructions that can't be followed, either because of illegal targets or other circumstances, are ignored. 

#### rule 359.3.e.7
**359.3.e.7.** If all of an instruction's [[#targeting|Targets ]]become [[#invalid|Invalid ]]or [[#unavailable|Unavailable ]]by the time the spell is ﬁnished being played, that instruction will not execute. 

#### rule 359.3.e.8
**359.3.e.8.** If an instruction has more than one [[#targeting|Target ]]and fewer than all of the [[#targeting|Targets ]]become [[#invalid|Invalid ]]or [[#unavailable|Unavailable ]]by the time the spell is ﬁnished being played, the instruction will execute, with only the [[#targeting|Targets ]]available and valid being operated on. 

#### rule 359.3.e.9
**359.3.e.9.** The process for a card's choice [[#becoming invalid|becoming Invalid ]]or [[#unavailable|Unavailable ]]is referred to as [[#mistargeting|mistargeting.  ]]Example: A spell has the instruction "Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld." Before that instruction can execute, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The instruction will not be executed, because it speciﬁes that the unit it chooses must be at a Battleﬁeld, and by the time it attempted to execute, the unit was no longer valid as a choice. 

#### rule 359.3.e.10
**359.3.e.10.** It is possible for none of a spell's instructions to be executed as it resolves, due to all of them requiring targets to act on and all of those targets becoming [[#invalid|Invalid ]]or [[#unavailable|Unavailable]]. In this case, the spell has no effect but is still considered played.  Example: A player plays a spell that reads "Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld" with no other instructions, and chooses an enemy unit at a battleﬁeld. They also control a unit with the ability "When you play a spell, give me +1 [M] this turn." Before the spell resolves, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The spell resolves and its only instruction cannot be executed, but the unit's ability still triggers as the spell resolves and gives it +1 [M]. 

#### rule 359.3.e.11
**359.3.e.11.** Instructions that can be partially followed are followed as much as possible and ignored otherwise.  Example: A player plays a spell that says "Discard 2, then draw 2" If their hand is empty, the instruction to discard 2 will be ignored. They'll still draw 2. If they had 1 card in hand, they would discard it and draw 2. 

#### rule 359.3.e.12
**359.3.e.12.** If the spell checks information about a target that is no longer legal or a card or permanent whose location, zone, or status has changed such that that information is no longer available, that check returns "null" and all calculations based on it are ignored.  Examples:  A unit that is no longer on the board is treated as having null Might, null cost, etc.  A unit that is no longer on the board has no location, is neither exhausted nor readied, etc.  Baited Hook says "[1][C], [E]: Kill a friendly unit. Look at the top 5 cards of your Main Deck. You may banish a unit from among them that has Might up to 1 more than the killed unit and play it, ignoring its cost. Then recycle the rest." While Baited Hook’s ability is on the chain, an opponent reacts with a spell that returns the friendly unit to its owner's hand. Because the friendly unit is no longer a legal target, it can't be killed and its Might is treated as null. Baited Hook’s controller looks at the top 5 cards of their Main Deck, but can’t choose any unit from among them. 

#### rule 359.3.e.12.a
**359.3.e.12.a.** If the spell checks information about a target that is legal, or a card or permanent whose location, zone, or status has not changed such that information is no longer available, that information is accessible. 

#### rule 359.3.e.13
**359.3.e.13.** A spell or ability that moves something to a different zone as a cost or effect can "look back" at its characteristics before it changes zones. 

#### rule 359.3.e.14
**359.3.e.14.** Some instructions may reference Game Objects affected by, or Game Actions performed in, other instructions in a card. The referenced and referencing instructions are called “linked instructions.” 

#### rule 359.3.e.14.a
**359.3.e.14.a.** In order for a later linked instruction to execute, its earlier linked instruction must have executed. If the earlier linked instruction is ignored for any reason, the later linked instruction will also be ignored. 

#### rule 359.3.e.14.b
**359.3.e.14.b.** If the Game Action performed in an earlier linked instruction is replaced, this will not affect the later linked instruction. 

#### rule 359.3.e.15
**359.3.e.15.** A spell or ability that leaves the chain during the process of its resolution will cease further execution of its instructions. This immediately causes the spell or ability to ﬁnish resolving. 

#### rule 359.3.f
**359.3.f.** Referents 

#### rule 359.3.f.1
**359.3.f.1.** Some information used by abilities is referenced from the source of those abilities, or from one or more targets of a spell or ability. This can usually be recognized by the presence of words like “here,” “my,” or “its.” 

#### rule 359.3.f.2
**359.3.f.2.** Information referenced in an instruction in this way will be checked on execution of the instruction. Examples:  A player moves Yasuo, Remorseful to an occupied enemy battleﬁeld and initiates combat there. In reaction to the Yasuo, Remorseful attack trigger, their opponent plays Fight or Flight from hidden targeting Yasuo, moving him back to base. When the attack trigger resolves, “here” is no longer the battleﬁeld where combat is ongoing and the attack trigger mistargets. In reaction to a Yasuo, Remorseful attack trigger, an opponent plays Stupefy targeting Yasuo. When Yasuo’s attack trigger resolves, it will deal damage equal to his current Might of 5.

#### rule 359.3.f.3
**359.3.f.3.** Some information used by triggered abilities is referenced from the trigger condition of the ability. This information is checked when the trigger condition is fulﬁlled.  Example: Lillia, Fae Fawn reads “when I move from a location, play a 3 [M] Sprite token with Temporary there.” If Lillia moves to a battleﬁeld, her triggered ability will be placed on the chain and it will note the location she moved from when it does so. If she moves to a non-board zone in reaction to the triggered ability on the chain, it will not affect where the Sprite token will be played when the triggered ability resolves. 

#### rule 359.3.f.3.a
**359.3.f.3.a.** In the case of a delayed triggered ability, the information is referenced when the triggered ability is created unless speciﬁed otherwise. 

#### rule 359.3.f.3.a.1
**359.3.f.3.a.1.** In the case of a linked ability that references information from a linked triggered ability, that information may be referenced from the trigger condition of the linked triggered ability if speciﬁed. 

#### rule 359.3.f.4
**359.3.f.4.** Some information used by the effect of a triggered ability is referenced from the triggered ability itself, such as “enemy” and “friendly” status. This information is checked on execution of the referencing instruction. Example: Yasuo, Remorseful reads “when I attack, deal damage equal to my Might to an enemy unit here.” Yasuo moves to an occupied enemy battleﬁeld and his attack trigger goes on the chain. In reaction to the attack trigger, the defending player plays a hidden Hostile Takeover and gains control of Yasuo. The triggered ability is unaffected by Yasuo changing controllers, and “enemy” is in reference to the triggered ability itself, so it will resolve with no issue. Example: In reaction to the same Yasuo, Remorseful trigger, say the defending player had instead played a spell that reads “[Reaction]. Gain control of a triggered ability. You may make new choices for it.” They chose the attack trigger. When Yasuo’s attack trigger resolves, if they didn’t make new choices for the trigger, the controller of the triggered ability will no longer be an enemy to the targeted unit, so the triggered ability will mistarget and do nothing. If they instead chose Yasuo with the attack trigger, he would be an enemy unit to the triggered ability and so it would deal damage equal to his Might to himself. 

### rule 360
**360.** [[#abilities|Abilities ]]

### rule 361
**361.** An [[#abilities|Ability ]]is the structured rules and capabilities of [[#game object|Game Objects ]]or [[#spells|Spells. ]]

#### rule 361.1
**361.1.** An [[#abilities|Ability ]]has multiple structures.  -[[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities  ]]-[[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects  ]]-[[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities  ]]-[[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities  ]]-[[#delayed abilities|Delayed Abilities ]]

### rule 362
**362.** A card can have more than one [[#abilities|Ability ]]and more than one type of [[#abilities|Ability. ]]

### rule 363
**363.** Passive Abilities 

### rule 364
**364.** Conditions, rules, constraints, or statements that affect the course of regular play. 

#### rule 364.1
**364.1.** These abilities have a wide variety of formats to recognize.  Example: "I get +1 [M] while you have 2 or more cards in your hand."  Example: "Friendly Yordles at my battleﬁeld have [Shield]." 

#### rule 364.2
**364.2.** They can be recognized by being [[#statements of fact|statements of fact. ]]

#### rule 364.3
**364.3.** [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities ]]can be conditional. 

#### rule 364.3.a
**364.3.a.** [[#conditional passive abilities|Conditional Passive Abilities ]]can be recognized by the occurrence of "if" or "while" as part of the statement of the ability.  Example: "[[#while|While ]]I'm attacking or defending alone, I have +2 [M]."  Example: "[[#invalid|If ]]an opponent controls a battleﬁeld, I enter ready." 

### rule 365
**365.** Presence on [[#permanents|Permanents ]]

#### rule 365.1
**365.1.** Passive Abilities of [[#permanents|Permanents ]]are typically only active while on [[#board|the Board. ]]

### rule 366
**366.** Presence on [[#card outside of the board|Card outside of the Board ]]

#### rule 366.1
**366.1.** [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities ]]of cards in zones that are outside of [[#board|the Board ]]will self-describe their context.  Example: The passive ability "Play me only during an opponent's turn." applies in any zone from which that card can be played. 

#### rule 366.2
**366.2.** [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities ]]can alter the costs of cards as they are played. 

#### rule 366.2.a
**366.2.a.** These apply at all times in any zone from which the card with the ability can be played. 

### rule 367
**367.** Replacement Effects 

### rule 368
**368.** An ability that alters the application of another game effect or game rule. 

#### rule 368.1
**368.1.** [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities ]]can be [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects. ]]

### rule 369
**369.** [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]intercede during the execution of a Game Effect and alter its execution. 

#### rule 369.1
**369.1.** A [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]can usually be identiﬁed by the presence of the terms “would” or "instead."  Example: Zhonya's Hourglass reads "The next time a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Heal that unit, exhaust it, and recall it." This is a replacement effect that alters the execution of any Game Effect that would kill a friendly unit. 

#### rule 369.2
**369.2.** Some [[#game actions|Game Actions ]]are themselves [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects. ]]Example: Burning Out is a replacement effect. Example: Preventing Damage is a replacement effect. 

### rule 370
**370.** A [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]can alter the typical flow of play, including other cards' executions. 

#### rule 370.1
**370.1.** [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]apply to any event or instruction that qualiﬁes for their application. A [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]will specify the circumstances by which an event or instruction will qualify to be replaced.  

#### rule 370.1.a
**370.1.a.** When a [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]applies, it replaces the qualifying event with one or more [[#game actions|Game Actions ]]or events, or the qualifying instruction with another instruction. 

#### rule 370.2
**370.2.** A [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]can only be applied once to an event, or to any [[#game actions|Game Actions ]]or events that replace that event. Example: A player plays a spell that reads “gear you control become 1 [M] gear units this turn.” They control two copies of Zhonya’s Hourglass when the spell resolves. If one of those copies is killed, both of their Replacement Effects will be applied. Whichever is applied ﬁrst, that Replacement Effect can’t be applied again. When it is applied, it kills its source, which creates an event the other can apply its Replacement Effect to. Once they’ve both applied their Replacement Effect to the original death event and the event that replaced it, they cannot go any further. At that point, whichever Zhonya’s Hourglass applied its Replacement Effect last will die. 

#### rule 370.3
**370.3.** If a [[#game object|Game Object ]]has a [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]that is active in a speciﬁc zone, it is evaluated and subsequently applied if it enters that zone before an event occurs that it could replace.  Example: A unit that reads “if a unit you control would die, you may banish me from your trash instead. If you do, heal that unit, exhaust it and recall it.” The ﬁrst unit dies simultaneously with a 1 [M] Recruit token. It does not enter the trash before the Recruit dies, so it will not be able to replace its death. 

### rule 371
**371.** Some [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]will begin with “once each turn.” 

#### rule 371.1
**371.1.** When an event the [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]could apply to occurs, the player who controls the [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]may choose to apply it to the event. 

#### rule 371.2
**371.2.** If they do not, it has not been applied this turn. 

### rule 372
**372.** If more than one [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]applies to the same event being executed, then the owner of the object being acted on determines the order the [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]will apply. 

#### rule 372.1
**372.1.** If it is a player being acted on, that player decides the order the [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]will apply. 

#### rule 372.2
**372.2.** If the affected object is an [[#uncontrolled battleﬁeld|Uncontrolled Battleﬁeld ]]then the [[#current turn player|Current Turn Player ]]decides the order the [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]will apply. 

### rule 373
**373.** If more than one event occurs simultaneously that [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]could apply to, each event is treated separately and individually for the purposes of [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects, ]]and [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]with the same controller are applied in the order of their controller’s choosing. Example: Two units controlled by the same player die in the same cleanup. That player also controls Zhonya’s Hourglass. They must decide which event to apply Zhonya’s Hourglass to ﬁrst. 

#### rule 373.1
**373.1.** Although these events are simultaneous, the applied [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]are ordered. If multiple applied Replacement Effects with different controllers would execute simultaneously, they execute in turn order.  

#### rule 373.2
**373.2.** When applying Replacement Effects to events that occur simultaneously, each Replacement Effect may only be applied in one sequence, to any number of events that are qualiﬁed to be replaced.  Example: Soraka, Wanderer reads “If another unit you control here would die, if it has less Might than me, instead heal it, exhaust it, and recall it.” Soraka dies simultaneously with two 1 [M] Recruit tokens at the same battleﬁeld and two 1 [M] Recruit tokens in base. Soraka has a Guardian Angel attached to her when she dies, which appends “If I would die, kill Guardian Angel instead. Heal me, exhaust me, and recall me” to Soraka’s rules text. There are several possible ways to order the Replacement Effects being applied to the various events: If Soraka’s Replacement Effect is applied ﬁrst, it saves the Recruits at the same battleﬁeld as her but not the Recruits in base. If the Replacement Effect appended by Guardian Angel then saves Soraka, she cannot apply her Replacement Effect to the Recruits in base as her Replacement Effect has already been applied to an event simultaneous with it dying. If the Replacement Effect appended by Guardian Angel is applied ﬁrst, it saves Soraka and recalls her - then when Soraka’s Replacement Effect is applied, it can only save the Recruits in base. 

#### rule 373.2.a
**373.2.a.** A sequence of Replacement Effects is an uninterrupted series of applications to a set of simultaneous events. 

#### rule 373.2.a.1
**373.2.a.1.** A Replacement Effect that replaces an event or Game Action that is part of another Replacement Effect will not interrupt the sequence of the replaced Replacement Effect’s application. 

### rule 374
**374.** A [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect]]’s controller is the player that controls the source of the [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect. ]]

### rule 375
**375.** If an event that a [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]applies to would be modiﬁed by a [[#game effects|Game Effect]], or the results of that event would be modiﬁed by a [[#game actions|Game Action, ]]the [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect ]]will inherit those modiﬁcations. Example: Treasure Hunter reads “When I move, play a Gold gear token exhausted.” A Replacement Effect that says “if you would play a token gear, play that token and an additional copy instead” is applied to the event of the Gold gear token being played. The additional copy will also be exhausted, as it inherits the “exhausted” modiﬁcation. Example: Another Replacement Effect says “if you would play a token, draw 1 instead.” The modiﬁcation cannot apply, so we ignore it. Example: A spell reads “play a ready 3 [M] Mech token. Then do this: Give it Temporary.” A Replacement Effect that says “if you would play a unit token, play that token and a 1 [M] Recruit token instead” is applied to the event of the Mech token being made. The Recruit token enters ready and is given Temporary. 

### rule 376
**376.** Activated Abilities 

### rule 377
**377.** [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities ]]are repeatable effects with a cost. They follow a process of going onto the chain and resolving, similar to [[#playing a card|Playing a Card.  ]]See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 377.1
