**377.1.** [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities ]]are recognized by the presence of a ":" in the text of the card, preceded by a cost and succeeded by an effect.  Example: "[2]: Draw 1" is an activated ability. The [[#cost|cost ]]is 2 energy. The [[#effect text|effect ]]is to draw 1 card. 

#### rule 377.2
**377.2.** Card text will refer to activating [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities ]]with the word “use.” 

#### rule 377.2.a
**377.2.a.** If “using” an [[#activated abilities|Activated Ability ]]is part of a trigger condition, that condition is fulﬁlled when the [[#activated abilities|Activated Ability ]]resolves. 

#### rule 377.2.b
**377.2.b.** If an Activated Ability has a condition on “using” it, that condition must be true in order to activate the ability in question. Example: Ultrasoft Poro reads “[E]: Play two 1 [M] Bird unit tokens with [Deflect]. Use this ability only while I'm at a battleﬁeld.” In order to activate the ability, Ultrasoft Poro must be located at a battleﬁeld. 

#### rule 377.3
**377.3.** [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities ]]use the chain. 

#### rule 377.3.a
**377.3.a.** Declare activation of the [[#abilities|Ability. ]]

#### rule 377.3.a.1
**377.3.a.1.** The ability goes on the chain but has no card to represent it, so players need to take note that it is now a [[#closed state|Closed State. ]]

#### rule 377.3.b
**377.3.b.** Proceed with executing the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 377.3.b.1
**377.3.b.1.** Follow the steps of “Playing or Activating Abilities” in [[##rule 398]]. This ability will become a [[#pending chain items|Pending Chain Item. ]]

#### rule 377.3.b.2
**377.3.b.2.** Opponents have an opportunity to respond, as appropriate, as if a card was played onto the chain. 

#### rule 377.3.b.3
**377.3.b.3.** If no further action is taken, execute the [[#activated abilities|Activated Ability. ]]

### rule 378
**378.** The controlling player chooses when and whether to activate an [[#activated abilities|Activated Ability. ]]

### rule 379
**379.** Activated abilities are present on [[#game object|Game Objects ]]and some [[#spells|Spells. ]]

### rule 380
**380.** Can primarily be activated while on [[#board|the Board. ]]

### rule 381
**381.** All [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities ]]can only be activated on the Controlling Player's Turn and during an [[#open state|Open State. ]]

### rule 382
**382.** Triggered Abilities 

### rule 383
**383.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]are repeatable effects that happen when a [[#condition|Condition ]]is met. 

#### rule 383.1
**383.1.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can usually be recognized by the word "when" followed by a game action or event; the word "at" followed by a point in time during the turn sequence; or the phrase “the [Nth] time” followed by a game action or event.  Examples:  "[[#while|When ]]you conquer here, you may spend a buff to draw 1."  "At the end of your turn, ready 2 runes."  “The ﬁrst time I move each turn, you may ready something else that's exhausted.” 

#### rule 383.1.a
**383.1.a.** The phrases that identify triggered abilities do not always appear at the beginning of sentences or abilities. 

#### rule 383.1.b
**383.1.b.** If an ability triggers “the [Nth] time” something happens and that trigger condition is met multiple times simultaneously, the ability’s controller picks one of those instances to serve as the trigger condition. The ability triggers only once, due to the chosen condition.  Example: Wraith of Echoes reads “The ﬁrst time another friendly unit dies each turn, draw 1.” That ability hasn’t triggered yet this turn. Two other friendly units die simultaneously (say, due to combat damage). The Wraith’s controller chooses one of those deaths to trigger Wraith’s ability. 

#### rule 383.2
**383.2.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]have a [[#condition|Condition ]]and an [[#effect text|Effect. ]]

#### rule 383.2.a
**383.2.a.** The [[#condition|Condition ]]follows the [[#while|When. ]]

#### rule 383.2.b
**383.2.b.** The [[#effect text|Effect ]]is the [[#instructions|Instruction ]]that follows the comma after the [[#condition|Condition. ]]

#### rule 383.2.c
**383.2.c.** The [[#condition|Condition ]]of a [[#trigger|Trigger ]]is evaluated after a potentially inciting event has been processed. 

#### rule 383.2.c.1
**383.2.c.1.** If a [[#game object|Game Object ]]with a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]that is active in a speciﬁc zone, it is evaluated and subsequently triggered if it enters that zone at the same time that its [[#trigger|Trigger]]’s condition is met.  Example: Immortal Phoenix says “When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.” This ability triggers if Immortal Phoenix is in your trash immediately after you kill a unit with a spell, even if the unit you killed with a spell was that Immortal Phoenix. 

#### rule 383.2.c.2
**383.2.c.2.** A [[#game object|Game Object ]]will not be able to successfully be able to evaluate its [[#trigger condition|Trigger Condition]], however, if it leaves the zone that its [[#trigger|Trigger ]]is active from at the same time that its [[#trigger|Trigger ]]is satisﬁed.  Example: Viktor, Leader says “When another non-Recruit unit you control dies, play a 1 [M] Recruit unit token into your base.” This ability triggers if Viktor is on the board immediately after another non-Recruit unit you control dies. It does not trigger if Viktor and another non-Recruit unit you control die during the same game action (for instance, if they are both killed in the same Cleanup due to the damage dealt by Unchecked Power). 

#### rule 383.3
**383.3.** When a [[#condition|Condition ]]is met, a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]behaves like an [[#activated abilities|Activated Ability ]]and is placed on the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 383.3.a
**383.3.a.** If a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]says “you may” as the ﬁrst part of its [[#effect text|Effect]], the controller of its source will choose whether or not to place the [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]on the chain when its trigger [[#condition|Condition ]]is fulﬁlled. 

#### rule 383.3.b
**383.3.b.** If a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]contains a cost within instructions, that cost is treated as the base cost of the [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability. ]]

#### rule 383.3.b.1
**383.3.b.1.** The cost must be paid in order to ﬁnalize the [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]to the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 383.3.b.2
**383.3.b.2.** Costs within instructions for [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]are not paid on resolution, unlike costs within instructions for [[#spells|Spells. ]]

#### rule 383.3.c
**383.3.c.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can be put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]during [[#closed state|Closed States ]]or [[#open state|Open States ]]on any player's turn. 

#### rule 383.3.d
**383.3.d.** If more than one [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]is [[#trigger|Triggered ]]simultaneously, then the player that controls the [[#abilities|Abilities ]]selects the order to place them on the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 383.3.d.1
**383.3.d.1.** If multiple players separately control [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]that are [[#trigger|Triggered ]]simultaneously, then starting with the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]and proceeding in [[#turn order|Turn Order]], each player orders their [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]on the [[#chain|Chain. ]]

#### rule 383.3.e
**383.3.e.** If a triggered ability has a conditional statement following the [[#condition|Condition, ]]that conditional statement must be true in order for the trigger to be placed on the [[#chain|Chain. ]]Example: Sona, Harmonious reads “At the end of your turn, if I'm at a battleﬁeld, ready up to 4 friendly runes.” Her Trigger Ability’s Condition will be fulﬁlled in the Ending Step, but the Triggered Ability will only be placed on the chain if she is located at a battleﬁeld when the Condition is fulﬁlled. 

#### rule 383.3.f
**383.3.f.** Some [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]will trigger “once each turn.” 

#### rule 383.3.f.1
**383.3.f.1.** When the [[#condition|Condition ]]is fulﬁlled, the player who controls the source of the [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]may choose to place it on the chain. 

#### rule 383.3.f.2
**383.3.f.2.** If they do not, it has not [[#trigger|Triggered ]]this turn. 

#### rule 383.4
**383.4.** Some [[#condition|Conditions ]]are commonly used and structured in a way that explicitly deﬁnes their use and other properties of the [[#effect text|Effect ]]that is associated with it. 

#### rule 383.4.a
**383.4.a.** [[#play effect|Play Effects ]]are [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]with the [[#condition|Condition ]]that the [[#permanents|Permanent ]]that has the [[#play effect|Play Effect ]]being played to the board. 

#### rule 383.4.a.1
**383.4.a.1.** These are commonly structured as “When you play me…” for [[#unit|Units ]]and “When you play this…” for [[#gear|Gear. ]]

#### rule 383.4.a.2
**383.4.a.2.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]are put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]after the [[#permanents|Permanent ]]these effects correspond to is ﬁnalized and enters the board. 

#### rule 383.4.a.3
**383.4.a.3.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can be referred to as Play Effects. 

#### rule 383.4.a.4
**383.4.a.4.** Abilities that trigger when another object is played are not considered Play Effects. 

#### rule 383.4.b
**383.4.b.** [[#targeting effects|Targeting Effects ]]are [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]with the [[#condition|Condition ]]that a [[#game object|Game Object ]]becomes targeted. 

#### rule 383.4.b.1
**383.4.b.1.** These are commonly structured as “When you choose me …” or “When you choose a [Game Object] …” 

#### rule 383.4.b.2
**383.4.b.2.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]are put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]after a spell or ability that targets an appropriate [[#game object|Game Object ]]is [[#finalized items|Finalized. ]]

#### rule 383.4.b.3
**383.4.b.3.** Although these abilities say “choose” in their [[#condition|Condition]], they trigger speciﬁcally when an appropriate [[#game object|Game Object ]]is [[#targeting|Targeted. ]]See [[##rule 355.6|rule 355.6.]] [[#targeting|Targeting]] for more information on what counts as [[#targeting|Targeting. ]]

#### rule 383.4.b.4
**383.4.b.4.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can be referred to as [[#targeting effects|Targeting Effects. ]]

#### rule 383.4.c
**383.4.c.** [[#conquer effects|Conquer Effects ]]are [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]with a [[#condition|Condition ]]of a [[#unit|Unit ]]participating in, and successfully [[#conquering|Conquering ]]a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld. ]]

#### rule 383.4.c.1
**383.4.c.1.** These are commonly structured as “When I conquer…” and “When you conquer…” 

#### rule 383.4.c.2
**383.4.c.2.** This category of [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]encompasses only those that are triggered from [[#unit|Units ]]that were present during the [[#conquering|Conquer ]]action, or [[#abilities|Abilities ]]that reference the player that performed the [[#conquering|Conquer ]]action. 

#### rule 383.4.c.2.a
**383.4.c.2.a.** The [[#conquer abilities|Conquer Abilities ]]of [[#unit|Units ]]are put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]after the [[#unit|Unit(s) ]]these effects correspond to are present at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from [[#conquering|Conquering. ]]

#### rule 383.4.c.2.b
**383.4.c.2.b.** The [[#conquer abilities|Conquer Abilities ]]of anything that references the player [[#conquering|Conquering ]]is put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]when the [[#condition|Condition ]]that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a [[#conquering|Conquer ]]and gained 1 Victory Point. 

#### rule 383.4.c.2.c
**383.4.c.2.c.** If the act of gaining one point from [[#conquering|Conquering ]]is negated or replaced in any way, the [[#conquer effects|Conquer Effect ]]will still trigger. 

#### rule 383.4.c.3
**383.4.c.3.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can be referred to as Conquer Effects. 

#### rule 383.4.d
**383.4.d.** [[#hold effects|Hold Effects ]]are [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]with a [[#condition|Condition ]]of a [[#unit|Unit ]]being present at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]during the [[#beginning phase|Beginning phase ]]when a player scores [[#victory points|Victory Points ]]from [[#holding|Holding. ]]

#### rule 383.4.d.1
**383.4.d.1.** These are commonly structured as “When I hold…” or “When you hold…” 

#### rule 383.4.d.2
**383.4.d.2.** This category of [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]encompasses only those that are triggered from [[#unit|Units ]]that were present during the [[#holding|Hold ]]action, or [[#abilities|Abilities ]]that reference the player that performed the [[#holding|Hold ]]action. 

#### rule 383.4.d.2.a
**383.4.d.2.a.** The [[#hold abilities|Hold Abilities ]]of [[#unit|Units ]]are put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]after the [[#unit|Unit ]]these effects correspond to are present at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their [[#beginning phase|Beginning Phase ]]from [[#holding|Holding. ]]

#### rule 383.4.d.2.b
**383.4.d.2.b.** The [[#hold abilities|Hold Abilities ]]of anything that references the player [[#holding|Holding ]]is put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]when the [[#condition|Condition ]]that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a [[#holding|Hold ]]and gained 1 Victory Point. 

#### rule 383.4.d.2.c
**383.4.d.2.c.** If the act of gaining one point from [[#holding|Holding ]]is negated or replaced in any way, the [[#hold effects|Hold Effect ]]will still trigger. 

#### rule 383.4.d.3
**383.4.d.3.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can be referred to as Hold Effects. 

#### rule 383.4.e
**383.4.e.** [[#attack triggers|Attack Triggers ]]are [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]that trigger when a [[#unit|Unit ]]gains the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat. 

#### rule 383.4.e.1
**383.4.e.1.** These are commonly structured as “When I attack…” 

#### rule 383.4.e.2
**383.4.e.2.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]are put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]after the [[#unit|Unit ]]these effects correspond to gains the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]designation during [[#combat|Combat]]. 

#### rule 383.4.e.2.a
**383.4.e.2.a.** These triggers will only have their condition checked once per combat, despite a [[#unit|Unit ]]being able to gain and lose the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]designation multiple times in the same combat. 

#### rule 383.4.e.2.b
**383.4.e.2.b.** If the trigger condition contains other requirements besides attacking and if those requirements are not fulﬁlled when the unit gains the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]designation, it will not trigger in that combat. 

#### rule 383.4.e.3
**383.4.e.3.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can be referred to as Attack Triggers. 

#### rule 383.4.f
**383.4.f.** [[#defend triggers|Defend Triggers ]]are [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]that trigger when a [[#unit|Unit ]]gains the [[#defender|Defender ]]designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat. 

#### rule 383.4.f.1
**383.4.f.1.** These are commonly structured as “When I defend…” 

#### rule 383.4.f.2
**383.4.f.2.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]are put on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]after the [[#unit|Unit ]]these effects correspond to gains the [[#defender|Defender ]]designation during [[#combat|Combat]]. 

#### rule 383.4.f.2.a
**383.4.f.2.a.** These triggers will only have their condition checked once per combat, despite a [[#unit|Unit ]]being able to gain and lose the [[#defender|Defender ]]designation multiple times in the same combat. 

#### rule 383.4.f.2.b
**383.4.f.2.b.** If the trigger condition contains other requirements besides defending and if those requirements are not fulﬁlled when the unit gains the [[#defender|Defender ]]designation, it will not trigger in that combat. 

#### rule 383.4.f.3
**383.4.f.3.** These [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can be referred to as Defend Triggers. 

### rule 384
**384.** Presence on [[#permanents|Permanents ]]

#### rule 384.1
**384.1.** Typically active while on [[#board|the Board. ]]

#### rule 384.2
**384.2.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]of [[#permanents|Permanents ]]are only able to have their [[#condition|Conditions ]]evaluated while on [[#board|the Board. ]]

### rule 385
**385.** Presence on [[#cards outside of the board|Cards outside of the Board ]]

#### rule 385.1
**385.1.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]on cards outside of [[#board|the Board ]]rely on the [[#information|Information Level ]]of the zone they are in. 

#### rule 385.2
**385.2.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]outside of [[#board|the Board ]]will self-describe their context.  Example: The triggered ability "When you conquer, you may discard 1 to return this from your trash to your hand." triggers while the card it's on is in the trash, and not anywhere else. 

### rule 386
**386.** Reflexive Triggers 

### rule 387
**387.** [[#reflexive triggers|Reflexive Triggers ]]are a type of [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]that create one or more [[#chain|Chain Items ]]when their condition is met. 

#### rule 387.1
**387.1.** [[#reflexive triggers|Reflexive Triggers ]]can be recognized by the phrase “Do this:” or “Do one of the following:”. 

#### rule 387.1.a
**387.1.a.** “Do this” can be followed by “N times.” The [[#reflexive triggers|Reflexive Trigger ]]will thus be added to the chain N times when its condition is met. 

#### rule 387.2
**387.2.** [[#reflexive triggers|Reflexive Triggers ]]will be preceded by their conditions, if any. If no condition is present in the ability then the [[#reflexive triggers|Reflexive Trigger ]]will always be added to the Chain. 

#### rule 387.3
**387.3.** If present, the [[#condition|Condition ]]of a [[#reflexive triggers|Reflexive Trigger ]]will follow the same format as a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability. ]]

### rule 388
**388.** [[#reflexive triggers|Reflexive Triggers ]]use the Chain. 

#### rule 388.1
**388.1.** A new ability is created and added to the chain as a [[#pending item|Pending Item]]. See [[##rule 398|rule 398.]] [[#playing or activating abilities|Playing or Activating Abilities]] for more information. 

#### rule 388.2
**388.2.** If a [[#reflexive triggers|Reflexive Trigger ]]creates more than one [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]it creates them all in order, but does not go beyond the ﬁrst step of adding them to the Chain.  See [[##rule 398|rule 398.]] [[#playing or activating abilities|Playing or Activating Abilities]] for more information. 

### rule 389
**389.** Delayed Abilities 

### rule 390
**390.** [[#delayed abilities|Delayed Abilities ]]are a type of [[#abilities|Ability ]]whose trigger Condition identiﬁes a speciﬁc time during a turn or a speciﬁc event that can occur during a speciﬁc timeframe. 

#### rule 390.1
**390.1.** [[#delayed abilities|Delayed Abilities ]]can be any other type of [[#abilities|Ability]], and contain all of the properties of that type in addition to the properties of [[#delayed abilities|Delayed Abilities. ]]

#### rule 390.2
**390.2.** [[#delayed triggers|Delayed Triggers ]]are [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]that can be recognized by describing a speciﬁc time of the turn, or by structuring a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]with a speciﬁc frame of time as a restriction. 

#### rule 390.3
**390.3.** [[#delayed replacements|Delayed Replacements ]]are [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects ]]that can be recognized by specifying the effect they are replacing at a speciﬁc time, or “the [Nth] time” in the description of the effect as it resolves. 

#### rule 390.4
**390.4.** [[#delayed passive abilities|Delayed Passive Abilities ]]are [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities ]]that are applicable only during a speciﬁed window of time. The time that the [[#delayed passive abilities|Delayed Passive Ability ]]applies will be recognized in the effect that initiates it. 

#### rule 390.5
**390.5.** [[#delayed linked abilities|Delayed Linked Abilities ]]are [[#linked abilities|Linked Abilities ]]that are generated by another [[#abilities|Ability ]]and reference that [[#abilities|Ability ]]or [[#game object|Game Objects ]]it affects. [[#delayed linked abilities|Delayed Linked Abilities ]]don’t necessarily identify a speciﬁc window of time, and instead are deﬁned by the [[#abilities|Ability ]]they are linked with. 

#### rule 390.5.a
**390.5.a.** If that [[#abilities|Ability ]]affects a [[#game object|Game Object]], the [[#delayed linked ability’s|Delayed Linked Ability’s ]]window will be as long as that [[#game object|Game Object ]]is in an appropriate zone. 

#### rule 390.5.b
**390.5.b.** If the [[#delayed linked ability’s|Delayed Linked Ability ]]references the source of the abilities, its window will be as long as the source is in an appropriate zone. 

### rule 391
**391.** [[#delayed abilities|Delayed Abilities ]]will resolve or be active just like the ability they augment, but only during the speciﬁed time in the effect that created the [[#delayed abilities|Delayed Ability.  ]]Example: Ravenborn Tome reads “The next spell you play this turn deals 1 Bonus Damage” is a [[#delayed passive abilities|Delayed Passive Ability ]]that passively adds 1 damage to just the next spell played. The next spell is a speciﬁc time, and the 1 Bonus Damage is a passive ability.  Example: Noxian Guillotine reads “Choose a unit. Kill it the next time it takes damage this turn.” When the chosen unit takes damage is the speciﬁed time, and killing it is the condition for a [[#delayed triggered ability|Delayed Triggered Ability. ]]

### rule 392
**392.** [[#delayed abilities|Delayed Abilities ]]are not associated with [[#unit|Units ]]or [[#gear|Gear; ]]they are created by other [[#abilities|Abilities ]]or [[#spells|Spells]]. As such they are executed when their condition and/or speciﬁed time occurs regardless of whether the source of the [[#delayed abilities|Delayed Ability ]]is still on the board or not. 

### rule 393
**393.** Linked Abilities  

### rule 394
**394.** [[#linked abilities|Linked Abilities ]]are a set of [[#abilities|Abilities ]]with one or more of the component [[#abilities|Abilities ]]referencing the other [[#abilities|Abilities ]]in the set. 

### rule 395
**395.** In order for a set of [[#abilities|Abilities ]]to be [[#linked|Linked]], they must be present in the printed Effect or Rules Text of the same [[#game object, or be granted by the same source to another game object|Game Object, or be granted by the same source to another Game Object. ]]

### rule 396
**396.** [[#linked abilities|Linked Abilities ]]can contain component [[#abilities|Abilities ]]of any type. 

### rule 397
**397.** A component [[#linked abilities|Linked Ability ]]that references a [[#game object|Game Object ]]affected by another [[#abilities|Ability ]]in the set may only interact with [[#game object|Game Objects ]]affected by the [[#abilities|Abilities ]]it is [[#linked|Linked ]]with. 

### rule 398
**398.** Playing or Activating Abilities 

### rule 399
**399.** Playing or activating [[#abilities|Abilities ]]follows the same steps of playing cards. 

### rule 400
**400.** [[#abilities|Abilities ]]when added to the Chain become [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]until they complete the steps of [[#playing|Playing. ]]

#### rule 400.1
**400.1.** When an [[#abilities|Ability ]]ﬁnishes the steps of playing it becomes a [[#chain|Chain Item ]]just like a [[#spells|Spell. ]]

#### rule 400.2
**400.2.** When an [[#abilities|Ability ]]with the [Add] action is ﬁnalized it resolves immediately instead of becoming a [[#chain|Chain Item]], like a [[#unit|Unit ]]or [[#gear|Gear. ]]

### rule 401
**401.** 1. Activate or trigger the [[#abilities|Ability ]]

#### rule 401.1
**401.1.** Add a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]to the chain representing the [[#abilities|Ability ]]that is either being Activated or Triggered. Notably, although this Chain Item will not have a card representing it, this will create a [[#closed state|Closed State.  ]]See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 401.2
**401.2.** If there is currently a game effect being resolved, continue resolving the game effect instead of continuing the following steps. 

### rule 402
**402.** 2. Make relevant choices 

#### rule 402.1
**402.1.** Make all choices required for this ability, such as targets, modes, or other relevant decisions.  See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information 

#### rule 402.2
**402.2.** If legal options are not available for an [[#activated abilities|Activated Ability, ]]it is not legal to activate it. 

#### rule 402.3
**402.3.** If there are not enough options to make legal choices for a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]that has been put on the chain, remove it from the Chain now. It ceases to be a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]but never becomes a [[#chain|Chain Item. ]]

#### rule 402.3.a
**402.3.a.** This is not an [[#abilities|Ability ]]being countered. 

#### rule 402.3.b
**402.3.b.** If there are legal options to choose, the ability’s controller must choose them. They may not decline this stage of playing a [[#trigger|Trigger. ]]

### rule 403
**403.** 3. Determine Total Cost 

#### rule 403.1
**403.1.** Determine the base cost of the [[#abilities|Ability. ]]

#### rule 403.1.a
**403.1.a.** [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities ]]will have a cost listed before the “:” in their text. 

#### rule 403.1.b
**403.1.b.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]will typically not have a base cost associated with them when placed on the chain due to their conditions. 

#### rule 403.1.b.1
**403.1.b.1.** If a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]has a cost within instructions (e.g. “[do X] to [do Y]”), the cost is taken as the base cost. See [[##rule 742.1|rule 742.1.]]for more information on costs within instructions. 

#### rule 403.2
**403.2.** Apply cost increases and decreases as a result of choices made in the prior step.  See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 403.3
**403.3.** Apply any other cost increases or decreases as necessary.  See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

### rule 404
**404.** 4. Pay Costs 

#### rule 404.1
**404.1.** Pay costs as determined in the prior step.  See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 404.2
**404.2.** At this stage, players may decline to pay for [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]that have incurred a cost. If they do, the ability will cease being a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]and be removed from the Chain. It never becomes a [[#chain|Chain Item. ]]

#### rule 404.2.a
**404.2.a.** This is not an [[#abilities|Ability ]]being countered. 

### rule 405
**405.** 5. Check Legality 

#### rule 405.1
**405.1.** Ensure that the [[#ability’s|Ability’s ]]targets are still legal. 

#### rule 405.2
**405.2.** Ensure that the [[#ability’s|Ability’s ]]effect would not create an illegal state. If it would, resolve in the same way you would resolve a [[#card|Card ]]that creates an illegal state. See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

### rule 406
**406.** 6. Proceed with Play 

#### rule 406.1
**406.1.** This [[#ability’s|Ability ]]is no longer [[#pending item|Pending. ]]

#### rule 406.2
**406.2.** This [[#ability’s|Ability ]]becomes a [[#chain|Chain Item. ]]

#### rule 406.3
**406.3.** If there are other [[#pending item|Pending Items ]]on the Chain, their controllers perform the remaining steps of playing now. 

#### rule 406.4
**406.4.** Other players have an opportunity to play [[#reaction|Reactions ]]before the resolution of spells.  See [[##rule 327|rule 327.]] [[#chain|Chains]] for more information. 

#### rule 406.5
**406.5.** Otherwise, execute the [[#ability’s|Ability ]]just like a [[#spells|Spell]], then clear the [[#chain|Chain Item ]]from the Chain. 

### rule 407
**407.** [[#game actions|Game Actions ]]

### rule 408
**408.** [[#game actions|Game Actions ]]are actions players may perform at any given time during the game. 

### rule 409
**409.** A player, unless otherwise speciﬁed or prompted, may only perform actions on their turn. 

### rule 410
**410.** There are two types of [[#game actions|Game Actions: ]]

#### rule 410.1
**410.1.** [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions ]]

#### rule 410.1.a
**410.1.a.** A [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Action ]]is a [[#game actions|Game Action ]]that may be performed [[#at any time|at any time ]]during a player's turn [[#during a neutral open state|during a Neutral Open State.  ]]See [[##rule 307|rule 307.]] [[#states of the turn|States of the Turn]] for more information. 

#### rule 410.1.b
**410.1.b.** A player may take any number of [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions ]]available to them during their turn. 

#### rule 410.1.b.1
**410.1.b.1.** As long as any conditions, if applicable, are met. 

#### rule 410.1.b.2
**410.1.b.2.** As long as any costs, if applicable, are paid. 

#### rule 410.1.b.3
**410.1.b.3.** As long as it does not result in any forbidden action being taken or game state being created.  Example: A player can't use the Standard Move discretionary action to move a unit to a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that's already occupied by [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by two other players. 

#### rule 410.2
**410.2.** [[#limited actions|Limited Actions ]]

#### rule 410.2.a
**410.2.a.** A [[#limited actions|Limited Action ]]is a game action that a spell, ability, or circumstance of the turn's progression causes the player to perform. A player cannot perform these actions at-will. 

#### rule 410.2.b
**410.2.b.** These actions can only be taken when a player is instructed to do so as the execution of an effect or during their speciﬁed occasion during the turn.  Example: A player may [[#drawn|Draw ]]during the [[#drawn|Draw Step ]]of the [[#beginning phase|Beginning Phase ]]of their turn or when instructed to do so by a spell or ability. They can't choose to [[#drawn|Draw ]]at any other time. 

### rule 411
**411.** [[#responsibility|Responsibility ]]

#### rule 411.1
**411.1.** [[#game actions|Game Actions ]]may be the responsibility of up to one player. The player that performs the [[#game actions|Game Action ]]is responsible for it. 

#### rule 411.2
**411.2.** In the case where a [[#game actions|Game Action ]]is performed by procedures of the game and not by any player, that [[#game actions|Game Action ]]is not the responsibility of any player. 

#### rule 411.3
**411.3.** Certain rules assign responsibility to players for [[#game actions|Game Actions ]]that they are not normally responsible for. 

#### rule 411.4
**411.4.** If an ability triggers when “you” do something, it triggers when a [[#game actions|Game Action ]]that you are responsible for occurs. Example: A gear reads “When you move an enemy unit, you may exhaust this to [Stun] it.” It will trigger whenever a move game action that you are responsible for causes an enemy unit to move. If an opponent plays a spell that reads “choose a Battleﬁeld. Each player may move a unit they don’t control to that battleﬁeld,” and a player that controls the gear chooses to move an enemy unit, their gear will trigger. 

#### rule 411.5
**411.5.** Note that certain [[#game actions|Game Actions]], speciﬁcally Kill, can be attributed to spells and abilities. This attribution is not the same as the responsibility a given player has for the kill game action. 

#### rule 411.5.a
**411.5.a.** Spells and abilities have attribution for game actions, while players have responsibility. 

### rule 412
**412.** Types of Actions 

### rule 413
**413.** [[#drawn|Draw ]]

#### rule 413.1
**413.1.** [[#drawn|Drawing ]]a card takes a single card from a zone and adding it to the player's [[#hand|Hand. ]]

#### rule 413.1.a
**413.1.a.** Unless speciﬁed otherwise, drawing takes cards from the [[#main deck|Main Deck. ]]

#### rule 413.2
**413.2.** This is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 413.2.a
**413.2.a.** Each player draws 1 during the [[#drawn|Draw Step ]]of their [[#beginning phase|Beginning Phase. ]]

#### rule 413.2.b
**413.2.b.** The player may draw cards when instructed to do so by other game effects. 

#### rule 413.3
**413.3.** This action, when instructed, is formatted as "Draw X." 

#### rule 413.4
**413.4.** If a player attempts to draw more cards than are available in their [[#main deck|Main Deck]], they do the following: 

#### rule 413.4.a
**413.4.a.** Draw as many as possible. 

#### rule 413.4.b
**413.4.b.** Perform a [[#burn out|Burn Out.  ]]See [[##rule 431|rule 431.]] [[#burn out|Burn Out]] for more information. 

#### rule 413.4.c
**413.4.c.** Draw the remaining cards needed to complete the [[#drawn|Draw ]]action. 

### rule 414
**414.** [[#exhausted|Exhaust ]]

#### rule 414.1
**414.1.** [[#exhausted|Exhausting ]]is an action that marks a non-spell [[#game object|Game Object ]]on the board as "spent." 

#### rule 414.1.a
**414.1.a.** To mark it, rotate the card 90 degrees opposite of [[#ready|Readying]], so that the orientation of the card is lengthwise in front of you. 

#### rule 414.1.b
**414.1.b.** A [[#unit|Unit ]]that is already [[#exhausted|Exhausted ]]cannot be [[#exhausted|Exhausted ]]again. 

#### rule 414.1.c
**414.1.c.** If a [[#unit|Unit ]]is instructed to be [[#exhausted|Exhausted ]]while it is already [[#exhausted|Exhausted]], nothing additional happens. 

#### rule 414.2
**414.2.** [[#exhausted|"Exhausted" ]]is a state for [[#game object|Game Objects ]]on the board that other game effects and rules can reference. 

#### rule 414.3
**414.3.** This is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 414.3.a
**414.3.a.** Most [[#exhausted|Exhaust ]]actions will be costs for Activated Abilities or [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Actions. ]]Example: A unit's Standard Move exhausts the unit as a cost. 

#### rule 414.4
**414.4.** When [[#exhausted|Exhausting ]]is listed as a [[#cost|Cost]], then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: A spell says "As an additional cost to play this, you may exhaust a friendly unit." An exhausted friendly unit may not be exhausted again as the additional cost for the spell, and the additional cost has not been paid. 

#### rule 414.5
**414.5.** In abilities, the [[#exhaust symbol|Exhaust symbol ]]represents the cost "Exhaust this" or "Exhaust me." It resembles a card turning sideways. 

### rule 415
**415.** [[#ready|Ready ]]

#### rule 415.1
**415.1.** [[#ready|Readying ]]is an action that marks a non-spell [[#game object|Game Object ]]on the board as available for action. 

#### rule 415.1.a
**415.1.a.** To mark it, rotate the card 90 degrees opposite of [[#exhausted|Exhausting]], so that it is vertically oriented in front of you. 

#### rule 415.1.b
**415.1.b.** A [[#unit|Unit ]]that is already [[#ready|Ready ]]cannot be [[#ready|Readied ]]again. 

#### rule 415.1.c
**415.1.c.** If a [[#unit|Unit ]]is instructed to be [[#ready|Readied ]]while it is already [[#ready|Ready]], nothing additional happens. 

#### rule 415.2
**415.2.** [[#ready|"Ready" ]]is a state for [[#game object|Game Objects ]]on the board that other game effects and rules can reference. 

#### rule 415.3
**415.3.** This is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 415.3.a
**415.3.a.** A player [[#ready|Readies ]]all non-spell [[#game object|Game Objects ]]they [[#control|Control ]]during the [[#ready|Ready Step ]]of the [[#beginning phase|Beginning Phase ]]on their turn. 

#### rule 415.3.b
**415.3.b.** Players may also [[#ready game objects|Ready Game Objects ]]on the board when effects or spells instruct them to do so. 

### rule 416
**416.** [[#recycled|Recycle ]]

#### rule 416.1
**416.1.** [[#recycled|Recycling ]]cards is the action in which a player takes one or more cards from a speciﬁc zone and then puts it on the bottom of the corresponding deck. 

#### rule 416.1.a
**416.1.a.** [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]cards are [[#recycled|Recycled ]]to the [[#main deck|Main Deck. ]]

#### rule 416.1.b
**416.1.b.** [[#rune|Runes ]]are [[#recycled|Recycled ]]to the [[#rune deck|Rune Deck. ]]

#### rule 416.1.c
**416.1.c.** Each player [[#recycles|Recycles ]]cards to their own [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]and [[#rune deck|Rune Deck]], regardless of which player is instructed to perform the [[#recycled|Recycle ]]action. 

#### rule 416.2
**416.2.** This is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 416.2.a
**416.2.a.** The player must [[#recycled|Recycle ]]cards from the speciﬁed zones when instructed to do so by game effects or costs. 

#### rule 416.3
**416.3.** When [[#recycled|Recycling ]]is listed as a [[#cost|Cost]], the action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: Vi, Destructive has the ability "Recycle 1 from your trash: Give me +1 [M] this turn." Each time a player activates the ability, they must recycle 1 card from their trash to pay its cost. If they have no cards in their trash, they can't activate the ability, because they can't pay its cost. 

#### rule 416.4
**416.4.** When [[#recycled|Recycling ]]is part of an effect, a player must [[#recycled|Recycle ]]as many cards as possible from the speciﬁed zone or zones. 

#### rule 416.5
**416.5.** If 2 or more cards are [[#recycled|Recycled ]]to the [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in a random order.  Example: Garbage Grabber has the ability "Recycle 3 from your trash, [1], [E]: Draw " To pay the cost of activating this ability, its controller chooses 3 cards from their trash and places them on the bottom of their [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]in a random order. 

#### rule 416.5.a
**416.5.a.** If 2 or more cards are [[#recycled|Recycled ]]to the [[#rune deck|Rune Deck ]]simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in the order of their owner's choosing. 

#### rule 416.6
**416.6.** This action, when instructed, is sometimes formatted as "[[#recycled|Recycle ]]X from [Zone]." That means to take X cards of the instructed player's choice from the relevant zone and recycle them.  Example: Dr. Mundo, Expert has the ability "At the start of your Beginning Phase, recycle 3 from your trash." As that ability resolves, its controller recycles 3 cards from their trash. If there are fewer than 3 cards in that player's trash, they recycle as many as they can. 

### rule 417
**417.** [[#decks|Deal ]]

#### rule 417.1
**417.1.** Spells, Units, Abilities, and other game effects may [[#deal damage|Deal Damage ]]to units. 

#### rule 417.1.a
**417.1.a.** Assigning [[#damage|Damage ]]during the Combat Damage Step is not [[#dealing damage|Dealing Damage, ]]but will cause [[#damage|Damage ]]to be [[#dealt|Dealt ]]when assignment is complete. 

#### rule 417.1.b
**417.1.b.** To [[#deal damage|Deal Damage ]]to [[#unit|Units, ]]mark the speciﬁed amount of [[#damage|Damage ]]on the [[#unit|Unit. ]]

#### rule 417.1.c
**417.1.c.** [[#damage|Damage ]]is marked on each unit separately. 

#### rule 417.1.d
**417.1.d.** [[#damage|Damage ]]can be [[#dealt|Dealt ]]to more than one [[#unit|Unit ]]at the same time. 

#### rule 417.1.e
**417.1.e.** [[#valid damage|Valid Damage ]]is a positive integer amount, greater than or equal to 1 [[#damage|Damage]]. 

#### rule 417.1.e.1
**417.1.e.1.** Only [[#valid damage|Valid Damage ]]is [[#dealt|Dealt. ]]Example: A unit has “when I take damage, give me +2 [M] this turn.” A spell is played that Prevents the next 3 damage the unit would take. If a player plays Hextech Ray targeting the unit, it will take no damage and its triggered ability will not trigger. If that player had played Void Seeker instead, it would be Dealt 1 and trigger its ability. Example: A unit is present at Void Gate. A spell is played that Prevents the next 3 damage the unit would take. If a player plays Hextech Ray targeting the unit, it will take no damage - in order to apply the Bonus Damage from Void Gate, the Deal game action would have to occur, and Hextech Ray did not Deal any damage. 

#### rule 417.2
**417.2.** Only [[#damage|Damage ]]can be [[#dealt|Dealt. ]]

#### rule 417.3
**417.3.** [[#dealing damage|Dealing Damage ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 417.3.a
**417.3.a.** Assigning [[#damage|Damage ]]causes [[#damage|Damage ]]to be dealt outside of being directed to [[#deal damage|Deal Damage.  ]]See [[##rule 454|rule 454.]] [[#combat|Combat]] for more information. 

#### rule 417.4
**417.4.** [[#dealt|Dealing ]]can have the intrinsic property of [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage. ]]

#### rule 417.5
**417.5.** [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]is a property granted to the action of [[#dealt|Dealing ]]and alters the amount of [[#damage|Damage ]]distributed by this action.  See [[##rule 712|rule 712.]] [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage]] for more information. 

#### rule 417.6
**417.6.** [[#dealt|Deal ]]actions can originate from one or more sources. 

#### rule 417.6.a
**417.6.a.** If a game effect does not specify a source, the game effect describing the [[#dealt|Deal ]]action is the source.  Example: Void Seeker is a spell that reads “Deal 4 to a unit at a battleﬁeld. Draw 1.” The damage that Void Seeker instructs you to deal is dealt by Void Seeker. 

#### rule 417.6.b
**417.6.b.** If a game effect does specify a source, then that source is what is considered the origin of the [[#damage|Damage ]]for this [[#dealt|Deal ]]action. 

#### rule 417.6.b.1
**417.6.b.1.** Units and Spells can be the source of [[#damage|Damage ]]for [[#dealt|Deal ]]actions. 

#### rule 417.6.b.2
**417.6.b.2.** Abilities can be the source of [[#damage|Damage ]]for [[#dealt|Deal ]]actions. 

#### rule 417.6.b.2.a
**417.6.b.2.a.** When an Ability is the source of [[#damage|Damage ]]for a [[#dealt|Deal ]]action, it is in addition to the Spell or Unit that created that Ability.  Example: Iron Ballista is a gear that says “[E]: Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld.” This damage is dealt both by a gear and by an ability. 

#### rule 417.6.b.3
**417.6.b.3.** When a spell or ability speciﬁes a Unit as the source of the [[#damage|Damage ]]for the [[#dealt|Deal ]]action, it is not in addition to the spell or ability that speciﬁed it.  Example: Challenge is a spell that reads “Choose a friendly unit and an enemy unit. They deal damage equal to their Mights to each other.” The damage that Challenge causes to be dealt is dealt by the chosen units, not by Challenge. 

#### rule 417.6.c
**417.6.c.** [[#damage|Damage Dealt ]]as a result of being assigned during [[#combat|Combat ]]has the [[#unit|Units ]]as its source. 

#### rule 417.6.c.1
**417.6.c.1.** The [[#damage|Damage ]]assigned, and subsequently [[#dealt|Dealt]], to attackers has the defenders as the source and vice versa. 

#### rule 417.7
**417.7.** [[#dealt|Deal ]]actions can distribute [[#damage|Damage ]]as part of combat actions or non-combat actions. 

### rule 418
**418.** [[#healed|Heal ]]

#### rule 418.1
**418.1.** [[#damage|Damage ]]being cleared from [[#unit|Units ]]is [[#healed|Healing. ]]

#### rule 418.1.a
**418.1.a.** If [[#damage|Damage ]]is cleared for any reason it is considered [[#healed|Healing. ]]

#### rule 418.2
**418.2.** More than one [[#unit|Unit ]]can be [[#healed|Healed ]]at the same time. 

#### rule 418.3
**418.3.** [[#healed|Healing ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 418.3.a
**418.3.a.** Players may only [[#healed|Heal ]]units when game effects instruct them to, or at speciﬁc points in the turn. 

### rule 419
**419.** [[#play|Play ]]

#### rule 419.1
**419.1.** A player [[#play|Plays ]]cards by placing them on the chain and queuing them to be ﬁnalized.  See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information on playing cards. See [[##rule 337|rule 337.]] [[#finalize|Finalize]] for more information on ﬁnalizing cards. 

#### rule 419.1.a
**419.1.a.** By default, a player can only [[#play|Play ]]cards from their hand or their Chosen Champion zone. 

#### rule 419.2
**419.2.** This is a [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Action. ]]

#### rule 419.2.a
**419.2.a.** As long as a player has the resources to pay the costs associated with the card and legal choices to make for their cards, they may [[#play|Play ]]cards. 

#### rule 419.3
**419.3.** Game effects may result in cards being [[#played|played ]]as part of their resolution. 

#### rule 419.3.a
**419.3.a.** This treats [[#play|Play ]]as a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 419.3.b
**419.3.b.** Treat all steps of [[#play|Play ]]as normal, except as noted by the game effect creating this [[#limited play effect|Limited Play Effect. ]]

#### rule 419.3.c
**419.3.c.** If there are no eligible cards to [[#play|Play ]]when instructed to [[#play|Play ]]in this manner like this, then nothing happens and resolution continues. 

#### rule 419.4
**419.4.** Some [[#abilities|Abilities ]]trigger when cards are played or otherwise check whether cards have been played. 

#### rule 419.4.a
**419.4.a.** These abilities trigger when the act of playing the card has been completed by the resolution of the card. 

#### rule 419.4.b
**419.4.b.** If a game effect prevents the resolution of the card—for example, because the card was [[#countered|countered]]—the card wasn't played and no abilities that trigger on playing cards trigger.  See [[##rule 425|rule 425.]] [[#countered|Counter]] for more information. 

### rule 420
**420.** [[#move|Move ]]

#### rule 420.1
**420.1.** [[#move|Moving ]]is the act of a [[#game object|Game Object ]]moving between two [[#location|Locations ]]on [[#board|The Board. ]]See [[##rule 440|rule 440.]] [[#move|Movement]] for more information on movement. 

#### rule 420.2
**420.2.** [[#move|Moving ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 420.2.a
**420.2.a.** Players may only move [[#game object|Game Objects ]]when instructed to do so by Game Effects or costs. 

#### rule 420.2.b
**420.2.b.** The [[#standard move|Standard Move ]]inherent to [[#unit|Units ]]may also cause [[#move|Movement.  ]]See [[##rule 144|rule 144.]]for more information on the [[#standard move|Standard Move]]. 

#### rule 420.3
**420.3.** The [[#standard move|Standard Move ]]inherent to [[#unit|Units ]]is a [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Action. ]]

#### rule 420.3.a
**420.3.a.** The [[#cost|Cost ]]is [[#exhausted|Exhausting ]]one or more [[#unit|Units. ]]

#### rule 420.3.b
**420.3.b.** The [[#effect text|Effect ]]is [[#move|Moving ]]those [[#unit|Unit. ]]

### rule 421
**421.** [[#hide|Hide ]]

#### rule 421.1
**421.1.** [[#hide|Hiding ]]a card is the act of placing a card facedown at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]you control. 

#### rule 421.2
**421.2.** [[#hide|Hiding ]]is a [[#discretionary actions|Discretionary Action. ]]

#### rule 421.2.a
**421.2.a.** The [[#hide|Hidden ]]keyword allows a player to pay a cost to [[#hide|Hide ]]a card any time they have a [[#hide|Hidden ]]card in their hand or Champion Zone and meet the prerequisites.  See [[##rule 811|rule 811.]] [[#hide|Hidden]] for more information. 

#### rule 421.3
**421.3.** Cards that are facedown at [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]have their gameplay properties and permissions deﬁned by the effect that put them there.  Example: Cards that players [[#hide|Hide ]]with the [[#hide|Hidden ]]keyword can be [[#played|Played ]]for [0] on any subsequent turn as a property of the [[#hide|Hidden ]]keyword. 

#### rule 421.4
**421.4.** If a facedown card would change zones or if the game ends, its owner reveals it to all players.  See [[##rule 128|rule 128.]] [[#privacy|Privacy]] for more information. 

### rule 422
**422.** [[#discard|Discard ]]

#### rule 422.1
**422.1.** [[#discard|Discarding ]]a card is moving it from a player's hand directly into their trash without activating or executing its normal rules text. 

#### rule 422.1.a
**422.1.a.** The player who is performing the action chooses which cards to send to their [[#trashes|Trash]], and may use [[#private information|Private Information ]]to do so. 

#### rule 422.1.b
**422.1.b.** “When I am discarded” abilities or other [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]that trigger on discarding are executed after discarding has occurred. 

#### rule 422.2
**422.2.** [[#discard|Discarding ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 422.2.a
**422.2.a.** A player must [[#discard|Discard ]]cards when instructed to do so by game effects or costs. 

#### rule 422.3
**422.3.** When [[#discard|Discarding ]]is listed as a [[#cost|Cost]], then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: A card has the ability "Discard 2: Deal 2 damage to a unit at a battleﬁeld." To activate the ability, the card's controller must have at least 2 cards in hand and must be able to discard them. 

#### rule 422.4
**422.4.** When [[#discard|Discarding ]]is part of an effect, then a player must [[#discard|Discard ]]as many cards as possible from their hand. If instructed to discard more cards than they have in their hand, further discard instructions are ignored.  Example: Undercover Agent has the ability "[Deathknell][>] Discard 2, then draw 2. (When I die, get the effect.)" If Undercover Agent's controller has 2 or more cards in hand, they must discard 2. If they have 1 card in hand, they discard 1, and the rest of the discard instruction is ignored. If they have no cards in hand, the entire discard instruction is ignored. Regardless of how many cards they discard, they then draw 2. 

#### rule 422.5
**422.5.** This action is formatted as "Discard X." 

### rule 423
**423.** [[#state|Stun ]]

#### rule 423.1
**423.1.** [[#stunning|Stunning ]]is the act of selecting one or more [[#unit|Units ]]on [[#board|the Board ]]and rendering them [[#stunning|Stunned. ]]

#### rule 423.1.a
**423.1.a.** [[#stunning|Stunned ]]is a binary state. A [[#unit|Unit ]]is [[#stunning|Stunned ]]or it isn't. 

#### rule 423.1.a.1
**423.1.a.1.** A [[#stunned unit|Stunned Unit ]]can not be [[#stunned unit|Stunned ]]again.  Example: Eclipse Herald has the ability "When you stun an enemy unit, ready me and give me +1 [M] this turn." Its controller plays a spell that reads "Stun a unit." They may choose a unit that's already stunned, but if they do, Eclipse Herald will not trigger. 

#### rule 423.1.a.2
**423.1.a.2.** [[#stunned unit|Stunned Units ]]lose the [[#stunned unit|Stunned ]]status at the beginning of the next [[#ending step|Ending Step. ]]

#### rule 423.1.b
**423.1.b.** A [[#stunned unit|Stunned Unit ]]does not contribute its might to damage in the combat damage step. See [[##rule 460|rule 460.]] [[#combat damage step|The Combat Damage Step]] for more information. 

#### rule 423.1.c
**423.1.c.** A [[#stunned unit|Stunned Unit ]]must still have damage applied to it equal to, or greater than, its full might value to be killed. 

#### rule 423.2
**423.2.** [[#stunning|Stunning ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 423.2.a
**423.2.a.** Players may only [[#stun units|Stun Units ]]when directed to by [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 424
**424.** [[#reveal|Reveal ]]

#### rule 424.1
**424.1.** [[#reveal|Revealing ]]is the act of presenting a card to all players from a zone that one or more players do not have access to the information of. 

#### rule 424.1.a
**424.1.a.** [[#reveal|Revealed ]]is a temporary state and is not a zone. 

#### rule 424.1.a.1
**424.1.a.1.** Other cards, including the card being revealed, can reference the act of being [[#reveal|Revealed. ]]

#### rule 424.1.a.2
**424.1.a.2.** Cards remain in the zone they are being [[#reveal|Revealed ]]from. Example: If a card is being [[#reveal|Revealed ]]from the top of a player's [[#main deck|Main Deck]], it is still the top card of that player's [[#main deck|Main Deck. ]]

#### rule 424.1.b
**424.1.b.** Unless otherwise described, [[#reveal|Revealed ]]cards do nothing else beyond become temporarily known information to all players. 

#### rule 424.2
**424.2.** [[#reveal|Revealing ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 424.2.a
**424.2.a.** Players may only [[#reveal|Reveal ]]cards from [[#private|Private ]]or [[#secret|Secret ]]zones when instructed to do so by [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 424.2.b
**424.2.b.** During the course of a game of [[#riftbound|Riftbound]], a player may choose to show [[#private|Private ]]information to one or more other players. This does not count as revealing and does not trigger any effects that trigger when cards are revealed. 

#### rule 424.3
**424.3.** This action is formatted as "Reveal cards from [zone]."  Example: "Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck" would be executed by taking the two cards from the top of your Main Deck, and then presenting them to all players to clearly read and understand at the table. Then, when all players have had a chance to understand the revealed information, return them to the top of the deck in the same order. 

#### rule 424.4
**424.4.** [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]can manipulate or modify the cards [[#reveal|Revealed ]]while they are [[#reveal|Revealed ]]

#### rule 424.4.a
**424.4.a.** While cards are [[#reveal|Revealed]], those cards can be further manipulated, or accessed. They can even have their destination modiﬁed for when the [[#reveal|Reveal ]]ends.  Example: "Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck. Put one into your hand and Recycle the other" would be executed by taking the top two cards from your Main Deck to the table, and once every player present has had a chance to understand them you would make the selection of one of them to add to your hand. The one you did not select would then be [[#recycled|Recycled ]]to the bottom of the [[#main deck|Main Deck. ]]

### rule 425
**425.** [[#countered|Counter ]]

#### rule 425.1
**425.1.** [[#countered|Countering ]]is the act of negating the execution, activation, or otherwise playing of a card or ability by a player. 

#### rule 425.1.a
**425.1.a.** A card or ability that is [[#countered|Countered ]]does nothing and is  cleared from the chain. 

#### rule 425.1.b
**425.1.b.** A card that is [[#countered|Countered ]]is not considered to have been played. 

#### rule 425.1.c
**425.1.c.** [[#countered|Countering ]]does not refund any costs paid to play a card, activate an ability, or trigger an ability. 

#### rule 425.1.c.1
**425.1.c.1.** This includes additional costs. 

#### rule 425.2
**425.2.** Countering is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 425.2.a
**425.2.a.** Players may only [[#countered|Counter ]]cards and abilities when directed to by [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 425.3
**425.3.** This action is formatted as "[[#countered|Counter ]][a card or ability on the chain]." 

### rule 426
**426.** [[#buffed|Buff ]]

#### rule 426.1
**426.1.** [[#bufﬁng|Bufﬁng ]]is the action of placing a [[#buffed|Buff ]]counter on a [[#unit|Unit]].  See [[##rule 701|rule 701.]] [[#buffed|Buffs]] for more information. 

#### rule 426.1.a
**426.1.a.** A [[#buffed|Buff ]]is also an object. 

#### rule 426.1.b
**426.1.b.** To [[#buffed|Buff ]]a unit, place a [[#buff counter|Buff Counter ]]on it if it does not have one already 

#### rule 426.1.b.1
**426.1.b.1.** If the unit already has a [[#buff counter|Buff Counter ]]on it, it does not get another one. 

#### rule 426.1.c
**426.1.c.** Units with [[#buff counter|Buff Counters ]]can still be chosen for actions that [[#buffed|Buff ]]units, but will not be [[#buffed|Buffed ]]as part of the execution.  Example: A spell reads "Buff a unit. Then, if it was buffed this way, draw a card." It will place a buff counter on a unit that has no buff counter, and then its controller will draw a card. However, if the player chooses a unit with a buff counter on it already, then the card will not be drawn. 

#### rule 426.2
**426.2.** [[#bufﬁng|Bufﬁng ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 426.2.a
**426.2.a.** Players may only [[#buffed|Buff ]]units when [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]direct them to do so. 

#### rule 426.3
**426.3.** This action is formatted as "[[#buffed|Buff ]][one or more units]."  e.g., "Buff a unit."  e.g., "Buff a friendly unit."  e.g., "Buff two friendly units at the same battleﬁeld." 

### rule 427
**427.** [[#banishments|Banish ]]

#### rule 427.1
**427.1.** [[#banishing|Banishing ]]is the action of placing a card from any zone to [[#banishments|Banishment.  ]]See [[##rule 108.6|rule 108.6.]] [[#banishments|Banishment]] for more information. 

#### rule 427.2
**427.2.** When a card is [[#banishing|Banished ]]it is placed directly into the [[#banishments|Banishment ]]zone from its origin. 

#### rule 427.2.a
**427.2.a.** Banish is not a subset of [[#killed|Kill. ]]

#### rule 427.2.b
**427.2.b.** Banish is not a subset of [[#discard|Discard. ]]

#### rule 427.3
**427.3.** Cards and effects can refer to cards that were banished by the same object. 

#### rule 427.3.a
**427.3.a.** Separate instances of an object or effect banishing cards do not reference other banished cards by objects of the same name or effects originating from cards of the same name.  Example: A spell reads "Banish the top card of your Main Deck. When you conquer this turn, draw it." This card effect allows you to draw the banished card from banishment if a condition is met. If more than one of these effects is played, each one triggers separately. Each card will be drawn separately. If the turn player passes the turn without playing the card, the card remains in banishment indeﬁnitely. If the same player plays another copy of the same spell, banishes another card, and satisﬁes its condition, they could play the new banished card, but not the original banished card. See [[##rule 393|rule 393.]] [[#linked abilities|Linked Abilities]] for more information. 

#### rule 427.4
**427.4.** [[#banishing|Banishing ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 427.4.a
**427.4.a.** Players may only [[#banishing|Banish ]]cards or permanents when [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]direct them to do so. 

#### rule 427.5
**427.5.** This action is formatted as "Banish [one or more permanents or cards]."  e.g., "Banish a card from your hand."  e.g., "Banish 2 cards from your trash." e.g., "Look at the top 2 cards of your Main Deck. Draw one of them and banish the other." 

### rule 428
**428.** [[#killed|Kill ]]

#### rule 428.1
**428.1.** [[#killed|Killing ]]is the action of a [[#permanents|Permanent ]]going to the trash from the board. 

#### rule 428.1.a
**428.1.a.** This can be [[#active|Active ]]or [[#passive|Passive. ]]

#### rule 428.1.a.1
**428.1.a.1.** [[#active|Active Kill ]]is when the action is taken when instructed by a game effect or as a cost for a card or ability. 

#### rule 428.1.a.1.a
**428.1.a.1.a.** This is referred to as a [[#kill instruction|Kill Instruction. ]]

#### rule 428.1.a.1.b
**428.1.a.1.b.** When a unit with a [[#deathknell|Deathknell  ]]is to be put in the [[#trashes|Trash ]]due to a [[#kill instruction|Kill Instruction]], it ﬁrst has its [[#deathknell|Deathknell ]]added to the chain as a [[#pending item|Pending Item. ]]Note the unit’s location, attributes, and other relevant information to process its [[#deathknell|Deathknell ]]when ﬁnalized before completing this [[#kill instruction|Kill Instruction]]. 

#### rule 428.1.a.2
**428.1.a.2.** [[#passive|Passive Kill ]]is when the action is taken as a result of [[#lethal damage|Lethal Damage ]]or as a consequence for any other state. 

#### rule 428.2
**428.2.** When a [[#permanents|permanent ]]is [[#killed|killed ]]it is placed directly in the trash from its place of origin. 

#### rule 428.2.a
**428.2.a.** It is only considered [[#killed|Killed ]]if its origin was any zone on the board. 

#### rule 428.2.b
**428.2.b.** This is not a subset of [[#move|Move. ]]

#### rule 428.3
**428.3.** [[#killed|Killing ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 428.3.a
**428.3.a.** Players may only [[#killed|Kill ]]units when [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]direct them to do so. 

#### rule 428.4
**428.4.** [[#killed|Killing ]]can also be the result of resolving a [[#cleanup|Cleanup. ]]

#### rule 428.5
**428.5.** [[#killed|Killing ]]can be attributed to one or more [[#game object|Game Objects. ]]

#### rule 428.5.a
**428.5.a.** The Killed [[#unit|Unit ]]or [[#gear|Gear ]]is said to be [[#killed|Killed ]]by that [[#game object|Game Object. ]]

#### rule 428.5.b
**428.5.b.** A spell or ability that contains a [[#killed|Kill ]]instruction is responsible for [[#killed|Killing ]]the [[#unit|Unit ]]or [[#gear|Gear. ]]

#### rule 428.5.c
**428.5.c.** When one or more [[#unit|Units ]]is killed due to a [[#cleanup|Cleanup]], that kill action is attributed to the spell or ability that resolved immediately prior to that [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]that dealt damage to the [[#unit|Unit ]]or [[#unit|Units]]. The player responsible for the deal action is responsible for the kill action. 

#### rule 428.5.d
**428.5.d.** [[#abilities|Abilities ]]originating from [[#game object|Game Objects ]]that are  attributed [[#kill actions|Kill Actions ]]are attributed in addition to the [[#game object|Game Object ]]that created them.  Example: There is a spell that says “Do this twice: Deal 3 to a unit.” Immortal Phoenix is a unit that says “When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.” A player plays the spell while Immortal Phoenix is in their trash. The “do this” phrasing means that it has a reflexive triggered ability, which places two triggered abilities on the chain. As each of those triggered abilities resolve, it deals damage to the unit chosen for that ability. If one of these abilities deals lethal damage to a unit, both the spell and its ability are considered sources of the damage, and so both the spell and its ability receive attribution for killing the unit. This means that the spell’s controller killed a unit with a spell, so Immortal Phoenix’s ability will trigger. 

#### rule 428.5.e
**428.5.e.** In order to [[#killed|Kill ]]something “with” a spell or ability, the [[#killed|Kill ]]action must be attributed to the spell or ability, the player must control that spell or ability, and the player must be responsible for the [[#killed|Kill ]]action. 

#### rule 428.6
**428.6.** This action is formatted as "Kill [one or more permanents]."  e.g., "Kill an enemy unit."  e.g., "Kill this, [2]: Draw 1."  e.g., "Kill all gear." 

### rule 429
**429.** [[#added|Add ]]

#### rule 429.1
**429.1.** [[#added|Adding ]]is the action of putting resources into a player's [[#rune pool|Rune Pool. ]]

#### rule 429.2
**429.2.** Spells, triggered abilities, and activated abilities that [[#added|Add ]]resources ﬁnalize immediately. 

#### rule 429.2.a
**429.2.a.** [[#priority|Priority ]]and [[#focus|Focus ]]will not pass from [[#added|Add ]]abilities being ﬁnalized or resolving, and will resolve before any other outstanding items on the chain are ﬁnalized. 

#### rule 429.3
**429.3.** Activated abilities that [[#added|Add ]]resources and have the [[#reaction|Reaction ]]tag can be activated during the playing or resolution of other spells and abilities, any time that those spells or abilities require resources be paid.  Example: A player can add Energy and Power through any means before initiating the process of playing a spell. After initiating that process, in the Pay Costs step, they may activate [[#add reactions|Add Reactions ]]to add Energy or Power to pay costs. 

#### rule 429.3.a
**429.3.a.** When an [[#added|Add ]]ability is activated in this way, it immediately ﬁnalizes and resolves, even during the resolution of spells and abilities. 

#### rule 429.4
**429.4.** [[#added|Adding ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 429.4.a
**429.4.a.** Players may only [[#added|Add ]]resources when [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]direct them to do so. 

#### rule 429.5
**429.5.** This action is formatted as "Add [one or more resources]."  e.g., "Add [2]." means "Add 2 Energy."  e.g., "[E]: Add [Y]." means "Add 1 Power of the Order domain."  e.g., "Add [1][G]." means "Add 1 Energy and 1 Power of the Calm domain." 

### rule 430
**430.** [[#channeled|Channel ]]

#### rule 430.1
**430.1.** [[#channeled|Channeling ]]is the action of taking one or more [[#rune|Runes ]]from the top of a player's [[#rune deck|Rune Deck ]]and putting them on the board. 

#### rule 430.2
**430.2.** The [[#game effects|Game Effect ]]that instructs a player to channel 1 or more runes may specify the conditions or circumstances under which those runes enter the board. Example: A spell reads "Channel 1 rune exhausted." As that spell resolves, its controller puts the top rune of their rune deck onto the board and that rune enters the board exhausted rather than ready. 

#### rule 430.3
**430.3.** [[#channeled|Channeling ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 430.3.a
**430.3.a.** Players may only channel runes when [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]direct them to do so. 

#### rule 430.4
**430.4.** This action is formatted as "Channel X rune(s)," optionally followed by conditions or stipulations.  e.g., "Channel 1 rune."  e.g., "When you play me, channel 1 rune exhausted."  e.g., "Channel 2 runes exhausted. If you couldn't channel 2 runes this way, draw 1." 

### rule 431
**431.** [[#burn out|Burn Out ]]

#### rule 431.1
**431.1.** [[#burning out|Burning Out ]]is an action a player must perform if they attempt to move one or more cards from their [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]to any other zone in excess of the number of cards remaining in their [[#main deck|Main Deck: ]]

#### rule 431.1.a
**431.1.a.** If a player must [[#drawn|Draw ]]cards in excess to the number of cards in their deck, they will [[#drawn|Draw ]]as many as possible, perform this action, then [[#drawn|Draw ]]the remaining amount instructed. 

#### rule 431.1.b
**431.1.b.** If a player must put one or more cards from their [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]in any other zone, such as the [[#trashes|Trash]], in excess of the number of cards in their deck they will do so as much as possible, perform this action, and then complete the remaining number required by the instruction. 

#### rule 431.1.c
**431.1.c.** If an instruction directs a player to look at or reveal cards in excess to the number of cards in a player’s [[#main deck|Main Deck]], that player looks at or [[#reveal|Reveals ]]as many as possible, but does not [[#burn out|Burn Out, ]]then proceeds with the rest of the instruction. 

#### rule 431.1.c.1
**431.1.c.1.** If there are insufﬁcient cards among the looked at or revealed cards to perform subsequent actions to the revealed or looked at cards, any further instructions are ignored. This does not cause a [[#burn out|Burn Out]], even if those instructions would cause those cards to change zones.  Reminder: Cards are considered in the zone of origin while being looked at or revealed, in this case the [[#main deck|Main Deck]]. 

#### rule 431.2
**431.2.** To [[#burn out|Burn Out]], a player does the following in sequence: 

#### rule 431.2.a
**431.2.a.** Performs as much of the prescribed action as possible. 

#### rule 431.2.b
**431.2.b.** Recycles their trash into their Main Deck.  Reminder: When multiple cards are [[#recycled|Recycled ]]to the [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]at the same time, those cards must be randomized 

#### rule 431.2.c
**431.2.c.** Chooses an opponent to gain 1 point. 

#### rule 431.2.d
**431.2.d.** Completes the remainder of the action that caused them to burn out.  Example: A player attempts to draw 1 during their Draw Phase while their Main Deck is empty. That player instead recycles their trash into their Main Deck, randomizing it as normal, then chooses an opponent to gain 1 point, and then draws 1. 

#### rule 431.3
**431.3.** A player's Main Deck may remain empty as they [[#burn out|Burn Out]], usually because their trash is also empty. When they attempt to perform the original action again, it will cause another [[#burn out|Burn Out]]. 

#### rule 431.3.a
**431.3.a.** Unless some effect intervenes, this will result in them burning out repeatedly, giving 1 point to an opponent each time, until an opponent passes the Victory Score and wins the game. 

#### rule 431.3.b
**431.3.b.** Points gained after the ﬁrst [[#burn out|Burn Out ]]being processed in sequence cannot be replaced or prevented by any means. Points gained after the ﬁrst [[#burn out|Burn Out ]]being processed in sequence that cause a player to reach or surpass the Victory Score for their game mode will cause that player to win the game if they also have more points than any opponent. The player wins immediately, without needing to wait for a cleanup to occur. 

#### rule 431.4
**431.4.** [[#burning out|Burning Out ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 431.4.a
**431.4.a.** Players may only burn out when [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]direct them to do so. 

#### rule 431.5
**431.5.** [[#burning out|Burning Out ]]is a [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effect.  ]]See [[##rule 367|rule 367.]] [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects]] for more information. 

### rule 432
**432.** [[#double|Double ]]

#### rule 432.1
**432.1.** [[#double|Doubling ]]is the act of [[#increasing|increasing  ]]a numeric attribute by an amount equal to that attribute’s current value. 

#### rule 432.1.a
**432.1.a.** This creates an effect that modulates that attribute by that speciﬁc amount for the duration speciﬁed by the [[#game effects|Game Effect ]]that instructed the player to perform this action. Example: A unit with 3 base Might and Shield 2 is in combat as a Defender. Since Shield applies, its current Might is 5. A player chooses it as the target for Last Stand, a spell that reads in part “Double a friendly unit's Might this turn.” Its current Might is 5, so it gets +5 Might this turn, for a current Might of 10. After combat, Shield no longer applies, but the +5 Might from Last Stand does, so the unit’s Might is 8. 

#### rule 432.2
**432.2.** [[#double|Doubling ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 432.2.a
**432.2.a.** Players may only Double when [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]direct them to do so. 

### rule 433
**433.** [[#swap|Swap ]]

#### rule 433.1
**433.1.** [[#swap|Swapping ]]is the act of increasing one numeric value and decreasing another numeric value on some number of [[#game object|Game Objects ]]such that their values are reversed. 

#### rule 433.1.a
**433.1.a.** [[#swap|Swapping ]]creates two different effects that apply to each attribute. One that [[#increasing|Increases ]]one value and one that [[#decreases|Decreases ]]the other. 

#### rule 433.1.b
**433.1.b.** To accomplish this, determine the difference between these values and then apply an [[#increasing|Increase ]]for that amount to the lower value  of the two attributes, and a [[#decreases|Decrease ]]of that amount to the higher value of the two attributes. 

#### rule 433.1.c
**433.1.c.** If both attributes are the same numeric value, [[#swap|Swapping ]]has no effect. 

#### rule 433.2
**433.2.** [[#swap|Swapping ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 433.2.a
**433.2.a.** Players may only swap when [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]direct them to do so. 

### rule 434
**434.** [[#attached|Attach ]]

#### rule 434.1
**434.1.** [[#attached|Attaching ]]is the act of linking two cards on the board together to combine their effects in some way. This causes one or more cards to become [[#attached|Attached ]]and at least one card to become a [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card. ]]See [[##rule 716|rule 716.]] [[#attachment|Attachment]] for more information. 

#### rule 434.1.a
**434.1.a.** [[#attached|Attaching ]]affects two cards at once. 

#### rule 434.1.a.1
**434.1.a.1.** One card will be designated as the one being [[#attached|Attached]], and thus become [[#attached|Attached. ]]The other will become the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card. ]]

#### rule 434.1.b
**434.1.b.** This is represented by physically laying the [[#top-most card|Top-Most card ]]on top of the other or others such that all [[#effect text|Effect Texts ]]and [[#might bonus|Might Bonuses ]]are showing, but nothing else from the card or cards [[#attached|Attached. ]]

#### rule 434.1.b.1
**434.1.b.1.** In the situation where there is more than one card attached to the [[#top-most card|Top-Most card]], they should be stacked in such a way that all [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]boxes and [[#might bonus|Might Bonuses ]]are readable. The order of the [[#attached|Attached ]]cards has no bearing on the application of effects. 

#### rule 434.1.c
**434.1.c.** The [[#top-most card|Top-Most card ]]has all [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]of all cards [[#attached|Attached ]]to it appended to its [[#rules text|Rules Text. ]]

#### rule 434.1.d
**434.1.d.** The [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]has its [[#might|Might ]]modulated by the [[#might bonus|Might Bonus ]]of all cards [[#attached|Attached ]]to it. 

#### rule 434.1.e
**434.1.e.** [[#attached|Attaching ]]one or more cards will cause those cards’ [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]to become [[#inactive|Inactive ]]for as long as they remain [[#attached|Attached. ]]See [[##rule 716|rule 716.]] [[#attachment|Attachment]] for more information. 

#### rule 434.1.f
**434.1.f.** [[#attached|Attaching ]]a card to a new [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]will cause it to [[#detach|Detach ]]from the card to which it is currently [[#attached|Attached. ]]

#### rule 434.1.g
**434.1.g.** [[#attached|Attaching ]]a card to its current [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card  ]]will not have any effect. 

#### rule 434.1.h
**434.1.h.** If a [[#game effects|Game Effect ]]instructs a player to [[#attached|Attach ]]a card to its current [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card]], nothing additional happens. 

#### rule 434.2
**434.2.** [[#attached|Attaching ]]is a Limited Action. 

#### rule 434.2.a
**434.2.a.** Players may only [[#attached|Attach ]]cards when directed to by [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 434.3
**434.3.** [[#attached|Attaching ]]cards does not inherently choose or specify a target. However, [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]that [[#attached|Attach ]]cards may do so. 

#### rule 434.4
**434.4.** When a card [[#attaches|Attaches ]]to a card, its location becomes the same as the new [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card. ]]

#### rule 434.4.a
**434.4.a.** This is not a [[#move|Move. ]]

### rule 435
**435.** [[#detach|Detach ]]

#### rule 435.1
**435.1.** [[#detach|Detaching ]]is the act of unlinking two cards that are currently linked through the act of [[#attached|Attaching]]. This causes one to cease being [[#attached|Attached]], and potentially causes the other to cease being a [[#top-most card|Top-Most card. ]]

#### rule 435.1.a
**435.1.a.** [[#detach|Detaching ]]affects only cards that are currently [[#attached|Attached ]]to another card. 

#### rule 435.1.a.1
**435.1.a.1.** Game effects that instruct a player to [[#detach|Detach ]]a card that is currently not [[#attached|Attached ]]to anything will do nothing. 

#### rule 435.1.b
**435.1.b.** When one or more cards become [[#detach|Detached]], they cease to be in the [[#attached|Attached ]]state. 

#### rule 435.1.b.1
**435.1.b.1.** To represent this, these cards should no longer be placed under the card they were previously placed under as [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card. ]]

#### rule 435.1.b.2
**435.1.b.2.** If the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]no longer has any cards [[#attached|Attached ]]to it after this, it is no longer a [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card. ]]

#### rule 435.1.c
**435.1.c.** The card being [[#detach|Detached ]]has its [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]become [[#inactive|Inactive ]]and its [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]cease being [[#inactive|Inactive. ]]

#### rule 435.1.d
**435.1.d.** The [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]ceases to have the [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]of the card being [[#detach|Detached ]]appended to its [[#rules text|Rules Text. ]]

#### rule 435.1.e
**435.1.e.** The [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]ceases to have its [[#might|Might ]]modulated by the [[#might bonus|Might Bonus ]]of the card being [[#detach|Detached. ]]

#### rule 435.2
**435.2.** [[#detach|Detaching ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 435.2.a
**435.2.a.** [[#player|Players ]]may only [[#detach|Detach ]]cards when directed to by [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 435.3
**435.3.** [[#detach|Detaching ]]cards does not inherently choose, or specify a target. However, Game Effects that [[#detach|Detach ]]cards may. 

#### rule 435.4
**435.4.** When a card [[#detach|Detaches ]]from a [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card]], its location is the same as the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]from which it [[#detach|Detached. ]]

#### rule 435.4.a
**435.4.a.** If the [[#detach|Detached ]]card was a [[#gear|Gear ]]and this causes it to become present at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld]], it will be [[#recalls|Recalled ]]during the next [[#cleanup|Cleanup. ]]

#### rule 435.4.b
**435.4.b.** If the [[#attached|Attached ]]card was [[#detach|Detached ]]because the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]changed zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, then the location that the [[#attached|Attached Card ]]will [[#detach|Detach ]]to is the last location the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]was at before changing from a board zone to a non-board zone. 

### rule 436
**436.** [[#predict|Predict ]]

#### rule 436.1
**436.1.** [[#predict|Predicting ]]a card is the act of looking at a single card from the top of the [[#main deck|Main Deck ]]and choosing whether or not to [[#recycled|Recycle ]]it. 

#### rule 436.1.a
**436.1.a.** When more than one card is [[#predict|Predicted]], the [[#predict|Predicting ]]player looks at that many cards and [[#recycles|Recycles ]]any number of them. 

#### rule 436.1.b
**436.1.b.** The [[#player|Player ]]who performs the game action may rearrange any cards not [[#recycled|Recycled ]]in this way.  

#### rule 436.2
**436.2.** [[#predict|Predicting ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 436.2.a
**436.2.a.** [[#player|Players ]]may only [[#predict|Predict ]]cards when instructed to do so by game effects. 

#### rule 436.3
**436.3.** This action, when instructed, is formatted as "Predict X." 

#### rule 436.3.a
**436.3.a.** If omitted, X is presumed to be 1. 

#### rule 436.4
**436.4.** If a player attempts to [[#predict|Predict ]]more cards than are available in their [[#main deck|Main Deck]], they will [[#predict|Predict ]]as many as possible instead. 

#### rule 436.4.a
**436.4.a.** The [[#player|Player ]]will not perform a [[#burn out|Burn Out ]]as a result of [[#predict|Predicting ]]with too few cards in their deck. 

### rule 437
**437.** [[#prevent|Prevent ]]
