#### rule 437.1
**437.1.** [[#prevent|Preventing ]]damage is the act of reducing the [[#damage|Damage ]]a set of game objects would take. 

#### rule 437.1.a
**437.1.a.** [[#prevent|Prevent ]]is an action that interacts with [[#damage|Damage. ]]

#### rule 437.1.b
**437.1.b.** [[#prevent|Prevent ]]appears in statements that deﬁne an amount of damage and the source of the damage it will affect, as well as the timespan it will be relevant for. 

#### rule 437.1.b.1
**437.1.b.1.** [[#prevent|Prevent ]]actions are usually formatted as “[[#prevent|Prevent ]]the next X [source] damage that would be dealt to a [unit] this turn.” 

#### rule 437.1.b.1.a
**437.1.b.1.a.** The X is referred to as the Prevent Value. 

#### rule 437.1.b.1.b
**437.1.b.1.b.** X can be “All,” which speciﬁes an inﬁnite amount of damage. 

#### rule 437.1.b.2
**437.1.b.2.** [[#prevent|Prevent ]]will always apply to the next damage that would be dealt to a unit affected by the [[#prevent|Prevent ]]action. 

#### rule 437.2
**437.2.** When damage is [[#prevent|Prevented]], it is replaced with an event where it deals that much damage reduced by the Prevent Value tracked on the [[#unit|Unit ]]speciﬁcally. 

#### rule 437.2.a
**437.2.a.** The damage being dealt as a result of [[#prevent|Preventing ]]can never be less than 0, but can be 0. This is equivalent to not dealing damage. 

#### rule 437.3
**437.3.** When damage is dealt this way, reduce the Prevent Value being tracked on the [[#unit|Unit ]]affected by the [[#prevent|Prevent ]]action by the prevented amount.  

#### rule 437.3.a
**437.3.a.** If the Prevent Value is 0 or less, then [[#prevent|Prevent ]]is no longer being tracked on the [[#unit|Unit ]]in question, and the effect expires. 

#### rule 437.3.b
**437.3.b.** The reduced value is the newly tracked Prevent Value. 

#### rule 437.3.c
**437.3.c.** If the Prevent Value is “All” then it remains “All.” 

#### rule 437.4
**437.4.** Damage dealt to a [[#unit|Unit ]]that has that all of that damage [[#prevent|Prevented ]]is not considered to have been dealt to it at all. 

#### rule 437.5
**437.5.** Damage can still be assigned to [[#unit|Units ]]in combat that are affected by [[#prevent|Prevent]]. The damage dealt as a result of that assignment will be affected by the [[#prevent|Prevent ]]action. 

#### rule 437.5.a
**437.5.a.** Damage can be assigned to a Unit up to a value that would be [[#lethal|Lethal ]]considering the Prevent Value of all [[#prevent actions|Prevent Actions ]]on a [[#unit|Unit. ]]Example:  A unit with 2 [M] is being assigned damage in the combat damage step. The unit has “prevent the ﬁrst 3 damage I would take each combat.” The unit would need to be assigned 5 damage in order to have lethal damage assigned to it. 

#### rule 437.5.b
**437.5.b.** No amount of damage is ever considered lethal if the Prevent Value is “All.” 

#### rule 437.6
**437.6.** [[#prevent|Prevent ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 437.6.a
**437.6.a.** [[#player|Players ]]may only [[#prevent damage|Prevent Damage ]]when directed to by [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 437.7
**437.7.** [[#prevent|Prevent ]]is a [[#delayed replacement effect|Delayed Replacement Effect. ]]See [[##rule 367|rule 367.]] [[#replacement effect|Replacement Effects]] for more information. See [[##rule 389|rule 389.]] [[#delayed abilities|Delayed Abilities]] for more information. 

### rule 438
**438.** [[#replace|Replace ]]

#### rule 438.1
**438.1.** [[#replace|Replacing ]]is the act of [[#creates|Creating ]]a token in the place of another card or token without playing it while inheriting all effects or statuses of the game object it replaced. 

#### rule 438.2
**438.2.** [[#replace|Replacing ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 438.2.a
**438.2.a.** The player may [[#replace|Replace ]]cards and tokens when instructed to do so by other game effects. 

#### rule 438.3
**438.3.** This action, when instructed, is formatted as "Replace [X] with [Y]." 

#### rule 438.3.a
**438.3.a.** The [X] is the target to be [[#replace|Replaced. ]]

#### rule 438.3.b
**438.3.b.** The [Y] is the object that will [[#replace|Replace ]]the target. 

#### rule 438.3.b.1
**438.3.b.1.** This will always specify a Token to create. 

#### rule 438.4
**438.4.** [[#replace|Replacing ]]is not a subset of [[#banishing|Banishing. ]]

#### rule 438.5
**438.5.** The card or token that is [[#replace|Replaced ]]is placed in Banishment. 

#### rule 438.5.a
**438.5.a.** While it resides in [[#banishments|Banishment, ]]it is considered to have been [[#replace|Replaced ]]and not [[#banishing|Banished. ]]

#### rule 438.6
**438.6.** If a token is [[#replace|Replaced ]]it will stop existing once it begins its occupancy in [[#banishments|Banishment. ]]

#### rule 438.6.a
**438.6.a.** This does not invalidate the token created, or the act of [[#replace|Replacement. ]]

#### rule 438.7
**438.7.** Tokens that have been [[#created|Created ]]through a [[#replace|Replace ]]action can be instructed to be “Swapped back.” 

#### rule 438.7.a
**438.7.a.** “Swapping Back” is an extension of the [[#replace|Replace ]]action. 

#### rule 438.7.b
**438.7.b.** To [[#swap|Swap Back]], the token stops existing and the original card is returned to the space that the token just occupied, inheriting all current effects and statuses. 

#### rule 438.7.c
**438.7.c.** If there is nothing in [[#banishments|Banishment ]]to swap back to, usually because a token was replaced, then this object can never swap back. 

### rule 439
**439.** [[#creates|Create ]]

#### rule 439.1
**439.1.** [[#creates|Creating ]]is the act of producing a [[#game object|Game Object ]]that previously did not exist in the game. 

#### rule 439.2
**439.2.** Effects that [[#creates|Create ]]one or more [[#game object|Game Objects ]]will direct where those [[#game object|Game Objects ]]must go - the [[#game object|Game Objects ]]are [[#created|Created ]]directly to the zones in question. 

#### rule 439.2.a
**439.2.a.** Prior to being [[#created|Created, ]]these [[#game object|Game Objects ]]did not exist outside of the zone they were [[#created|Created ]]to. After being [[#created|Created]], they may change zones as appropriate for [[#game object|Game Objects ]]of their type. 

#### rule 439.2.b
**439.2.b.** If a zone is not speciﬁed by the effect, the [[#game object|Game Object ]]will be created to the appropriate zone for its type. Permanents will be [[#created|Created ]]to any location on the Board that they can be played to. 

#### rule 439.2.b.1
**439.2.b.1.** Spells will be [[#created|Created ]]to the Chain. 

#### rule 439.2.b.2
**439.2.b.2.** Runes will be [[#created to base|Created to base. ]]

#### rule 439.2.b.3
**439.2.b.3.** Legends will be [[#created|Created ]]to the Legend Zone. 

#### rule 439.2.b.4
**439.2.b.4.** Battleﬁelds will be [[#created|Created ]]to the Battleﬁeld Zone. 

#### rule 439.3
**439.3.** An effect that [[#creates|Creates ]]a [[#game object|Game Object ]]will specify the nature of the [[#game object|Game Object ]]created.

#### rule 439.3.a
**439.3.a.** If the [[#game object|Game Object ]]is a token, it will follow the normal rules for tokens. See [[##rule 176|rule 176.]] [[#token|Tokens]] for more information. 

#### rule 439.4
**439.4.** Unless speciﬁed otherwise by the [[#game effects|Game Effect ]]that [[#creates|Creates ]]a [[#game object|Game Object]], any such [[#game object|Game Object ]]is owned by the player who [[#created|Created ]]it. [[#control|Control ]]is established as usual for [[#game object|Game Objects ]]of the appropriate type.

#### rule 439.4.a
**439.4.a.** A [[#created|Created ]]permanent, rune, legend, or spell is controlled by its owner as it is created. 

#### rule 439.4.b
**439.4.b.** A [[#created|Created ]]battleﬁeld is uncontrolled as it is created. 

#### rule 439.5
**439.5.** This action, when instructed, is usually formatted as "Create [X] to [Y]" or “Add [X] to [Y].” 

#### rule 439.6
**439.6.** [[#creates|Creating ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 439.6.a
**439.6.a.** Players may only [[#create game objects|Create Game Objects ]]when directed to by [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 440
**440.** [[#move|Movement ]]

### rule 441
**441.** [[#move|Moving ]]is a [[#limited actions|Limited Action. ]]

#### rule 441.1
**441.1.** A [[#permanents|Permanent ]]changing its position from any space on [[#board|the Board ]]to another space on [[#board|the Board ]]is a [[#move|Move]], unless it is caused by a corrective [[#recalls|Recall]].  See [[##rule 420|rule 420.]] [[#move|Move]] for more information. 

#### rule 441.2
**441.2.** A card changing game zones does not in itself constitute a [[#move|Move. ]]

#### rule 441.3
**441.3.** [[#move|Moving ]]is instantaneous. 

#### rule 441.3.a
**441.3.a.** There is no state for [[#permanents|Permanents ]]between locations. 

#### rule 441.3.b
**441.3.b.** [[#permanents|Permanents ]]are either at their [[#origins|Origin ]]before [[#move|Moving ]]or their [[#destination|Destination ]]after [[#move|Moving. ]]

#### rule 441.3.c
**441.3.c.** [[#move|Moving ]]does not use the [[#chain|Chain]], nor is it able to be [[#reaction|Reacted ]]to. 

### rule 442
**442.** [[#move|Moving ]]is deﬁned by the [[#origins|Origin ]]and [[#destination|Destination ]]of the [[#permanents|Permanent ]]that is changing locations. 

#### rule 442.1
**442.1.** The [[#origins|Origin ]]is where the [[#permanents|Permanent ]]is starting from. 

#### rule 442.2
**442.2.** The [[#destination|Destination ]]is where the [[#permanents|Permanent ]]is going to. 

#### rule 442.2.a
**442.2.a.** In [[#modes of play|Modes of Play ]]with more than two players, [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]with [[#staged combats|Staged Combats ]]or [[#combats in progress|Combats in Progress ]]are [[#invalid destinations|Invalid Destinations ]]for [[#move|Moves ]]of all kinds ([[#standard move|Standard Moves ]]or otherwise) by [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by [[#player|Players ]]not involved in those [[#combat|Combats ]]or who don't already have permanents at that [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld]]. 

#### rule 442.2.b
**442.2.b.** In [[#modes of play|Modes of Play ]]with teammates, [[#battleﬁelds controlled|Battleﬁelds Controlled ]]by a player’s teammates are [[#invalid destinations|Invalid Destinations ]]for [[#move|Moves ]]of all kinds ([[#standard move|Standard Moves ]]or otherwise) by [[#unit|Units ]]that player controls. 

#### rule 442.2.c
**442.2.c.** If an action would require a [[#move|Move ]]that would cause a [[#unit|Unit ]]to become present in a [[#location|Location ]]where it cannot move for any reason, such as a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]with two players that are [[#name|not ]]the controller of the [[#unit|Unit ]]performing this [[#move|Move ]]action are in a [[#combat|Combat ]]or such a [[#combat|Combat ]]is [[#state|Staged]], it instead [[#recalls|Recalls. ]]See [[##rule 449|rule 449.]] [[#recalls|Recalls]] for more information. 

#### rule 442.3
**442.3.** [[#unit|Units ]]are the only [[#permanents|Permanents ]]that can [[#move|Move. ]]

### rule 443
**443.** Players may choose to move their [[#unit|Units ]]with the [[#standard move|Standard Move. ]]See [[##rule 144|rule 144.]]for more information on the [[#standard move|Standard Move. ]]

### rule 444
**444.** [[#spells|Spells]], [[#abilities|Abilities]], or other effects may cause a [[#move|Move ]]to occur. 

#### rule 444.1
**444.1.** The source of the [[#move|Move ]]will provide details on any restrictions on legality for [[#destination|Destination. ]]

#### rule 444.2
**444.2.** [[#units cannot move|Units cannot Move ]]to a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that already has units from 2 other players present by any means. 

### rule 445
**445.** The [[#destination|Destination ]]becomes [[#contested|Contested ]]if it is a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]not controlled by the controller of the [[#unit|Unit ]]or [[#unit|Units ]]that moved. 

### rule 446
**446.** [[#unit|Units ]]may cause a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]without a [[#combat|Combat ]]when they [[#move|Move. ]]

#### rule 446.1
**446.1.** A [[#showdown|Showdown ]]is opened when a [[#move|Move ]]causes a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]to become [[#contested|Contested ]]while it has no [[#unit|Units ]]present from any player other than those that just moved. 

### rule 447
**447.** [[#unit|Units ]]may cause [[#combat|Combat ]]when they [[#move|Move. ]]

#### rule 447.1
**447.1.** A [[#combat|Combat ]]is opened when a [[#move|Move ]]causes a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]to become [[#contested|Contested ]]and [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by opposing players, or when a [[#move|Move ]]causes [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by opposing players to become present in the same [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]where a [[#showdown|Showdown ]]is ongoing. See [[##rule 454|rule 454.]] [[#combat|Combat]] for more information. 

### rule 448
**448.** When a [[#move|Move ]]action is complete, perform a [[#cleanup|Cleanup. ]]

### rule 449
**449.** Recalls 

### rule 450
**450.** A [[#recalls|Recall ]]is when a [[#permanents|Permanent ]]is relocated from anywhere to its [[#bases|Base ]]without it being a [[#move|Move. ]]

### rule 451
**451.** [[#recalls|Recalls ]]are not [[#move|Moves. ]]

#### rule 451.1
**451.1.** They do not cause [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]to trigger that are triggered by [[#move|Move ]]actions. 

#### rule 451.2
**451.2.** A [[#recalls|Recall ]]causes a [[#permanents|Permanent ]]to change locations. 

#### rule 451.3
**451.3.** A [[#recalls|Recall ]]cannot be prevented by actions and [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]that restrict or block [[#move|Movement. ]]

### rule 452
**452.** Gear can be [[#recalls|Recalled. ]]

#### rule 452.1
**452.1.** When an un-attached [[#gear|Gear ]]is created or played at a battleﬁeld, or is at a battleﬁeld for any other reason, it is [[#recalls|Recalled ]]to its controller's base during the next [[#cleanup|Cleanup.  ]]Example: An Equipment is attached to a unit at a battleﬁeld, so the Equipment is present at that battleﬁeld. If the unit dies, the Equipment will be recalled during the next cleanup. 

### rule 453
**453.** Recalls do not affect the state of the [[#permanents|Permanent ]]being recalled. 

#### rule 453.1
**453.1.** Unless otherwise stated by the source of the [[#recalls|Recall]], Damage, Exhausted Status, Buffed Status, and applied Layer alterations will all remain unaffected by a [[#recalls|Recall]]. 

### rule 454
**454.** [[#combat|Combat ]]

### rule 455
**455.** A [[#combat|Combat ]]occurs when a [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]occurs, there are no items on the [[#chain|Chain]], there is a staged [[#combat|Combat ]]at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld, ]]and no [[#showdown|Showdown ]]or [[#combat|Combat ]]is ongoing at any other [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld. ]]See [[##rule 318|rule 318.]] [[#cleanup|Cleanups]] for more information. 

#### rule 455.1
**455.1.** If there is an ongoing Showdown at the Battleﬁeld where the [[#combat|Combat ]]is staged, that [[#showdown|Showdown ]]will become a [[#combat showdown|Combat Showdown ]]and a [[#combat|Combat ]]will be initiated there. 

### rule 456
**456.** [[#combat|Combat ]]is considered [[#state|Staged ]]if there are units controlled by two opposing players at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]but the [[#steps of combat|Steps of Combat ]]have not been initiated. 

#### rule 456.1
**456.1.** If more than one [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]has [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by opposing players at it at the same time, the [[#turn player|Turn Player ]]decides which [[#combat|Combat ]]to resolve ﬁrst. 

#### rule 456.2
**456.2.** If [[#staged combats|Staged Combats ]]stop being [[#state|Staged ]]before the [[#steps of combat|Steps of Combat ]]are initiated, they are not resolved or executed. 

#### rule 456.3
**456.3.** If a [[#combat|Combat ]]and [[#showdown|Showdown ]]are staged at the same [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]and the turn player initiates the [[#showdown|Showdown]], it will open as a [[#combat showdown|Combat Showdown. ]]

### rule 457
**457.** [[#combat|Combat ]]can only occur between [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by exactly two players. 

#### rule 457.1
**457.1.** In [[#modes of play|Modes of Play ]]with more than two players, [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]with [[#staged combats|Staged Combats ]]or [[#combats in progress|Combats in Progress ]]are [[#invalid destinations|Invalid Destinations ]]for [[#move|Moves ]]of all kinds ([[#standard move|Standard Moves ]]or otherwise) by [[#unit|Units ]]controlled by [[#player|Players ]]not involved in those [[#combat|Combats ]]or who don't already have [[#unit|Units ]]at that [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld.  ]]See [[##rule 442.2.a|rule 442.2.a.]]for more information on [[#invalid destinations|Invalid Destinations. ]]

#### rule 457.2
**457.2.** In [[#modes of play|Modes of Play ]]with more than two players, [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]with [[#staged combats|Staged Combats ]]or [[#combats in progress|Combats in Progress ]]are [[#invalid|Invalid ]]to be chosen as a location to play one or more [[#unit|Units ]]by a player not involved in that [[#combat|Combat ]]by any means, 

#### rule 457.2.a
**457.2.a.** If an effect would require a [[#unit|Unit ]]be played to a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]with a [[#staged combats|Staged Combat ]]or a [[#combat in progress|Combat in Progress]], where the controller of the played unit is not a participant, instead the [[#unit|Unit ]]is played to its controller's [[#bases|Base. ]]

#### rule 457.2.b
**457.2.b.** Any subsequent reference to "here" in the corresponding effect is reassigned to the Controller's [[#bases|Base]], where the [[#unit|Unit ]]was played. Any further effects that may be invalidated are invalidated as if the effect was mistargeted. See [[##rule 355.6|rule 355.6.]] [[#targeting|Targeting]] for more information on [[#mistargeting|Mistargeting. ]]

#### rule 457.3
**457.3.** All choices that would result in a [[#combat|Combat ]]occurring between more than two players simultaneously are invalid and ineligible to be completed. 

### rule 458
**458.** [[#steps of combat|The Steps of Combat ]]

### rule 459
**459.** [[#step 1: the combat showdown step|Step 1: The Combat Showdown Step ]]

#### rule 459.1
**459.1.** [[#combat|Combat ]]will open in one of two ways: when a [[#combat|Combat ]]and [[#showdown|Showdown ]]are staged at the same [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]and the turn player initiates the [[#showdown|Showdown]]; or when the turn is in a [[#showdown open state|Showdown Open State ]]and a [[#combat|Combat ]]is staged at the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]where the current [[#showdown|Showdown ]]is ongoing. See [[##rule 318|rule 318.]] [[#cleanup|Cleanups]] for more information. 

#### rule 459.2
**459.2.** When Combat opens, it either opens with a Combat Showdown, or the current Showdown becomes a Combat Showdown. 

#### rule 459.2.a
**459.2.a.** The following [[#task|Tasks ]]become [[#outstanding|Outstanding]], in the order described: 

#### rule 459.2.b
**459.2.b.** 1. Establish who is [[#attacker|Attacker ]]and who is [[#defender|Defender. ]]

#### rule 459.2.b.1
**459.2.b.1.** The [[#attacker|Attacker ]]is the player whose unit(s) applied the [[#contested|Contested ]]status to the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld. ]]They gain the [[#attacker designation|Attacker designation ]]now. 

#### rule 459.2.b.1.a
**459.2.b.1.a.** This player gains Focus as the showdown begins. 

#### rule 459.2.b.2
**459.2.b.2.** The [[#defender|Defender ]]is the player who did not apply the [[#contested|Contested ]]status to the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld. ]]They gain the [[#defender|Defender ]]designation now. 

#### rule 459.2.b.3
**459.2.b.3.** Units at the [[#contested battleﬁeld|Contested Battleﬁeld ]]controlled by the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]gain the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]designation now. 

#### rule 459.2.b.3.a
**459.2.b.3.a.** If a [[#unit|Unit ]]controlled by the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]becomes present at this [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]after this moment, it will gain the [[#attacker|Attacker ]]designation during the [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]phase following the action that caused it to become present 

#### rule 459.2.b.4
**459.2.b.4.** Units at the [[#contested battleﬁeld|Contested Battleﬁeld ]]controlled by the [[#defender|Defender ]]gain the [[#defender|Defender ]]designation now. 

#### rule 459.2.b.4.a
**459.2.b.4.a.** If a [[#unit|Unit ]]controlled by the [[#defender|Defender ]]becomes present at this [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]after this moment it will gain the [[#defender|Defender ]]designation during the [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]phase following the action that caused it to become present 

#### rule 459.2.c
**459.2.c.** 2. The [[#attacker|Attacker ]]gains [[#focus|Focus. ]]

#### rule 459.2.d
**459.2.d.** 3. Add items to the [[#combat|Combat Chain ]]if establishing [[#attacker|Attacker ]]and [[#defender|Defender ]]has caused [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]to become [[#pending item|Pending. ]]

#### rule 459.2.d.1
**459.2.d.1.** The [[#attacker|Attacking ]]player, who has [[#focus|Focus]], places [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]on the Chain ﬁrst, followed by all non-[[#defender|Defender ]]players in [[#turn order|Turn Order]], followed by the [[#defending player|Defending Player. ]]

#### rule 459.2.e
**459.2.e.** The [[#state closes|State Closes ]]if a [[#combat|Combat Chain ]]was created. 

#### rule 459.2.e.1
**459.2.e.1.** Otherwise the [[#combat showdown|Combat Showdown ]]continues, with the [[#state|State Open ]]as normal. 

#### rule 459.2.f
**459.2.f.** Players proceed with any play on the [[#chain|Chain ]]as normal. 

#### rule 459.2.g
**459.2.g.** Focus does not pass upon closure of the Combat Chain, if any. 

### rule 460
**460.** [[#step 2: the combat damage step|Step 2: The Combat Damage Step ]]

#### rule 460.1
**460.1.** If both [[#attacker|Attacking ]]and [[#defender|Defending ]]units remain at this battleﬁeld, the following [[#task|Tasks ]]become [[#outstanding|Outstanding]], in the speciﬁed order: 

#### rule 460.2
**460.2.** 1. When the [[#showdown|Showdown ]]closes, [[#attacker|Attackers ]]and [[#defender|Defenders ]]resolve [[#combat damage step|Combat Damage ]]at the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that was attacked, using their current [[#might|Might. ]]

#### rule 460.2.a
**460.2.a.** Sum the [[#might|Might ]]of all [[#attacking units|Attacking Units. ]]

#### rule 460.2.b
**460.2.b.** Sum the [[#might|Might ]]of all [[#defending units|Defending Units. ]]

#### rule 460.2.c
**460.2.c.** Starting with the [[#attacker|Attacker]], each player assigns an amount of damage equal to their summed [[#might|Might ]]among the other's [[#unit|Units. ]]

#### rule 460.2.c.1
**460.2.c.1.** Assigning [[#damage|Damage ]]is not [[#dealing damage|Dealing Damage. ]]

#### rule 460.2.c.1.a
**460.2.c.1.a.** When all [[#damage|Damage ]]is assigned, it will be [[#dealt|Dealt ]]simultaneously. These actions are not synonymous. 

#### rule 460.2.c.2
**460.2.c.2.** Abilities or effects may influence the order in which damage is assigned. [[#reminder: lethal damage is non-zero damage equaling or exceeding the might of a unit|Reminder: Lethal Damage is non-zero damage equaling or exceeding the Might of a Unit. ]]

#### rule 460.2.c.3
**460.2.c.3.** [[#unit|Units ]]must have lethal damage assigned to them in full before damage is assigned to a different [[#unit|Unit.  ]]Example: If a player has 5 damage to distribute among four 3 Might units, they may not choose to assign 2 damage to one of the units and 1 damage to each of the remaining 3. They must assign at least 3 damage to one, and the remaining 2 to another. 

#### rule 460.2.c.4
**460.2.c.4.** [[#unit|Units ]]cannot have more damage assigned to them than the minimum required to constitute lethal damage unless no further units remain to have damage assigned to them. 

#### rule 460.2.c.5
**460.2.c.5.** A player must obey all requirements and restrictions on damage assignment if able.  Example: A player is assigning damage to the following units: a unit with [[#tank|Tank ]]("I must be assigned combat damage ﬁrst."); Caitlyn, Patrolling ("I must be assigned combat damage last."); and another unit without any abilities. That player must assign combat damage ﬁrst to the unit with Tank, then to the unit with no abilities, then to Caitlyn. 

#### rule 460.2.c.6
**460.2.c.6.** If multiple [[#unit|Units ]]have abilities or effects that require a player to assign them damage with the same priority, that player may assign damage to those units in any order.  Example: A player is assigning damage to the following units: two units with [[#tank|Tank ]]("I must be assigned combat damage ﬁrst.") and one unit with no abilities. That player chooses one of the units with Tank and assigns combat damage to it. Then they must assign any remaining damage ﬁrst to the other unit with Tank, then to the unit with no abilities. 

#### rule 460.2.c.7
**460.2.c.7.** If a [[#unit|Unit ]]has one or more [[#abilities|Abilities ]]or effects applying to it that demand it be assigned damage in a speciﬁc way that is exclusionary, then the assigning player chooses only one of those abilities to apply when assigning damage. Example: Caitlyn, Patrolling ("I must be assigned combat damage last.") has been given the Tank ability ("I must be assigned combat damage ﬁrst."). A player is assigning damage to this Caitlyn with Tank and two units with no abilities. That player can’t fulﬁll both of Caitlyn’s damage requirements, so they may choose to assign damage to Caitlyn ﬁrst, fulﬁlling the Tank requirement, or last, fulﬁlling Caitlyn’s printed requirement. They can’t choose to apply damage to Caitlyn in between the other two units, because that wouldn’t fulﬁll either requirement. 

#### rule 460.2.c.8
**460.2.c.8.** If there is more than one unit in which this situation applies to, each unit is dealt with individually. The assigning player chooses which ability or effect applies, and then resolves the assignment. If this creates a situation where now more than one unit must be assigned with the same priority, those units may be assigned damage in any order as normal within that priority.   Example: Two copies of Caitlyn, Patrolling ("I must be assigned combat damage last.") have been given the Tank ability ("I must be assigned combat damage ﬁrst."). A player assigning damage to these two Caitlyns and one unit with no abilities could choose to fulﬁll both Caitlyns’ Tank requirements by assigning them both damage before the other unit. 

#### rule 460.2.c.9
**460.2.c.9.** If a unit cannot be dealt damage, then no amount of damage can be considered lethal. Such a unit is exempt from any considerations of mandatory assignment.   Example: Kayn, Unleashed says “If I have moved twice this turn, I don't take damage.” While Kayn can’t take damage, it is ignored for the purposes of assigning lethal damage in combat. 

#### rule 460.2.d
**460.2.d.** Deal [[#damage|Damage ]]to each unit equal to the amount assigned to it. 

#### rule 460.3
**460.3.** 2. Skip the [[#fepr|FEPR ]]process and proceed to the [[#resolution|Resolution Step. ]]

### rule 461
**461.** [[#step 3: the resolution step|Step 3: The Resolution Step ]]

#### rule 461.1
**461.1.** 1. Perform a [[#combat cleanup|Combat Cleanup. ]]

#### rule 461.1.a
**461.1.a.** Invoke a [[#combat special cleanup|Combat Special Cleanup. ]]

#### rule 461.1.a.1
**461.1.a.1.** Insert “3c. [[#healed|Heal  ]]all [[#unit|Units.]]” 

#### rule 461.1.a.2
**461.1.a.2.** Insert “3d. Recall [[#attacker|Attackers ]]present at the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]if [[#defender|Defenders ]]are still present.” See [[##rule 449|rule 449.]] [[#recalls|Recalls]] for more information. 

#### rule 461.2
**461.2.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding: ]]

#### rule 461.3
**461.3.** 1. Determine Combat Result 

#### rule 461.3.a
**461.3.a.** A [[#player|Player ]]has won a combat if they received either the attacker or defender designation and are the only [[#player|Player ]]that has units remaining at this battleﬁeld during this step. 

#### rule 461.3.b
**461.3.b.** A [[#player|Player ]]has lost a combat if they received either the attacker or defender designation and are the only [[#player|Player ]]that does not have any units remaining at this battleﬁeld during this step. 

#### rule 461.3.c
**461.3.c.** [[#unit|Units ]]at this battleﬁeld inherit the same combat result as their controllers 

#### rule 461.3.d
**461.3.d.** There is “No Result” if either both [[#player|Players ]]have [[#unit|units ]]present during this step, or neither player has [[#unit|units ]]present during this step. 

#### rule 461.3.d.1
**461.3.d.1.** If “No Result” was reached, and both players have [[#unit|units ]]remaining, stage a [[#combat|Combat ]]at this battleﬁeld.  

#### rule 461.4
**461.4.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding: ]]

#### rule 461.5
**461.5.** 1. If no Showdown or Combat is staged at this location, the player with [[#unit|Units ]]remaining here [[#establishes control|Establishes Control]]. 

#### rule 461.5.a
**461.5.a.** Clear the [[#contested status|Contested Status]]. 

#### rule 461.5.b
**461.5.b.** If there are no [[#unit|Units ]]remaining here controlled by any player, the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]becomes [[#uncontrolled|Uncontrolled. ]]

#### rule 461.5.c
**461.5.c.** Remove all [[#hide|Hidden ]]cards from this [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that do not share a controller with the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld]].  

#### rule 461.5.d
**461.5.d.** [[#establishing control|Establishing Control ]]results in a [[#conquering|Conquer ]]if that player has not yet scored this [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]this turn. See [[##rule 185|rule 185.]] [[#control|Control]] for more information on [[#control|Control.  ]]See [[##rule 464.1|rule 464.1.]]for more information on [[#conquering|Conquering. ]]

#### rule 461.5.e
**461.5.e.** This does not have to be the player that applied [[#contested|Contested ]]to the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld. ]]

#### rule 461.6
**461.6.** The following [[#task|Task ]]becomes [[#outstanding|Outstanding]]: 

#### rule 461.7
**461.7.** 1. Combat ends. 

#### rule 461.7.a
**461.7.a.** Remove Attacker and Defender Designation from all [[#unit|Units ]]and [[#player|Players]]. 

#### rule 461.7.b
**461.7.b.** All “this combat” effects expire simultaneously. 

### rule 462
**462.** [[#scoring|Scoring ]]

### rule 463
**463.** [[#scoring|Scoring ]]is the act of a [[#player|Player ]]gaining a point through the process of seizing or maintaining control over [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]]. 

#### rule 463.1
**463.1.** Every instance of [[#scoring|Scoring ]]is also an instance of [[#gaining|Gaining ]]points 

### rule 464
**464.** A player [[#scoring|Scores ]]in one of two ways: 

#### rule 464.1
**464.1.** [[#conquering|Conquer: ]]A player gains [[#control|Control ]]of a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]they did not yet [[#scoring|Score ]]this turn. 

#### rule 464.1.a
**464.1.a.** In [[#modes of play|Modes of Play ]]with teammates, [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]under the [[#control|Control ]]of a teammate during the [[#beginning phase|Beginning Phase ]]are also disqualiﬁed from being [[#scoring|Scored ]]through [[#conquering|Conquer ]]by any means. 

#### rule 464.1.b
**464.1.b.** A player will gain control of a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]after establishing [[#control|Control ]]by applying [[#contested|Contested ]]ﬁrst. 

#### rule 464.2
**464.2.** [[#holding|Hold: ]]A player maintains [[#control|Control ]]of a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]during their [[#beginning phase|Beginning Phase. ]]

### rule 465
**465.** A player may only [[#scoring|Score]], from either method, once per [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]per turn. 

### rule 466
**466.** When a player [[#scoring|Scores]], two things occur: 

#### rule 466.1
**466.1.** The player [[#gaining|Gains ]]up to one [[#point|Point]], depending on their current score. 

#### rule 466.1.a
**466.1.a.** The [[#winning point|Winning Point ]]has additional restrictions. 

#### rule 466.1.a.1
**466.1.a.1.** Notably, points [[#gaining|Gained ]]from sources that are not [[#conquering|Conquer ]]or [[#holding|Hold ]]are not beholden to these restrictions. 

#### rule 466.1.b
**466.1.b.** When a player tries to [[#gaining|Gain ]]a [[#point|Point ]]through a [[#scoring|Score]], and their current [[#point|Point Total ]]is 1 point from the [[#victory score|Victory Score ]]of the [[#mode of play|Mode of Play ]]or higher, the following occurs: 

#### rule 466.1.b.1
**466.1.b.1.** If the player has [[#scoring|Scored ]]through [[#holding|Hold]], that player [[#gaining|Gains ]]the [[#winning point|Winning Point. ]]

#### rule 466.1.b.2
**466.1.b.2.** If the player has [[#scoring|Scored ]]through a [[#conquering|Conquer ]]and has [[#scoring|Scored ]]every [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]through either method this turn, that player [[#gaining|Gains ]]the [[#winning point|Winning Point. ]]If the player has [[#scoring|Scored ]]through a [[#conquering|Conquer ]]and has not [[#scoring|Scored ]]every [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]this turn, that player draws a card. 

#### rule 466.2
**466.2.** Trigger [[#score abilities|Score abilities ]]at the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that [[#scoring|Scored. ]]

#### rule 466.2.a
**466.2.a.** [[#conquer abilities|Conquer abilities ]]trigger at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that was [[#conquering|Conquered. ]]

#### rule 466.2.b
**466.2.b.** [[#hold abilities|Hold abilities ]]trigger at a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]that was [[#held|Held. ]]

#### rule 466.2.c
**466.2.c.** These will only trigger when the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]is [[#scoring|Scored; ]]I.E. These cannot be triggered more than once per turn for a player. 

### rule 467
**467.** When a cleanup occurs and a player has accrued [[#point|Points ]]greater than or equal to the [[#victory score|Victory Score ]]for their [[#mode of play|Mode of Play, ]]and if they have more points than any opponent, they [[#win the game|Win the Game]]. 

### rule 468
**468.** [[#layers|Layers ]]

### rule 469
**469.** Layers are the mechanism in which [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]alter the Traits, Intrinsic Abilities, or other properties of [[#game object|Game Objects. ]]

### rule 470
**470.** Layers are an organizational structure. 

#### rule 470.1
**470.1.** Layers only serve to structure the application and order that [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]apply to [[#game object|Game Objects ]]to maintain consistency. 

### rule 471
**471.** The layers are applied [[#repeatedly|repeatedly ]]until [[#all effects operating on objects have been applied once|all effects operating on objects have been applied once ]]and [[#no changes have been processed|no changes have been processed. ]]

#### rule 471.1
**471.1.** Layers are applied in sequence. Each effect in them is applied as soon as able, and only a single time across all sequences. 

#### rule 471.2
**471.2.** When a sequence of applications completes, recur the process, and evaluate each layer again applying any effects that may now be applicable. 

#### rule 471.3
**471.3.** The removal or disqualiﬁcation of an effect is separate from the application of the effect, but still can only be applied once.  Example: Fiora, Victorious has printed Might 4 and says “While I'm Mighty, I have Deflect, Ganking, and Shield.” If a player places a buff on Fiora, her Might is increased in the Arithmetic layer, after the layer for Ability-Altering Effects. The Ability-Altering Effect layer is then re-checked and the abilities Deflect, Ganking, and Shield applied. Since each effect has been applied once and there are no other effects to apply, Fiora’s characteristics are ﬁnalized as 5 Might with Deflect, Ganking, and Shield. While a buffed Fiora, Victorious is in combat as a defender, an additional +1 Might will be applied in the Arithmetic layer, giving her 6 Might and the 3 keywords.  Example: A buffed Fiora, Victorious is in combat as a defender when her buff is removed. Reevaluating the layers in sequence, she no longer gains Deflect, Ganking, and Shield during the Ability-Altering Effect layer, so when the Arithmetic layer is evaluated, neither the buff (which is gone) nor Shield (which she no longer has) apply. She goes directly from 6 Might with three keywords to 4 Might with no keywords. 

### rule 472
**472.** Layers are applied in the following order: 

#### rule 472.1
**472.1.** 1. Trait-Altering Effects 

#### rule 472.1.a
**472.1.a.** This layer deals with effects that grant, remove, or replace inherent traits of [[#game object|Game Objects.  ]]Name Super Type Type Tags Controller Cost Domain 

#### rule 472.1.a.1
**472.1.a.1.** Assignment of Might is dealt with in this layer.  Example: A spell reads "A unit's Might becomes 4 this turn." The unit's Might is set to 4 in this layer. 

#### rule 472.1.b
**472.1.b.** Copy effects are applied in this layer. 

#### rule 472.1.b.1
**472.1.b.1.** When one [[#game object|Game Object ]]becomes a copy of another, all Traits, including the Rules Text, replace or are added to those of the original [[#game object|Game Object ]]as speciﬁed by the [[#game effects|Game Effect ]]directing the Copy. This is applied in this layer. 

#### rule 472.1.b.2
**472.1.b.2.** Some [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]may specify copying certain traits of a card - only the traits speciﬁed by the [[#game effects|Game Effect ]]will be copied. 

#### rule 472.1.b.3
**472.1.b.3.** Copy effects will copy the copyable traits of a [[#game object|Game Object: ]]by default, those are the printed traits of the [[#game object|Game Object]]. When a [[#game object|Game Object ]]becomes a copy of something, its copyable traits are updated to the new traits it has received. Example: A player triggers Leblanc, Deceiver’s hold effect and plays a Reflection token, making it a copy of Honest Broker. That player then plays Mirror Image, targeting the Reflection token. When the Mirror Image Reflection token is played, it copies all of the copyable traits of the original Reflection token - which are currently those of Honest Broker which it is a copy of. That player will have three units named Honest Broker in play, two of which are token Copies with Temporary. 

#### rule 472.1.c
**472.1.c.** Effects for this layer can be identiﬁed by the phrase "become(s)", "give," "is," or "are" in the text.  Example: A permanent has the ability "Other friendly units are Yordles." Other friendly units gain the Yordle tag in this layer. 

#### rule 472.2
**472.2.** 2. Ability-Altering Effects 

#### rule 472.2.a
**472.2.a.** This layer deals with effects that grant, remove, or replace the abilities or rules text of [[#game object|Game Objects]].  Keywords Passive Abilities Appending rules text Removing rules text Duplicating Rules Text from one [[#game object|Game Object ]]to another 

#### rule 472.2.b
**472.2.b.** Effects for this layer can be identiﬁed by the phrase "become(s)," "give," "lose(s)," "have," "has," "is," or "are" in the text.  Example: A permanent has the ability "Other friendly units have [Vision]." Other friendly units gain the [[#vision|Vision ]]keyword in this layer. 

#### rule 472.2.c
**472.2.c.** [[#abilities|Abilities ]]of [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]of [[#attached|Attached ]]cards are appended in this layer. 

#### rule 472.3
**472.3.** 3. Arithmetic 

#### rule 472.3.a
**472.3.a.** This layer deals with the mathematics of increasing and decreasing the numeric values of the traits of [[#game object|Game Objects.  ]]Might Energy Cost Power Cost 

#### rule 472.3.b
**472.3.b.** When an arithmetic effect has a limitation that applies, it is limited at the time of its application, and is “remembered” at that limited level for the duration of its effect. This process is called “snapshotting.”  Example: If an effect gives a unit “-4 [M] to a min of 1 this turn” choosing a unit with 2 [M], then the effect will generate -1 [M] this turn. 

#### rule 472.3.c
**472.3.c.** [[#might bonus|Might Bonuses ]]of [[#attached|Attached ]]cards are applied in this layer. 

#### rule 472.3.d
**472.3.d.** This layer applies arithmetic in the following way. 

#### rule 472.3.d.1
**472.3.d.1.** 1. Increases 

#### rule 472.3.d.1.a
**472.3.d.1.a.** Positive values, or increases, to Might are applied ﬁrst. 

#### rule 472.3.d.1.b
**472.3.d.1.b.** If there is a restriction or limitation to this increase, the limitation is “snapshotted” for the duration of the effect. 

#### rule 472.3.d.2
**472.3.d.2.** 2. Decreases 

#### rule 472.3.d.2.a
**472.3.d.2.a.** Negative values, or decreases, to Might are applied last. 

#### rule 472.3.d.2.b
**472.3.d.2.b.** If there is a restriction or limitation to this decrease, the limitation is snapshotted for the duration of the effect. 

### rule 473
**473.** If more than one effect applies to the same [[#game object|Game Object ]]in the [[#same layer|Same Layer]], or to each other in the same layer, then both effects will apply but their order may be determined by [[#dependency|Dependency. ]]

#### rule 473.1
**473.1.** A [[#dependency|Dependency ]]is established if: 

#### rule 473.1.a
**473.1.a.** Applying one of the effects alters the existence of the other; or 

#### rule 473.1.b
**473.1.b.** Applying one of the effects alters the number of objects the other effect can influence 

#### rule 473.1.c
**473.1.c.** Applying one of the effects alters the outcome when applying the other. 

### rule 474
**474.** To determine which effect [[#depends on|Depends on ]]another, determine which of the prior criteria applies, and then also which effect’s evaluation is altered by the sequence of applications. That effect is said to [[#depend on|Depend on ]]the other. 

#### rule 474.1
**474.1.** To resolve a dependency, the effects within the same layer that created the dependency must be applied such that:  1. Identify which effect [[#depends on|Depends on ]]the other within the Layer.  2. Apply the effect that is depended on ﬁrst.  3. Immediately apply the effect that Depends on the ﬁrst effect next. 

### rule 475
**475.** If more than one effect applies in the same layer but no dependency is established, then [[#timestamp|Timestamp ]]order is applied to the effects within that layer and sublayer 

#### rule 475.1
**475.1.** When an effect begins applying, it establishes a time for which it is compared against other Game Effects for purposes of resolving Layered effects as its [[#timestamp|Timestamp. ]]

#### rule 475.1.a
**475.1.a.** [[#timestamp|Timestamps ]]are not rote values. 

#### rule 475.1.b
**475.1.b.** [[#timestamp|Timestamps ]]are relative comparisons between effects and when they began applying to the game. 

#### rule 475.1.c
**475.1.c.** [[#timestamp|Timestamps ]]are not referenced by Game Effects in any way. They are only used to ﬁnalize layered effects. 

#### rule 475.2
**475.2.** When [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]becomes [[#inactive|Inactive ]]for any reason, it loses its [[#timestamp|Timestamp. ]]When it ceases to be [[#inactive|Inactive, ]]a new [[#timestamp|Timestamp ]]is established. 

#### rule 475.3
**475.3.** Effects are applied such that the earliest [[#timestamp|Timestamp ]]within each Layer and Sublayer applies ﬁrst, followed by other Effects in that Layer and Sublayer in chronological order. 

### rule 476
**476.** [[#modes of play|Modes of Play ]]

### rule 477
**477.** There are multiple methods of playing [[#riftbound|Riftbound. ]]

### rule 478
**478.** A [[#mode of play|Mode of Play ]]must deﬁne several variables for the game. 

#### rule 478.1
**478.1.** [[#number of players|Number of Players]]: How many people are playing the game. 

#### rule 478.2
**478.2.** [[#formation of players|Formation of Players]]: How the players are organized while playing. 

#### rule 478.2.a
**478.2.a.** This deﬁnes if a player is alone or on a team. 

#### rule 478.2.b
**478.2.b.** This deﬁnes the number of opponents. 

#### rule 478.3
**478.3.** [[#victory score|Victory Score: ]]The point total a player or team must reach to win. 

#### rule 478.3.a
**478.3.a.** [[#victory score|Victory Scores ]]can be any positive number. 

#### rule 478.4
**478.4.** [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld Count: ]]Determines how many [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]are in play, contributed by players, during play. 

#### rule 478.4.a
**478.4.a.** This may influence deck building requirements in competitive settings. 

#### rule 478.4.b
**478.4.b.** This may involve utilizing less [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]than there are players. 

#### rule 478.5
**478.5.** [[#setup|Setup: ]]Any changes to initial setup required for this mode. 

#### rule 478.6
**478.6.** [[#format|Format: ]]Conditions to win or additional rules added over play. 

#### rule 478.7
**478.7.** [[#first turn process|First Turn Process: ]]Adjustments to each player's ﬁrst turn. 

#### rule 478.8
**478.8.** [[#unique rules|Unique Rules ]]

#### rule 478.8.a
**478.8.a.** If any, they will be appended here. 

### rule 479
**479.** Sanctioned Modes 

### rule 480
**480.** 1v1 (Duel) 

#### rule 480.1
**480.1.** 2 Players 

#### rule 480.2
**480.2.** 1v1 1 opponent each No teams 

#### rule 480.3
**480.3.** [[#victory score|Victory Score: ]]8 

#### rule 480.4
**480.4.** [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld Count: ]]2 

#### rule 480.4.a
**480.4.a.** Each player provides three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]], included in their deck during deck building. Only 1 will be used, chosen during setup. 

#### rule 480.5
**480.5.** [[#setup|Setup: ]]Each player randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]]. The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]are placed simultaneously in [[#battleﬁelds|the Battleﬁeld Zone. ]]

#### rule 480.6
**480.6.** [[#format|Format: ]]Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the [[#victory score|Victory Score ]]in [[#point|Points ]]wins the [[#match|Match. ]]

#### rule 480.7
**480.7.** [[#first turn process|First Turn Process: ]]The player going second channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst [[#channel phase|Channel Phase ]]of the game. 

### rule 481
**481.** 1v1 (Match) 

#### rule 481.1
**481.1.** 2 Players 

#### rule 481.2
**481.2.** 1v1  1 opponent each  No teams 

#### rule 481.3
**481.3.** [[#victory score|Victory Score: ]]8 

#### rule 481.4
**481.4.** [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld Count: ]]2 

#### rule 481.4.a
**481.4.a.** Each player provides three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]], included in their deck during deck building. Only 1 will be used, chosen during setup. 

#### rule 481.5
**481.5.** [[#setup|Setup: ]]Each player selects one (1) of their three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]]. The other two are set aside and will not be used for this round of play. The selected [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]are placed simultaneously in [[#battleﬁelds|the Battleﬁeld Zone]]. After this game, the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]that were used are to be removed and not selected again for this [[#match|Match]]. One of the remaining [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]that were set aside must be chosen instead. 

#### rule 481.6
**481.6.** [[#format|Format: ]]Best of 3. The ﬁrst player to reach the [[#victory score|Victory Score ]]in [[#point|Points ]]wins the game. The winner of that game earns [[#one game win|One Game Win. ]]Players then reset the game state, remove the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]in play from the game, choose new [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]from those set aside, and play again. The ﬁrst player to earn [[#two game wins|Two Game Wins ]]wins the match. 

#### rule 481.7
**481.7.** [[#first turn process|First Turn Process: ]]The player going second channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst [[#channel phase|Channel Phase ]]of the game. 

### rule 482
**482.** FFA3 (Skirmish) 

#### rule 482.1
**482.1.** 3 Players 

#### rule 482.2
**482.2.** FFA  2 opponents each  No teams 

#### rule 482.3
**482.3.** [[#victory score|Victory Score: ]]8 

#### rule 482.4
**482.4.** [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld Count: ]]3 

#### rule 482.4.a
**482.4.a.** Each player provides three (3) Battleﬁelds, included in their deck during deck building. Only 1 will be used, chosen during setup. 

#### rule 482.5
**482.5.** [[#setup|Setup: ]]Each player randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]]. The other two are discarded and will not be used for this game. The selected [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]are placed simultaneously between the three Players before play and will be used for this game. 

#### rule 482.6
**482.6.** [[#format|Format: ]]Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the [[#victory score|Victory Score ]]in [[#point|Points ]]wins the [[#match|Match. ]]

#### rule 482.7
**482.7.** [[#first turn process|First Turn Process: ]]The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst [[#drawn|Draw Phase ]]of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst [[#channel phase|Channel Phase ]]of the game. 

### rule 483
**483.** FFA4 (War) 

#### rule 483.1
**483.1.** 4 Players 

#### rule 483.2
**483.2.** FFA  3 opponents each  No teams 

#### rule 483.3
**483.3.** [[#victory score|Victory Score: ]]8 

#### rule 483.4
**483.4.** [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld Count: ]]3 

#### rule 483.4.a
**483.4.a.** Each player provides three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]], included in their deck during deck building. 

#### rule 483.4.b
**483.4.b.** The player who is taking the ﬁrst turn removes their [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds. ]]They will not be used. 

#### rule 483.5
**483.5.** [[#setup|Setup: ]]Each player who is not going ﬁrst randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]]. The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]are placed simultaneously between the players before play and will be used for this game. 

#### rule 483.6
**483.6.** [[#format|Format: ]]Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the [[#victory score|Victory Score ]]in [[#point|Points ]]wins the [[#match|Match. ]]

#### rule 483.7
**483.7.** [[#first turn process|First Turn Process: ]]The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst [[#drawn|Draw Phase ]]of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst [[#channel phase|Channel Phase ]]of the game. 

### rule 484
**484.** 2v2 (Magma Chamber) 

#### rule 484.1
**484.1.** 4 Players 

#### rule 484.2
**484.2.** 2v2  2 opponents each  1 teammate 

#### rule 484.3
**484.3.** [[#victory score|Victory Score: ]]11 

#### rule 484.4
**484.4.** [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld Count: ]]3 

#### rule 484.4.a
**484.4.a.** Each player provides three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]], included in their deck during deck building. 

#### rule 484.5
**484.5.** [[#setup|Setup: ]]

#### rule 484.5.a
**484.5.a.** Each player who is not going ﬁrst randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds]]. The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]are placed simultaneously between the players before play and will be used for this game. 

#### rule 484.5.b
**484.5.b.** The player who is taking the ﬁrst turn removes their [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds. ]]They will not be used. 

#### rule 484.5.c
**484.5.c.** Turn order alternates teams. 

#### rule 484.5.c.1
**484.5.c.1.** The ﬁrst player will be followed by an opponent, then the ﬁrst player's teammate, then the ﬁrst opponent's teammate, and so on. 

#### rule 484.5.c.2
**484.5.c.2.** If allies are sitting across from each other, turn order proceeds clockwise as normal. 

#### rule 484.5.c.3
**484.5.c.3.** If allies are sitting next to each other, turn order is passed across the table. 

#### rule 484.6
**484.6.** [[#format|Format: ]]Best of 1. The ﬁrst team to reach the [[#victory score|Victory Score ]]in [[#point|Points ]]wins the [[#match|Match. ]]

#### rule 484.6.a
**484.6.a.** Teammates win or lose together. 

#### rule 484.6.a.1
**484.6.a.1.** If one player [[#concedes|Concedes]], then the entire team loses. 

#### rule 484.6.a.2
**484.6.a.2.** If one player [[#loses|Loses, ]]then the entire team loses. 

#### rule 484.6.a.3
**484.6.a.3.** If one player [[#wins|Wins]], then the entire team wins. 

#### rule 484.7
**484.7.** [[#first turn process|First Turn Process: ]]The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst [[#drawn|Draw Phase ]]of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst [[#channel phase|Channel Phase ]]of the game. 

#### rule 484.8
**484.8.** [[#unique rules|Unique Rules ]]

#### rule 484.8.a
**484.8.a.** Players may play spells or activate abilities during their [[#teams|Teammate's ]][[#turn order|Turn.]]In order to do so, their [[#teams|Teammate ]]will invite them to play a spell or activate an ability using their own [[#priority|Priority. ]]

#### rule 484.8.b
**484.8.b.** [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]controlled during the [[#beginning phase|Beginning Phase ]]of a player's turn by that player's teammate are [[#disqualiﬁed from being scored|disqualiﬁed from being scored ]]by that Team, that turn. Example: A player may not induce their partner to retreat, and then conquer a [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]their teammate was controlling. 

#### rule 484.8.c
**484.8.c.** [[#control|Control ]]is not shared. 

#### rule 484.8.c.1
**484.8.c.1.** Players may not [[#hide|Hide ]]cards at [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds ]]controlled by their Teammate. 

#### rule 484.8.c.2
**484.8.c.2.** Players may not issue [[#standard move|Standard Movement ]]to their Teammate's [[#unit|Units. ]]

#### rule 484.8.d
**484.8.d.** [[#friendly|Friendly ]]describes controlled [[#game object|Game Objects ]]by a player or their Teammate. Example: "When I am played, ready a friendly unit" could target a player's own [[#unit|Units ]]or their teammate's [[#unit|Units. ]]

#### rule 484.8.e
**484.8.e.** Hands are [[#private information|Private Information. ]]Players may show their [[#private information|Private Information ]]to one or more players at any time during play, including their teammate. 

#### rule 484.8.e.1
**484.8.e.1.** [[#revealing cards|Revealing Cards ]]is still a game action and cannot be done unless instructed.  See [[##rule 424|rule 424.]] [[#reveal|Reveal]] for more information. 

#### rule 484.8.f
**484.8.f.** The [[#final point|Final Point ]]has an adjustment to the criteria when scoring. 

#### rule 484.8.f.1
**484.8.f.1.** When scoring the [[#final point|Final Point ]]from [[#conquering|Conquer]], a player must [[#scoring|Score ]]each [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]in the same turn, excepting any that were occupied by their ally during that turn’s [[#beginning phase|Beginning Phase]]. 

#### rule 484.8.f.2
**484.8.f.2.** No other changes to [[#final point|Final Point ]]restrictions. 

#### rule 484.8.g
**484.8.g.** Teammates may not utilize the same [[#champion legend|Champion Legend. ]]

#### rule 484.8.h
**484.8.h.** Teammates may not utilize the same [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁelds. ]]

### rule 649
**649.** [[#concedes|Conceding ]]

### rule 650
**650.** A player may concede at any time. 

### rule 651
**651.** When a player concedes, they are removed from the game in progress. 

#### rule 651.1
**651.1.** If only one other player is remaining after a player has conceded, the player remaining [[#wins|Wins. ]]

#### rule 651.2
**651.2.** If more than one player remains after a concession, follow the steps for the [[#removal of a player|Removal of a Player. ]]

#### rule 651.3
**651.3.** Removal of a player involves them no longer being able to make choices or otherwise influence the game. 

#### rule 651.4
**651.4.** If the player has [[#teams|Teammates ]]due to the [[#mode of play|Mode of Play]], that player’s [[#teams|Teammates ]]also lose and are removed from the game. 

### rule 652
**652.** If the game continues, follow these steps for [[#removal of a player|Removal of a Player. ]]

#### rule 652.1
**652.1.** [[#banishing|Banish ]]all permanents, runes, and facedown cards they currently control and all permanents, runes, and facedown cards they own.  

#### rule 652.2
**652.2.** Remove the [[#battleﬁelds|Battleﬁeld ]]they contributed to the game if it is in use. 

#### rule 652.2.a
**652.2.a.** If it was in use, [[#replace|Replace ]]it with a token battleﬁeld with no abilities. 

#### rule 652.2.b
**652.2.b.** Any units or hidden cards there do not move and are otherwise unaffected by this process. See [[##rule 438|rule 438.]] [[#replace|Replace]] for more information. 

#### rule 652.2.c
**652.2.c.** If the removed battleﬁeld was applying any continuous effects, those continuous effects immediately cease, which may cause changes in the characteristics of units or hidden cards there.  Example: A battleﬁeld reads "Units here have +1 [M]." If that battleﬁeld's owner concedes and the battleﬁeld is removed from the game as a result, units there immediately cease to get +1 [M]. 

#### rule 652.3
**652.3.** Remove all cards they own from the game. 

#### rule 652.4
**652.4.** [[#countered|Counter ]]all spells and abilities of all types controlled by the player that has conceded. 

#### rule 652.5
**652.5.** Proceed with the game. 

#### rule 652.5.a
**652.5.a.** Turn 

#### rule 652.5.a.1
**652.5.a.1.** If the removed player was the [[#turn player|Turn Player]], play proceeds in [[#turn order|Turn Order ]]to the next available player in order. 

#### rule 652.5.b
**652.5.b.** Focus 

#### rule 652.5.b.1
**652.5.b.1.** If the removed player had [[#focus|Focus ]]in a [[#showdown|Showdown]], the next [[#player|Player ]]in order receives [[#focus|Focus]]. 

#### rule 652.5.b.2
**652.5.b.2.** If the player being removed creates a state where all [[#player|Players ]]have [[#passive|Passed ]]their [[#focus|Focus]], the [[#showdown|Showdown ]]ends and play proceeds as necessary, E.G. [[#combat|Combat ]]is resolved or a [[#cleanup|Cleanup ]]is completed. 

#### rule 652.5.c
**652.5.c.** Priority 

#### rule 652.5.c.1
**652.5.c.1.** If the removed player had [[#priority|Priority ]]during a [[#chain|Chain]], the next [[#player|Player ]]in order receives [[#priority|Priority]]. 

#### rule 652.5.c.2
**652.5.c.2.** If the player being removed creates a state where all [[#player|Players ]]have passed [[#priority|Priority]], then the most recent spell or ability on the [[#chain|Chain ]]will resolve with [[#priority|Priority ]]being re-established as appropriate for the state after the resolution of that spell or ability. 

## rule 700
**700.** Additional Rules 

### rule 701
**701.** [[#buffed|Buffs ]]

### rule 702
**702.** [[#buffed|Buffs ]]are objects placed on [[#unit|Units. ]]

#### rule 702.1
**702.1.** [[#buffed|Buffs ]]can be tracked with a buff reminder card from a [[#riftbound|Riftbound ]]booster pack or with any spare object in your surroundings. 

#### rule 702.2
**702.2.** [[#buffed|Buffs ]]can be added or spent. 

#### rule 702.2.a
**702.2.a.** To [[#buffed|Buff ]]a [[#unit|Unit]], a player chooses a [[#unit|Unit ]]and then places a buff on it. That [[#unit|Unit ]]is [[#buffed|Buffed ]]for as long as the buff remains on it. 

#### rule 702.2.b
**702.2.b.** [[#spending|Spending ]]a [[#buffed|Buff ]]removes a single [[#buffed|Buff ]]counter from a [[#unit|Unit]]. 

#### rule 702.2.b.1
**702.2.b.1.** A buff cannot be spent from a [[#unit|Unit ]]that does not have a buff. 

#### rule 702.2.b.2
**702.2.b.2.** A player can only spend buffs on units they control. 

#### rule 702.3
**702.3.** There can only be one [[#buffed|Buff ]]on a [[#unit|Unit ]]at a time. 

#### rule 702.3.a
**702.3.a.** If a [[#buffed|Buff ]]is added, or instructed to be added, on a [[#unit|Unit ]]that already has a [[#buffed|Buff]], it is not placed instead. 

### rule 703
**703.** Each [[#buffed|Buff ]]individually contributes +1 [[#might|Might ]]to a [[#unit|Unit. ]]

### rule 704
**704.** [[#buffed|Buffs ]]are [[#game object|Game Objects ]]and may be referenced, counted, or targeted by other effects as speciﬁed. 

### rule 705
**705.** If a [[#unit|Unit ]]leaves play, remove all [[#buffed|Buffs ]]from it. 

#### rule 705.1
**705.1.** [[#champion tags|Champions ]]do not retain [[#buffed|Buffs ]]in the Champion Zone, even if they return there somehow. 

### rule 706
**706.** [[#might|Mighty ]]

### rule 707
**707.** [[#might|Mighty ]]is a description that applies to some units. Other game effects can check whether a unit is [[#might|Mighty. ]]

### rule 708
**708.** A [[#unit|Unit ]]"is Mighty" as long as its Might is 5 or greater. 

### rule 709
**709.** A [[#unit|Unit ]]"becomes Mighty" at the moment its Might changes from being less than 5 to being 5 or greater.  Example: A Unit with Might 4 that gets +1 [M] becomes [[#might|Mighty]].  Example: A Unit with Might 5 that gets +1 [M] does not become [[#might|Mighty]], because it was already [[#might|Mighty. ]]

### rule 710
**710.** Units on the board are evaluated according to their current Might.  Example: A unit with a base Might of 3 is targeted by a spell that reads "A unit gets +3 [M] this turn." As that spell resolves, its Might changes from 3 to 6, and it becomes [[#might|Mighty]]. When that effect expires at the end of the turn, it will no longer be [[#might|Mighty. ]]

### rule 711
**711.** Units in [[#non-board zones|Non-Board Zones ]]are evaluated according to their inherent Might.  Example: A unit in the trash is [[#might|Mighty ]]if its printed Might is 5 or greater. It doesn't matter if there were effects raising or lowering its might while it was on the board. 

### rule 712
**712.** [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]

### rule 713
**713.** [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]is an intrinsic property that can be granted to [[#dealt|Deal ]]actions that influence the amount of [[#damage|Damage ]]that the action is distributing. 

### rule 714
**714.** If more than one instance of [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]is applied or granted to a [[#dealt|Deal ]]action, all instances are summed and applied once. 

#### rule 714.1
**714.1.** Bonus Damage can only be a positive value, and can only increase the amount of [[#damage|Damage ]]being distributed. 

#### rule 714.2
**714.2.** If, for any reason, [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]would be a negative number, then no [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]is applied to the action. 

### rule 715
**715.** Bonus Damage applies to the total damage [[#dealt|Dealt ]]by one instance of the action. 

#### rule 715.1
**715.1.** If the [[#dealt|Deal ]]action has a single target, the amount of [[#damage|Damage ]]to that target will be increased by the [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]granted to it. 

#### rule 715.2
**715.2.** If the [[#dealt|Deal ]]action has multiple targets, the amount of [[#damage|Damage ]]dealt to each target is increased by [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]individually and separately.  Example: Singularity is a spell that says “Deal 6 to each of up to two units.” A player plays Singularity while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Singularity deals 1 Bonus Damage to both of its targets, dealing 7 to each. 

#### rule 715.3
**715.3.** If the [[#dealt|Deal ]]action [[#splitting|Splits ]]damage, then the [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]applies to the amount of [[#damage|Damage ]]that will be [[#splitting|Split]]. This can alter the number of targets eligible to be chosen.  Example: Volibear, Furious is a unit that says in part “When I attack, deal 5 damage split among any number of enemy units here.” A player attacks with Volibear, Furious while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Volibear, Furious now deals 6 damage split among any number of enemy units at its location, and can choose to split that damage among up to 6 units rather than the usual 5. 

#### rule 715.4
**715.4.** If no damage was [[#dealt|Dealt, ]]because it was replaced or reduced by any means, then [[#bonus damage|Bonus Damage ]]will not apply. 

### rule 716
**716.** [[#attachment|Attachment ]]

### rule 717
**717.** [[#attached|Attaching ]]is a limited action that causes cards to become linked to each other to combine their effects in some way. This causes one card to become [[#attached|Attached ]]and the other to become [[#a top-most card|A Top-Most Card. ]]See [[##rule 434|rule 434.]] [[#attached|Attach]] for more information. 

### rule 718
**718.** [[#attached|Attached ]]is the state of a card being linked to another card in this way. 

#### rule 718.1
**718.1.** A card remains in this state until [[#detach|Detached. ]]

#### rule 718.2
**718.2.** While in this state, the card’s printed [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]is [[#inactive|Inactive. ]]See [[##rule 720|rule 720.]] [[#inactive|Inactive]] for more information. 

#### rule 718.3
**718.3.** While in this state, [[#abilities|Abilities ]]in the card’s [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]are appended to the [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]of the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card. ]]

#### rule 718.4
**718.4.** While in this state, the card’s [[#might bonus|Might Bonus ]]modulates the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card]]’s [[#might|Might ]]by the value listed. 

#### rule 718.5
**718.5.** [[#attached|Attached ]]cards still have all properties of being a card on the board while in this state. 

#### rule 718.5.a
**718.5.a.** [[#attached|Attached ]]cards still have all [[#type|Types ]]and [[#tags|Tags ]]while [[#attached|Attached. ]]

#### rule 718.5.b
**718.5.b.** [[#attached|Attached ]]cards still can be chosen or targeted by game effects while [[#attached|Attached. ]]

#### rule 718.5.c
**718.5.c.** [[#attached|Attached ]]cards cannot be moved separately from the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]they are [[#attached|Attached ]]to. 

#### rule 718.5.d
**718.5.d.** A card may be [[#attached|Attached ]]only to a single [[#top-most card|Top-Most card ]]at a time. 

#### rule 718.5.e
**718.5.e.** [[#attached|Attached ]]cards may have different [[#control|Controllers ]]from their [[#top-most card|Top-Most card.  ]]

#### rule 718.5.f
**718.5.f.** Changes in [[#control|Control ]]of the [[#top-most card|Top-Most card ]]do not impact [[#control|Control ]]of [[#attached|Attached ]]cards and vice versa. 

#### rule 718.5.g
**718.5.g.** An [[#attached|Attached ]]card still appends the abilities in its [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]to the [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]of the [[#top-most card|Top-Most card ]]and modulates the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card]]’s [[#might|Might ]]by its [[#might bonus|Might Bonus. ]]

### rule 719
**719.** A [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]is a card that has one or more cards linked to it through the process of [[#attached|Attaching. ]]

#### rule 719.1
**719.1.** The [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]of all cards [[#attached|Attached ]]to this card are appended to the [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]of this card for as long as they remain [[#attached|Attached. ]]

#### rule 719.2
**719.2.** This card ceases being a [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]when there are no longer any cards [[#attached|Attached ]]to it. 

#### rule 719.3
**719.3.** A [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]and all cards [[#attached|Attached ]]to it are at the same location. 

#### rule 719.3.a
**719.3.a.** When the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]moves, all [[#attached|Attached ]]cards move with it. 

#### rule 719.4
**719.4.** The [[#exhausted|Exhausted ]]and [[#ready|Ready ]]state of the [[#top-most card|Top-Most ]]card does not affect nor change the status of the [[#attached|Attached ]]cards and vice versa. 

#### rule 719.5
**719.5.** When a [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]changes zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, all [[#attached|Attached ]]cards [[#detach|Detach ]]from it, remaining in their current zones. 

#### rule 719.5.a
**719.5.a.** The player that controls the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]that changed zones decides the order these cards [[#detach|Detach ]]in, and thus the order of any relevant effects that occur due to the [[#detach|Detach ]]occurring. 

### rule 720
**720.** [[#inactive|Inactive ]]

### rule 721
**721.** Card text can occasionally be assigned to be ignored, disregarded, or otherwise rendered as not applicable during the course of play. This state is referred to as [[#inactive|Inactive. ]]

#### rule 721.1
**721.1.** Text marked this way is not applied at all while in this state. 

#### rule 721.2
**721.2.** [[#inactive|Inactive ]]Abilities do not trigger, do not apply, and cannot be activated. [[#inactive|Inactive ]]instructions are not processed. 

### rule 722
**722.** [[#inactive|Inactive ]]text is still present on cards. 

#### rule 722.1
**722.1.** Cards with [[#inactive|Inactive ]]text still have keywords for the sake of Game Effects that want to reference or see if a card has a keyword. 

#### rule 722.2
**722.2.** Game Effects that parse or interpret text to determine target eligibility may still parse [[#inactive|Inactive ]]text for the sake of eligibility. Example: Spinning Axe is a gear with [Temporary]. While it’s attached and its rules text is inactive, its [Temporary] ability doesn’t trigger. However, a spell that reads “Destroy a gear with [Temporary]” could still choose and destroy Spinning Axe. 

### rule 723
**723.** [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]is never [[#inactive|Inactive ]]by default. 

### rule 724
**724.** [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]is [[#inactive|Inactive ]]unless the card with the [[#effect text|Effect Text ]]is [[#attached|Attached. ]]

### rule 725
**725.** [[#inactive|Inactive ]]text can partially cease to be [[#inactive|Inactive ]]under speciﬁc circumstances and exceptions. 

#### rule 725.1
**725.1.** If an [[#attached|Attached ]]card has a [[#passive|Passive ]]or [[#replace|Replacement ]]ability that applies during the process of [[#attached|Attaching ]]or a [[#trigger|Triggered ]]ability that triggers off of [[#attached|Attaching]], that text exists and can be processed as it [[#attaches|Attaches. ]]

#### rule 725.2
**725.2.** If an [[#attached|Attached ]]card has a [[#passive|Passive ]]or [[#replace|Replacement ]]ability that applies during the process of [[#detach|Detaching ]]or a [[#trigger|Triggered ]]ability that triggers off of [[#detach|Detaching]], that text exists and can be processed as it [[#detach|Detaches. ]]

#### rule 725.3
**725.3.** If an [[#attached|Attached ]]card has an [[#equip|Equip ]]ability, the [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]keyword can reference that [[#equip|Equip ]]ability and any abilities that passively modify that [[#equip|Equip ]]ability. 

### rule 726
**726.** [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keywords ]]

### rule 727
**727.** [[#keywords|Keywords ]]can be [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keywords ]]

#### rule 727.1
**727.1.** A [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keyword ]]is comprised of both a [[#condition|Condition ]]that it is short for, and an ability of some format immediately after the [[#keywords|Keyword ]]itself. EXAMPLE: Noxus Hopeful has “[Legion][>] I cost [2] less.” [Legion] is short for the condition “if you have played another card this turn, this card gains [Text],” while “I cost [2] less” is the dependent ability. 

#### rule 727.1.a
**727.1.a.** A [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keyword ]]will always be functionally short for a [[#condition|Condition. ]]

#### rule 727.1.a.1
**727.1.a.1.** This [[#condition|Condition ]]may also have a determined [[#duration|Duration]], [[#timestamp|Time]], or [[#limitation|Limitation ]]as part of its deﬁnition. EXAMPLE: Legion speciﬁes the duration of its condition: “if you have played another card this turn.” This turn is the duration. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “Until you have spent [3] this turn” would include a limitation on its condition. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “After you’ve become an attacker this turn” would include a time after which the condition is active. 

#### rule 727.1.b
**727.1.b.** The [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability ]]associated with the [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keyword ]]is [[#inactive|Inactive ]]on the card with the [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keyword ]]until the [[#condition|Condition ]]is met, when it becomes [[#active|Active ]]

#### rule 727.1.b.1
**727.1.b.1.** The [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability ]]is present on the card for the sake of reference or evaluation until the [[#condition|Condition ]]is met See [[##rule 720|rule 720.]] [[#inactive|Inactive]] for more information 

#### rule 727.1.b.2
**727.1.b.2.** The [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability ]]is [[#active|Active ]]exactly as written while the [[#condition|Condition ]]is true Example: Gustwalker has “[Level3][>] I have +1 [M] and Ganking.” As long as its controller has 3 XP, Gustwalker’s Ganking is active. 

#### rule 727.1.c
**727.1.c.** The [[#dependent ability|Dependent Abilities ]]of [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keywords ]]can be of any type 

#### rule 727.1.c.1
**727.1.c.1.** [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]of [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keywords ]]must be [[#active|Active ]]for their trigger to be evaluated. 

#### rule 727.1.c.1.a
**727.1.c.1.a.** If a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]becomes active at the same time as its trigger condition would be fulﬁlled, it triggers. 

#### rule 727.1.c.2
**727.1.c.2.** [[#passive abilities|Passive Abilities ]]begin applying at the same time the [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keyword ]]becomes true. 

#### rule 727.1.c.3
**727.1.c.3.** [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities ]]that become [[#active|Active ]]from [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keywords ]]can be activated at their associated timing after that ability has been granted 

#### rule 727.1.c.3.a
**727.1.c.3.a.** If the condition for the [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keyword ]]causes the A[[#ctivated ability|ctivated Ability ]]to become [[#inactive|Inactive ]]after it has been added to the chain as a [[#pending item|Pending Item]], that chain item will not be affected and will proceed with being played as normal. 

### rule 728
**728.** [[#xp|XP ]]

### rule 729
**729.** [[#xp|XP ]]is a resource that is accrued, spent, or otherwise modiﬁed by [[#player|Players ]]through the course of play. 

#### rule 729.1
**729.1.** The amount of [[#xp|XP ]]that a player has should be marked clearly. 

#### rule 729.1.a
**729.1.a.** [[#xp|XP ]]is a value that can be tracked by counters, dice, cards, or any method that clearly displays the speciﬁc value of [[#xp|XP ]]that is currently on a [[#player|Player. ]]

#### rule 729.2
**729.2.** The amount of [[#xp|XP ]]a [[#player|Player ]]has is [[#public information|Public Information. ]]

### rule 730
**730.** [[#xp|XP ]]can be [[#gaining|Gained ]]and [[#spending|Spent. ]]

#### rule 730.1
**730.1.** To [[#gain xp|Gain XP]], increase the value of [[#xp|XP ]]marked on the [[#player|Player ]]gaining it. 

#### rule 730.2
**730.2.** To [[#spend xp|Spend XP]], reduce the value of [[#xp|XP ]]marked on the [[#player|Player ]]spending it. 

### rule 731
**731.** [[#xp|XP ]]is not a [[#game object|Game Object. ]]

#### rule 731.1
**731.1.** [[#xp|XP ]]cannot be targeted, readied, or exhausted. 

### rule 732
**732.** [[#xp|XP ]]is not shared between [[#allies|Allies ]]in [[#game modes|Game Modes ]]with [[#teams|Teammates. ]]

### rule 733
**733.** There is no limit to an amount of [[#xp|XP ]]a player can accrue. 

### rule 734
**734.** [[#additional turns|Additional Turns ]]

### rule 735
**735.** Certain [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]will instruct a player to “take a turn after this.” These effects create a temporary [[#additional turns|Additional Turn ]]owned by that player that is inserted into the turn queue after the current turn. 

### rule 736
**736.** Turn order is established when the game begins as a repeating set of players. This populates a looping queue of turns that each player will take, starting with the ﬁrst turn taken by the First Player, and repeating indeﬁnitely. 

### rule 737
**737.** When an [[#additional turns|Additional Turn ]]is inserted into this queue, it does not change the [[#turn order|Turn Order ]]of the game. The owner of the [[#additional turns|Additional Turn ]]just has the next queued turn. After that turn is completed, it will be removed and the queue will proceed with its previously queued turns. 

### rule 738
**738.** If multiple [[#additional turns|Additional Turns ]]are queued, they are added to the queue in the order the [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]that generated them occurred. Example: The First Player plays, through some means, two Time Warps during their turn. The Time Warps create two Additional Turns for their controller and insert them into the turn queue after the current turn. If the turn queue is represented as [> A > B > C > D >], then these Additional Turns will appear as [> A > A* > A* > B > C > D >]. After the last Additional Turn is played, the queue returns to its previously queued turns. The “*” denotes that a turn is an Additional Turn. Example: The First Player plays Promising Future during their turn, during the resolution of which the Second and Fourth Player choose, banish, and play one Time Warp each. The Fourth Player’s Time Warp resolves ﬁrst, inserting an Additional Turn for them in the queue as such: [> A > D* > B > C > D >]. The Second Player’s Time Warp resolves afterwards, inserting that turn: [> A > B* > D* > B > C > D >]. When the First Player passes the turn, the Second Player will take their turn, followed by the Fourth Player, after which the queue returns to its previously queued turns. 

### rule 739
**739.** [[#special terms|Special Terms ]]

### rule 740
**740.** Some card text refers to [[#game object|Game Objects ]]in particular ways: 

#### rule 740.1
**740.1.** Two [[#game object|Game Objects ]]are [[#friendly|friendly ]]if they share a controller, or if one’s controller is teammates with the other’s. 

#### rule 740.2
**740.2.** Two [[#game object|Game Objects ]]are [[#enemies|enemies ]]if one’s controller is an opponent of the other’s. 

### rule 741
**741.** Some card text refers to [[#unit|Units ]]in particular ways: 

#### rule 741.1
**741.1.** A unit is [[#alone|alone ]]when there are no other friendly units at the same location. 

#### rule 741.2
**741.2.** A unit is [[#one on one|one on one ]]when it and the enemy unit at the same location are both [[#alone|alone. ]]

#### rule 741.3
**741.3.** A unit is [[#in combat|in combat ]]if it is occupying a battleﬁeld where combat is ongoing and has a combat designation. 

### rule 742
**742.** Some terms in this document are used in particular ways: 

#### rule 742.1
**742.1.** [[#costs within instructions|Costs within instructions ]]are instructions that take a particular form (“[do X] to [do Y]”). [Do X] is the cost associated with the instruction, and [do Y] is the effect. 

#### rule 742.1.a
**742.1.a.** For spells, costs within instructions are paid on resolution of the spell. In order to get the effect, the cost must be paid. 

#### rule 742.1.b
**742.1.b.** For triggered abilities, costs within instructions are paid on ﬁnalization of the triggered ability. In order to place the triggered ability on the chain, the cost must be paid. 

## rule 800
**800.** [[#keywords|Keywords ]]

### rule 801
**801.** A [[#keywords|Keyword ]]is a speciﬁc term that appears on [[#card|Cards ]]that acts as a shorthand for a speciﬁc game effect, or [[#ability’s|ability ]]of any variety. 

#### rule 801.1
**801.1.** A [[#keywords|Keyword ]]can be an ability. 

#### rule 801.2
**801.2.** [[#keywords|Keywords ]]can be identiﬁed by having a [[#colored highlight|colored highlight ]]behind them. 

#### rule 801.2.a
**801.2.a.** The color of the highlight has no effect on gameplay. 

#### rule 801.3
