**801.3.** [[#keywords|Keywords ]]can be referenced or speciﬁed by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 801.3.a
**801.3.a.** Other effects may grant [[#keywords|Keywords. ]]

#### rule 801.3.a.1
**801.3.a.1.** The deﬁnition and rules of the speciﬁc [[#keywords|Keyword ]]will determine the behavior if a [[#keywords|Keyword ]]is granted while it is already present. 

#### rule 801.3.a.2
**801.3.a.2.** The effect that granted the [[#keywords|Keyword ]]will specify the duration for which it is granted. 

#### rule 801.3.a.3
**801.3.a.3.** If an effect that grants a [[#keywords|Keyword ]]does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that [[#game object|Game Object ]]remains on [[#board|the Board ]]or in its current [[#non-board zones|Non-Board Zone. ]]

#### rule 801.3.b
**801.3.b.** Other effects may remove [[#keywords|Keywords. ]]

#### rule 801.3.b.1
**801.3.b.1.** The effect that removed the [[#keywords|Keyword ]]will specify the duration it is removed. 

#### rule 801.3.b.2
**801.3.b.2.** If an effect that removes a [[#keywords|Keyword ]]does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that [[#game object|Game Object ]]remains on [[#board|the Board ]]or in its current [[#non-board zones|Non-Board Zone. ]]

### rule 802
**802.** A card can have any number of [[#keywords|Keywords. ]]

### rule 803
**803.** Similar to other rules text, execute any effects of [[#keywords|Keywords ]]in the order listed when reading the card from top to bottom of the rules text. 

### rule 804
**804.** Keyword Glossary 

### rule 805
**805.** [[#accelerate|Accelerate ]]

#### rule 805.1
**805.1.** Accelerate is a [[#unit|Unit ]]ability. 

#### rule 805.1.a
**805.1.a.** Accelerate is functionally short for "As you play me, you may pay [1] and 1 Power as an additional cost. If you do, I enter ready." 

#### rule 805.1.a.1
**805.1.a.1.** If the unit has a single domain, the Power portion of the Accelerate cost can be paid only with a Power that matches the domain of the unit. 

#### rule 805.1.a.2
**805.1.a.2.** If the unit has no domain or more than one domain, the Power portion of the Accelerate cost can be paid with [A] (a Power of any domain). 

#### rule 805.2
**805.2.** Accelerate is an [[#optional additional costs|Optional Additional Cost ]]to be paid as a player plays the unit with the ability. 

#### rule 805.2.a
**805.2.a.** Accelerate costs cannot be paid while the unit is on the board, only as part of the steps of playing a card. 

#### rule 805.3
**805.3.** Accelerate has no function while on the board. 

#### rule 805.4
**805.4.** Multiple instances of Accelerate are redundant. 

#### rule 805.5
**805.5.** Accelerate, and whether or not a unit has Accelerate, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 805.6
**805.6.** Accelerate influences the state of the unit entering the Board. It does not enter exhausted and then become ready. 

#### rule 805.6.a
**805.6.a.** Accelerate will not interact with, or trigger, abilities that are affected by units becoming ready. 

### rule 806
**806.** [[#action|Action ]]

#### rule 806.1
**806.1.** Action is a [[#permissive|Permissive ]]keyword. 

#### rule 806.1.a
**806.1.a.** It can be present on [[#cards, rune abilities, legend abilities|Cards, Rune Abilities, Legend Abilities ]]or [[#permanent abilities|Permanent Abilities. ]]

#### rule 806.1.b
**806.1.b.** Action grants the corresponding card or effect permission to be played or activated during [[#showdown|Showdowns, ]]even when it is not the Controlling player's turn. 

#### rule 806.1.c
**806.1.c.** Action is functionally short for the following: 

#### rule 806.1.c.1
**806.1.c.1.** On Cards: "This can be played during showdowns on any player's turn." 

#### rule 806.1.c.2
**806.1.c.2.** On Rune, Legend, or Permanent Abilities: "This can be activated during showdowns on any player's turn." 

#### rule 806.1.d
**806.1.d.** Action is formatted as “[Action]” on spells, or “[Action][>]” on abilities. 

#### rule 806.2
**806.2.** The card or effect with this keyword is not restricted to showdowns. This permission is inclusive of all other timings and options available to the ability as written or by default. 

#### rule 806.3
**806.3.** Action does not alter the function of any instruction of the corresponding card or effect it is on. It is only permission.  Example: Playing a [[#unit|Unit ]]with Action still has the inherent restrictions of playing [[#unit|Units ]]without Action. It can only be played to the controlling player's base or a battleﬁeld they control. 

#### rule 806.4
**806.4.** Some passive abilities may grant a card or ability Action under certain conditions. The card or ability does not have the Action keyword unless and until those circumstances are true. 

#### rule 806.4.a
**806.4.a.** Those conditions might only be fulﬁlled while the card or ability is on the chain. In such a case, it can still be played or activated at the appropriate timing as long as doing so could fulﬁll the conditions. 

#### rule 806.4.b
**806.4.b.** If the chain item does not fulﬁll the conditions by the time step 5: check legality has been reached, the actions taken while playing or activating the chain item are undone and it is returned to the zone it was played from if it is a card. 

#### rule 806.5
**806.5.** Action is a referenceable characteristic. 

#### rule 806.5.a
**806.5.a.** Whether or not a [[#game object|Game Object ]]has Action is a characteristic of that [[#game object|Game Object ]]and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 806.5.b
**806.5.b.** Whether or not a [[#spells|Spell ]]has Action is a characteristic of that [[#spells|Spell ]]and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 806.5.c
**806.5.c.** Whether or not an [[#ability’s|Ability ]]has Action is a characteristic of that [[#ability’s|Ability ]]and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 807
**807.** [[#assault|Assault ]]

#### rule 807.1
**807.1.** Assault is a [[#passive abilities|Passive Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 807.1.a
**807.1.a.** It is present on Units. 

#### rule 807.1.b
**807.1.b.** Assault is formatted as "Assault [X]". 

#### rule 807.1.b.1
**807.1.b.1.** The X is referenced in the functional text of the ability. 

#### rule 807.1.b.2
**807.1.b.2.** The X is referred to as the Assault Value. 

#### rule 807.1.b.3
**807.1.b.3.** If X is omitted, it is presumed to be 1. 

#### rule 807.1.c
**807.1.c.** It is functionally short for "While I am an attacker, I have +X [M]." 

#### rule 807.1.d
**807.1.d.** Being an attacker means the Unit has gained the Attacker designation during Combat.  See [[##rule 454|rule 454.]] [[#combat|Combat]] for more information. 

#### rule 807.1.d.1
**807.1.d.1.** Assault remains in effect as long as the Unit maintains the Attacker designation. 

#### rule 807.2
**807.2.** If a Unit has Assault or has been granted Assault and is granted Assault by an additional source, the Assault Value of all granted Assault keywords is summed.  Example: Petty Ofﬁcer has Assault. It is chosen as the target of Cleave, which says "Give a unit [Assault 3] this turn." After Cleave resolves, Petty Ofﬁcer has Assault 4 this turn. 

#### rule 807.3
**807.3.** Assault, and whether or not a unit has Assault, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 808
**808.** [[#deathknell|Deathknell ]]

#### rule 808.1
**808.1.** Deathknell is a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 808.1.a
**808.1.a.** It is present on [[#permanents|Permanents. ]]

#### rule 808.1.b
**808.1.b.** It is formatted as "[Deathknell][>] [Effect]". 

#### rule 808.1.b.1
**808.1.b.1.** [Effect] is the rules text for the speciﬁc instance of Deathknell. This is referred to as the Deathknell effect. 

#### rule 808.1.c
**808.1.c.** It is functionally short for "When I die, [Effect]." 

#### rule 808.1.c.1
**808.1.c.1.** [Effect] is the rules text of the Deathknell effect. 

#### rule 808.1.d
**808.1.d.** The Trigger for this effect is the Permanent being [[#killed|Killed ]]and sent to the [[#trashes|Trash. ]]

#### rule 808.1.d.1
**808.1.d.1.** If the Permanent with the effect is not sent to the [[#trashes|Trash]], for example because its "killed" event was replaced with a recall, the Deathknell will not occur. 

#### rule 808.1.d.2
**808.1.d.2.** The trigger will be added to the chain as a [[#pending item|Pending Item ]]before the card with [[#deathknell|Deathknell ]]is moved to the trash due to a [[#killed|Kill ]]instruction or a [[#cleanup|Cleanup. ]]

#### rule 808.1.d.3
**808.1.d.3.** Before the card with [[#deathknell|Deathknell ]]is moved to the [[#trashes|Trash]], note its location, its attributes, and any other details related to the effect of its [[#deathknell|Deathknell ]]to process the trigger after it has been [[#finalize|Finalized]]. 

#### rule 808.2
**808.2.** Each instance of Deathknell a Permanent may have will trigger separately. 

#### rule 808.2.a
**808.2.a.** The controller will choose the order to add these [[#trigger|Triggers ]]to the chain. 

#### rule 808.3
**808.3.** Deathknell, and whether or not a permanent has Deathknell, is a characteristic of the permanent and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 809
**809.** [[#deflect|Deflect ]]

#### rule 809.1
**809.1.** Deflect is a [[#passive abilities|Passive Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 809.1.a
**809.1.a.** It is present on Permanents. 

#### rule 809.1.b
**809.1.b.** It is formatted as "Deflect [X]". 

#### rule 809.1.b.1
**809.1.b.1.** The X is referenced in the functional text of the ability. 

#### rule 809.1.b.2
**809.1.b.2.** The X is referred to as the Deflect Value. 

#### rule 809.1.b.3
**809.1.b.3.** If X is omitted, it is presumed to be 1. 

#### rule 809.1.c
**809.1.c.** It is functionally short for "Spells and abilities an opponent controls that choose me cost an amount of Power equal to [Deflect Value] more to play as an additional cost for each time they choose me." 

#### rule 809.1.c.1
**809.1.c.1.** The Power used to pay this cost may always be of any Domain.  Example: A Fury spell targets an Order unit with Deflect. The Power used to pay the Deflect cost can be any Domain; it does not need to match the Domain of the spell or the target. 

#### rule 809.1.d
**809.1.d.** It is an effect that imposes a Mandatory Additional Cost on Spells and Abilities that choose the permanent that has this ability.  See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 809.2
**809.2.** If a Unit has Deflect, or has been granted Deflect, and is granted Deflect by an additional source, the Deflect Value of all granted Deflect keywords is summed. 

#### rule 809.3
**809.3.** Deflect, and whether or not a permanent has Deflect, is a characteristic of the permanent and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 810
**810.** [[#ganking|Ganking ]]

#### rule 810.1
**810.1.** Ganking is a [[#passive abilities|Passive Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 810.1.a
**810.1.a.** It is present on Units. 

#### rule 810.1.b
**810.1.b.** It is functionally short for "I may move to a battleﬁeld from another battleﬁeld with a standard move." 

#### rule 810.1.c
**810.1.c.** It is a passive ability that adds permissions to the Unit's Standard Move. 

#### rule 810.1.c.1
**810.1.c.1.** It does not restrict or remove options from the Unit's Standard Move. 

#### rule 810.1.c.2
**810.1.c.2.** It does not have an activation cost. 

#### rule 810.1.c.3
**810.1.c.3.** It does not give additional abilities or activations of Movement, only new options for the Standard Move. 

#### rule 810.2
**810.2.** Multiple instances of Ganking are redundant. 

#### rule 810.3
**810.3.** Ganking, and whether or not a unit has Ganking, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 811
**811.** [[#hide|Hidden ]]

#### rule 811.1
**811.1.** Hidden is a keyword that acts as a prerequisite to perform the [[#hide|Hide ]]Discretionary Action. 

#### rule 811.1.a
**811.1.a.** It is present on Spells, Units, and Gear. 

#### rule 811.1.b
**811.1.b.** It is functionally short for "While this card is in your hand or in your Champion Zone on your turn during an Open State, you may pay [A] to hide this facedown at a battleﬁeld you control that doesn't already have a facedown card hidden there for as long as you control that battleﬁeld. Beginning on the next turn, this gains [Reaction] and you may play this, ignoring its base cost." 

#### rule 811.1.c
**811.1.c.** It allows the player to take the Discretionary Action [[#hide|Hide]]. 

#### rule 811.1.c.1
**811.1.c.1.** Hide is not a subset of [[#play|Play]]. 

#### rule 811.1.c.2
**811.1.c.2.** Hiding a card does not open a chain. 

#### rule 811.1.c.3
**811.1.c.3.** Playing a card from facedown (or "from Hidden") does open a chain. 

#### rule 811.1.d
**811.1.d.** Some choices made while playing a card from Hidden are restricted to the battleﬁeld where it was hidden. A card cannot be played from Hidden if it is a spell with no valid targets under these restrictions.  See [[##rule 355.6|rule 355.6.]] [[#targeting|Targeting]] for more information. 

#### rule 811.1.d.1
**811.1.d.1.** A hidden permanent must be played to that battleﬁeld. 

#### rule 811.1.d.1.a
**811.1.d.1.a.** This includes hidden gear, and overrides the normal restriction that gear have in only being allowed to be played to base. 

#### rule 811.1.d.2
**811.1.d.2.** If a hidden spell or a play effect of a hidden permanent chooses any targets, those targets must be chosen from among options at that battleﬁeld, unless the ability explicitly restricts targeting in a way that makes this impossible.  Example: Blastcone Fae is a unit with Hidden and “When you play me, give a unit -2 [M] this turn, to a minimum of 1 [M].” Because this is a play effect, its target must be chosen from among units at the same battleﬁeld if Blastcone Fae was played from Hidden.  Example: Tideturner is a unit with Hidden and “When you play me, you may choose a unit you control at another location. Move me to its location and it to my original location.” Because its play ability has a targeting restriction that can never be fulﬁlled by a unit at its battleﬁeld, its target may be chosen freely from among the available options. 

#### rule 811.1.d.3
**811.1.d.3.** If a hidden spell or a play effect of a hidden permanent causes you to play a unit, you must choose to play that unit at that battleﬁeld. 

#### rule 811.2
**811.2.** Abilities and instructions of hidden cards other than the choices listed above function as normal.  Example: Stand United is a spell that has Hidden and says “Buff a friendly unit. Buffs give an additional +1 might to friendly units this turn.” If it’s played from Hidden, the ﬁrst part of its ability must choose a friendly unit at the same battleﬁeld, but the second part of its ability affects all friendly units with buffs, no matter where they are. 

#### rule 811.3
**811.3.** Instead of being hidden, a card with Hidden may be played for its cost as normal, at its normal timing with no restrictions on targeting. 

#### rule 811.4
**811.4.** Multiple instances of Hidden are redundant. 

#### rule 811.5
**811.5.** Hidden, and whether or not a card has Hidden, is a characteristic of the card and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 811.5.a
**811.5.a.** This is independent of the state of being facedown. 

#### rule 811.6
**811.6.** A card that is [[#hide|Hidden ]]gains [[#reaction|Reaction ]]while facedown or played from facedown, and may be played any time a card with [[#reaction|Reaction ]]may be played as a result. 

#### rule 811.6.a
**811.6.a.** The property is granted to the card in its facedown state, and is not publicly known. 

### rule 812
**812.** [[#legion|Legion ]]

#### rule 812.1
**812.1.** Legion is a [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keyword. ]]

#### rule 812.1.a
**812.1.a.** It is formatted as "[Legion][>] [Text]". 

#### rule 812.1.b
**812.1.b.** Starting from the Keyword to the end of the clause, the entire statement is the [[#legion ability|Legion Ability]]. 

#### rule 812.1.b.1
**812.1.b.1.** [[#legion|Legion ]]is functionally short for “If you have played another card this turn, this card gains [Text].” 

#### rule 812.1.b.2
**812.1.b.2.** The [Text] is the [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability. ]]

#### rule 812.1.c
**812.1.c.** As long as a card different than the one with the [[#legion|Legion ]]ability has been [[#finalize|Finalized ]]on the same turn then the [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability ]]is [[#active|Active ]]on the card with [[#legion|Legion. ]]

#### rule 812.2
**812.2.** All instances of [[#legion|Legion ]]on cards a player controls are satisﬁed by that player playing a single card.  Example: One card has three different Legion Abilities. The Legion Text of all three abilities will be active as long as one card has been played by the card's controller earlier in the same turn. 

#### rule 812.3
**812.3.** [[#legion|Legion]], and whether or not a card has [[#legion|Legion]], is a characteristic of the card and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 813
**813.** [[#reaction|Reaction ]]

#### rule 813.1
**813.1.** Reaction is a [[#permissive|Permissive ]]keyword. 

#### rule 813.1.a
**813.1.a.** It can be present on [[#cards, rune abilities, legend abilities|Cards, Rune Abilities, Legend Abilities ]]and [[#permanent abilities|Permanent Abilities. ]]

#### rule 813.1.b
**813.1.b.** [[#reaction|Reaction ]]grants the corresponding card or effect all abilities and permissions of [[#action|Action. ]]

#### rule 813.1.c
**813.1.c.** [[#reaction|Reaction]], additionally, is functionally short for the following: 

#### rule 813.1.c.1
**813.1.c.1.** On Cards: "This can be played during [[#closed state|Closed States ]]on any player's turn." 

#### rule 813.1.c.2
**813.1.c.2.** On Rune, Legend, or Permanent Abilities: "This can be activated during [[#closed state|Closed States ]]on any player's turn." 

#### rule 813.1.d
**813.1.d.** Reaction is formatted as “[Reaction]” on cards, or “[Reaction][>]” on abilities. 

#### rule 813.2
**813.2.** The corresponding card or effect with this keyword is not restricted to [[#closed state|Closed States ]]or [[#showdown|Showdowns]]. This permission is inclusive of all other timings and options available to the ability as written, Action's permissions, or by default. 

#### rule 813.3
**813.3.** Reaction does not alter the function of any instruction of the Card, Rune, or Effect it is on. It is only Permission. 

#### rule 813.3.a
**813.3.a.** Playing [[#unit|Units ]]with Reaction still has the inherent restrictions of playing [[#unit|Units ]]without Reaction. It can only be played to the controlling player's base or a battleﬁeld they control. 

#### rule 813.4
**813.4.** Some passive abilities may grant a card or ability Reaction under certain conditions. The card or ability does not have the Reaction keyword unless and until those circumstances are true. 

#### rule 813.4.a
**813.4.a.** Those conditions might only be fulﬁlled while the card or ability is on the chain. In such a case, it can still be played or activated at the appropriate timing as long as doing so could fulﬁll the conditions. 

#### rule 813.4.b
**813.4.b.** If the chain item does not fulﬁll the conditions by the time step 5: check legality has been reached, the actions taken while playing or activating the chain item are undone and it is returned to the zone it was played from if it is a card. 

#### rule 813.5
**813.5.** Reaction is a referencable characteristic. 

#### rule 813.5.a
**813.5.a.** Whether or not a [[#game object|Game Object ]]has Reaction is a characteristic of that [[#game object|Game Object ]]and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 813.5.b
**813.5.b.** Whether or not a [[#spells|Spell ]]has Reaction is a characteristic of that [[#spells|Spell ]]and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 813.5.c
**813.5.c.** Whether or not an [[#ability’s|Ability ]]has Reaction is a characteristic of that [[#ability’s|Ability ]]and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 814
**814.** [[#shield|Shield ]]

#### rule 814.1
**814.1.** Shield is a [[#passive abilities|Passive Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 814.1.a
**814.1.a.** It is present on Units. 

#### rule 814.1.b
**814.1.b.** Shield is formatted as "Shield [X]". 

#### rule 814.1.b.1
**814.1.b.1.** The X is referenced in the functional text of the ability. 

#### rule 814.1.b.2
**814.1.b.2.** The X is referred to as the Shield Value. 

#### rule 814.1.b.3
**814.1.b.3.** If X is omitted, it is presumed to be 1. 

#### rule 814.1.c
**814.1.c.** It is functionally short for "While I am a defender, I have +X [M]." 

#### rule 814.1.d
**814.1.d.** Being a defender means the Unit has gained the Defender designation during Combat. See [[##rule 454|rule 454.]] [[#combat|Combat]] for more information. 

#### rule 814.1.d.1
**814.1.d.1.** Shield remains in effect as long as the Unit maintains the Defender designation. 

#### rule 814.2
**814.2.** If a Unit has Shield, or has been granted Shield, and is granted Shield by an additional source, the Shield Value of all granted Shield keywords is summed.  Example: Stalwart Poro has Shield. It is chosen as the target of Block, which says "Give a unit [Shield 3] and [Tank] this turn." After Block resolves, Stalwart Poro has Shield 4 this turn. 

#### rule 814.3
**814.3.** Shield, and whether or not a unit has Shield, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 815
**815.** [[#tank|Tank ]]

#### rule 815.1
**815.1.** Tank is a [[#passive abilities|Passive Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 815.1.a
**815.1.a.** It is present on Units. 

#### rule 815.1.b
**815.1.b.** It is functionally short for "I must be assigned lethal damage before any other unit with the same controller as me that does not have [Tank] during the Combat Damage step." 

#### rule 815.1.c
**815.1.c.** It alters how players can elect to assign combat damage during combat. 

#### rule 815.1.c.1
**815.1.c.1.** Players must still assign lethal damage to a unit before moving to the next when assigning their damage. 

#### rule 815.1.c.2
**815.1.c.2.** If more than one unit with Tank is present with the same controller in Combat, damage may be assigned to any of them. Units without Tank are invalid assignments until all units with Tank have lethal damage assigned to them. 

#### rule 815.2
**815.2.** Multiple instances of Tank are redundant. 

#### rule 815.3
**815.3.** Tank, and whether or not a unit has Tank, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 816
**816.** [[#temporary|Temporary ]]

#### rule 816.1
**816.1.** Temporary is a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 816.1.a
**816.1.a.** It is present on Permanents. 

#### rule 816.1.b
**816.1.b.** It is functionally short for "At the start of this permanent's controller's Beginning Phase, before scoring, kill this." 

#### rule 816.1.c
**816.1.c.** The Trigger Condition is the controller of the permanent's Beginning Phase starting. 

#### rule 816.2
**816.2.** Multiple instances of Temporary are redundant. 

#### rule 816.2.a
**816.2.a.** Regardless of how many instances there are, the ability will only trigger once. 

#### rule 816.3
**816.3.** Temporary, and whether or not a permanent has Temporary, is a characteristic of the permanent and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 817
**817.** [[#vision|Vision ]]

#### rule 817.1
**817.1.** Vision is a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 817.1.a
**817.1.a.** It is present on Permanents. 

#### rule 817.1.b
**817.1.b.** It is functionally short for "When this is played, look at the top card of your Main Deck. You may recycle it." 

#### rule 817.1.c
**817.1.c.** The trigger is the permanent entering the Board. 

#### rule 817.2
**817.2.** Multiple instances of Vision trigger separately. 

#### rule 817.2.a
**817.2.a.** The player may choose to recycle or not recycle for each instance of Vision separately. 

#### rule 817.2.b
**817.2.b.** If the player does not recycle the top card and nothing else happens in between the triggers resolving, each instance of Vision will see the same card. 

#### rule 817.3
**817.3.** Vision, and whether or not a permanent has Vision, is a characteristic of the permanent and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 818
**818.** [[#equip|Equip ]]

#### rule 818.1
**818.1.** [[#equip|Equip ]]is an [[#activated abilities|Activated Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 818.1.a
**818.1.a.** [[#equip|Equip ]]is normally present on [[#gear|Gear ]]with the tag [[#equip|Equipment. ]]

#### rule 818.1.b
**818.1.b.** [[#equip|Equip ]]has a cost to activate and [[#attaches|Attaches ]]the card with [[#equip|Equip ]]to a chosen [[#unit|Unit ]]when the cost is paid. 

#### rule 818.1.b.1
**818.1.b.1.** [[#equip|Equip’s ]]choice is a [[#targeting|Target. ]]

#### rule 818.1.b.2
**818.1.b.2.** The chosen [[#unit|Unit ]]will become the [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]for the [[#attached|Attach ]]action. 

#### rule 818.1.c
**818.1.c.** [[#equip|Equip ]]is formatted as “[[#equip|Equip ]][Cost]” 

#### rule 818.1.c.1
**818.1.c.1.** If paying costs or making choices for this ability causes triggered abilities to trigger, they will be placed on the chain above this ability in a [[#pending item|Pending ]]state. See [[##rule 376|rule 376.]] [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities]] for more information. 

#### rule 818.1.c.2
**818.1.c.2.** [[#equip|Equip ]]is functionally short for “[Cost]: [[#attached|Attach ]]this gear to a unit you control.” 

#### rule 818.1.c.3
**818.1.c.3.** [[#equip|Equip ]]costs may include both resource costs and non-resource costs. 

#### rule 818.1.c.4
**818.1.c.4.** [[#equip|Equip ]]abilities may also include text that alters the [[#equip|Equip ]]cost. Such text is taken into account when determining a card’s [[#equip|Equip ]]cost for any reason.

#### rule 818.1.c.5
**818.1.c.5.** [[#equip|Equip ]]abilities may include text that alters the timing or targeting of the [[#equip|Equip ]]ability. 

#### rule 818.2
**818.2.** When the [[#attached|Attach ]]action completes from this keyword, the [[#unit|Unit ]]that was chosen is considered to have been [[#equip|Equipped ]]by the [[#gear|Gear ]]with this ability. 

#### rule 818.2.a
**818.2.a.** This is an event other [[#game effects|Game Effects ]]and [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Abilities ]]can reference. 

#### rule 818.3
**818.3.** [[#equip|Equipped ]]is the state of a [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]being [[#attached|Attached ]]by one or more cards that are [[#equip|Equipment. ]]

#### rule 818.3.a
**818.3.a.** The state of being [[#equip|Equipped ]]is synchronous with that of the [[#attached|Attached ]]state of the [[#equip|Equipment. ]]

#### rule 818.3.b
**818.3.b.** A [[#top-most card|Top-Most Card ]]is [[#equip|Equipped ]]as long as one or more of its [[#attached|Attached ]]cards are [[#equip|Equipment. ]]

#### rule 818.3.c
**818.3.c.** The state of being [[#equip|Equipped ]]corresponds to a [[#top-most card|Top-Most card ]]having a card with [[#equip|Equip ]]that is [[#attached|Attached ]]to it. 

#### rule 818.4
**818.4.** Multiple instances of [[#equip|Equip ]]are equivalent to multiple [[#activated abilities|Activated Abilities ]]and can each be activated separately by paying the corresponding costs. 

#### rule 818.5
**818.5.** [[#equip|Equip, ]]and whether or not a [[#gear|Gear ]]has [[#equip|Equip, ]]is a characteristic of the Gear and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

#### rule 818.5.a
**818.5.a.** Whether or not a [[#gear|Gear ]]has [[#equip|Equip ]]may be referenced even if the [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]of the [[#gear|Gear ]]is [[#inactive|Inactive. ]]See [[##rule 716|rule 716.]] [[#attachment|Attachment]] for more information. 

### rule 819
**819.** [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw ]]

#### rule 819.1
**819.1.** [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw ]]is a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]keyword. It is also a [[#permissive|Permissive ]]keyword. 

#### rule 819.1.a
**819.1.a.** [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw ]]is present on [[#gear|Gear ]]with [[#equip|Equip ]]abilities. 

#### rule 819.1.b
**819.1.b.** Cards with [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw ]]have [[#reaction|Reaction ]]inherently. 

#### rule 819.1.c
**819.1.c.** [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw ]]allows cards to be played and [[#attached|Attached ]]using [[#reaction|Reaction ]]timing. 

#### rule 819.1.d
**819.1.d.** [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw ]]is functionally short for “[[#reaction|[Reaction]]]” and “When you play this, [[#attached|attach ]]it to a [[#unit|Unit ]]you control.” See [[##rule 716|rule 716.]] [[#attachment|Attachment]] for more information. 

#### rule 819.2
**819.2.** Multiple instances of [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw ]]do not trigger separately and have no effect beyond the ﬁrst. 

#### rule 819.3
**819.3.** [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw]], and whether or not a gear has [[#quick-draw|Quick-Draw]], is a characteristic of the Gear and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 820
**820.** [[#repeat|Repeat ]]

#### rule 820.1
**820.1.** [[#repeat|Repeat ]]is an [[#optional additional costs|Optional Additional Cost ]]keyword. 

#### rule 820.1.a
**820.1.a.** [[#repeat|Repeat ]]is present on [[#spells|Spells. ]]

#### rule 820.1.b
**820.1.b.** [[#repeat|Repeat ]]is an optional cost that a player may pay to execute the effect of their spells a second time. 

#### rule 820.1.c
**820.1.c.** [[#repeat|Repeat ]]is formatted as “[[#repeat|Repeat ]][Cost]” 

#### rule 820.1.c.1
**820.1.c.1.** The Cost is an [[#additional costs|Additional Cost ]]to be paid during the steps of playing the spell. 

#### rule 820.1.c.2
**820.1.c.2.** If a spell has more than one instance of [[#repeat|Repeat]], each Cost may be paid or not paid individually.  

#### rule 820.1.c.3
**820.1.c.3.** Each [[#repeat|Repeat Cost ]]can be paid only a single time. 

#### rule 820.1.d
**820.1.d.** [[#repeat|Repeat ]]is functionally short for “You may pay [[#cost|[Cost] ]]as an additional cost as you play this spell. If you do, execute the instructions of this spell one additional time.” 

#### rule 820.1.d.1
**820.1.d.1.** When the additional cost is paid, the effect of the spell, upon resolution, will be performed an additional time. Example: Desert’s Call is a spell with [Repeat] [2] and “Play a 2 [S] Sand Soldier unit token.” If its controller pays its Repeat cost as they play it, the card’s instruction to play a Sand Soldier is executed twice, as though the card says “Play a 2 [S] Sand Soldier unit token. Play a 2 [S] Sand Soldier unit token.” 

#### rule 820.2
**820.2.** When a spell’s effect is performed an additional time with [[#repeat|Repeat]], choices must be made at the usual time during the [[#make relevant choices|Make Relevant Choices ]]step of [[#playing a card|Playing a Card. ]]See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information. 

#### rule 820.2.a
**820.2.a.** Choices made for the additional execution do not have to be the same as the choices made for the initial execution. Example: Rocket Barrage is a spell with [Repeat] [4][C] and “Choose one — Deal 4 to a unit in a base. [or] Kill a gear.” If Rocket Barrage’s controller pays its Repeat cost as they play it, they may choose the same mode or a different one, and if they choose the same mode, may choose the same target or a different one. If they choose “Kill a gear” twice and choose two different gear, they must specify which gear is the ﬁrst target and which is the second. As the spell resolves, those two gear will be killed in the chosen order. 

#### rule 820.3
**820.3.** Multiple instances of [[#repeat|Repeat ]]can be paid for separately. The spell’s instructions  will be executed an additional time for each instance of [[#repeat|Repeat ]]that is paid for. 

#### rule 820.3.a
**820.3.a.** Regardless of the number of times a spell's instructions are executed with this keyword, the spell is only [[#played|Played ]]once. 

#### rule 820.4
**820.4.** [[#repeat|Repeat]], and whether or not a spell has [[#repeat|Repeat]], is a characteristic of the Spell and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 821
**821.** [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]

#### rule 821.1
**821.1.** [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]is a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 821.1.a
**821.1.a.** [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]is present on [[#unit|Units. ]]

#### rule 821.1.b
**821.1.b.** [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]is a [[#play effect|Play Effect ]]that chooses an [[#equip|Equipment ]]you control and allows you to pay its [[#equip|Equip ]]cost at a discount, regardless of the usual timing of the [[#equip|Equip ]]ability, to [[#attached|Attach ]]that [[#equip|Equipment ]]to the unit with [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster. ]]

#### rule 821.1.c
**821.1.c.** [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]is functionally short for: “When you play me, you may choose a [[#card|Card ]]you control with the [[#equip|Equipment ]]tag. Necessary portions of its [[#rules text|Rules Text ]]are no longer Inactive if they are currently [[#inactive|Inactive. ]]Pay the cost of its [[#equip|Equip ]]ability, reduced by [A], to attach it to this unit.” See [[##rule 716|rule 716.]] [[#attachment|Attachment]] for more information. 

#### rule 821.1.c.1
**821.1.c.1.** [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]can choose an [[#equip|Equipment ]]whether it has an [[#equip|Equip ]]ability or not. 

#### rule 821.1.c.2
**821.1.c.2.** The cost of the [[#equip|Equip ]]ability is determined as though that [[#equip|Equip ]]ability was being activated choosing the unit with the [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]ability, as modulated by any abilities that alter [[#equip|Equip ]]costs. 

#### rule 821.1.c.3
**821.1.c.3.** If the chosen card’s [[#equip|Equip ]]cost does not contain [A], it can still be paid, but will not be reduced. 

#### rule 821.1.c.4
**821.1.c.4.** If the chosen card doesn’t have an [[#equip|Equip ]]cost, it can’t be paid. 

#### rule 821.1.c.5
**821.1.c.5.** If the chosen card’s [[#equip|Equip ]]cost can’t be paid, if it can’t be detached from its current [[#top-most card|Top-Most ]]card, or if it can’t be attached to the unit with the [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]ability, it stays in its current location, [[#attached|Attached ]]to anything it was already [[#attached|Attached ]]to. 

#### rule 821.1.c.6
**821.1.c.6.** The [[#equip|Equip ]]ability is not activated this way, and the unit with the [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]ability is not chosen. 

#### rule 821.1.c.7
**821.1.c.7.** Multiple instances of [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]trigger separately, and can choose different targets. 

#### rule 821.1.d
**821.1.d.** If you choose the same target with multiple instances of [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster]], each will resolve separately. 

#### rule 821.2
**821.2.** [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster ]]has no function while on the board. 

#### rule 821.3
**821.3.** [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster]], and whether or not a unit has [[#weaponmaster|Weaponmaster]], is a characteristic of the [[#unit|Unit ]]and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 822
**822.** [[#ambush|Ambush ]]

#### rule 822.1
**822.1.** [[#ambush|Ambush ]]is a [[#passive abilities|Passive Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 822.1.a
**822.1.a.** It is present on [[#unit|Units]]. 

#### rule 822.1.b
**822.1.b.** It is functionally short for "I may be played to a battleﬁeld where you control [[#unit|Units]]" and “I have [[#[reaction|Reaction]]] as long as I’m being played to a battleﬁeld where you control [[#unit|Units]].”  

#### rule 822.1.c
**822.1.c.** It is a passive ability that adds options to locations that are valid for a [[#unit|Unit ]]to be played to during the Make Relevant Choices step of Playing a Card See [[##rule 349|rule 349.]] [[#playing cards|Playing Cards]] for more information 

#### rule 822.2
**822.2.** Multiple instances of [[#ambush|Ambush ]]are redundant. 

#### rule 822.3
**822.3.** If there are no units at the location chosen before [[#finalize|Finalization ]]completes for any reason, then it is no longer a valid location by [[#ambush|Ambush]]’s reasoning and cannot be played there 

#### rule 822.3.a
**822.3.a.** Other effects and permissions may still enable this [[#unit|Unit ]]to be able to be played to the selected location, but [[#ambush|Ambush’s ]]permission will not be valid 

#### rule 822.4
**822.4.** [[#ambush|Ambush]], and whether or not a unit has [[#ambush|Ambush]], is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 823
**823.** [[#hunt|Hunt ]]

#### rule 823.1
**823.1.** [[#hunt|Hunt ]]is a [[#triggered abilities|Triggered Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 823.1.a
**823.1.a.** [[#hunt|Hunt ]]is present on [[#unit|Units. ]]

#### rule 823.1.b
**823.1.b.** [[#hunt|Hunt ]]is both a [[#conquering|Conquer ]]and a [[#holding|Hold ]]effect. 

#### rule 823.1.c
**823.1.c.** [[#hunt|Hunt ]]is formatted as “[[#hunt|Hunt ]]X” 

#### rule 823.1.c.1
**823.1.c.1.** [[#hunt|Hunt ]]is functionally short for: “When I [[#conquering|Conquer ]]or [[#holding|Hold]], my controller gains X XP.” See [[##rule 728|rule 728.]] [[#xp|XP]] for more information 

#### rule 823.1.c.2
**823.1.c.2.** If X is omitted, it is presumed to be 1. 

#### rule 823.1.c.3
**823.1.c.3.** X is referred to as the Hunt Value. 

#### rule 823.2
**823.2.** If a Unit has [[#hunt|Hunt]], or has been granted [[#hunt|Hunt]], and is granted [[#hunt|Hunt ]]by an additional source, the Hunt Value of all granted [[#hunt|Hunt ]]keywords is summed.  

#### rule 823.3
**823.3.** [[#hunt|Hunt]], and whether or not a unit has [[#hunt|Hunt]], is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 824
**824.** [[#level|Level ]]

#### rule 824.1
**824.1.** [[#level|Level ]]is a [[#dependent keywords|Dependent Keyword. ]]

#### rule 824.1.a
**824.1.a.** It is formatted as "[Level [N]][>] [Text]". 

#### rule 824.1.b
**824.1.b.** Starting from the Keyword to the end of the clause, the entire statement is the [[#level ability|Level Ability]]. 

#### rule 824.1.b.1
**824.1.b.1.** It is functionally short for “While you have [N] or more XP, this card gains “[Text]”.” 

#### rule 824.1.b.2
**824.1.b.2.** The [Text] here is the [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability ]]

#### rule 824.1.c
**824.1.c.** As long as the controlling player has [N] XP, then the [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability ]]will be be [[#active|Active ]]on the card with [[#level|Level ]]

#### rule 824.1.c.1
**824.1.c.1.** If the controller of the card with [[#level|Level ]]changes, then the [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability ]]will be rendered [[#active|Active ]]or [[#inactive|Inactive ]]based on the new controller’s XP. 

#### rule 824.1.d
**824.1.d.** The [[#dependent ability|Dependent Ability ]]will be [[#inactive|Inactive ]]as soon as the controlling player has less than [N] XP. 

#### rule 824.2
**824.2.** [[#level|Level, ]]and whether or not a card has [[#level|Level ]]is a characteristic of the card and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 825
**825.** [[#unit|Unique ]]

#### rule 825.1
**825.1.** [[#unit|Unique ]]is a [[#deck constraint permission|Deck Constraint Permission. ]]

#### rule 825.2
**825.2.** [[#unit|Unique ]]is not functionally short for any rules text, and instead provides a restriction to players during Deck Construction. 

#### rule 825.2.a
**825.2.a.** A Deck can contain only one card of a given name if the card has [[#unit|Unique ]]

#### rule 825.2.b
**825.2.b.** If a card is a [[#signature|Signature ]]card and is also [[#unit|Unique]], then that Deck can contain any combination of three [[#signature|Signature ]]cards, but still only one of each named [[#unit|Unique ]]card. 

#### rule 825.3
**825.3.** Cards with [[#unit|Unique ]]have no additional effects during gameplay. 

#### rule 825.4
**825.4.** [[#unit|Unique]], and whether or not a Card has [[#unit|Unique]], is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]

### rule 826
**826.** [[#backline|Backline ]]

#### rule 826.1
**826.1.** [[#backline|Backline ]]is a [[#passive abilities|Passive Ability ]]keyword. 

#### rule 826.2
**826.2.** It is present on Units. 

#### rule 826.3
**826.3.** It is functionally short for “I must be assigned lethal damage after any other unit with the same controller as me that does not have [Backline] during the Combat Damage step.” 

#### rule 826.4
**826.4.** It alters how players can elect to assign combat damage during combat. 

#### rule 826.4.a
**826.4.a.** [[#players must still assign lethal damage to a unit before moving to the next when assigning their damage|Players must still assign lethal damage to a unit before moving to the next when assigning their damage. ]]

#### rule 826.4.b
**826.4.b.** If more than one unit with Backline is present with the same controller in Combat, damage may be assigned to any of them. Units with Backline are invalid assignments until all units without Backline have lethal damage assigned to them. 

#### rule 826.5
**826.5.** Multiple Instances of Backline are redundant. 

#### rule 826.6
**826.6.** Backline, and whether or not a unit has Backline, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or referenced by other [[#game effects|Game Effects. ]]


##  Terms

###  group A

####  a main deck of at least 40 cards

**A Main Deck Of At Least 40 Cards**

- [[##rule 103.2|103.2.]] A Main Deck of at least 40 cards 1 Chosen Champion Unit, Units, Gear, Spells

####  a top-most card

**A Top-most Card**

- [[##rule 717|717.]] Attaching is a limited action that causes cards to become linked to each other to combine their effects in some way. This causes one card to become Attached and the other to become A Top-Most Card. See rule 434. Attach for more information.

####  abilities

**Abilities**

- [[##rule 135.2.a|135.2.a.]] Abilities
- [[##rule 135.2.a.1|135.2.a.1.]] Abilities are discrete pieces of text that describe what a card may or must do.  See rule 360. Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 136.2|136.2.]] Effect Text can contain additional Abilities.
- [[##rule 163.2|163.2.]] A Basic Rune always has the following two Abilities:
- [[##rule 165.2|165.2.]] Players must ﬁrst add Energy and Power to their Rune Pool in order to be able to spend it to play cards or pay for Abilities with costs.
- [[##rule 167|167.]] All Abilities that include the action "Add" are abilities that are adding Energy or Power to the Rune Pool. See rule 429. Add for more information.
- [[##rule 187.6|187.6.]] Control of a Battleﬁeld determines Control of its Abilities.
- [[##rule 187.6.a|187.6.a.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Controlled, its Controller controls its Abilities. That player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, and makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed.
- [[##rule 187.6.b|187.6.b.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Uncontrolled, its Abilities are also Uncontrolled. The Turn Player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed, and is treated as their Controller if any game rule or effect requires one. Example: The Arena’s Greatest is a battleﬁeld that reads “At the start of each player's ﬁrst Beginning Phase, that player gains 1 point.” This ability will usually trigger while the battleﬁeld has no controller. If it does, the Turn Player goes through the steps of adding the ability to the chain and receives priority after doing so, exactly as if they controlled the ability.
- [[##rule 188.4|188.4.]] For Abilities, they are the Ability’s Controller.
- [[##rule 188.4.a|188.4.a.]] By default, the Controller of an Ability’s Source is the Controller of that Ability.
- [[##rule 188.4.b|188.4.b.]] Changes to Control of an Ability’s Source do not change Control of that Ability.
- [[##rule 328.2|328.2.]] Abilities are queued here as part of the process of resolving.  See rule 360. Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 347.2|347.2.]] Activate Abilities of Game Objects that are legally timed.  See rule 360. Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 355.3|355.3.]] For Spells and Abilities with a bulleted list of modes to choose from, make the appropriate choices now.
- [[##rule 355.4|355.4.]] For Spells and Abilities that Move one or more Units, choose a valid Location as the Move Destination for each Move that will be performed.
- [[##rule 360|360.]] Abilities
- [[##rule 361|361.]] An Ability is the structured rules and capabilities of Game Objects or Spells.
- [[##rule 361.1|361.1.]] An Ability has multiple structures.  -Passive Abilities  -Replacement Effects  -Activated Abilities  -Triggered Abilities  -Delayed Abilities
- [[##rule 362|362.]] A card can have more than one Ability and more than one type of Ability.
- [[##rule 377.3.a|377.3.a.]] Declare activation of the Ability.
- [[##rule 383.3.d|383.3.d.]] If more than one Triggered Ability is Triggered simultaneously, then the player that controls the Abilities selects the order to place them on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2|383.4.c.2.]] This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Conquer action, or Abilities that  the player that performed the Conquer action.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2|383.4.d.2.]] This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Hold action, or Abilities that  the player that performed the Hold action.
- [[##rule 390|390.]] Delayed Abilities are a type of Ability whose trigger Condition identiﬁes a speciﬁc time during a turn or a speciﬁc event that can occur during a speciﬁc timeframe.
- [[##rule 390.1|390.1.]] Delayed Abilities can be any other type of Ability, and contain all of the properties of that type in addition to the properties of Delayed Abilities.
- [[##rule 390.5|390.5.]] Delayed Linked Abilities are Linked Abilities that are generated by another Ability and  that Ability or Game Objects it affects. Delayed Linked Abilities don’t necessarily identify a speciﬁc window of time, and instead are deﬁned by the Ability they are linked with.
- [[##rule 390.5.a|390.5.a.]] If that Ability affects a Game Object, the Delayed Linked Ability’s window will be as long as that Game Object is in an appropriate zone.
- [[##rule 392|392.]] Delayed Abilities are not associated with Units or Gear; they are created by other Abilities or Spells. As such they are executed when their condition and/or speciﬁed time occurs regardless of whether the source of the Delayed Ability is still on the board or not.
- [[##rule 394|394.]] Linked Abilities are a set of Abilities with one or more of the component Abilities referencing the other Abilities in the set.
- [[##rule 395|395.]] In order for a set of Abilities to be Linked, they must be present in the printed Effect or Rules Text of the same Game Object, or be granted by the same source to another Game Object.
- [[##rule 396|396.]] Linked Abilities can contain component Abilities of any type.
- [[##rule 397|397.]] A component Linked Ability that s a Game Object affected by another Ability in the set may only interact with Game Objects affected by the Abilities it is Linked with.
- [[##rule 399|399.]] Playing or activating Abilities follows the same steps of playing cards.
- [[##rule 400|400.]] Abilities when added to the Chain become Pending Items until they complete the steps of Playing.
- [[##rule 400.1|400.1.]] When an Ability ﬁnishes the steps of playing it becomes a Chain Item just like a Spell.
- [[##rule 400.2|400.2.]] When an Ability with the [Add] action is ﬁnalized it resolves immediately instead of becoming a Chain Item, like a Unit or Gear.
- [[##rule 401|401.]] 1. Activate or trigger the Ability
- [[##rule 401.1|401.1.]] Add a Pending Item to the chain representing the Ability that is either being Activated or Triggered. Notably, although this Chain Item will not have a card representing it, this will create a Closed State.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 402.3.a|402.3.a.]] This is not an Ability being countered.
- [[##rule 403.1|403.1.]] Determine the base cost of the Ability.
- [[##rule 404.2.a|404.2.a.]] This is not an Ability being countered.
- [[##rule 419.4|419.4.]] Some Abilities trigger when cards are played or otherwise check whether cards have been played.
- [[##rule 428.5.d|428.5.d.]] Abilities originating from Game Objects that are  attributed Kill Actions are attributed in addition to the Game Object that created them.  Example: There is a spell that says “Do this twice: Deal 3 to a unit.” Immortal Phoenix is a unit that says “When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.” A player plays the spell while Immortal Phoenix is in their trash. The “do this” phrasing means that it has a reflexive triggered ability, which places two triggered abilities on the chain. As each of those triggered abilities resolve, it deals damage to the unit chosen for that ability. If one of these abilities deals lethal damage to a unit, both the spell and its ability are considered sources of the damage, and so both the spell and its ability receive attribution for killing the unit. This means that the spell’s controller killed a unit with a spell, so Immortal Phoenix’s ability will trigger.
- [[##rule 444|444.]] Spells, Abilities, or other effects may cause a Move to occur.
- [[##rule 460.2.c.7|460.2.c.7.]] If a Unit has one or more Abilities or effects applying to it that demand it be assigned damage in a speciﬁc way that is exclusionary, then the assigning player chooses only one of those abilities to apply when assigning damage. Example: Caitlyn, Patrolling ("I must be assigned combat damage last.") has been given the Tank ability ("I must be assigned combat damage ﬁrst."). A player is assigning damage to this Caitlyn with Tank and two units with no abilities. That player can’t fulﬁll both of Caitlyn’s damage requirements, so they may choose to assign damage to Caitlyn ﬁrst, fulﬁlling the Tank requirement, or last, fulﬁlling Caitlyn’s printed requirement. They can’t choose to apply damage to Caitlyn in between the other two units, because that wouldn’t fulﬁll either requirement.
- [[##rule 472.2.c|472.2.c.]] Abilities of Effect Text of Attached cards are appended in this layer.
- [[##rule 718.3|718.3.]] While in this state, Abilities in the card’s Effect Text are appended to the Rules Text of the Top-Most Card.

####  ability’s

**Ability’s**

- [[##rule 405.1|405.1.]] Ensure that the Ability’s targets are still legal.
- [[##rule 405.2|405.2.]] Ensure that the Ability’s effect would not create an illegal state. If it would, resolve in the same way you would resolve a Card that creates an illegal state. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 406.1|406.1.]] This Ability is no longer Pending.
- [[##rule 406.2|406.2.]] This Ability becomes a Chain Item.
- [[##rule 406.5|406.5.]] Otherwise, execute the Ability just like a Spell, then clear the Chain Item from the Chain.
- [[##rule 801|801.]] A Keyword is a speciﬁc term that appears on Cards that acts as a shorthand for a speciﬁc game effect, or ability of any variety.
- [[##rule 806.5.c|806.5.c.]] Whether or not an Ability has Action is a characteristic of that Ability and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 813.5.c|813.5.c.]] Whether or not an Ability has Reaction is a characteristic of that Ability and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

####  ability’s controller

**Ability’s Controller**

- [[##rule 188.4|188.4.]] For Abilities, they are the Ability’s Controller.

####  ability’s source

**Ability’s Source**

- [[##rule 188.4.a|188.4.a.]] By default, the Controller of an Ability’s Source is the Controller of that Ability.
- [[##rule 188.4.b|188.4.b.]] Changes to Control of an Ability’s Source do not change Control of that Ability.

####  accelerate

**Accelerate**

- [[##rule 143.4.a|143.4.a.]] This can be altered by Accelerate or similar game effects.  See rule 805. Accelerate for more information.
- [[##rule 805|805.]] Accelerate

####  action

**Action**

- [[##rule 158.2.a|158.2.a.]] Action
- [[##rule 158.2.a.1|158.2.a.1.]] This indicates that, in addition to being able to be played during an Open State, this spell may also be played during Open States during Showdowns. See rule 806. Action for more information.
- [[##rule 158.2.b.1|158.2.b.1.]] Grants all cases and rules of Action.
- [[##rule 308.1.a|308.1.a.]] Only cards and abilities with the Action or Reaction keywords can be played or activated in a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 313.1.a|313.1.a.]] The player with Focus must obey any additional restrictions on which Discretionary Actions may be performed.  Example: A player with Focus may not play spells or activate abilities that don't have the Action or Reaction keywords.
- [[##rule 316.2.b.1|316.2.b.1.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, the Turn Player's teammates may play spells and activate abilities, including ones without Action or Reaction. They can only do so when the Turn Player invites them to do so with their own Priority.
- [[##rule 316.5.c|316.5.c.]] A Showdown is a structured Window of Opportunity where Players may play cards and activate abilities with Action or Reaction. See rule 341. Showdowns for more information.
- [[##rule 806|806.]] Action
- [[##rule 813.1.b|813.1.b.]] Reaction grants the corresponding card or effect all abilities and permissions of Action.

####  activate abilities

**Activate Abilities**

- [[##rule 338.1.b|338.1.b.]] Activate Abilities of Game Objects that are legally timed.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 347.2|347.2.]] Activate Abilities of Game Objects that are legally timed.  See rule 360. Abilities for more information.

####  activated abilities

**Activated Abilities**

- [[##rule 145|145.]] Units may have Activated Abilities.
- [[##rule 145.1|145.1.]] Activated Abilities are Game Effects that are written as Costs followed by a ":", and then succeeded by an effect.  See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 145.2|145.2.]] The Activated Ability of Units may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 150|150.]] Gear may have Activated Abilities.
- [[##rule 150.1|150.1.]] Activated Abilities are Game Effects that are written as Costs followed by a ":", and then succeeded by an effect.  See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 150.2|150.2.]] The Activated Ability of Gear may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 173.8|173.8.]] Legends can have Activated Abilities. See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 361.1|361.1.]] An Ability has multiple structures.  -Passive Abilities  -Replacement Effects  -Activated Abilities  -Triggered Abilities  -Delayed Abilities
- [[##rule 377|377.]] Activated Abilities are repeatable effects with a cost. They follow a process of going onto the chain and resolving, similar to Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 377.1|377.1.]] Activated Abilities are recognized by the presence of a ":" in the text of the card, preceded by a cost and succeeded by an effect.  Example: "[2]: Draw 1" is an activated ability. The cost is 2 energy. The effect is to draw 1 card.
- [[##rule 377.2|377.2.]] Card text will refer to activating Activated Abilities with the word “use.”
- [[##rule 377.2.a|377.2.a.]] If “using” an Activated Ability is part of a trigger condition, that condition is fulﬁlled when the Activated Ability resolves.
- [[##rule 377.3|377.3.]] Activated Abilities use the chain.
- [[##rule 377.3.b.3|377.3.b.3.]] If no further action is taken, execute the Activated Ability.
- [[##rule 378|378.]] The controlling player chooses when and whether to activate an Activated Ability.
- [[##rule 381|381.]] All Activated Abilities can only be activated on the Controlling Player's Turn and during an Open State.
- [[##rule 383.3|383.3.]] When a Condition is met, a Triggered Ability behaves like an Activated Ability and is placed on the Chain.
- [[##rule 402.2|402.2.]] If legal options are not available for an Activated Ability, it is not legal to activate it.
- [[##rule 403.1.a|403.1.a.]] Activated Abilities will have a cost listed before the “:” in their text.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.3|727.1.c.3.]] Activated Abilities that become Active from Dependent Keywords can be activated at their associated timing after that ability has been granted
- [[##rule 818.1|818.1.]] Equip is an Activated Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 818.1.c.1|818.1.c.1.]] If paying costs or making choices for this ability causes triggered abilities to trigger, they will be placed on the chain above this ability in a Pending state. See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 818.4|818.4.]] Multiple instances of Equip are equivalent to multiple Activated Abilities and can each be activated separately by paying the corresponding costs.

####  active

**Active**

- [[##rule 135.4.b|135.4.b.]] Any granted or appended Rules Text on a card is still Active even if that card is Attached to another card.
- [[##rule 428.1.a|428.1.a.]] This can be Active or Passive.
- [[##rule 428.1.a.1|428.1.a.1.]] Active Kill is when the action is taken when instructed by a game effect or as a cost for a card or ability.
- [[##rule 727.1.b|727.1.b.]] The Dependent Ability associated with the Dependent Keyword is Inactive on the card with the Dependent Keyword until the Condition is met, when it becomes Active
- [[##rule 727.1.b.2|727.1.b.2.]] The Dependent Ability is Active exactly as written while the Condition is true Example: Gustwalker has “[Level3][>] I have +1 [M] and Ganking.” As long as its controller has 3 XP, Gustwalker’s Ganking is active.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.1|727.1.c.1.]] Triggered Abilities of Dependent Keywords must be Active for their trigger to be evaluated.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.3|727.1.c.3.]] Activated Abilities that become Active from Dependent Keywords can be activated at their associated timing after that ability has been granted
- [[##rule 812.1.c|812.1.c.]] As long as a card different than the one with the Legion ability has been Finalized on the same turn then the Dependent Ability is Active on the card with Legion.
- [[##rule 824.1.c|824.1.c.]] As long as the controlling player has [N] XP, then the Dependent Ability will be be Active on the card with Level
- [[##rule 824.1.c.1|824.1.c.1.]] If the controller of the card with Level changes, then the Dependent Ability will be rendered Active or Inactive based on the new controller’s XP.

####  active player

**Active Player**

- [[##rule 337.1.c.3|337.1.c.3.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are no Pending Items, the controller of the newest item on the chain gains Priority and becomes the Active Player. Proceed to Step 2: Execute.

####  add reactions

**Add Reactions**

- [[##rule 429.3|429.3.]] Activated abilities that Add resources and have the Reaction tag can be activated during the playing or resolution of other spells and abilities, any time that those spells or abilities require resources be paid.  Example: A player can add Energy and Power through any means before initiating the process of playing a spell. After initiating that process, in the Pay Costs step, they may activate Add Reactions to add Energy or Power to pay costs.

####  added

**Added**

- [[##rule 135.2.e.5.b|135.2.e.5.b.]] When Added to a player’s Rune Pool, [A] can be spent to pay a Power cost of any Domain.
- [[##rule 167|167.]] All Abilities that include the action "Add" are abilities that are adding Energy or Power to the Rune Pool. See rule 429. Add for more information.
- [[##rule 337.1.c|337.1.c.]] Units, Gear, and abilities that Add resources resolve immediately when Finalized and do not progress to Step 2: Execute.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 346.1|346.1.]] Focus will not pass in this way if the chain opened as a result of a triggered ability being added to the chain, nor if it opened as a result of an Add ability being added to the chain. Example: the Initial Chain opens as a result of triggered abilities being added to the chain, so when the last item on the Initial Chain resolves and the turn returns to an Open State, Focus will not pass.
- [[##rule 357.1.a|357.1.a.]] During this step, the card's controller can use activated abilities with the Reaction tag that Add resources to add Energy and Power to pay the card's costs.  See rule 164. Rune Pools and rule 429. Add for more information.
- [[##rule 429|429.]] Add
- [[##rule 429.1|429.1.]] Adding is the action of putting resources into a player's Rune Pool.
- [[##rule 429.2|429.2.]] Spells, triggered abilities, and activated abilities that Add resources ﬁnalize immediately.
- [[##rule 429.2.a|429.2.a.]] Priority and Focus will not pass from Add abilities being ﬁnalized or resolving, and will resolve before any other outstanding items on the chain are ﬁnalized.
- [[##rule 429.3|429.3.]] Activated abilities that Add resources and have the Reaction tag can be activated during the playing or resolution of other spells and abilities, any time that those spells or abilities require resources be paid.  Example: A player can add Energy and Power through any means before initiating the process of playing a spell. After initiating that process, in the Pay Costs step, they may activate Add Reactions to add Energy or Power to pay costs.
- [[##rule 429.3.a|429.3.a.]] When an Add ability is activated in this way, it immediately ﬁnalizes and resolves, even during the resolution of spells and abilities.
- [[##rule 429.4|429.4.]] Adding is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 429.4.a|429.4.a.]] Players may only Add resources when Game Effects direct them to do so.

####  additional costs

**Additional Costs**

- [[##rule 356.2.a.1|356.2.a.1.]] Some Additional Costs speciﬁed by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Mandatory, and must be paid to complete playing the card. They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and don't include the word "may."  Example: A unit has the passive ability "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." To play that unit, a player must kill a friendly unit.  See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 820.1.c.1|820.1.c.1.]] The Cost is an Additional Cost to be paid during the steps of playing the spell.

####  additional turns

**Additional Turns**

- [[##rule 734|734.]] Additional Turns
- [[##rule 735|735.]] Certain Game Effects will instruct a player to “take a turn after this.” These effects create a temporary Additional Turn owned by that player that is inserted into the turn queue after the current turn.
- [[##rule 737|737.]] When an Additional Turn is inserted into this queue, it does not change the Turn Order of the game. The owner of the Additional Turn just has the next queued turn. After that turn is completed, it will be removed and the queue will proceed with its previously queued turns.
- [[##rule 738|738.]] If multiple Additional Turns are queued, they are added to the queue in the order the Game Effects that generated them occurred. Example: The First Player plays, through some means, two Time Warps during their turn. The Time Warps create two Additional Turns for their controller and insert them into the turn queue after the current turn. If the turn queue is represented as [> A > B > C > D >], then these Additional Turns will appear as [> A > A* > A* > B > C > D >]. After the last Additional Turn is played, the queue returns to its previously queued turns. The “*” denotes that a turn is an Additional Turn. Example: The First Player plays Promising Future during their turn, during the resolution of which the Second and Fourth Player choose, banish, and play one Time Warp each. The Fourth Player’s Time Warp resolves ﬁrst, inserting an Additional Turn for them in the queue as such: [> A > D* > B > C > D >]. The Second Player’s Time Warp resolves afterwards, inserting that turn: [> A > B* > D* > B > C > D >]. When the First Player passes the turn, the Second Player will take their turn, followed by the Fourth Player, after which the queue returns to its previously queued turns.

####  all effects operating on objects have been applied once

**All Effects Operating On Objects Have Been Applied Once**

- [[##rule 471|471.]] The layers are applied repeatedly until all effects operating on objects have been applied once and no changes have been processed.

####  all forms of closed state

**All Forms Of Closed State**

- [[##rule 158.2.b.2|158.2.b.2.]] In addition to all prior cases, may also be played during all forms of Closed State.

####  allies

**Allies**

- [[##rule 732|732.]] XP is not shared between Allies in Game Modes with Teammates.

####  alone

**Alone**

- [[##rule 741.1|741.1.]] A unit is alone when there are no other friendly units at the same location.
- [[##rule 741.2|741.2.]] A unit is one on one when it and the enemy unit at the same location are both alone.

####  ambush

**Ambush**

- [[##rule 822|822.]] Ambush
- [[##rule 822.1|822.1.]] Ambush is a Passive Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 822.2|822.2.]] Multiple instances of Ambush are redundant.
- [[##rule 822.3|822.3.]] If there are no units at the location chosen before Finalization completes for any reason, then it is no longer a valid location by Ambush’s reasoning and cannot be played there
- [[##rule 822.3.a|822.3.a.]] Other effects and permissions may still enable this Unit to be able to be played to the selected location, but Ambush’s permission will not be valid
- [[##rule 822.4|822.4.]] Ambush, and whether or not a unit has Ambush, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

####  assault

**Assault**

- [[##rule 807|807.]] Assault

####  at any time

**At Any Time**

- [[##rule 410.1.a|410.1.a.]] A Discretionary Action is a Game Action that may be performed at any time during a player's turn during a Neutral Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.

####  attached

**Attached**

- [[##rule 135.4|135.4.]] A card’s printed Rules Text is Inactive while that card is Attached to another card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 135.4.b|135.4.b.]] Any granted or appended Rules Text on a card is still Active even if that card is Attached to another card.
- [[##rule 136.2.b|136.2.b.]] Effect Text is inactive unless the card with the Effect Text is Attached to another card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 136.2.c|136.2.c.]] The abilities in the Effect Text section of a card are appended to the Rules Text of the card to which the card with the Effect Text is Attached.
- [[##rule 137.3|137.3.]] A card’s Might Bonus modulates the Might of the card to which the card that has the Might Bonus is Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 137.3.a|137.3.a.]] The Might Bonus is applied while Attached and stops applying as soon as the card with the Might Bonus is no longer Attached.
- [[##rule 137.3.b|137.3.b.]] If the card to which a card with a Might Bonus is Attached has no Might value, the Might Bonus is ignored.
- [[##rule 434|434.]] Attach
- [[##rule 434.1|434.1.]] Attaching is the act of linking two cards on the board together to combine their effects in some way. This causes one or more cards to become Attached and at least one card to become a Top-Most Card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 434.1.a|434.1.a.]] Attaching affects two cards at once.
- [[##rule 434.1.a.1|434.1.a.1.]] One card will be designated as the one being Attached, and thus become Attached. The other will become the Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 434.1.b|434.1.b.]] This is represented by physically laying the Top-Most card on top of the other or others such that all Effect Texts and Might Bonuses are showing, but nothing else from the card or cards Attached.
- [[##rule 434.1.b.1|434.1.b.1.]] In the situation where there is more than one card attached to the Top-Most card, they should be stacked in such a way that all Effect Text boxes and Might Bonuses are readable. The order of the Attached cards has no bearing on the application of effects.
- [[##rule 434.1.c|434.1.c.]] The Top-Most card has all Effect Text of all cards Attached to it appended to its Rules Text.
- [[##rule 434.1.d|434.1.d.]] The Top-Most Card has its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of all cards Attached to it.
- [[##rule 434.1.e|434.1.e.]] Attaching one or more cards will cause those cards’ Rules Text to become Inactive for as long as they remain Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 434.1.f|434.1.f.]] Attaching a card to a new Top-Most Card will cause it to Detach from the card to which it is currently Attached.
- [[##rule 434.1.g|434.1.g.]] Attaching a card to its current Top-Most Card  will not have any effect.
- [[##rule 434.1.h|434.1.h.]] If a Game Effect instructs a player to Attach a card to its current Top-Most Card, nothing additional happens.
- [[##rule 434.2|434.2.]] Attaching is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 434.2.a|434.2.a.]] Players may only Attach cards when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 434.3|434.3.]] Attaching cards does not inherently choose or specify a target. However, Game Effects that Attach cards may do so.
- [[##rule 435.1|435.1.]] Detaching is the act of unlinking two cards that are currently linked through the act of Attaching. This causes one to cease being Attached, and potentially causes the other to cease being a Top-Most card.
- [[##rule 435.1.a|435.1.a.]] Detaching affects only cards that are currently Attached to another card.
- [[##rule 435.1.a.1|435.1.a.1.]] Game effects that instruct a player to Detach a card that is currently not Attached to anything will do nothing.
- [[##rule 435.1.b|435.1.b.]] When one or more cards become Detached, they cease to be in the Attached state.
- [[##rule 435.1.b.2|435.1.b.2.]] If the Top-Most Card no longer has any cards Attached to it after this, it is no longer a Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 435.4.b|435.4.b.]] If the Attached card was Detached because the Top-Most Card changed zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, then the location that the Attached Card will Detach to is the last location the Top-Most Card was at before changing from a board zone to a non-board zone.
- [[##rule 472.2.c|472.2.c.]] Abilities of Effect Text of Attached cards are appended in this layer.
- [[##rule 472.3.c|472.3.c.]] Might Bonuses of Attached cards are applied in this layer.
- [[##rule 717|717.]] Attaching is a limited action that causes cards to become linked to each other to combine their effects in some way. This causes one card to become Attached and the other to become A Top-Most Card. See rule 434. Attach for more information.
- [[##rule 718|718.]] Attached is the state of a card being linked to another card in this way.
- [[##rule 718.5|718.5.]] Attached cards still have all properties of being a card on the board while in this state.
- [[##rule 718.5.a|718.5.a.]] Attached cards still have all Types and Tags while Attached.
- [[##rule 718.5.b|718.5.b.]] Attached cards still can be chosen or targeted by game effects while Attached.
- [[##rule 718.5.c|718.5.c.]] Attached cards cannot be moved separately from the Top-Most Card they are Attached to.
- [[##rule 718.5.d|718.5.d.]] A card may be Attached only to a single Top-Most card at a time.
- [[##rule 718.5.e|718.5.e.]] Attached cards may have different Controllers from their Top-Most card.
- [[##rule 718.5.f|718.5.f.]] Changes in Control of the Top-Most card do not impact Control of Attached cards and vice versa.
- [[##rule 718.5.g|718.5.g.]] An Attached card still appends the abilities in its Effect Text to the Rules Text of the Top-Most card and modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by its Might Bonus.
- [[##rule 719|719.]] A Top-Most Card is a card that has one or more cards linked to it through the process of Attaching.
- [[##rule 719.1|719.1.]] The Effect Text of all cards Attached to this card are appended to the Rules Text of this card for as long as they remain Attached.
- [[##rule 719.2|719.2.]] This card ceases being a Top-Most Card when there are no longer any cards Attached to it.
- [[##rule 719.3|719.3.]] A Top-Most Card and all cards Attached to it are at the same location.
- [[##rule 719.3.a|719.3.a.]] When the Top-Most Card moves, all Attached cards move with it.
- [[##rule 719.4|719.4.]] The Exhausted and Ready state of the Top-Most card does not affect nor change the status of the Attached cards and vice versa.
- [[##rule 719.5|719.5.]] When a Top-Most Card changes zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, all Attached cards Detach from it, remaining in their current zones.
- [[##rule 724|724.]] Effect Text is Inactive unless the card with the Effect Text is Attached.
- [[##rule 725.1|725.1.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Attaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Attaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Attaches.
- [[##rule 725.2|725.2.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Detaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Detaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Detaches.
- [[##rule 725.3|725.3.]] If an Attached card has an Equip ability, the Weaponmaster keyword can  that Equip ability and any abilities that passively modify that Equip ability.
- [[##rule 818.1.b.2|818.1.b.2.]] The chosen Unit will become the Top-Most Card for the Attach action.
- [[##rule 818.1.c.2|818.1.c.2.]] Equip is functionally short for “[Cost]: Attach this gear to a unit you control.”
- [[##rule 818.2|818.2.]] When the Attach action completes from this keyword, the Unit that was chosen is considered to have been Equipped by the Gear with this ability.
- [[##rule 818.3|818.3.]] Equipped is the state of a Top-Most Card being Attached by one or more cards that are Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.3.a|818.3.a.]] The state of being Equipped is synchronous with that of the Attached state of the Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.3.b|818.3.b.]] A Top-Most Card is Equipped as long as one or more of its Attached cards are Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.3.c|818.3.c.]] The state of being Equipped corresponds to a Top-Most card having a card with Equip that is Attached to it.
- [[##rule 819.1.c|819.1.c.]] Quick-Draw allows cards to be played and Attached using Reaction timing.
- [[##rule 819.1.d|819.1.d.]] Quick-Draw is functionally short for “[Reaction]” and “When you play this, attach it to a Unit you control.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 821.1.b|821.1.b.]] Weaponmaster is a Play Effect that chooses an Equipment you control and allows you to pay its Equip cost at a discount, regardless of the usual timing of the Equip ability, to Attach that Equipment to the unit with Weaponmaster.
- [[##rule 821.1.c.5|821.1.c.5.]] If the chosen card’s Equip cost can’t be paid, if it can’t be detached from its current Top-Most card, or if it can’t be attached to the unit with the Weaponmaster ability, it stays in its current location, Attached to anything it was already Attached to.

####  attaches

**Attaches**

- [[##rule 434.4|434.4.]] When a card Attaches to a card, its location becomes the same as the new Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 725.1|725.1.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Attaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Attaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Attaches.
- [[##rule 818.1.b|818.1.b.]] Equip has a cost to activate and Attaches the card with Equip to a chosen Unit when the cost is paid.

####  attachment

**Attachment**

- [[##rule 135.4|135.4.]] A card’s printed Rules Text is Inactive while that card is Attached to another card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 136.2.b|136.2.b.]] Effect Text is inactive unless the card with the Effect Text is Attached to another card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 137.3|137.3.]] A card’s Might Bonus modulates the Might of the card to which the card that has the Might Bonus is Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 151.2|151.2.]] Gear cannot normally become located at a Battleﬁeld unless by some special means. Example: Gear are always played to Base. The only exception is a gear played from Facedown, which is played to the Battleﬁeld it was played from. Gear can also become located at a Battleﬁeld if they are attached to a unit who becomes located at a Battleﬁeld. See rule 811. Hidden for more information. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 434.1|434.1.]] Attaching is the act of linking two cards on the board together to combine their effects in some way. This causes one or more cards to become Attached and at least one card to become a Top-Most Card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 434.1.e|434.1.e.]] Attaching one or more cards will cause those cards’ Rules Text to become Inactive for as long as they remain Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 716|716.]] Attachment
- [[##rule 818.5.a|818.5.a.]] Whether or not a Gear has Equip may be d even if the Rules Text of the Gear is Inactive. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 819.1.d|819.1.d.]] Quick-Draw is functionally short for “[Reaction]” and “When you play this, attach it to a Unit you control.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 821.1.c|821.1.c.]] Weaponmaster is functionally short for: “When you play me, you may choose a Card you control with the Equipment tag. Necessary portions of its Rules Text are no longer Inactive if they are currently Inactive. Pay the cost of its Equip ability, reduced by [A], to attach it to this unit.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.

####  attack triggers

**Attack Triggers**

- [[##rule 383.4.e|383.4.e.]] Attack Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Attacker designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat.

####  attacker

**Attacker**

- [[##rule 323.2|323.2.]] 2. Assign or Remove the Attacker or Defender designation from Units as needed if there is a Combat in progress
