- [[##rule 323.2.c|323.2.c.]] If there are Units at locations other than the Battleﬁeld that the Combat is taking place at, but have either Attacker or Defender designations, they lose those designations now
- [[##rule 383.4.e|383.4.e.]] Attack Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Attacker designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2|383.4.e.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Attacker designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2.a|383.4.e.2.a.]] These triggers will only have their condition checked once per combat, despite a Unit being able to gain and lose the Attacker designation multiple times in the same combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2.b|383.4.e.2.b.]] If the trigger condition contains other requirements besides attacking and if those requirements are not fulﬁlled when the unit gains the Attacker designation, it will not trigger in that combat.
- [[##rule 459.2.b|459.2.b.]] 1. Establish who is Attacker and who is Defender.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.1|459.2.b.1.]] The Attacker is the player whose unit(s) applied the Contested status to the Battleﬁeld. They gain the Attacker designation now.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.3|459.2.b.3.]] Units at the Contested Battleﬁeld controlled by the Attacker gain the Attacker designation now.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.3.a|459.2.b.3.a.]] If a Unit controlled by the Attacker becomes present at this Battleﬁeld after this moment, it will gain the Attacker designation during the Cleanup phase following the action that caused it to become present
- [[##rule 459.2.c|459.2.c.]] 2. The Attacker gains Focus.
- [[##rule 459.2.d|459.2.d.]] 3. Add items to the Combat Chain if establishing Attacker and Defender has caused Triggered Abilities to become Pending.
- [[##rule 459.2.d.1|459.2.d.1.]] The Attacking player, who has Focus, places Triggered Abilities on the Chain ﬁrst, followed by all non-Defender players in Turn Order, followed by the Defending Player.
- [[##rule 460.1|460.1.]] If both Attacking and Defending units remain at this battleﬁeld, the following Tasks become Outstanding, in the speciﬁed order:
- [[##rule 460.2|460.2.]] 1. When the Showdown closes, Attackers and Defenders resolve Combat Damage at the Battleﬁeld that was attacked, using their current Might.
- [[##rule 460.2.c|460.2.c.]] Starting with the Attacker, each player assigns an amount of damage equal to their summed Might among the other's Units.
- [[##rule 461.1.a.2|461.1.a.2.]] Insert “3d. Recall Attackers present at the Battleﬁeld if Defenders are still present.” See rule 449. Recalls for more information.

####  attacker designation

**Attacker Designation**

- [[##rule 459.2.b.1|459.2.b.1.]] The Attacker is the player whose unit(s) applied the Contested status to the Battleﬁeld. They gain the Attacker designation now.

####  attacking units

**Attacking Units**

- [[##rule 460.2.a|460.2.a.]] Sum the Might of all Attacking Units.

####  back side

**Back Side**

####  backline

**Backline**

- [[##rule 826|826.]] Backline
- [[##rule 826.1|826.1.]] Backline is a Passive Ability keyword.

####  banishing

**Banishing**

- [[##rule 427.1|427.1.]] Banishing is the action of placing a card from any zone to Banishment.  See rule 108.6. Banishment for more information.
- [[##rule 427.2|427.2.]] When a card is Banished it is placed directly into the Banishment zone from its origin.
- [[##rule 427.4|427.4.]] Banishing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 427.4.a|427.4.a.]] Players may only Banish cards or permanents when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 438.4|438.4.]] Replacing is not a subset of Banishing.
- [[##rule 438.5.a|438.5.a.]] While it resides in Banishment, it is considered to have been Replaced and not Banished.
- [[##rule 652.1|652.1.]] Banish all permanents, runes, and facedown cards they currently control and all permanents, runes, and facedown cards they own.

####  banishments

**Banishments**

- [[##rule 108.6|108.6.]] Banishments
- [[##rule 108.6.a|108.6.a.]] Each player has their own Banishment.
- [[##rule 108.6.e|108.6.e.]] The cards in any player's Banishment are Public Information. See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 427|427.]] Banish
- [[##rule 427.1|427.1.]] Banishing is the action of placing a card from any zone to Banishment.  See rule 108.6. Banishment for more information.
- [[##rule 427.2|427.2.]] When a card is Banished it is placed directly into the Banishment zone from its origin.
- [[##rule 438.5.a|438.5.a.]] While it resides in Banishment, it is considered to have been Replaced and not Banished.
- [[##rule 438.6|438.6.]] If a token is Replaced it will stop existing once it begins its occupancy in Banishment.
- [[##rule 438.7.c|438.7.c.]] If there is nothing in Banishment to swap back to, usually because a token was replaced, then this object can never swap back.

####  baron pit battleﬁeld token

**Baron Pit Battleﬁeld Token**

- [[##rule 184.9|184.9.]] The Baron Pit battleﬁeld token is a domainless battleﬁeld token with “Units can move here from anywhere.”

####  base cost(s)

**Base Cost(s)**

- [[##rule 356.1.a|356.1.a.]] If an ability or instruction allows you to play a card “for [Cost]”, replace the card’s Base Costs with [Cost].
- [[##rule 356.1.b|356.1.b.]] If an ability or instruction allows you to "ignore" one or more of a card's costs, set the appropriate Base Cost(s) of the card to zero.
- [[##rule 356.1.b.3|356.1.b.3.]] Further additional costs and/or cost increases applied in subsequent steps may raise the card's Total Cost above zero.  Example: Legion Rearguard is a Fury unit that costs 2 Energy and 0 Power and has Accelerate. A player plays Legion Rearguard and is instructed to ignore its costs, but chooses to pay the Accelerate cost. They ignore Legion Rearguard's Base Cost of 2 Energy, but the optional additional cost of 1 Energy and 1 Fury Power is added to its Total Cost and must be paid.

####  bases

**Bases**

- [[##rule 107.1|107.1.]] Bases
- [[##rule 107.1.a|107.1.a.]] Each player has their own Base.
- [[##rule 107.1.c|107.1.c.]] Permanents and Runes controlled by a player reside in that player's Base.
- [[##rule 107.1.c.1|107.1.c.1.]] Permanents attached to Permanents controlled by a player may also be found in that player’s Base.
- [[##rule 107.1.d|107.1.d.]] Permanents and Runes in Bases are Public Information.
- [[##rule 141.1.a.1|141.1.a.1.]] Units are at one of several Locations while on the Board: a Battleﬁeld or their Base.
- [[##rule 144.4.a|144.4.a.]] Units may move from their Base to a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 144.4.b|144.4.b.]] Units may move from a Battleﬁeld to their Base.
- [[##rule 146.1|146.1.]] A Unit’s Location is the Base or Battleﬁeld it currently occupies.
- [[##rule 148.1.a.1|148.1.a.1.]] Gear can only be played to a player's Base unless an effect speciﬁes otherwise.
- [[##rule 149.2|149.2.]] Gear can only be played to a player's Base unless an effect speciﬁes otherwise.
- [[##rule 149.3|149.3.]] If an unattached Gear is at a Battleﬁeld for any reason during a cleanup, then it is recalled to its controller's Base as a corrective action.  See rule 449. Recalls for more information. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 151.1|151.1.]] A Gear’s Location is the Base or Battleﬁeld it currently occupies.
- [[##rule 323.7|323.7.]] 5. Recall all Unattached non-Unit Gear at Battleﬁelds, and all Permanents and Runes in Bases other than their controller’s. Remove all Hidden cards from all Battleﬁelds that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's Trash.
- [[##rule 355.2.a|355.2.a.]] By default, Valid locations include the controller’s Base or a Battleﬁeld the controller controls.
- [[##rule 359.2.d|359.2.d.]] If it is a Gear, it enters the Board Ready at the player's Base.
- [[##rule 450|450.]] A Recall is when a Permanent is relocated from anywhere to its Base without it being a Move.
- [[##rule 457.2.a|457.2.a.]] If an effect would require a Unit be played to a Battleﬁeld with a Staged Combat or a Combat in Progress, where the controller of the played unit is not a participant, instead the Unit is played to its controller's Base.
- [[##rule 457.2.b|457.2.b.]] Any subsequent  to "here" in the corresponding effect is reassigned to the Controller's Base, where the Unit was played. Any further effects that may be invalidated are invalidated as if the effect was mistargeted. See rule 355.6. Targeting for more information on Mistargeting.

####  basic runes

**Basic Runes**

- [[##rule 163|163.]] Basic Runes
- [[##rule 163.1|163.1.]] There are six Basic Runes, each with a Domain corresponding to its name:  Fury Rune  Calm Rune  Mind Rune  Body Rune  Chaos Rune  Order Rune
- [[##rule 163.2|163.2.]] A Basic Rune always has the following two Abilities:

####  battleﬁelds

**Battleﬁelds**

- [[##rule 103|103.]] To play Riftbound, a player must have two Decks, a Champion Legend, and a number of Battleﬁelds determined by the Mode of Play.
- [[##rule 103.4|103.4.]] Battleﬁelds
- [[##rule 103.4.c|103.4.c.]] Cannot include more than one of a Battleﬁeld of the same name when there are more than one required for the deck.
- [[##rule 107.2|107.2.]] Battleﬁeld Zone
- [[##rule 107.2.a|107.2.a.]] The Battleﬁeld Zone houses multiple Battleﬁelds.
- [[##rule 107.2.b|107.2.b.]] Each Battleﬁeld is individually a Location.
- [[##rule 107.2.c|107.2.c.]] Battleﬁelds and permanents at Battleﬁelds are Public Information.
- [[##rule 107.3.c|107.3.c.]] Cards can only be placed in or occupy the Facedown Zone if the controller of the card also controls the associated Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 107.3.d|107.3.d.]] If a player loses Control of a Battleﬁeld, any cards in the Facedown Zone associated with that Battleﬁeld are removed during the next Cleanup. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information. See rule 421. Hide for more information.
- [[##rule 114|114.]] Each player sets aside their Battleﬁelds.
- [[##rule 114.1|114.1.]] Your Mode of Play will dictate how these are used and placed into the Battleﬁeld Zone.  See rule 476. Modes of Play for more information.
- [[##rule 127.1|127.1.]] For gameplay purposes, a card's Owner is the player who brought it into the game, either as their Champion Legend, one of their Battleﬁelds, or part of their Main Deck or Rune Deck. The legal owner of a card doesn't matter during gameplay.  Example: Bo didn't bring a deck, so Alice loans him a deck. During the game, Bo is considered the owner of those cards, even though legally they belong to Alice.
- [[##rule 129.2|129.2.]] There is a unique pattern of back side for each of the three categories of card: Main Deck cards, Rune Deck cards, and Battleﬁelds and Champion Legends.
- [[##rule 133.6.a|133.6.a.]] Battleﬁelds
- [[##rule 141.1.a.1|141.1.a.1.]] Units are at one of several Locations while on the Board: a Battleﬁeld or their Base.
- [[##rule 144.4.a|144.4.a.]] Units may move from their Base to a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 144.4.a.1|144.4.a.1.]] Units cannot Move to a Battleﬁeld that already has units from 2 other players present, or where a Combat is ongoing that has 2 other players as participants.
- [[##rule 144.4.b|144.4.b.]] Units may move from a Battleﬁeld to their Base.
- [[##rule 144.4.c.1|144.4.c.1.]] Units with Ganking may use their Standard Move to Move from Battleﬁeld to Battleﬁeld.  See rule 810. Ganking for more information.
- [[##rule 146.1|146.1.]] A Unit’s Location is the Base or Battleﬁeld it currently occupies.
- [[##rule 149.3|149.3.]] If an unattached Gear is at a Battleﬁeld for any reason during a cleanup, then it is recalled to its controller's Base as a corrective action.  See rule 449. Recalls for more information. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 151.1|151.1.]] A Gear’s Location is the Base or Battleﬁeld it currently occupies.
- [[##rule 151.2|151.2.]] Gear cannot normally become located at a Battleﬁeld unless by some special means. Example: Gear are always played to Base. The only exception is a gear played from Facedown, which is played to the Battleﬁeld it was played from. Gear can also become located at a Battleﬁeld if they are attached to a unit who becomes located at a Battleﬁeld. See rule 811. Hidden for more information. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 168|168.]] Battleﬁelds
- [[##rule 169|169.]] Battleﬁelds are Game Objects.
- [[##rule 169.1|169.1.]] Battleﬁelds are Owned by a player.
- [[##rule 169.2|169.2.]] Battleﬁelds are not shuffled into Decks at the start of a game.
- [[##rule 169.2.a|169.2.a.]] Battleﬁelds are not played during the course of regular play.
- [[##rule 169.2.b|169.2.b.]] Battleﬁelds are established at the start of a game and remain in place for the duration of regular play.
- [[##rule 169.3|169.3.]] Battleﬁelds cannot be Killed during the course of regular play.
- [[##rule 169.4|169.4.]] Battleﬁelds cannot be Moved.
- [[##rule 169.5|169.5.]] Battleﬁelds are Locations.
- [[##rule 169.5.a|169.5.a.]] Battleﬁelds can be Origins of moves.
- [[##rule 169.5.b|169.5.b.]] Battleﬁelds can be Destinations of moves.
- [[##rule 169.6|169.6.]] Any number of Units can be present at a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 169.7|169.7.]] Battleﬁelds can be targeted by spells or game effects.
- [[##rule 169.8|169.8.]] Battleﬁelds can have Passive Abilities. See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 169.9|169.9.]] Battleﬁelds can have Triggered Abilities. See rule 382. Triggered Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 169.10|169.10.]] Battleﬁelds can be d in different states in card text:
- [[##rule 169.10.a|169.10.a.]] Battleﬁelds can be “occupied.” This means they have a Unit present.
- [[##rule 169.10.b|169.10.b.]] Battleﬁelds can be “uncontrolled.” This means no player controls them.
- [[##rule 169.10.c|169.10.c.]] Battleﬁelds can be “open.” This means they are unoccupied and uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 170|170.]] Battleﬁelds are not Permanents.
- [[##rule 171|171.]] The number of Battleﬁelds on the Board is determined by the Mode of Play.
- [[##rule 187|187.]] Battleﬁelds
- [[##rule 187.1|187.1.]] Control is established over Battleﬁelds through the course of play.
- [[##rule 187.2|187.2.]] Control is a binary state for Battleﬁelds and an Identiﬁer for players.
- [[##rule 187.2.a|187.2.a.]] A Battleﬁeld is Controlled or Uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 187.2.b|187.2.b.]] A Battleﬁeld is Controlled by a speciﬁc player or Controlled by no one.
- [[##rule 187.3.a|187.3.a.]] Contested is a temporary status applied to the battleﬁeld when a Unit controlled by a Player who does not currently Control that Battleﬁeld Moves or otherwise becomes present there.
- [[##rule 187.3.b|187.3.b.]] A Battleﬁeld remains Contested until Control is established or re-established.
- [[##rule 187.3.c|187.3.c.]] The state of a Battleﬁeld being Contested is used to determine when Combat should occur, when a Non-Combat Showdown should occur, and when Control will change.
- [[##rule 187.4|187.4.]] Control is established by having Units at a Battleﬁeld at the end of a Showdown or Combat after applying the contested status.
- [[##rule 187.4.a|187.4.a.]] If a player controls Units at a Battleﬁeld, outside of Combat, they maintain Control of that Battleﬁeld for as long as they have Units at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 187.4.b|187.4.b.]] While a Combat or Showdown is ongoing at a Battleﬁeld, Control of that Battleﬁeld cannot change until instructed by steps of the Combat or Showdown.
- [[##rule 187.4.c|187.4.c.]] If a player has no Units at a Battleﬁeld and the turn is in an Open state, they lose Control of that Battleﬁeld in the following cleanup, unless there is a Combat or Showdown ongoing there.
- [[##rule 187.6|187.6.]] Control of a Battleﬁeld determines Control of its Abilities.
- [[##rule 187.6.a|187.6.a.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Controlled, its Controller controls its Abilities. That player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, and makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed.
- [[##rule 187.6.b|187.6.b.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Uncontrolled, its Abilities are also Uncontrolled. The Turn Player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed, and is treated as their Controller if any game rule or effect requires one. Example: The Arena’s Greatest is a battleﬁeld that reads “At the start of each player's ﬁrst Beginning Phase, that player gains 1 point.” This ability will usually trigger while the battleﬁeld has no controller. If it does, the Turn Player goes through the steps of adding the ability to the chain and receives priority after doing so, exactly as if they controlled the ability.
- [[##rule 315.2.b.2|315.2.b.2.]] 1. The Turn Player Holds all Battleﬁelds they Control. See rule 462. Scoring for more information.
- [[##rule 315.2.b.3|315.2.b.3.]] Reminder: In Modes of Play with Teams, Battleﬁelds held by a Teammate of the Turn Player during this phase are disqualiﬁed from being scored this turn by the Turn Player.
- [[##rule 316.4.a|316.4.a.]] A Combat occurs as a result of Units controlled by opposing players being present at the same Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 316.5.b|316.5.b.]] A Showdown is marked as Staged at a Battleﬁeld when the Contested status is applied to a Battleﬁeld with no current controller.
- [[##rule 316.5.b.1|316.5.b.1.]] Showdowns that occur as a result of a player moving to an empty Battleﬁeld are a stand-alone Phase and do not create a Combat.
- [[##rule 323.2.a|323.2.a.]] If there are Units present at the Battleﬁeld the Combat is taking place at, but do not have a designation, they gain the same designation as their Controller now
- [[##rule 323.2.b|323.2.b.]] If there are Units present at the Battleﬁeld the Combat is taking place at, but have the opposite designation of their controller, they lose that designation, and gain the same designation as their controller now
- [[##rule 323.2.c|323.2.c.]] If there are Units at locations other than the Battleﬁeld that the Combat is taking place at, but have either Attacker or Defender designations, they lose those designations now
- [[##rule 323.7|323.7.]] 5. Recall all Unattached non-Unit Gear at Battleﬁelds, and all Permanents and Runes in Bases other than their controller’s. Remove all Hidden cards from all Battleﬁelds that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's Trash.
- [[##rule 323.8|323.8.]] 6. Mark a Showdown as Staged at each Battleﬁeld that Contested was applied to.
- [[##rule 323.8.a|323.8.a.]] The Showdown remains Staged at each Battleﬁeld that is Contested and has units present controlled by the player that applied Contested.
- [[##rule 323.9|323.9.]] 7. Mark a Combat as Staged at each Battleﬁeld that Contested was applied to that have Units present controlled by opposing players.
- [[##rule 323.9.a|323.9.a.]] The Combat remains Staged at that Battleﬁeld as long as there are Units present from two opposing players there.
- [[##rule 323.10|323.10.]] 7a. If Units of two opposing players are no longer present at a Battleﬁeld that has a Combat Staged before it has opened, the Combat will cease being Staged
- [[##rule 323.11|323.11.]] 8. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and one or more Showdowns are Staged, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. A Showdown begins there.
- [[##rule 323.12|323.12.]] 8a. If a Showdown and Combat are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player chooses to initiate the Showdown there, the Showdown will open as a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 323.13|323.13.]] 9. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and Combat is Staged at one or more Battleﬁelds, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. Combat begins there.
- [[##rule 323.14|323.14.]] 9a. If the current state is Showdown Open State and Combat is Staged at a Battleﬁeld where there is a Non-Combat Showdown ongoing, that Showdown becomes a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 344|344.]] A Showdown begins when Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the turn is in a Neutral Open State.
- [[##rule 344.1|344.1.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested between two players, then a Showdown will be opened as the ﬁrst step of Combat.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 344.2|344.2.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the Battleﬁeld in question is uncontrolled when it becomes Contested, a Showdown is opened during the Cleanup at the end of the action that caused the Battleﬁeld to become Contested.
- [[##rule 345|345.]] As a Showdown begins, the player who applied Contested status to the Battleﬁeld gains Focus.
- [[##rule 348.2.a|348.2.a.]] If only one player’s Units remain at the Battleﬁeld, and if that player does not already Control the Battleﬁeld, that player establishes Control over the Battleﬁeld. See rule 185. Control for more information on Control.  See rule 464.1.for more information on Conquering.
- [[##rule 348.2.a.1|348.2.a.1.]] This results in a Conquer if that player has not yet scored that Battleﬁeld this turn.
- [[##rule 355.2.a|355.2.a.]] By default, Valid locations include the controller’s Base or a Battleﬁeld the controller controls.
- [[##rule 383.4.c|383.4.c.]] Conquer Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit participating in, and successfully Conquering a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.a|383.4.c.2.a.]] The Conquer Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit(s) these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from Conquering.
- [[##rule 383.4.d|383.4.d.]] Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battleﬁeld during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.a|383.4.d.2.a.]] The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.
- [[##rule 410.1.b.3|410.1.b.3.]] As long as it does not result in any forbidden action being taken or game state being created.  Example: A player can't use the Standard Move discretionary action to move a unit to a Battleﬁeld that's already occupied by Units controlled by two other players.
- [[##rule 421.1|421.1.]] Hiding a card is the act of placing a card facedown at a Battleﬁeld you control.
- [[##rule 421.3|421.3.]] Cards that are facedown at Battleﬁelds have their gameplay properties and permissions deﬁned by the effect that put them there.  Example: Cards that players Hide with the Hidden keyword can be Played for [0] on any subsequent turn as a property of the Hidden keyword.
- [[##rule 435.4.a|435.4.a.]] If the Detached card was a Gear and this causes it to become present at a Battleﬁeld, it will be Recalled during the next Cleanup.
- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 442.2.c|442.2.c.]] If an action would require a Move that would cause a Unit to become present in a Location where it cannot move for any reason, such as a Battleﬁeld with two players that are not the controller of the Unit performing this Move action are in a Combat or such a Combat is Staged, it instead Recalls. See rule 449. Recalls for more information.
- [[##rule 444.2|444.2.]] Units cannot Move to a Battleﬁeld that already has units from 2 other players present by any means.
- [[##rule 445|445.]] The Destination becomes Contested if it is a Battleﬁeld not controlled by the controller of the Unit or Units that moved.
- [[##rule 446.1|446.1.]] A Showdown is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested while it has no Units present from any player other than those that just moved.
- [[##rule 447.1|447.1.]] A Combat is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested and Units controlled by opposing players, or when a Move causes Units controlled by opposing players to become present in the same Battleﬁeld where a Showdown is ongoing. See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 455|455.]] A Combat occurs when a Cleanup occurs, there are no items on the Chain, there is a staged Combat at a Battleﬁeld, and no Showdown or Combat is ongoing at any other Battleﬁeld. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 456|456.]] Combat is considered Staged if there are units controlled by two opposing players at a Battleﬁeld but the Steps of Combat have not been initiated.
- [[##rule 456.1|456.1.]] If more than one Battleﬁeld has Units controlled by opposing players at it at the same time, the Turn Player decides which Combat to resolve ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 456.3|456.3.]] If a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown, it will open as a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.
- [[##rule 457.2|457.2.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid to be chosen as a location to play one or more Units by a player not involved in that Combat by any means,
- [[##rule 457.2.a|457.2.a.]] If an effect would require a Unit be played to a Battleﬁeld with a Staged Combat or a Combat in Progress, where the controller of the played unit is not a participant, instead the Unit is played to its controller's Base.
- [[##rule 459.1|459.1.]] Combat will open in one of two ways: when a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown; or when the turn is in a Showdown Open State and a Combat is staged at the Battleﬁeld where the current Showdown is ongoing. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.1|459.2.b.1.]] The Attacker is the player whose unit(s) applied the Contested status to the Battleﬁeld. They gain the Attacker designation now.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.2|459.2.b.2.]] The Defender is the player who did not apply the Contested status to the Battleﬁeld. They gain the Defender designation now.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.3.a|459.2.b.3.a.]] If a Unit controlled by the Attacker becomes present at this Battleﬁeld after this moment, it will gain the Attacker designation during the Cleanup phase following the action that caused it to become present
- [[##rule 459.2.b.4.a|459.2.b.4.a.]] If a Unit controlled by the Defender becomes present at this Battleﬁeld after this moment it will gain the Defender designation during the Cleanup phase following the action that caused it to become present
- [[##rule 460.2|460.2.]] 1. When the Showdown closes, Attackers and Defenders resolve Combat Damage at the Battleﬁeld that was attacked, using their current Might.
- [[##rule 461.1.a.2|461.1.a.2.]] Insert “3d. Recall Attackers present at the Battleﬁeld if Defenders are still present.” See rule 449. Recalls for more information.
- [[##rule 461.5.b|461.5.b.]] If there are no Units remaining here controlled by any player, the Battleﬁeld becomes Uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 461.5.c|461.5.c.]] Remove all Hidden cards from this Battleﬁeld that do not share a controller with the Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 461.5.d|461.5.d.]] Establishing Control results in a Conquer if that player has not yet scored this Battleﬁeld this turn. See rule 185. Control for more information on Control.  See rule 464.1.for more information on Conquering.
- [[##rule 461.5.e|461.5.e.]] This does not have to be the player that applied Contested to the Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 463|463.]] Scoring is the act of a Player gaining a point through the process of seizing or maintaining control over Battleﬁelds.
- [[##rule 464.1|464.1.]] Conquer: A player gains Control of a Battleﬁeld they did not yet Score this turn.
- [[##rule 464.1.a|464.1.a.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds under the Control of a teammate during the Beginning Phase are also disqualiﬁed from being Scored through Conquer by any means.
- [[##rule 464.1.b|464.1.b.]] A player will gain control of a Battleﬁeld after establishing Control by applying Contested ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 464.2|464.2.]] Hold: A player maintains Control of a Battleﬁeld during their Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 465|465.]] A player may only Score, from either method, once per Battleﬁeld per turn.
- [[##rule 466.1.b.2|466.1.b.2.]] If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has Scored every Battleﬁeld through either method this turn, that player Gains the Winning Point. If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has not Scored every Battleﬁeld this turn, that player draws a card.
- [[##rule 466.2|466.2.]] Trigger Score abilities at the Battleﬁeld that Scored.
- [[##rule 466.2.a|466.2.a.]] Conquer abilities trigger at a Battleﬁeld that was Conquered.
- [[##rule 466.2.b|466.2.b.]] Hold abilities trigger at a Battleﬁeld that was Held.
- [[##rule 466.2.c|466.2.c.]] These will only trigger when the Battleﬁeld is Scored; I.E. These cannot be triggered more than once per turn for a player.
- [[##rule 478.4|478.4.]] Battleﬁeld Count: Determines how many Battleﬁelds are in play, contributed by players, during play.
- [[##rule 478.4.b|478.4.b.]] This may involve utilizing less Battleﬁelds than there are players.
- [[##rule 480.4|480.4.]] Battleﬁeld Count: 2
- [[##rule 480.4.a|480.4.a.]] Each player provides three (3) Battleﬁelds, included in their deck during deck building. Only 1 will be used, chosen during setup.
- [[##rule 480.5|480.5.]] Setup: Each player randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously in the Battleﬁeld Zone.
- [[##rule 481.4|481.4.]] Battleﬁeld Count: 2
- [[##rule 481.4.a|481.4.a.]] Each player provides three (3) Battleﬁelds, included in their deck during deck building. Only 1 will be used, chosen during setup.
- [[##rule 481.5|481.5.]] Setup: Each player selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are set aside and will not be used for this round of play. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously in the Battleﬁeld Zone. After this game, the Battleﬁelds that were used are to be removed and not selected again for this Match. One of the remaining Battleﬁelds that were set aside must be chosen instead.
- [[##rule 481.6|481.6.]] Format: Best of 3. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the game. The winner of that game earns One Game Win. Players then reset the game state, remove the Battleﬁelds in play from the game, choose new Battleﬁelds from those set aside, and play again. The ﬁrst player to earn Two Game Wins wins the match.
- [[##rule 482.4|482.4.]] Battleﬁeld Count: 3
- [[##rule 482.5|482.5.]] Setup: Each player randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are discarded and will not be used for this game. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously between the three Players before play and will be used for this game.
- [[##rule 483.4|483.4.]] Battleﬁeld Count: 3
- [[##rule 483.4.a|483.4.a.]] Each player provides three (3) Battleﬁelds, included in their deck during deck building.
- [[##rule 483.4.b|483.4.b.]] The player who is taking the ﬁrst turn removes their Battleﬁelds. They will not be used.
- [[##rule 483.5|483.5.]] Setup: Each player who is not going ﬁrst randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously between the players before play and will be used for this game.
- [[##rule 484.4|484.4.]] Battleﬁeld Count: 3
- [[##rule 484.4.a|484.4.a.]] Each player provides three (3) Battleﬁelds, included in their deck during deck building.
- [[##rule 484.5.a|484.5.a.]] Each player who is not going ﬁrst randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously between the players before play and will be used for this game.
- [[##rule 484.5.b|484.5.b.]] The player who is taking the ﬁrst turn removes their Battleﬁelds. They will not be used.
- [[##rule 484.8.b|484.8.b.]] Battleﬁelds controlled during the Beginning Phase of a player's turn by that player's teammate are disqualiﬁed from being scored by that Team, that turn. Example: A player may not induce their partner to retreat, and then conquer a Battleﬁeld their teammate was controlling.
- [[##rule 484.8.c.1|484.8.c.1.]] Players may not Hide cards at Battleﬁelds controlled by their Teammate.
- [[##rule 484.8.f.1|484.8.f.1.]] When scoring the Final Point from Conquer, a player must Score each Battleﬁeld in the same turn, excepting any that were occupied by their ally during that turn’s Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 484.8.h|484.8.h.]] Teammates may not utilize the same Battleﬁelds.
- [[##rule 652.2|652.2.]] Remove the Battleﬁeld they contributed to the game if it is in use.

####  battleﬁelds controlled

**Battleﬁelds Controlled**

- [[##rule 442.2.b|442.2.b.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds Controlled by a player’s teammates are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units that player controls.

####  becoming invalid

**Becoming Invalid**

- [[##rule 359.3.e.9|359.3.e.9.]] The process for a card's choice becoming Invalid or Unavailable is referred to as mistargeting.  Example: A spell has the instruction "Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld." Before that instruction can execute, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The instruction will not be executed, because it speciﬁes that the unit it chooses must be at a Battleﬁeld, and by the time it attempted to execute, the unit was no longer valid as a choice.

####  beginning phase

**Beginning Phase**

- [[##rule 383.4.d|383.4.d.]] Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battleﬁeld during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.a|383.4.d.2.a.]] The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.
- [[##rule 410.2.b|410.2.b.]] These actions can only be taken when a player is instructed to do so as the execution of an effect or during their speciﬁed occasion during the turn.  Example: A player may Draw during the Draw Step of the Beginning Phase of their turn or when instructed to do so by a spell or ability. They can't choose to Draw at any other time.
- [[##rule 413.2.a|413.2.a.]] Each player draws 1 during the Draw Step of their Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 415.3.a|415.3.a.]] A player Readies all non-spell Game Objects they Control during the Ready Step of the Beginning Phase on their turn.
- [[##rule 464.1.a|464.1.a.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds under the Control of a teammate during the Beginning Phase are also disqualiﬁed from being Scored through Conquer by any means.
- [[##rule 464.2|464.2.]] Hold: A player maintains Control of a Battleﬁeld during their Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 484.8.b|484.8.b.]] Battleﬁelds controlled during the Beginning Phase of a player's turn by that player's teammate are disqualiﬁed from being scored by that Team, that turn. Example: A player may not induce their partner to retreat, and then conquer a Battleﬁeld their teammate was controlling.
- [[##rule 484.8.f.1|484.8.f.1.]] When scoring the Final Point from Conquer, a player must Score each Battleﬁeld in the same turn, excepting any that were occupied by their ally during that turn’s Beginning Phase.

####  bird token

**Bird Token**

- [[##rule 184.7|184.7.]] A 1 [M] Bird token is a domainless unit token with 1 Might, the Bird tag, and the Deflect keyword. See rule 809. Deflect for more information.

####  board

**Board**

- [[##rule 106|106.]] The Play Area is a collection of logical Zones that are deﬁned by their behaviors and relationships to Players. These Zones are grouped into The Board and Non-Board Zones.
- [[##rule 107|107.]] The Board
- [[##rule 134.2.d|134.2.d.]] Body is associated with the color orange and represented by a blocky diamond-shaped symbol. Its shorthand is [O].
- [[##rule 141.1.a|141.1.a.]] While on the Board:
- [[##rule 141.1.a.1|141.1.a.1.]] Units are at one of several Locations while on the Board: a Battleﬁeld or their Base.
- [[##rule 141.1.a.2|141.1.a.2.]] Units and their details are Public Information while on the Board.
- [[##rule 141.1.b.2|141.1.b.2.]] They retain the properties of being a Unit, but are not on the Board and thus cannot take actions or be affected by spells, abilities, or game actions that target Units on the Board.
- [[##rule 148.1.a|148.1.a.]] While on the Board.
- [[##rule 148.1.a.2|148.1.a.2.]] Gear and their details are Public Information while on the Board.
- [[##rule 148.1.b.2|148.1.b.2.]] They retain the properties of being Gear, but are not on the Board and thus cannot take actions or be affected by spells, abilities, or game actions that affect Gear on the Board.
- [[##rule 160.1.a|160.1.a.]] This means, despite remaining on the Board until Recycled or otherwise removed from the board, it is not a Permanent.
- [[##rule 171|171.]] The number of Battleﬁelds on the Board is determined by the Mode of Play.
- [[##rule 359.2.d|359.2.d.]] If it is a Gear, it enters the Board Ready at the player's Base.
- [[##rule 365.1|365.1.]] Passive Abilities of Permanents are typically only active while on the Board.
- [[##rule 366.1|366.1.]] Passive Abilities of cards in zones that are outside of the Board will self-describe their context.  Example: The passive ability "Play me only during an opponent's turn." applies in any zone from which that card can be played.
- [[##rule 380|380.]] Can primarily be activated while on the Board.
- [[##rule 384.1|384.1.]] Typically active while on the Board.
- [[##rule 384.2|384.2.]] Triggered Abilities of Permanents are only able to have their Conditions evaluated while on the Board.
- [[##rule 385.1|385.1.]] Triggered Abilities on cards outside of the Board rely on the Information Level of the zone they are in.
- [[##rule 385.2|385.2.]] Triggered Abilities outside of the Board will self-describe their context.  Example: The triggered ability "When you conquer, you may discard 1 to return this from your trash to your hand." triggers while the card it's on is in the trash, and not anywhere else.
- [[##rule 420.1|420.1.]] Moving is the act of a Game Object moving between two Locations on The Board. See rule 440. Movement for more information on movement.
- [[##rule 423.1|423.1.]] Stunning is the act of selecting one or more Units on the Board and rendering them Stunned.
- [[##rule 441.1|441.1.]] A Permanent changing its position from any space on the Board to another space on the Board is a Move, unless it is caused by a corrective Recall.  See rule 420. Move for more information.
- [[##rule 801.3.a.3|801.3.a.3.]] If an effect that grants a Keyword does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that Game Object remains on the Board or in its current Non-Board Zone.
- [[##rule 801.3.b.2|801.3.b.2.]] If an effect that removes a Keyword does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that Game Object remains on the Board or in its current Non-Board Zone.

####  board exhausted

**Board Exhausted**

- [[##rule 143.4|143.4.]] Units enter the Board exhausted.
- [[##rule 359.2.c|359.2.c.]] If it is a Unit, it enters the Board exhausted at the Location that was chosen.

####  bonus damage

**Bonus Damage**

- [[##rule 417.4|417.4.]] Dealing can have the intrinsic property of Bonus Damage.
- [[##rule 417.5|417.5.]] Bonus Damage is a property granted to the action of Dealing and alters the amount of Damage distributed by this action.  See rule 712. Bonus Damage for more information.
- [[##rule 712|712.]] Bonus Damage
- [[##rule 713|713.]] Bonus Damage is an intrinsic property that can be granted to Deal actions that influence the amount of Damage that the action is distributing.
- [[##rule 714|714.]] If more than one instance of Bonus Damage is applied or granted to a Deal action, all instances are summed and applied once.
- [[##rule 714.2|714.2.]] If, for any reason, Bonus Damage would be a negative number, then no Bonus Damage is applied to the action.
- [[##rule 715.1|715.1.]] If the Deal action has a single target, the amount of Damage to that target will be increased by the Bonus Damage granted to it.
- [[##rule 715.2|715.2.]] If the Deal action has multiple targets, the amount of Damage dealt to each target is increased by Bonus Damage individually and separately.  Example: Singularity is a spell that says “Deal 6 to each of up to two units.” A player plays Singularity while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Singularity deals 1 Bonus Damage to both of its targets, dealing 7 to each.
- [[##rule 715.3|715.3.]] If the Deal action Splits damage, then the Bonus Damage applies to the amount of Damage that will be Split. This can alter the number of targets eligible to be chosen.  Example: Volibear, Furious is a unit that says in part “When I attack, deal 5 damage split among any number of enemy units here.” A player attacks with Volibear, Furious while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Volibear, Furious now deals 6 damage split among any number of enemy units at its location, and can choose to split that damage among up to 6 units rather than the usual 5.
- [[##rule 715.4|715.4.]] If no damage was Dealt, because it was replaced or reduced by any means, then Bonus Damage will not apply.

####  brush battleﬁeld token

**Brush Battleﬁeld Token**

- [[##rule 184.8|184.8.]] A Brush battleﬁeld token is a domainless battleﬁeld token with “Bird, Cat, Dog, Poro, and Ivern units here have +1 [M]” and “When you score here, you may replace this with the battleﬁeld it replaced.”

####  buff counter

**Buff Counter**

- [[##rule 426.1.b|426.1.b.]] To Buff a unit, place a Buff Counter on it if it does not have one already
- [[##rule 426.1.b.1|426.1.b.1.]] If the unit already has a Buff Counter on it, it does not get another one.
- [[##rule 426.1.c|426.1.c.]] Units with Buff Counters can still be chosen for actions that Buff units, but will not be Buffed as part of the execution.  Example: A spell reads "Buff a unit. Then, if it was buffed this way, draw a card." It will place a buff counter on a unit that has no buff counter, and then its controller will draw a card. However, if the player chooses a unit with a buff counter on it already, then the card will not be drawn.

####  buffed

**Buffed**

- [[##rule 109.2|109.2.]] The State of all Game Objects in the Play Area is also Public Information.  Examples:   If a Unit is Buffed  If a Gear is Exhausted  Etc.
- [[##rule 110|110.]] Whenever a Game Object changes zones to or from a Non-Board Zone, all Temporary Modiﬁcations of all kinds cease to be tracked on it in all capacities.  Examples:  Damage is cleared.  Buffs are removed.  Granted Keywords are no longer granted.
- [[##rule 426|426.]] Buff
- [[##rule 426.1|426.1.]] Bufﬁng is the action of placing a Buff counter on a Unit.  See rule 701. Buffs for more information.
- [[##rule 426.1.a|426.1.a.]] A Buff is also an object.
- [[##rule 426.1.b|426.1.b.]] To Buff a unit, place a Buff Counter on it if it does not have one already
- [[##rule 426.1.c|426.1.c.]] Units with Buff Counters can still be chosen for actions that Buff units, but will not be Buffed as part of the execution.  Example: A spell reads "Buff a unit. Then, if it was buffed this way, draw a card." It will place a buff counter on a unit that has no buff counter, and then its controller will draw a card. However, if the player chooses a unit with a buff counter on it already, then the card will not be drawn.
- [[##rule 426.2.a|426.2.a.]] Players may only Buff units when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 426.3|426.3.]] This action is formatted as "Buff [one or more units]."  e.g., "Buff a unit."  e.g., "Buff a friendly unit."  e.g., "Buff two friendly units at the same battleﬁeld."
- [[##rule 701|701.]] Buffs
- [[##rule 702|702.]] Buffs are objects placed on Units.
- [[##rule 702.1|702.1.]] Buffs can be tracked with a buff reminder card from a Riftbound booster pack or with any spare object in your surroundings.
- [[##rule 702.2|702.2.]] Buffs can be added or spent.
- [[##rule 702.2.a|702.2.a.]] To Buff a Unit, a player chooses a Unit and then places a buff on it. That Unit is Buffed for as long as the buff remains on it.
- [[##rule 702.2.b|702.2.b.]] Spending a Buff removes a single Buff counter from a Unit.
- [[##rule 702.3|702.3.]] There can only be one Buff on a Unit at a time.
- [[##rule 702.3.a|702.3.a.]] If a Buff is added, or instructed to be added, on a Unit that already has a Buff, it is not placed instead.
- [[##rule 703|703.]] Each Buff individually contributes +1 Might to a Unit.
- [[##rule 704|704.]] Buffs are Game Objects and may be d, counted, or targeted by other effects as speciﬁed.
- [[##rule 705|705.]] If a Unit leaves play, remove all Buffs from it.
- [[##rule 705.1|705.1.]] Champions do not retain Buffs in the Champion Zone, even if they return there somehow.

####  bufﬁng

**Bufﬁng**

- [[##rule 426.1|426.1.]] Bufﬁng is the action of placing a Buff counter on a Unit.  See rule 701. Buffs for more information.
- [[##rule 426.2|426.2.]] Bufﬁng is a Limited Action.

####  burn out

**Burn Out**

- [[##rule 315.4.b.1|315.4.b.1.]] If there are no cards remaining in their Main Deck to draw, the Turn Player has been Burned Out.  See rule 431. Burn Out for more information.
- [[##rule 315.4.b.2|315.4.b.2.]] After completing the Burn Out the Turn Player still Draws 1.
- [[##rule 413.4.b|413.4.b.]] Perform a Burn Out.  See rule 431. Burn Out for more information.
- [[##rule 431|431.]] Burn Out
- [[##rule 431.1.c|431.1.c.]] If an instruction directs a player to look at or reveal cards in excess to the number of cards in a player’s Main Deck, that player looks at or Reveals as many as possible, but does not Burn Out, then proceeds with the rest of the instruction.
- [[##rule 431.1.c.1|431.1.c.1.]] If there are insufﬁcient cards among the looked at or revealed cards to perform subsequent actions to the revealed or looked at cards, any further instructions are ignored. This does not cause a Burn Out, even if those instructions would cause those cards to change zones.  Reminder: Cards are considered in the zone of origin while being looked at or revealed, in this case the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 431.2|431.2.]] To Burn Out, a player does the following in sequence:
- [[##rule 431.3|431.3.]] A player's Main Deck may remain empty as they Burn Out, usually because their trash is also empty. When they attempt to perform the original action again, it will cause another Burn Out.
- [[##rule 431.3.b|431.3.b.]] Points gained after the ﬁrst Burn Out being processed in sequence cannot be replaced or prevented by any means. Points gained after the ﬁrst Burn Out being processed in sequence that cause a player to reach or surpass the Victory Score for their game mode will cause that player to win the game if they also have more points than any opponent. The player wins immediately, without needing to wait for a cleanup to occur.
- [[##rule 436.4.a|436.4.a.]] The Player will not perform a Burn Out as a result of Predicting with too few cards in their deck.

####  burned out

**Burned Out**

- [[##rule 315.4.b.1|315.4.b.1.]] If there are no cards remaining in their Main Deck to draw, the Turn Player has been Burned Out.  See rule 431. Burn Out for more information.

####  burning out

**Burning Out**

- [[##rule 431.1|431.1.]] Burning Out is an action a player must perform if they attempt to move one or more cards from their Main Deck to any other zone in excess of the number of cards remaining in their Main Deck:
- [[##rule 431.4|431.4.]] Burning Out is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 431.5|431.5.]] Burning Out is a Replacement Effect.  See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information.

###  group C

####  calm

**Calm**

- [[##rule 134.2.b|134.2.b.]] Calm is associated with the color green and represented by a symbol resembling a leaf. Its shorthand is [G].
- [[##rule 335|335.]] Whenever a Player takes one or more actions that incur Tasks they should refer to the process of HOT FEPR: Handle Outstanding Tasks; then Finalize, Execute, Pass, Resolve.

####  card

**Card**

- [[##rule 052|052.]] Card, when written in card effects, is shorthand for "Main Deck card." Runes, legends, and battleﬁelds are not considered cards when executing the abilities and effects of game objects. They are considered cards for the purposes of these rules.
- [[##rule 125|125.]] Cards
- [[##rule 141.1.b.1|141.1.b.1.]] Units are treated as Cards, similar to when in the Hand.
- [[##rule 148.1.b.1|148.1.b.1.]] Gear are treated as Cards before Game Objects, similar to the Hand.
- [[##rule 160|160.]] Rune is a Card Type.
- [[##rule 188.1|188.1.]] When a player Plays a Card or other Game Object, they are established as that Game Object's Controller.
- [[##rule 338.1.a|338.1.a.]] Play a Card that is legally timed.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.1|338.1.a.1.]] Cards, by default, cannot be played during a Closed State.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.2|338.1.a.2.]] A Legally Timed Card would be a Card with Reaction or a card that will have Reaction when played under appropriate circumstances.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.6|338.1.a.6.]] Whether a Card is legally timed is evaluated during the “Check Legality” step of Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 405.2|405.2.]] Ensure that the Ability’s effect would not create an illegal state. If it would, resolve in the same way you would resolve a Card that creates an illegal state. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 801|801.]] A Keyword is a speciﬁc term that appears on Cards that acts as a shorthand for a speciﬁc game effect, or ability of any variety.
- [[##rule 821.1.c|821.1.c.]] Weaponmaster is functionally short for: “When you play me, you may choose a Card you control with the Equipment tag. Necessary portions of its Rules Text are no longer Inactive if they are currently Inactive. Pay the cost of its Equip ability, reduced by [A], to attach it to this unit.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.

####  card outside of the board

**Card Outside Of The Board**

- [[##rule 366|366.]] Presence on Card outside of the Board

####  cards outside of the board

**Cards Outside Of The Board**

- [[##rule 385|385.]] Presence on Cards outside of the Board

####  cards, rune abilities, legend abilities

**Cards, Rune Abilities, Legend Abilities**

- [[##rule 806.1.a|806.1.a.]] It can be present on Cards, Rune Abilities, Legend Abilities or Permanent Abilities.
- [[##rule 813.1.a|813.1.a.]] It can be present on Cards, Rune Abilities, Legend Abilities and Permanent Abilities.

####  category

**Category**

- [[##rule 133|133.]] Category
- [[##rule 133.1|133.1.]] A card can have one or more Categories and Sub-Categories based on the properties of its front and back sides.
- [[##rule 133.2|133.2.]] These Categories and Sub-Categories dictate the behaviors of the card during play.
- [[##rule 133.7|133.7.]] Supertypes are Categories that may apply to game objects of multiple types. They are listed before a card’s type.
- [[##rule 133.8|133.8.]] Tags are Categories that may apply to game objects of multiple types. They are listed after a card’s type.

####  chain

**Chain**

- [[##rule 108.1|108.1.]] The Chain
- [[##rule 108.1.a|108.1.a.]] Cards and abilities are placed here as part of the process of being played. See rule 327. Chains for more information.
- [[##rule 108.1.b|108.1.b.]] Cards and abilities on the Chain are Public Information.
- [[##rule 187.6.a|187.6.a.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Controlled, its Controller controls its Abilities. That player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, and makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed.
- [[##rule 187.6.b|187.6.b.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Uncontrolled, its Abilities are also Uncontrolled. The Turn Player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed, and is treated as their Controller if any game rule or effect requires one. Example: The Arena’s Greatest is a battleﬁeld that reads “At the start of each player's ﬁrst Beginning Phase, that player gains 1 point.” This ability will usually trigger while the battleﬁeld has no controller. If it does, the Turn Player goes through the steps of adding the ability to the chain and receives priority after doing so, exactly as if they controlled the ability.
- [[##rule 305|305.]] When there are no items on the Chain and the Turn Player cannot or chooses not to perform any Discretionary Actions, the current phase or step of the turn ends and the next phase, step, or turn begins.
- [[##rule 309.1|309.1.]] If a Chain exists, the turn is in a Closed State.
- [[##rule 309.2|309.2.]] If no Chain exists, the turn is in an Open State.
- [[##rule 310.1|310.1.]] Neutral Open: There is no Showdown or Combat in progress and no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.2|310.2.]] Neutral Closed: There is no Showdown or Combat in progress and a Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.3|310.3.]] Showdown Open: A Showdown or Combat is in progress and no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.4|310.4.]] Showdown Closed: A Showdown or Combat is in progress and a Chain exists.
- [[##rule 312.2.c|312.2.c.]] When the turn is in a Closed State and they control the next item on the Chain.
- [[##rule 319.3|319.3.]] After a Pending Item is added to the Chain
- [[##rule 319.4|319.4.]] After a Pending Item becomes a Legal Item on the Chain
- [[##rule 319.5|319.5.]] After a Chain Item is removed from the Chain for any reason
- [[##rule 320|320.]] While a Cleanup is occurring, Chain Items cannot be Resolved.
- [[##rule 321|321.]] Similarly, while Chain Items are Resolving, a Cleanup cannot occur.
- [[##rule 321.1|321.1.]] If an event occurs during the Resolution of a Chain Item that qualiﬁes for a Cleanup, that Cleanup will be made an Outstanding Task.
- [[##rule 326.1|326.1.]] During a Chain
- [[##rule 328|328.]] The Chain is a Non-Board Zone that temporarily exists whenever a card is played or an ability is activated.
- [[##rule 329|329.]] Cards and abilities added to the chain are added as Pending Chain Items that become Finalized Chain Items.
- [[##rule 329.2|329.2.]] Chain Items are Pending until the “Check Legality” step of playing a card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 329.3|329.3.]] When a Pending Chain Item is no longer Pending it is ﬁnalized and becomes a Finalized Chain Item.
- [[##rule 330|330.]] The Chain exists as long as a Chain Item is on it.
- [[##rule 330.1|330.1.]] Only one Chain can exist at a time.
- [[##rule 330.2|330.2.]] If a card would begin to be played while a Chain already exists, it is placed on the existing Chain.
- [[##rule 331|331.]] The State of the Turn is partially determined by whether or not the Chain currently exists.
- [[##rule 331.1|331.1.]] The turn is said to be in a Closed State if a Chain exists.
- [[##rule 331.2|331.2.]] The turn is said to be in an Open State if no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 333|333.]] Whenever a card or token is played or an ability is activated or triggered, a Chain is created.
- [[##rule 335.1|335.1.]] In the course of Handling Outstanding Tasks, Chain Items may be added to the Chain. They will remain there until the Tasks are complete.
- [[##rule 335.2|335.2.]] When all Outstanding Tasks are completed, all pending Chain Items will subsequently be processed by the FEPR process.
- [[##rule 335.3|335.3.]] If there are no Outstanding Tasks, no pending Chain Items, and it is the Main Phase, the Turn Player receives priority. If there are no Outstanding Tasks, no pending items, and it is any other phase of the turn, proceed to the next substep, step, phase, or turn.
- [[##rule 336|336.]] When there are no outstanding Tasks and there are pending Chain Items on the Chain, players should refer to the FEPR process to proceed.
- [[##rule 336.1|336.1.]] In the sequence of resolving FEPR more Chain Items may become Pending Chain Items. These will be processed by the same FEPR process that produced them.
- [[##rule 337.1|337.1.]] If one or more Items are Pending, their controllers must complete the steps of Playing those Pending Items until they are Finalized Items or leave the Chain.
- [[##rule 337.1.b|337.1.b.]] Each Item is Finalized in the order it was appended to the Chain.
- [[##rule 337.1.c.1|337.1.c.1.]] If the Chain is empty, play proceeds in an Open State.
- [[##rule 337.1.c.2|337.1.c.2.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are one or more Pending Items, repeat Step 1.
- [[##rule 337.1.c.3|337.1.c.3.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are no Pending Items, the controller of the newest item on the chain gains Priority and becomes the Active Player. Proceed to Step 2: Execute.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.5|338.1.a.5.]] This can be an additional card to the item that Started the Chain in the case of the ﬁrst player with Priority after creating the Chain.
- [[##rule 339.1|339.1.]] If all players have passed Priority without adding any items to the Chain, proceed to Step 4: Resolve.
- [[##rule 340.1|340.1.]] The newest item on the Chain resolves. Execute its game effects in their entirety. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information on resolving spells.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information on resolving abilities.
- [[##rule 340.2|340.2.]] If the Chain is empty, play proceeds in an Open State.
- [[##rule 340.3|340.3.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are one or more Pending Items, return to Step 1: Finalize.
- [[##rule 340.4|340.4.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are no Pending Items, the controller of the newest item on the chain gains Priority. Return to Step 2: Execute.
- [[##rule 342.1|342.1.]] Each spell played this way creates a Chain as normal.
- [[##rule 347.1.a|347.1.a.]] The card will start a Chain as normal.
- [[##rule 354|354.]] 1. Remove the card from the zone you are playing it from and put it onto the Chain.
- [[##rule 359.2|359.2.]] A Permanent leaves the Chain and becomes a Game Object.
- [[##rule 359.3|359.3.]] A Spell lingers on the Chain.
- [[##rule 359.3.a|359.3.a.]] This card becomes a Finalized Chain Item.
- [[##rule 359.3.b|359.3.b.]] If there are other Pending Items on the Chain, then the controller of those Pending Items completes Steps 2 through 5 of Playing Cards for those items before continuing.  See rule 327. Chains for more information.
- [[##rule 359.3.c|359.3.c.]] Other players have an opportunity to play Reactions before the resolution of spells.  See rule 327. Chains for more information.
- [[##rule 377.3.b|377.3.b.]] Proceed with executing the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3|383.3.]] When a Condition is met, a Triggered Ability behaves like an Activated Ability and is placed on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.b.1|383.3.b.1.]] The cost must be paid in order to ﬁnalize the Triggered Ability to the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.c|383.3.c.]] Triggered Abilities can be put on the Chain during Closed States or Open States on any player's turn.
- [[##rule 383.3.d|383.3.d.]] If more than one Triggered Ability is Triggered simultaneously, then the player that controls the Abilities selects the order to place them on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.d.1|383.3.d.1.]] If multiple players separately control Triggered Abilities that are Triggered simultaneously, then starting with the Turn Player and proceeding in Turn Order, each player orders their Triggered Abilities on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.e|383.3.e.]] If a triggered ability has a conditional statement following the Condition, that conditional statement must be true in order for the trigger to be placed on the Chain. Example: Sona, Harmonious reads “At the end of your turn, if I'm at a battleﬁeld, ready up to 4 friendly runes.” Her Trigger Ability’s Condition will be fulﬁlled in the Ending Step, but the Triggered Ability will only be placed on the chain if she is located at a battleﬁeld when the Condition is fulﬁlled.
- [[##rule 383.4.a.2|383.4.a.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Permanent these effects correspond to is ﬁnalized and enters the board.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.2|383.4.b.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after a spell or ability that targets an appropriate Game Object is Finalized.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.a|383.4.c.2.a.]] The Conquer Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit(s) these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from Conquering.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.b|383.4.c.2.b.]] The Conquer Abilities of anything that s the player Conquering is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Conquer and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.a|383.4.d.2.a.]] The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.b|383.4.d.2.b.]] The Hold Abilities of anything that s the player Holding is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Hold and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2|383.4.e.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Attacker designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2|383.4.f.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Defender designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 387|387.]] Reflexive Triggers are a type of Triggered Ability that create one or more Chain Items when their condition is met.
- [[##rule 400.1|400.1.]] When an Ability ﬁnishes the steps of playing it becomes a Chain Item just like a Spell.
- [[##rule 400.2|400.2.]] When an Ability with the [Add] action is ﬁnalized it resolves immediately instead of becoming a Chain Item, like a Unit or Gear.
- [[##rule 402.3|402.3.]] If there are not enough options to make legal choices for a Triggered Ability that has been put on the chain, remove it from the Chain now. It ceases to be a Pending Item but never becomes a Chain Item.
- [[##rule 404.2|404.2.]] At this stage, players may decline to pay for Triggered Abilities that have incurred a cost. If they do, the ability will cease being a Pending Item and be removed from the Chain. It never becomes a Chain Item.
- [[##rule 406.2|406.2.]] This Ability becomes a Chain Item.
- [[##rule 406.4|406.4.]] Other players have an opportunity to play Reactions before the resolution of spells.  See rule 327. Chains for more information.
- [[##rule 406.5|406.5.]] Otherwise, execute the Ability just like a Spell, then clear the Chain Item from the Chain.
- [[##rule 441.3.c|441.3.c.]] Moving does not use the Chain, nor is it able to be Reacted to.
- [[##rule 455|455.]] A Combat occurs when a Cleanup occurs, there are no items on the Chain, there is a staged Combat at a Battleﬁeld, and no Showdown or Combat is ongoing at any other Battleﬁeld. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 459.2.f|459.2.f.]] Players proceed with any play on the Chain as normal.
- [[##rule 652.5.c.1|652.5.c.1.]] If the removed player had Priority during a Chain, the next Player in order receives Priority.
- [[##rule 652.5.c.2|652.5.c.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have passed Priority, then the most recent spell or ability on the Chain will resolve with Priority being re-established as appropriate for the state after the resolution of that spell or ability.

####  chains and showdowns

**Chains And Showdowns**

- [[##rule 325|325.]] Chains and Showdowns

####  champion legend

**Champion Legend**

- [[##rule 103|103.]] To play Riftbound, a player must have two Decks, a Champion Legend, and a number of Battleﬁelds determined by the Mode of Play.
- [[##rule 103.1|103.1.]] 1 Champion Legend
- [[##rule 103.1.b.2|103.1.b.2.]] Your deck’s Domain Identity is dictated by the domains of your Champion Legend. In the default card frame, these domains appear as symbols in the legend’s upper left corner.
- [[##rule 103.2.a.2|103.2.a.2.]] Must be a champion unit with a champion tag that matches the tag on your Champion Legend. Example: Loose Cannon has the tag Jinx. Therefore, a player could choose Jinx, Rebel or Jinx, Demolitionist as their Chosen Champion, because they also have the tag Jinx. Example: Tibbers has the tag Annie, but it is a signature unit, not a champion unit. It cannot be your Chosen Champion, even if your Champion Legend has the tag Annie.
- [[##rule 103.2.d|103.2.d.]] Your deck may only contain 3 total Signature cards that have the same Champion tag as your Champion Legend.
- [[##rule 103.2.d.2|103.2.d.2.]] All of the Signature cards must have the Champion tag that corresponds to the Champion Legend of the deck.
- [[##rule 103.3.a.1|103.3.a.1.]] Cards in this deck must be of the Domain Identity of your Champion Legend.
- [[##rule 107.4.a|107.4.a.]] The space for each player's Champion Legend.
- [[##rule 107.4.c|107.4.c.]] The Champion Legend here is a Game Object. See rule 120. Game Objects for more information.
- [[##rule 107.4.d|107.4.d.]] The Champion Legend cannot be removed, moved, or displaced from this zone.
- [[##rule 112|112.]] Each player separates their Champion Legend and places it in the Legend Zone.
- [[##rule 127.1|127.1.]] For gameplay purposes, a card's Owner is the player who brought it into the game, either as their Champion Legend, one of their Battleﬁelds, or part of their Main Deck or Rune Deck. The legal owner of a card doesn't matter during gameplay.  Example: Bo didn't bring a deck, so Alice loans him a deck. During the game, Bo is considered the owner of those cards, even though legally they belong to Alice.
- [[##rule 129.2|129.2.]] There is a unique pattern of back side for each of the three categories of card: Main Deck cards, Rune Deck cards, and Battleﬁelds and Champion Legends.
- [[##rule 484.8.g|484.8.g.]] Teammates may not utilize the same Champion Legend.

####  champion tags

**Champion Tags**

- [[##rule 133.8.b|133.8.b.]] Tags used to link Legends, Champion Units, and Signature cards are known as Champion Tags.
- [[##rule 705.1|705.1.]] Champions do not retain Buffs in the Champion Zone, even if they return there somehow.

####  champion unit

**Champion Unit**

- [[##rule 103.2.a.3|103.2.a.3.]] A player’s Chosen Champion is both the speciﬁc card chosen for this slot during Deck Building and also any Champion Unit with the same name as the speciﬁc card selected for this speciﬁc slot during the course of play.  Example: A player chose Jinx, Rebel as their Chosen Champion. One copy of Jinx, Rebel starts the game in their Chosen Champion zone. Any additional copies of Jinx, Rebel in their Main Deck, their hand, their trash, or on the board also count as their Chosen Champion for any game rules and effects that care about Chosen Champion status during the game.
- [[##rule 133.8.b|133.8.b.]] Tags used to link Legends, Champion Units, and Signature cards are known as Champion Tags.

####  champion zone

**Champion Zone**

- [[##rule 103.2.a.1|103.2.a.1.]] This will be placed in the Champion Zone at the start of the game.
- [[##rule 103.2.d.3|103.2.d.3.]] Signature cards are not Champion units and cannot be placed in the Champion Zone.
- [[##rule 108.3|108.3.]] Champion Zones
- [[##rule 108.3.a|108.3.a.]] Each player has their own Champion Zone.
- [[##rule 108.3.e|108.3.e.]] Cards in a player’s Champion Zone are Public Information.
- [[##rule 113|113.]] Each player separates their Chosen Champion and places it in the Champion Zone.
- [[##rule 133.4|133.4.]] Main Deck Cards begin the game in the Main Deck or (in the case of a Chosen Champion) the Champion Zone.
- [[##rule 133.7.a|133.7.a.]] Champion is a supertype that applies exclusively to units. It impacts the rules for deckbuilding. See rule 103.2.a. Chosen Champion for more information.

####  channel phase

**Channel Phase**

- [[##rule 480.7|480.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going second channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 481.7|481.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going second channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 482.7|482.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 483.7|483.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 484.7|484.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.

####  channeled

**Channeled**

- [[##rule 133.5.a.1|133.5.a.1.]] A sub-category encompassing cards with the rune type. These are channeled rather than played. They remain on the board after being channeled, but they are not permanents, as they are not Main Deck cards.
- [[##rule 315.3.b|315.3.b.]] 1. The Turn Player channels 2 runes from their Rune Deck.  See rule 430. Channel for more information.
- [[##rule 430|430.]] Channel
- [[##rule 430.1|430.1.]] Channeling is the action of taking one or more Runes from the top of a player's Rune Deck and putting them on the board.
- [[##rule 430.3|430.3.]] Channeling is a Limited Action.

####  chaos

**Chaos**

- [[##rule 134.2.e|134.2.e.]] Chaos is associated with the color purple and represented by a hexagonal symbol with swirls emanating from its center. Its shorthand is [P].

####  choice

**Choice**

- [[##rule 355.5.a|355.5.a.]] This does not include cards that affect one or more Game Objects based on criteria.  Example: "Stun a unit at a battleﬁeld" is a Choice.  Example: "Kill all gear" is not a Choice.

####  chooses

**Chooses**

- [[##rule 355.7|355.7.]] When a card Chooses one or more speciﬁc Game Objects to affect, it is Targeted unless indicated otherwise by the rules in this section.

####  chosen

**Chosen**

- [[##rule 355.14.d|355.14.d.]] Each Target is valid, and contributes to Chosen triggers individually.

####  chosen champion

**Chosen Champion**

- [[##rule 103.2.a|103.2.a.]] Chosen Champion
- [[##rule 103.2.a.2|103.2.a.2.]] Must be a champion unit with a champion tag that matches the tag on your Champion Legend. Example: Loose Cannon has the tag Jinx. Therefore, a player could choose Jinx, Rebel or Jinx, Demolitionist as their Chosen Champion, because they also have the tag Jinx. Example: Tibbers has the tag Annie, but it is a signature unit, not a champion unit. It cannot be your Chosen Champion, even if your Champion Legend has the tag Annie.
- [[##rule 103.2.a.3|103.2.a.3.]] A player’s Chosen Champion is both the speciﬁc card chosen for this slot during Deck Building and also any Champion Unit with the same name as the speciﬁc card selected for this speciﬁc slot during the course of play.  Example: A player chose Jinx, Rebel as their Chosen Champion. One copy of Jinx, Rebel starts the game in their Chosen Champion zone. Any additional copies of Jinx, Rebel in their Main Deck, their hand, their trash, or on the board also count as their Chosen Champion for any game rules and effects that care about Chosen Champion status during the game.
- [[##rule 103.2.b.1|103.2.b.1.]] This includes your Chosen Champion. Example: A deck could include Volibear, Furious as its Chosen Champion and still include 2 more copies of Volibear, Furious.
- [[##rule 108.3.b|108.3.b.]] The space each player puts their Chosen Champion at the start of the game.
- [[##rule 108.3.c|108.3.c.]] The Chosen Champion cannot be returned to this zone by normal means.
- [[##rule 108.3.c.1|108.3.c.1.]] If a Chosen Champion is instructed to be returned to this zone, it can only do so if there is not a card already in this zone.
- [[##rule 108.3.d|108.3.d.]] The Chosen Champion can be played from here as normal, following the rules of Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 113|113.]] Each player separates their Chosen Champion and places it in the Champion Zone.
- [[##rule 133.4|133.4.]] Main Deck Cards begin the game in the Main Deck or (in the case of a Chosen Champion) the Champion Zone.
- [[##rule 133.7.a|133.7.a.]] Champion is a supertype that applies exclusively to units. It impacts the rules for deckbuilding. See rule 103.2.a. Chosen Champion for more information.

####  cleanup

**Cleanup**

- [[##rule 107.3.d|107.3.d.]] If a player loses Control of a Battleﬁeld, any cards in the Facedown Zone associated with that Battleﬁeld are removed during the next Cleanup. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information. See rule 421. Hide for more information.
- [[##rule 149.3|149.3.]] If an unattached Gear is at a Battleﬁeld for any reason during a cleanup, then it is recalled to its controller's Base as a corrective action.  See rule 449. Recalls for more information. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 317.2.a|317.2.a.]] Invoke an Ending Special Cleanup.  See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 318|318.]] Cleanups
- [[##rule 319|319.]] A Cleanup will be made an Outstanding Task at the following times:
- [[##rule 320|320.]] While a Cleanup is occurring, Chain Items cannot be Resolved.
- [[##rule 321|321.]] Similarly, while Chain Items are Resolving, a Cleanup cannot occur.
- [[##rule 321.1|321.1.]] If an event occurs during the Resolution of a Chain Item that qualiﬁes for a Cleanup, that Cleanup will be made an Outstanding Task.
- [[##rule 322|322.]] If an event occurs during a Cleanup that qualiﬁes for a Cleanup, another Cleanup will occur immediately after the ﬁrst completes, repeating until a Cleanup occurs with no new change in the game’s state.
- [[##rule 322.1|322.1.]] These new Cleanups are themselves Outstanding Tasks.
- [[##rule 323|323.]] When a Cleanup occurs, the following Tasks become Outstanding in the order described:
- [[##rule 324|324.]] Special Cleanups are Cleanup steps invoked at speciﬁc times that have additional steps not present in a normal Cleanup.
- [[##rule 324.1|324.1.]] When a Special Cleanup is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a Combat Cleanup is invoked, the Combat section deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 461. The Resolution Step for more information. Example: When an End of Turn Cleanup is invoked, the End of Turn Phase subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 317. The Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 324.2|324.2.]] If events during a Special Cleanup require another Cleanup, a normal Cleanup is invoked, not another iteration of the Special Cleanup.
- [[##rule 334.1|334.1.]] Tasks include, but are not limited to: Cleanups, the actions performed during the Start of Turn Process, throughout Combat in its various steps, and the actions performed during the End of Turn  Process. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information on Cleanups See rule 315. Start of Turn for more information on the Start of Turn process See rule 454. Combat for more information on the steps of Combat See rule 317. Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 344.2|344.2.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the Battleﬁeld in question is uncontrolled when it becomes Contested, a Showdown is opened during the Cleanup at the end of the action that caused the Battleﬁeld to become Contested.
- [[##rule 347.3.a.1|347.3.a.1.]] Perform a Cleanup.
- [[##rule 428.4|428.4.]] Killing can also be the result of resolving a Cleanup.
- [[##rule 428.5.c|428.5.c.]] When one or more Units is killed due to a Cleanup, that kill action is attributed to the spell or ability that resolved immediately prior to that Cleanup that dealt damage to the Unit or Units. The player responsible for the deal action is responsible for the kill action.
- [[##rule 435.4.a|435.4.a.]] If the Detached card was a Gear and this causes it to become present at a Battleﬁeld, it will be Recalled during the next Cleanup.
- [[##rule 448|448.]] When a Move action is complete, perform a Cleanup.
- [[##rule 452.1|452.1.]] When an un-attached Gear is created or played at a battleﬁeld, or is at a battleﬁeld for any other reason, it is Recalled to its controller's base during the next Cleanup.  Example: An Equipment is attached to a unit at a battleﬁeld, so the Equipment is present at that battleﬁeld. If the unit dies, the Equipment will be recalled during the next cleanup.
- [[##rule 455|455.]] A Combat occurs when a Cleanup occurs, there are no items on the Chain, there is a staged Combat at a Battleﬁeld, and no Showdown or Combat is ongoing at any other Battleﬁeld. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 459.1|459.1.]] Combat will open in one of two ways: when a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown; or when the turn is in a Showdown Open State and a Combat is staged at the Battleﬁeld where the current Showdown is ongoing. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.3.a|459.2.b.3.a.]] If a Unit controlled by the Attacker becomes present at this Battleﬁeld after this moment, it will gain the Attacker designation during the Cleanup phase following the action that caused it to become present
- [[##rule 459.2.b.4.a|459.2.b.4.a.]] If a Unit controlled by the Defender becomes present at this Battleﬁeld after this moment it will gain the Defender designation during the Cleanup phase following the action that caused it to become present
- [[##rule 652.5.b.2|652.5.b.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have Passed their Focus, the Showdown ends and play proceeds as necessary, E.G. Combat is resolved or a Cleanup is completed.
- [[##rule 808.1.d.2|808.1.d.2.]] The trigger will be added to the chain as a Pending Item before the card with Deathknell is moved to the trash due to a Kill instruction or a Cleanup.

####  closed state

**Closed State**

- [[##rule 144.1.b|144.1.b.]] This action cannot be performed during a Closed State.
