- [[##rule 309|309.]] At any given time, the turn is in either an Open State or a Closed State.
- [[##rule 309.1|309.1.]] If a Chain exists, the turn is in a Closed State.
- [[##rule 309.1.a|309.1.a.]] Only cards and abilities with the Reaction keyword can be played or activated in a Closed State.
- [[##rule 312.2.c|312.2.c.]] When the turn is in a Closed State and they control the next item on the Chain.
- [[##rule 312.2.d|312.2.d.]] When the turn is in a Closed State, they are the next Player in Turn Order, and the player with Priority passes.
- [[##rule 319.1|319.1.]] After the game transitions to or from an Open or Closed state
- [[##rule 331.1|331.1.]] The turn is said to be in a Closed State if a Chain exists.
- [[##rule 331.1.a|331.1.a.]] Cards of all Categories, by default, cannot be played during a Closed State.
- [[##rule 331.1.b|331.1.b.]] Card abilities, by default, cannot be played during a Closed State.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.1|338.1.a.1.]] Cards, by default, cannot be played during a Closed State.
- [[##rule 377.3.a.1|377.3.a.1.]] The ability goes on the chain but has no card to represent it, so players need to take note that it is now a Closed State.
- [[##rule 383.3.c|383.3.c.]] Triggered Abilities can be put on the Chain during Closed States or Open States on any player's turn.
- [[##rule 401.1|401.1.]] Add a Pending Item to the chain representing the Ability that is either being Activated or Triggered. Notably, although this Chain Item will not have a card representing it, this will create a Closed State.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 813.1.c.1|813.1.c.1.]] On Cards: "This can be played during Closed States on any player's turn."
- [[##rule 813.1.c.2|813.1.c.2.]] On Rune, Legend, or Permanent Abilities: "This can be activated during Closed States on any player's turn."
- [[##rule 813.2|813.2.]] The corresponding card or effect with this keyword is not restricted to Closed States or Showdowns. This permission is inclusive of all other timings and options available to the ability as written, Action's permissions, or by default.

####  closes the state

**Closes The State**

- [[##rule 354.1|354.1.]] This Closes the State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.

####  colored highlight

**Colored Highlight**

- [[##rule 801.2|801.2.]] Keywords can be identiﬁed by having a colored highlight behind them.

####  combat

**Combat**

- [[##rule 143.2|143.2.]] Might: The combat statistic of a Unit. Used to determine a Unit's contribution to Combat, as well as when it is Killed by damaging effects.
- [[##rule 144.1.c|144.1.c.]] This action cannot be performed during a Showdown or Combat.
- [[##rule 144.4.a.1|144.4.a.1.]] Units cannot Move to a Battleﬁeld that already has units from 2 other players present, or where a Combat is ongoing that has 2 other players as participants.
- [[##rule 187.3.c|187.3.c.]] The state of a Battleﬁeld being Contested is used to determine when Combat should occur, when a Non-Combat Showdown should occur, and when Control will change.
- [[##rule 187.4.a|187.4.a.]] If a player controls Units at a Battleﬁeld, outside of Combat, they maintain Control of that Battleﬁeld for as long as they have Units at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 187.4.b|187.4.b.]] While a Combat or Showdown is ongoing at a Battleﬁeld, Control of that Battleﬁeld cannot change until instructed by steps of the Combat or Showdown.
- [[##rule 187.4.c|187.4.c.]] If a player has no Units at a Battleﬁeld and the turn is in an Open state, they lose Control of that Battleﬁeld in the following cleanup, unless there is a Combat or Showdown ongoing there.
- [[##rule 308.1|308.1.]] If a Showdown or Combat is in progress, the turn is in a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 308.2|308.2.]] If no Showdown or Combat is in progress, the turn is in a Neutral State.
- [[##rule 310.1|310.1.]] Neutral Open: There is no Showdown or Combat in progress and no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.2|310.2.]] Neutral Closed: There is no Showdown or Combat in progress and a Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.3|310.3.]] Showdown Open: A Showdown or Combat is in progress and no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.4|310.4.]] Showdown Closed: A Showdown or Combat is in progress and a Chain exists.
- [[##rule 316.4|316.4.]] Combat
- [[##rule 316.4.a|316.4.a.]] A Combat occurs as a result of Units controlled by opposing players being present at the same Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 316.4.c|316.4.c.]] The source effect does not change the structure or flow of Combat once initiated.
- [[##rule 316.4.d|316.4.d.]] A Combat can only occur between two players.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 316.5.a|316.5.a.]] A Showdown occurs when a Combat occurs.
- [[##rule 316.5.a.1|316.5.a.1.]] Showdowns that occur as a result of Combat are a Sub-Phase of Combat.
- [[##rule 316.5.b.1|316.5.b.1.]] Showdowns that occur as a result of a player moving to an empty Battleﬁeld are a stand-alone Phase and do not create a Combat.
- [[##rule 323.2|323.2.]] 2. Assign or Remove the Attacker or Defender designation from Units as needed if there is a Combat in progress
- [[##rule 323.2.a|323.2.a.]] If there are Units present at the Battleﬁeld the Combat is taking place at, but do not have a designation, they gain the same designation as their Controller now
- [[##rule 323.2.b|323.2.b.]] If there are Units present at the Battleﬁeld the Combat is taking place at, but have the opposite designation of their controller, they lose that designation, and gain the same designation as their controller now
- [[##rule 323.2.c|323.2.c.]] If there are Units at locations other than the Battleﬁeld that the Combat is taking place at, but have either Attacker or Defender designations, they lose those designations now
- [[##rule 323.6|323.6.]] 4. If the turn is in an Open State, Battleﬁelds with no Units occupying them and no Showdown or Combat ongoing become Uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 323.9|323.9.]] 7. Mark a Combat as Staged at each Battleﬁeld that Contested was applied to that have Units present controlled by opposing players.
- [[##rule 323.9.a|323.9.a.]] The Combat remains Staged at that Battleﬁeld as long as there are Units present from two opposing players there.
- [[##rule 323.10|323.10.]] 7a. If Units of two opposing players are no longer present at a Battleﬁeld that has a Combat Staged before it has opened, the Combat will cease being Staged
- [[##rule 323.12|323.12.]] 8a. If a Showdown and Combat are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player chooses to initiate the Showdown there, the Showdown will open as a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 323.13|323.13.]] 9. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and Combat is Staged at one or more Battleﬁelds, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. Combat begins there.
- [[##rule 323.14|323.14.]] 9a. If the current state is Showdown Open State and Combat is Staged at a Battleﬁeld where there is a Non-Combat Showdown ongoing, that Showdown becomes a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 324.1|324.1.]] When a Special Cleanup is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a Combat Cleanup is invoked, the Combat section deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 461. The Resolution Step for more information. Example: When an End of Turn Cleanup is invoked, the End of Turn Phase subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 317. The Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 334.1|334.1.]] Tasks include, but are not limited to: Cleanups, the actions performed during the Start of Turn Process, throughout Combat in its various steps, and the actions performed during the End of Turn  Process. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information on Cleanups See rule 315. Start of Turn for more information on the Start of Turn process See rule 454. Combat for more information on the steps of Combat See rule 317. Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 343|343.]] The State of the turn is partially determined by whether or not a Showdown or Combat is in progress.
- [[##rule 343.1|343.1.]] The turn is said to be in a Showdown State if a Showdown or Combat is in progress.
- [[##rule 343.2|343.2.]] The turn is said to be in a Neutral State if no Showdown or Combat is in progress.
- [[##rule 344.1|344.1.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested between two players, then a Showdown will be opened as the ﬁrst step of Combat.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 348.1|348.1.]] If it is a Combat Showdown, proceed with the remaining steps of Combat to resolve the phase.  See rule 458. The Steps of Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2|383.4.e.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Attacker designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2|383.4.f.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Defender designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 417.3.a|417.3.a.]] Assigning Damage causes Damage to be dealt outside of being directed to Deal Damage.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 417.6.c|417.6.c.]] Damage Dealt as a result of being assigned during Combat has the Units as its source.
- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 442.2.c|442.2.c.]] If an action would require a Move that would cause a Unit to become present in a Location where it cannot move for any reason, such as a Battleﬁeld with two players that are not the controller of the Unit performing this Move action are in a Combat or such a Combat is Staged, it instead Recalls. See rule 449. Recalls for more information.
- [[##rule 446|446.]] Units may cause a Showdown without a Combat when they Move.
- [[##rule 447|447.]] Units may cause Combat when they Move.
- [[##rule 447.1|447.1.]] A Combat is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested and Units controlled by opposing players, or when a Move causes Units controlled by opposing players to become present in the same Battleﬁeld where a Showdown is ongoing. See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 454|454.]] Combat
- [[##rule 455|455.]] A Combat occurs when a Cleanup occurs, there are no items on the Chain, there is a staged Combat at a Battleﬁeld, and no Showdown or Combat is ongoing at any other Battleﬁeld. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 455.1|455.1.]] If there is an ongoing Showdown at the Battleﬁeld where the Combat is staged, that Showdown will become a Combat Showdown and a Combat will be initiated there.
- [[##rule 456|456.]] Combat is considered Staged if there are units controlled by two opposing players at a Battleﬁeld but the Steps of Combat have not been initiated.
- [[##rule 456.1|456.1.]] If more than one Battleﬁeld has Units controlled by opposing players at it at the same time, the Turn Player decides which Combat to resolve ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 456.3|456.3.]] If a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown, it will open as a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 457|457.]] Combat can only occur between Units controlled by exactly two players.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.
- [[##rule 457.2|457.2.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid to be chosen as a location to play one or more Units by a player not involved in that Combat by any means,
- [[##rule 457.3|457.3.]] All choices that would result in a Combat occurring between more than two players simultaneously are invalid and ineligible to be completed.
- [[##rule 459.1|459.1.]] Combat will open in one of two ways: when a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown; or when the turn is in a Showdown Open State and a Combat is staged at the Battleﬁeld where the current Showdown is ongoing. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 459.2.d|459.2.d.]] 3. Add items to the Combat Chain if establishing Attacker and Defender has caused Triggered Abilities to become Pending.
- [[##rule 459.2.e|459.2.e.]] The State Closes if a Combat Chain was created.
- [[##rule 461.3.d.1|461.3.d.1.]] If “No Result” was reached, and both players have units remaining, stage a Combat at this battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 652.5.b.2|652.5.b.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have Passed their Focus, the Showdown ends and play proceeds as necessary, E.G. Combat is resolved or a Cleanup is completed.
- [[##rule 807.1.d|807.1.d.]] Being an attacker means the Unit has gained the Attacker designation during Combat.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 814.1.d|814.1.d.]] Being a defender means the Unit has gained the Defender designation during Combat. See rule 454. Combat for more information.

####  combat cleanup

**Combat Cleanup**

- [[##rule 143.3.b.2|143.3.b.2.]] During a Combat Cleanup. See rule 461.1.for more information about Combat Cleanups.
- [[##rule 324.1|324.1.]] When a Special Cleanup is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a Combat Cleanup is invoked, the Combat section deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 461. The Resolution Step for more information. Example: When an End of Turn Cleanup is invoked, the End of Turn Phase subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 317. The Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 461.1|461.1.]] 1. Perform a Combat Cleanup.

####  combat damage step

**Combat Damage Step**

- [[##rule 143.2.b|143.2.b.]] If a unit's Might is ever less than 0, it is treated as 0 when d by spells and abilities, and when summing Might to be assigned as damage in the Combat Damage Step. See rule 460. The Combat Damage Step for more information.
- [[##rule 423.1.b|423.1.b.]] A Stunned Unit does not contribute its might to damage in the combat damage step. See rule 460. The Combat Damage Step for more information.
- [[##rule 460.2|460.2.]] 1. When the Showdown closes, Attackers and Defenders resolve Combat Damage at the Battleﬁeld that was attacked, using their current Might.

####  combat in progress

**Combat In Progress**

- [[##rule 457.2.a|457.2.a.]] If an effect would require a Unit be played to a Battleﬁeld with a Staged Combat or a Combat in Progress, where the controller of the played unit is not a participant, instead the Unit is played to its controller's Base.

####  combat showdown

**Combat Showdown**

- [[##rule 316.5.b.1.a|316.5.b.1.a.]] These Showdowns are called Non-Combat Showdowns. During the proceedings of a Non-Combat Showdown, units controlled by a different player may become present at the Battleﬁeld where the Showdown is ongoing. This will cause the Showdown to become a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 323.12|323.12.]] 8a. If a Showdown and Combat are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player chooses to initiate the Showdown there, the Showdown will open as a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 323.14|323.14.]] 9a. If the current state is Showdown Open State and Combat is Staged at a Battleﬁeld where there is a Non-Combat Showdown ongoing, that Showdown becomes a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 348.1|348.1.]] If it is a Combat Showdown, proceed with the remaining steps of Combat to resolve the phase.  See rule 458. The Steps of Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 455.1|455.1.]] If there is an ongoing Showdown at the Battleﬁeld where the Combat is staged, that Showdown will become a Combat Showdown and a Combat will be initiated there.
- [[##rule 456.3|456.3.]] If a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown, it will open as a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 459.2.e.1|459.2.e.1.]] Otherwise the Combat Showdown continues, with the State Open as normal.

####  combat special cleanup

**Combat Special Cleanup**

- [[##rule 461.1.a|461.1.a.]] Invoke a Combat Special Cleanup.

####  combat staged

**Combat Staged**

- [[##rule 323.10|323.10.]] 7a. If Units of two opposing players are no longer present at a Battleﬁeld that has a Combat Staged before it has opened, the Combat will cease being Staged

####  combats in progress

**Combats In Progress**

- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.
- [[##rule 457.2|457.2.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid to be chosen as a location to play one or more Units by a player not involved in that Combat by any means,

####  concedes

**Concedes**

- [[##rule 484.6.a.1|484.6.a.1.]] If one player Concedes, then the entire team loses.
- [[##rule 649|649.]] Conceding

####  condition

**Condition**

- [[##rule 383|383.]] Triggered Abilities are repeatable effects that happen when a Condition is met.
- [[##rule 383.2|383.2.]] Triggered Abilities have a Condition and an Effect.
- [[##rule 383.2.a|383.2.a.]] The Condition follows the When.
- [[##rule 383.2.b|383.2.b.]] The Effect is the Instruction that follows the comma after the Condition.
- [[##rule 383.2.c|383.2.c.]] The Condition of a Trigger is evaluated after a potentially inciting event has been processed.
- [[##rule 383.3|383.3.]] When a Condition is met, a Triggered Ability behaves like an Activated Ability and is placed on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.a|383.3.a.]] If a Triggered Ability says “you may” as the ﬁrst part of its Effect, the controller of its source will choose whether or not to place the Triggered Ability on the chain when its trigger Condition is fulﬁlled.
- [[##rule 383.3.e|383.3.e.]] If a triggered ability has a conditional statement following the Condition, that conditional statement must be true in order for the trigger to be placed on the Chain. Example: Sona, Harmonious reads “At the end of your turn, if I'm at a battleﬁeld, ready up to 4 friendly runes.” Her Trigger Ability’s Condition will be fulﬁlled in the Ending Step, but the Triggered Ability will only be placed on the chain if she is located at a battleﬁeld when the Condition is fulﬁlled.
- [[##rule 383.3.f.1|383.3.f.1.]] When the Condition is fulﬁlled, the player who controls the source of the Triggered Ability may choose to place it on the chain.
- [[##rule 383.4|383.4.]] Some Conditions are commonly used and structured in a way that explicitly deﬁnes their use and other properties of the Effect that is associated with it.
- [[##rule 383.4.a|383.4.a.]] Play Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that the Permanent that has the Play Effect being played to the board.
- [[##rule 383.4.b|383.4.b.]] Targeting Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that a Game Object becomes targeted.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.3|383.4.b.3.]] Although these abilities say “choose” in their Condition, they trigger speciﬁcally when an appropriate Game Object is Targeted. See rule 355.6. Targeting for more information on what counts as Targeting.
- [[##rule 383.4.c|383.4.c.]] Conquer Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit participating in, and successfully Conquering a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.b|383.4.c.2.b.]] The Conquer Abilities of anything that s the player Conquering is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Conquer and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 383.4.d|383.4.d.]] Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battleﬁeld during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.b|383.4.d.2.b.]] The Hold Abilities of anything that s the player Holding is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Hold and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 384.2|384.2.]] Triggered Abilities of Permanents are only able to have their Conditions evaluated while on the Board.
- [[##rule 387.3|387.3.]] If present, the Condition of a Reflexive Trigger will follow the same format as a Triggered Ability.
- [[##rule 727.1|727.1.]] A Dependent Keyword is comprised of both a Condition that it is short for, and an ability of some format immediately after the Keyword itself. EXAMPLE: Noxus Hopeful has “[Legion][>] I cost [2] less.” [Legion] is short for the condition “if you have played another card this turn, this card gains [Text],” while “I cost [2] less” is the dependent ability.
- [[##rule 727.1.a|727.1.a.]] A Dependent Keyword will always be functionally short for a Condition.
- [[##rule 727.1.a.1|727.1.a.1.]] This Condition may also have a determined Duration, Time, or Limitation as part of its deﬁnition. EXAMPLE: Legion speciﬁes the duration of its condition: “if you have played another card this turn.” This turn is the duration. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “Until you have spent [3] this turn” would include a limitation on its condition. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “After you’ve become an attacker this turn” would include a time after which the condition is active.
- [[##rule 727.1.b|727.1.b.]] The Dependent Ability associated with the Dependent Keyword is Inactive on the card with the Dependent Keyword until the Condition is met, when it becomes Active
- [[##rule 727.1.b.1|727.1.b.1.]] The Dependent Ability is present on the card for the sake of  or evaluation until the Condition is met See rule 720. Inactive for more information
- [[##rule 727.1.b.2|727.1.b.2.]] The Dependent Ability is Active exactly as written while the Condition is true Example: Gustwalker has “[Level3][>] I have +1 [M] and Ganking.” As long as its controller has 3 XP, Gustwalker’s Ganking is active.

####  conditional passive abilities

**Conditional Passive Abilities**

- [[##rule 364.3.a|364.3.a.]] Conditional Passive Abilities can be recognized by the occurrence of "if" or "while" as part of the statement of the ability.  Example: "While I'm attacking or defending alone, I have +2 [M]."  Example: "If an opponent controls a battleﬁeld, I enter ready."

####  conquer abilities

**Conquer Abilities**

- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.a|383.4.c.2.a.]] The Conquer Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit(s) these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from Conquering.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.b|383.4.c.2.b.]] The Conquer Abilities of anything that s the player Conquering is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Conquer and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 466.2.a|466.2.a.]] Conquer abilities trigger at a Battleﬁeld that was Conquered.

####  conquer effects

**Conquer Effects**

- [[##rule 383.4.c|383.4.c.]] Conquer Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit participating in, and successfully Conquering a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.c|383.4.c.2.c.]] If the act of gaining one point from Conquering is negated or replaced in any way, the Conquer Effect will still trigger.

####  conquering

**Conquering**

- [[##rule 348.2.a|348.2.a.]] If only one player’s Units remain at the Battleﬁeld, and if that player does not already Control the Battleﬁeld, that player establishes Control over the Battleﬁeld. See rule 185. Control for more information on Control.  See rule 464.1.for more information on Conquering.
- [[##rule 383.4.c|383.4.c.]] Conquer Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit participating in, and successfully Conquering a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2|383.4.c.2.]] This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Conquer action, or Abilities that  the player that performed the Conquer action.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.a|383.4.c.2.a.]] The Conquer Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit(s) these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from Conquering.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.b|383.4.c.2.b.]] The Conquer Abilities of anything that s the player Conquering is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Conquer and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.c|383.4.c.2.c.]] If the act of gaining one point from Conquering is negated or replaced in any way, the Conquer Effect will still trigger.
- [[##rule 461.5.d|461.5.d.]] Establishing Control results in a Conquer if that player has not yet scored this Battleﬁeld this turn. See rule 185. Control for more information on Control.  See rule 464.1.for more information on Conquering.
- [[##rule 464.1|464.1.]] Conquer: A player gains Control of a Battleﬁeld they did not yet Score this turn.
- [[##rule 464.1.a|464.1.a.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds under the Control of a teammate during the Beginning Phase are also disqualiﬁed from being Scored through Conquer by any means.
- [[##rule 466.1.a.1|466.1.a.1.]] Notably, points Gained from sources that are not Conquer or Hold are not beholden to these restrictions.
- [[##rule 466.1.b.2|466.1.b.2.]] If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has Scored every Battleﬁeld through either method this turn, that player Gains the Winning Point. If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has not Scored every Battleﬁeld this turn, that player draws a card.
- [[##rule 466.2.a|466.2.a.]] Conquer abilities trigger at a Battleﬁeld that was Conquered.
- [[##rule 484.8.f.1|484.8.f.1.]] When scoring the Final Point from Conquer, a player must Score each Battleﬁeld in the same turn, excepting any that were occupied by their ally during that turn’s Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 823.1.b|823.1.b.]] Hunt is both a Conquer and a Hold effect.
- [[##rule 823.1.c.1|823.1.c.1.]] Hunt is functionally short for: “When I Conquer or Hold, my controller gains X XP.” See rule 728. XP for more information

####  contested

**Contested**

- [[##rule 187.3|187.3.]] Control can be Contested through the course of play.
- [[##rule 187.3.a|187.3.a.]] Contested is a temporary status applied to the battleﬁeld when a Unit controlled by a Player who does not currently Control that Battleﬁeld Moves or otherwise becomes present there.
- [[##rule 187.3.b|187.3.b.]] A Battleﬁeld remains Contested until Control is established or re-established.
- [[##rule 187.3.c|187.3.c.]] The state of a Battleﬁeld being Contested is used to determine when Combat should occur, when a Non-Combat Showdown should occur, and when Control will change.
- [[##rule 316.5.b|316.5.b.]] A Showdown is marked as Staged at a Battleﬁeld when the Contested status is applied to a Battleﬁeld with no current controller.
- [[##rule 323.8|323.8.]] 6. Mark a Showdown as Staged at each Battleﬁeld that Contested was applied to.
- [[##rule 323.8.a|323.8.a.]] The Showdown remains Staged at each Battleﬁeld that is Contested and has units present controlled by the player that applied Contested.
- [[##rule 323.9|323.9.]] 7. Mark a Combat as Staged at each Battleﬁeld that Contested was applied to that have Units present controlled by opposing players.
- [[##rule 344|344.]] A Showdown begins when Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the turn is in a Neutral Open State.
- [[##rule 344.1|344.1.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested between two players, then a Showdown will be opened as the ﬁrst step of Combat.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 344.2|344.2.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the Battleﬁeld in question is uncontrolled when it becomes Contested, a Showdown is opened during the Cleanup at the end of the action that caused the Battleﬁeld to become Contested.
- [[##rule 345|345.]] As a Showdown begins, the player who applied Contested status to the Battleﬁeld gains Focus.
- [[##rule 445|445.]] The Destination becomes Contested if it is a Battleﬁeld not controlled by the controller of the Unit or Units that moved.
- [[##rule 446.1|446.1.]] A Showdown is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested while it has no Units present from any player other than those that just moved.
- [[##rule 447.1|447.1.]] A Combat is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested and Units controlled by opposing players, or when a Move causes Units controlled by opposing players to become present in the same Battleﬁeld where a Showdown is ongoing. See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.1|459.2.b.1.]] The Attacker is the player whose unit(s) applied the Contested status to the Battleﬁeld. They gain the Attacker designation now.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.2|459.2.b.2.]] The Defender is the player who did not apply the Contested status to the Battleﬁeld. They gain the Defender designation now.
- [[##rule 461.5.e|461.5.e.]] This does not have to be the player that applied Contested to the Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 464.1.b|464.1.b.]] A player will gain control of a Battleﬁeld after establishing Control by applying Contested ﬁrst.

####  contested battleﬁeld

**Contested Battleﬁeld**

- [[##rule 459.2.b.3|459.2.b.3.]] Units at the Contested Battleﬁeld controlled by the Attacker gain the Attacker designation now.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.4|459.2.b.4.]] Units at the Contested Battleﬁeld controlled by the Defender gain the Defender designation now.

####  contested status

**Contested Status**

- [[##rule 461.5.a|461.5.a.]] Clear the Contested Status.

####  control

**Control**

- [[##rule 107.3.d|107.3.d.]] If a player loses Control of a Battleﬁeld, any cards in the Facedown Zone associated with that Battleﬁeld are removed during the next Cleanup. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information. See rule 421. Hide for more information.
- [[##rule 179|179.]] A token's controller is the controller of the spell or ability that created it, unless the token's type innately determines control or that spell or ability speciﬁes that a different player is the token's controller.
- [[##rule 185|185.]] Control
- [[##rule 186|186.]] Control is the concept of a player having influence of a Game Object and applies differently to different card types.
- [[##rule 187.1|187.1.]] Control is established over Battleﬁelds through the course of play.
- [[##rule 187.2|187.2.]] Control is a binary state for Battleﬁelds and an Identiﬁer for players.
- [[##rule 187.2.a|187.2.a.]] A Battleﬁeld is Controlled or Uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 187.3|187.3.]] Control can be Contested through the course of play.
- [[##rule 187.3.a|187.3.a.]] Contested is a temporary status applied to the battleﬁeld when a Unit controlled by a Player who does not currently Control that Battleﬁeld Moves or otherwise becomes present there.
- [[##rule 187.3.b|187.3.b.]] A Battleﬁeld remains Contested until Control is established or re-established.
- [[##rule 187.3.c|187.3.c.]] The state of a Battleﬁeld being Contested is used to determine when Combat should occur, when a Non-Combat Showdown should occur, and when Control will change.
- [[##rule 187.4|187.4.]] Control is established by having Units at a Battleﬁeld at the end of a Showdown or Combat after applying the contested status.
- [[##rule 187.4.a|187.4.a.]] If a player controls Units at a Battleﬁeld, outside of Combat, they maintain Control of that Battleﬁeld for as long as they have Units at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 187.4.b|187.4.b.]] While a Combat or Showdown is ongoing at a Battleﬁeld, Control of that Battleﬁeld cannot change until instructed by steps of the Combat or Showdown.
- [[##rule 187.4.c|187.4.c.]] If a player has no Units at a Battleﬁeld and the turn is in an Open state, they lose Control of that Battleﬁeld in the following cleanup, unless there is a Combat or Showdown ongoing there.
- [[##rule 187.5|187.5.]] Control is a constant state.
- [[##rule 187.6|187.6.]] Control of a Battleﬁeld determines Control of its Abilities.
- [[##rule 187.6.a|187.6.a.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Controlled, its Controller controls its Abilities. That player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, and makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed.
- [[##rule 187.6.b|187.6.b.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Uncontrolled, its Abilities are also Uncontrolled. The Turn Player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed, and is treated as their Controller if any game rule or effect requires one. Example: The Arena’s Greatest is a battleﬁeld that reads “At the start of each player's ﬁrst Beginning Phase, that player gains 1 point.” This ability will usually trigger while the battleﬁeld has no controller. If it does, the Turn Player goes through the steps of adding the ability to the chain and receives priority after doing so, exactly as if they controlled the ability.
- [[##rule 187.6.c|187.6.c.]] “You” in a battleﬁeld’s abilities refers to the battleﬁeld’s Controller, as does the implied “you” in instructions like “draw 1.” If the battleﬁeld has no Controller, “you” refers to no one, and all such instructions are ignored.
- [[##rule 188.1|188.1.]] When a player Plays a Card or other Game Object, they are established as that Game Object's Controller.
- [[##rule 188.2|188.2.]] For Spells, they are the Spell's Controller.
- [[##rule 188.3|188.3.]] For Permanents and Runes, when they Enter the Board, that player is assigned as that Game Object's Controller.
- [[##rule 188.4.a|188.4.a.]] By default, the Controller of an Ability’s Source is the Controller of that Ability.
- [[##rule 188.4.b|188.4.b.]] Changes to Control of an Ability’s Source do not change Control of that Ability.
- [[##rule 189|189.]] When a game effect or rules text refers to the Controller of a speciﬁc object, it can be referring to either context interchangeably.
- [[##rule 189.1|189.1.]] The method of assignment of control is different, but the status of Control is the same across all Game Objects.
- [[##rule 315.2.b.2|315.2.b.2.]] 1. The Turn Player Holds all Battleﬁelds they Control. See rule 462. Scoring for more information.
- [[##rule 323.2.a|323.2.a.]] If there are Units present at the Battleﬁeld the Combat is taking place at, but do not have a designation, they gain the same designation as their Controller now
- [[##rule 344|344.]] A Showdown begins when Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the turn is in a Neutral Open State.
- [[##rule 344.1|344.1.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested between two players, then a Showdown will be opened as the ﬁrst step of Combat.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 344.2|344.2.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the Battleﬁeld in question is uncontrolled when it becomes Contested, a Showdown is opened during the Cleanup at the end of the action that caused the Battleﬁeld to become Contested.
- [[##rule 348.2.a|348.2.a.]] If only one player’s Units remain at the Battleﬁeld, and if that player does not already Control the Battleﬁeld, that player establishes Control over the Battleﬁeld. See rule 185. Control for more information on Control.  See rule 464.1.for more information on Conquering.
- [[##rule 415.3.a|415.3.a.]] A player Readies all non-spell Game Objects they Control during the Ready Step of the Beginning Phase on their turn.
- [[##rule 439.4|439.4.]] Unless speciﬁed otherwise by the Game Effect that Creates a Game Object, any such Game Object is owned by the player who Created it. Control is established as usual for Game Objects of the appropriate type.
- [[##rule 461.5.d|461.5.d.]] Establishing Control results in a Conquer if that player has not yet scored this Battleﬁeld this turn. See rule 185. Control for more information on Control.  See rule 464.1.for more information on Conquering.
- [[##rule 464.1|464.1.]] Conquer: A player gains Control of a Battleﬁeld they did not yet Score this turn.
- [[##rule 464.1.a|464.1.a.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds under the Control of a teammate during the Beginning Phase are also disqualiﬁed from being Scored through Conquer by any means.
- [[##rule 464.1.b|464.1.b.]] A player will gain control of a Battleﬁeld after establishing Control by applying Contested ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 464.2|464.2.]] Hold: A player maintains Control of a Battleﬁeld during their Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 484.8.c|484.8.c.]] Control is not shared.
- [[##rule 718.5.e|718.5.e.]] Attached cards may have different Controllers from their Top-Most card.
- [[##rule 718.5.f|718.5.f.]] Changes in Control of the Top-Most card do not impact Control of Attached cards and vice versa.

####  controlled by a speciﬁc player

**Controlled By A Speciﬁc Player**

- [[##rule 187.2.b|187.2.b.]] A Battleﬁeld is Controlled by a speciﬁc player or Controlled by no one.

####  controlled by no one

**Controlled By No One**

- [[##rule 187.2.b|187.2.b.]] A Battleﬁeld is Controlled by a speciﬁc player or Controlled by no one.

####  cost

**Cost**

- [[##rule 131|131.]] Cost
- [[##rule 131.1|131.1.]] Main Deck cards have a Cost, listed in the upper left corner of the front face of the card. See rule 164. Rune Pools for more information.
- [[##rule 131.2.a|131.2.a.]] The numeral listed in the Cost element in the upper left corner of the card.
- [[##rule 131.3.a|131.3.a.]] The symbols, listed vertically, in the Cost element in the upper left corner of the card.
- [[##rule 144.2|144.2.]] Exhausting the Unit is the Cost for this action.
- [[##rule 144.3.c|144.3.c.]] The Costs of Exhausting the Units are also paid Simultaneously.
- [[##rule 145.1|145.1.]] Activated Abilities are Game Effects that are written as Costs followed by a ":", and then succeeded by an effect.  See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 150.1|150.1.]] Activated Abilities are Game Effects that are written as Costs followed by a ":", and then succeeded by an effect.  See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 165|165.]] The Rune Pool is a conceptual collection of a player's available Energy and Power available to pay Costs.
- [[##rule 182.2.a|182.2.a.]] Tokens do not have costs.
- [[##rule 356.6|356.6.]] Costs may be Energy costs, Power costs, or non-standard costs. Example: A card reads "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." Killing a friendly unit is an additional cost to play that card.
- [[##rule 357.2|357.2.]] In addition, pay any non-standard Cost summed in step 3 in any order.
- [[##rule 377.1|377.1.]] Activated Abilities are recognized by the presence of a ":" in the text of the card, preceded by a cost and succeeded by an effect.  Example: "[2]: Draw 1" is an activated ability. The cost is 2 energy. The effect is to draw 1 card.
- [[##rule 414.4|414.4.]] When Exhausting is listed as a Cost, then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: A spell says "As an additional cost to play this, you may exhaust a friendly unit." An exhausted friendly unit may not be exhausted again as the additional cost for the spell, and the additional cost has not been paid.
- [[##rule 416.3|416.3.]] When Recycling is listed as a Cost, the action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: Vi, Destructive has the ability "Recycle 1 from your trash: Give me +1 [M] this turn." Each time a player activates the ability, they must recycle 1 card from their trash to pay its cost. If they have no cards in their trash, they can't activate the ability, because they can't pay its cost.
- [[##rule 420.3.a|420.3.a.]] The Cost is Exhausting one or more Units.
- [[##rule 422.3|422.3.]] When Discarding is listed as a Cost, then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: A card has the ability "Discard 2: Deal 2 damage to a unit at a battleﬁeld." To activate the ability, the card's controller must have at least 2 cards in hand and must be able to discard them.
- [[##rule 820.1.d|820.1.d.]] Repeat is functionally short for “You may pay [Cost] as an additional cost as you play this spell. If you do, execute the instructions of this spell one additional time.”

####  costs within instructions

**Costs Within Instructions**

- [[##rule 742.1|742.1.]] Costs within instructions are instructions that take a particular form (“[do X] to [do Y]”). [Do X] is the cost associated with the instruction, and [do Y] is the effect.

####  countered

**Countered**

- [[##rule 419.4.b|419.4.b.]] If a game effect prevents the resolution of the card—for example, because the card was countered—the card wasn't played and no abilities that trigger on playing cards trigger.  See rule 425. Counter for more information.
- [[##rule 425|425.]] Counter
- [[##rule 425.1|425.1.]] Countering is the act of negating the execution, activation, or otherwise playing of a card or ability by a player.
- [[##rule 425.1.a|425.1.a.]] A card or ability that is Countered does nothing and is  cleared from the chain.
- [[##rule 425.1.b|425.1.b.]] A card that is Countered is not considered to have been played.
- [[##rule 425.1.c|425.1.c.]] Countering does not refund any costs paid to play a card, activate an ability, or trigger an ability.
- [[##rule 425.2.a|425.2.a.]] Players may only Counter cards and abilities when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 425.3|425.3.]] This action is formatted as "Counter [a card or ability on the chain]."
- [[##rule 652.4|652.4.]] Counter all spells and abilities of all types controlled by the player that has conceded.

####  create game objects

**Create Game Objects**

- [[##rule 439.6.a|439.6.a.]] Players may only Create Game Objects when directed to by Game Effects.

####  created

**Created**

- [[##rule 183|183.]] Tokens are Created on the board or the Chain and cannot exist elsewhere.
- [[##rule 438.7|438.7.]] Tokens that have been Created through a Replace action can be instructed to be “Swapped back.”
- [[##rule 439.2|439.2.]] Effects that Create one or more Game Objects will direct where those Game Objects must go - the Game Objects are Created directly to the zones in question.
- [[##rule 439.2.a|439.2.a.]] Prior to being Created, these Game Objects did not exist outside of the zone they were Created to. After being Created, they may change zones as appropriate for Game Objects of their type.
- [[##rule 439.2.b|439.2.b.]] If a zone is not speciﬁed by the effect, the Game Object will be created to the appropriate zone for its type. Permanents will be Created to any location on the Board that they can be played to.
- [[##rule 439.2.b.1|439.2.b.1.]] Spells will be Created to the Chain.
- [[##rule 439.2.b.3|439.2.b.3.]] Legends will be Created to the Legend Zone.
- [[##rule 439.2.b.4|439.2.b.4.]] Battleﬁelds will be Created to the Battleﬁeld Zone.
- [[##rule 439.4|439.4.]] Unless speciﬁed otherwise by the Game Effect that Creates a Game Object, any such Game Object is owned by the player who Created it. Control is established as usual for Game Objects of the appropriate type.
- [[##rule 439.4.a|439.4.a.]] A Created permanent, rune, legend, or spell is controlled by its owner as it is created.
- [[##rule 439.4.b|439.4.b.]] A Created battleﬁeld is uncontrolled as it is created.

####  created to base

**Created To Base**

- [[##rule 439.2.b.2|439.2.b.2.]] Runes will be Created to base.

####  creates

**Creates**

- [[##rule 184|184.]] The spell or ability that Creates a token speciﬁes some of its characteristics. It may have other characteristics, as listed below.
- [[##rule 438.1|438.1.]] Replacing is the act of Creating a token in the place of another card or token without playing it while inheriting all effects or statuses of the game object it replaced.
- [[##rule 439|439.]] Create
- [[##rule 439.1|439.1.]] Creating is the act of producing a Game Object that previously did not exist in the game.
- [[##rule 439.2|439.2.]] Effects that Create one or more Game Objects will direct where those Game Objects must go - the Game Objects are Created directly to the zones in question.
- [[##rule 439.3|439.3.]] An effect that Creates a Game Object will specify the nature of the Game Object created.
- [[##rule 439.4|439.4.]] Unless speciﬁed otherwise by the Game Effect that Creates a Game Object, any such Game Object is owned by the player who Created it. Control is established as usual for Game Objects of the appropriate type.
- [[##rule 439.6|439.6.]] Creating is a Limited Action.

####  ctivated ability

**Ctivated Ability**

- [[##rule 727.1.c.3.a|727.1.c.3.a.]] If the condition for the Dependent Keyword causes the Activated Ability to become Inactive after it has been added to the chain as a Pending Item, that chain item will not be affected and will proceed with being played as normal.

####  current turn player

**Current Turn Player**

- [[##rule 372.2|372.2.]] If the affected object is an Uncontrolled Battleﬁeld then the Current Turn Player decides the order the Replacement Effects will apply.

###  group D

####  damage

**Damage**

- [[##rule 142|142.]] Damage is a marked value that is applied to Units.
- [[##rule 142.1|142.1.]] Damage is not a Game Object.
- [[##rule 142.2|142.2.]] Damage is a value tracked per-Unit.
- [[##rule 142.3|142.3.]] Damage tracks how close a Unit is to being Killed.  See rule 428. Kill for more information.
- [[##rule 142.4|142.4.]] Damage can be Healed.  See rule 418. Heal for more information.
- [[##rule 143.3.b|143.3.b.]] Damage is Healed from Units at two speciﬁc times:
- [[##rule 323.4|323.4.]] 3a. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might that have Deathknell abilities will trigger their Deathknell ability now, making note of their current location, attributes, and other information relevant to add the trigger as a Pending Item See rule 808 Deathknell for more information.
- [[##rule 323.5|323.5.]] 3b. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might are killed and placed in their owners' Trash.
- [[##rule 417.1.a|417.1.a.]] Assigning Damage during the Combat Damage Step is not Dealing Damage, but will cause Damage to be Dealt when assignment is complete.
- [[##rule 417.1.b|417.1.b.]] To Deal Damage to Units, mark the speciﬁed amount of Damage on the Unit.
- [[##rule 417.1.c|417.1.c.]] Damage is marked on each unit separately.
- [[##rule 417.1.d|417.1.d.]] Damage can be Dealt to more than one Unit at the same time.
- [[##rule 417.1.e|417.1.e.]] Valid Damage is a positive integer amount, greater than or equal to 1 Damage.
- [[##rule 417.2|417.2.]] Only Damage can be Dealt.
- [[##rule 417.3.a|417.3.a.]] Assigning Damage causes Damage to be dealt outside of being directed to Deal Damage.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 417.5|417.5.]] Bonus Damage is a property granted to the action of Dealing and alters the amount of Damage distributed by this action.  See rule 712. Bonus Damage for more information.
- [[##rule 417.6.b|417.6.b.]] If a game effect does specify a source, then that source is what is considered the origin of the Damage for this Deal action.
- [[##rule 417.6.b.1|417.6.b.1.]] Units and Spells can be the source of Damage for Deal actions.
- [[##rule 417.6.b.2|417.6.b.2.]] Abilities can be the source of Damage for Deal actions.
- [[##rule 417.6.b.2.a|417.6.b.2.a.]] When an Ability is the source of Damage for a Deal action, it is in addition to the Spell or Unit that created that Ability.  Example: Iron Ballista is a gear that says “[E]: Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld.” This damage is dealt both by a gear and by an ability.
- [[##rule 417.6.b.3|417.6.b.3.]] When a spell or ability speciﬁes a Unit as the source of the Damage for the Deal action, it is not in addition to the spell or ability that speciﬁed it.  Example: Challenge is a spell that reads “Choose a friendly unit and an enemy unit. They deal damage equal to their Mights to each other.” The damage that Challenge causes to be dealt is dealt by the chosen units, not by Challenge.
- [[##rule 417.6.c|417.6.c.]] Damage Dealt as a result of being assigned during Combat has the Units as its source.
- [[##rule 417.6.c.1|417.6.c.1.]] The Damage assigned, and subsequently Dealt, to attackers has the defenders as the source and vice versa.
- [[##rule 417.7|417.7.]] Deal actions can distribute Damage as part of combat actions or non-combat actions.
- [[##rule 418.1|418.1.]] Damage being cleared from Units is Healing.
- [[##rule 418.1.a|418.1.a.]] If Damage is cleared for any reason it is considered Healing.
- [[##rule 437.1|437.1.]] Preventing damage is the act of reducing the Damage a set of game objects would take.
- [[##rule 437.1.a|437.1.a.]] Prevent is an action that interacts with Damage.
- [[##rule 460.2.c.1|460.2.c.1.]] Assigning Damage is not Dealing Damage.
- [[##rule 460.2.c.1.a|460.2.c.1.a.]] When all Damage is assigned, it will be Dealt simultaneously. These actions are not synonymous.
- [[##rule 460.2.d|460.2.d.]] Deal Damage to each unit equal to the amount assigned to it.
- [[##rule 713|713.]] Bonus Damage is an intrinsic property that can be granted to Deal actions that influence the amount of Damage that the action is distributing.
- [[##rule 714.1|714.1.]] Bonus Damage can only be a positive value, and can only increase the amount of Damage being distributed.
- [[##rule 715.1|715.1.]] If the Deal action has a single target, the amount of Damage to that target will be increased by the Bonus Damage granted to it.
- [[##rule 715.2|715.2.]] If the Deal action has multiple targets, the amount of Damage dealt to each target is increased by Bonus Damage individually and separately.  Example: Singularity is a spell that says “Deal 6 to each of up to two units.” A player plays Singularity while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Singularity deals 1 Bonus Damage to both of its targets, dealing 7 to each.
- [[##rule 715.3|715.3.]] If the Deal action Splits damage, then the Bonus Damage applies to the amount of Damage that will be Split. This can alter the number of targets eligible to be chosen.  Example: Volibear, Furious is a unit that says in part “When I attack, deal 5 damage split among any number of enemy units here.” A player attacks with Volibear, Furious while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Volibear, Furious now deals 6 damage split among any number of enemy units at its location, and can choose to split that damage among up to 6 units rather than the usual 5.

####  deal damage

**Deal Damage**

- [[##rule 417.1|417.1.]] Spells, Units, Abilities, and other game effects may Deal Damage to units.
- [[##rule 417.1.b|417.1.b.]] To Deal Damage to Units, mark the speciﬁed amount of Damage on the Unit.
- [[##rule 417.3.a|417.3.a.]] Assigning Damage causes Damage to be dealt outside of being directed to Deal Damage.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.

####  dealing damage

**Dealing Damage**

- [[##rule 417.1.a|417.1.a.]] Assigning Damage during the Combat Damage Step is not Dealing Damage, but will cause Damage to be Dealt when assignment is complete.
- [[##rule 417.3|417.3.]] Dealing Damage is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 460.2.c.1|460.2.c.1.]] Assigning Damage is not Dealing Damage.

####  dealt

**Dealt**

- [[##rule 417.1.a|417.1.a.]] Assigning Damage during the Combat Damage Step is not Dealing Damage, but will cause Damage to be Dealt when assignment is complete.
- [[##rule 417.1.d|417.1.d.]] Damage can be Dealt to more than one Unit at the same time.
- [[##rule 417.1.e.1|417.1.e.1.]] Only Valid Damage is Dealt. Example: A unit has “when I take damage, give me +2 [M] this turn.” A spell is played that Prevents the next 3 damage the unit would take. If a player plays Hextech Ray targeting the unit, it will take no damage and its triggered ability will not trigger. If that player had played Void Seeker instead, it would be Dealt 1 and trigger its ability. Example: A unit is present at Void Gate. A spell is played that Prevents the next 3 damage the unit would take. If a player plays Hextech Ray targeting the unit, it will take no damage - in order to apply the Bonus Damage from Void Gate, the Deal game action would have to occur, and Hextech Ray did not Deal any damage.
- [[##rule 417.2|417.2.]] Only Damage can be Dealt.
- [[##rule 417.4|417.4.]] Dealing can have the intrinsic property of Bonus Damage.
- [[##rule 417.5|417.5.]] Bonus Damage is a property granted to the action of Dealing and alters the amount of Damage distributed by this action.  See rule 712. Bonus Damage for more information.
- [[##rule 417.6|417.6.]] Deal actions can originate from one or more sources.
- [[##rule 417.6.a|417.6.a.]] If a game effect does not specify a source, the game effect describing the Deal action is the source.  Example: Void Seeker is a spell that reads “Deal 4 to a unit at a battleﬁeld. Draw 1.” The damage that Void Seeker instructs you to deal is dealt by Void Seeker.
- [[##rule 417.6.b|417.6.b.]] If a game effect does specify a source, then that source is what is considered the origin of the Damage for this Deal action.
- [[##rule 417.6.b.1|417.6.b.1.]] Units and Spells can be the source of Damage for Deal actions.
- [[##rule 417.6.b.2|417.6.b.2.]] Abilities can be the source of Damage for Deal actions.
- [[##rule 417.6.b.2.a|417.6.b.2.a.]] When an Ability is the source of Damage for a Deal action, it is in addition to the Spell or Unit that created that Ability.  Example: Iron Ballista is a gear that says “[E]: Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld.” This damage is dealt both by a gear and by an ability.
- [[##rule 417.6.b.3|417.6.b.3.]] When a spell or ability speciﬁes a Unit as the source of the Damage for the Deal action, it is not in addition to the spell or ability that speciﬁed it.  Example: Challenge is a spell that reads “Choose a friendly unit and an enemy unit. They deal damage equal to their Mights to each other.” The damage that Challenge causes to be dealt is dealt by the chosen units, not by Challenge.
- [[##rule 417.6.c.1|417.6.c.1.]] The Damage assigned, and subsequently Dealt, to attackers has the defenders as the source and vice versa.
- [[##rule 417.7|417.7.]] Deal actions can distribute Damage as part of combat actions or non-combat actions.
- [[##rule 460.2.c.1.a|460.2.c.1.a.]] When all Damage is assigned, it will be Dealt simultaneously. These actions are not synonymous.
- [[##rule 713|713.]] Bonus Damage is an intrinsic property that can be granted to Deal actions that influence the amount of Damage that the action is distributing.
- [[##rule 714|714.]] If more than one instance of Bonus Damage is applied or granted to a Deal action, all instances are summed and applied once.
- [[##rule 715|715.]] Bonus Damage applies to the total damage Dealt by one instance of the action.
- [[##rule 715.1|715.1.]] If the Deal action has a single target, the amount of Damage to that target will be increased by the Bonus Damage granted to it.
- [[##rule 715.2|715.2.]] If the Deal action has multiple targets, the amount of Damage dealt to each target is increased by Bonus Damage individually and separately.  Example: Singularity is a spell that says “Deal 6 to each of up to two units.” A player plays Singularity while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Singularity deals 1 Bonus Damage to both of its targets, dealing 7 to each.
- [[##rule 715.3|715.3.]] If the Deal action Splits damage, then the Bonus Damage applies to the amount of Damage that will be Split. This can alter the number of targets eligible to be chosen.  Example: Volibear, Furious is a unit that says in part “When I attack, deal 5 damage split among any number of enemy units here.” A player attacks with Volibear, Furious while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Volibear, Furious now deals 6 damage split among any number of enemy units at its location, and can choose to split that damage among up to 6 units rather than the usual 5.
- [[##rule 715.4|715.4.]] If no damage was Dealt, because it was replaced or reduced by any means, then Bonus Damage will not apply.

####  deathknell

**Deathknell**

- [[##rule 323.4|323.4.]] 3a. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might that have Deathknell abilities will trigger their Deathknell ability now, making note of their current location, attributes, and other information relevant to add the trigger as a Pending Item See rule 808 Deathknell for more information.
- [[##rule 428.1.a.1.b|428.1.a.1.b.]] When a unit with a Deathknell  is to be put in the Trash due to a Kill Instruction, it ﬁrst has its Deathknell added to the chain as a Pending Item. Note the unit’s location, attributes, and other relevant information to process its Deathknell when ﬁnalized before completing this Kill Instruction.
- [[##rule 808|808.]] Deathknell
- [[##rule 808.1.d.2|808.1.d.2.]] The trigger will be added to the chain as a Pending Item before the card with Deathknell is moved to the trash due to a Kill instruction or a Cleanup.
- [[##rule 808.1.d.3|808.1.d.3.]] Before the card with Deathknell is moved to the Trash, note its location, its attributes, and any other details related to the effect of its Deathknell to process the trigger after it has been Finalized.

####  deck constraint permission

**Deck Constraint Permission**

- [[##rule 825.1|825.1.]] Unique is a Deck Constraint Permission.

####  deck construction

**Deck Construction**

- [[##rule 101|101.]] Deck Construction
- [[##rule 175.1|175.1.]] The Legend determines the Domain Identity of cards its owner can include. See rule 101. Deck Construction for more information.

####  decks

**Decks**

- [[##rule 103|103.]] To play Riftbound, a player must have two Decks, a Champion Legend, and a number of Battleﬁelds determined by the Mode of Play.
- [[##rule 103.1.b.1|103.1.b.1.]] Cards included in your Deck must abide by your Domain Identity.
- [[##rule 355.14.g|355.14.g.]] Valid damage is a positive integer amount, greater than or equal to 1 damage. See rule 417. Deal for more information.
- [[##rule 417|417.]] Deal

####  decreases

**Decreases**

- [[##rule 433.1.a|433.1.a.]] Swapping creates two different effects that apply to each attribute. One that Increases one value and one that Decreases the other.
- [[##rule 433.1.b|433.1.b.]] To accomplish this, determine the difference between these values and then apply an Increase for that amount to the lower value  of the two attributes, and a Decrease of that amount to the higher value of the two attributes.

####  defend triggers

**Defend Triggers**

- [[##rule 383.4.f|383.4.f.]] Defend Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Defender designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat.

####  defender

**Defender**

- [[##rule 323.2|323.2.]] 2. Assign or Remove the Attacker or Defender designation from Units as needed if there is a Combat in progress
- [[##rule 323.2.c|323.2.c.]] If there are Units at locations other than the Battleﬁeld that the Combat is taking place at, but have either Attacker or Defender designations, they lose those designations now
- [[##rule 383.4.f|383.4.f.]] Defend Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Defender designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2|383.4.f.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Defender designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2.a|383.4.f.2.a.]] These triggers will only have their condition checked once per combat, despite a Unit being able to gain and lose the Defender designation multiple times in the same combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2.b|383.4.f.2.b.]] If the trigger condition contains other requirements besides defending and if those requirements are not fulﬁlled when the unit gains the Defender designation, it will not trigger in that combat.
- [[##rule 459.2.b|459.2.b.]] 1. Establish who is Attacker and who is Defender.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.2|459.2.b.2.]] The Defender is the player who did not apply the Contested status to the Battleﬁeld. They gain the Defender designation now.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.4|459.2.b.4.]] Units at the Contested Battleﬁeld controlled by the Defender gain the Defender designation now.
- [[##rule 459.2.b.4.a|459.2.b.4.a.]] If a Unit controlled by the Defender becomes present at this Battleﬁeld after this moment it will gain the Defender designation during the Cleanup phase following the action that caused it to become present
- [[##rule 459.2.d|459.2.d.]] 3. Add items to the Combat Chain if establishing Attacker and Defender has caused Triggered Abilities to become Pending.
- [[##rule 459.2.d.1|459.2.d.1.]] The Attacking player, who has Focus, places Triggered Abilities on the Chain ﬁrst, followed by all non-Defender players in Turn Order, followed by the Defending Player.
- [[##rule 460.1|460.1.]] If both Attacking and Defending units remain at this battleﬁeld, the following Tasks become Outstanding, in the speciﬁed order:
- [[##rule 460.2|460.2.]] 1. When the Showdown closes, Attackers and Defenders resolve Combat Damage at the Battleﬁeld that was attacked, using their current Might.
- [[##rule 461.1.a.2|461.1.a.2.]] Insert “3d. Recall Attackers present at the Battleﬁeld if Defenders are still present.” See rule 449. Recalls for more information.

####  defending player

**Defending Player**

- [[##rule 459.2.d.1|459.2.d.1.]] The Attacking player, who has Focus, places Triggered Abilities on the Chain ﬁrst, followed by all non-Defender players in Turn Order, followed by the Defending Player.

####  defending units

**Defending Units**

- [[##rule 460.2.b|460.2.b.]] Sum the Might of all Defending Units.

####  deflect

**Deflect**

- [[##rule 184.7|184.7.]] A 1 [M] Bird token is a domainless unit token with 1 Might, the Bird tag, and the Deflect keyword. See rule 809. Deflect for more information.
- [[##rule 356.2.a.2|356.2.a.2.]] The cost imposed by the Deflect keyword is a Mandatory Additional Cost.  See rule 809. Deflect for more information.
- [[##rule 809|809.]] Deflect

####  delayed abilities

**Delayed Abilities**

- [[##rule 361.1|361.1.]] An Ability has multiple structures.  -Passive Abilities  -Replacement Effects  -Activated Abilities  -Triggered Abilities  -Delayed Abilities
- [[##rule 390|390.]] Delayed Abilities are a type of Ability whose trigger Condition identiﬁes a speciﬁc time during a turn or a speciﬁc event that can occur during a speciﬁc timeframe.
- [[##rule 390.1|390.1.]] Delayed Abilities can be any other type of Ability, and contain all of the properties of that type in addition to the properties of Delayed Abilities.
- [[##rule 391|391.]] Delayed Abilities will resolve or be active just like the ability they augment, but only during the speciﬁed time in the effect that created the Delayed Ability.  Example: Ravenborn Tome reads “The next spell you play this turn deals 1 Bonus Damage” is a Delayed Passive Ability that passively adds 1 damage to just the next spell played. The next spell is a speciﬁc time, and the 1 Bonus Damage is a passive ability.  Example: Noxian Guillotine reads “Choose a unit. Kill it the next time it takes damage this turn.” When the chosen unit takes damage is the speciﬁed time, and killing it is the condition for a Delayed Triggered Ability.
- [[##rule 392|392.]] Delayed Abilities are not associated with Units or Gear; they are created by other Abilities or Spells. As such they are executed when their condition and/or speciﬁed time occurs regardless of whether the source of the Delayed Ability is still on the board or not.
- [[##rule 437.7|437.7.]] Prevent is a Delayed Replacement Effect. See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information. See rule 389. Delayed Abilities for more information.

####  delayed linked abilities

**Delayed Linked Abilities**

- [[##rule 390.5|390.5.]] Delayed Linked Abilities are Linked Abilities that are generated by another Ability and  that Ability or Game Objects it affects. Delayed Linked Abilities don’t necessarily identify a speciﬁc window of time, and instead are deﬁned by the Ability they are linked with.

####  delayed linked ability’s

**Delayed Linked Ability’s**

- [[##rule 390.5.a|390.5.a.]] If that Ability affects a Game Object, the Delayed Linked Ability’s window will be as long as that Game Object is in an appropriate zone.
- [[##rule 390.5.b|390.5.b.]] If the Delayed Linked Ability s the source of the abilities, its window will be as long as the source is in an appropriate zone.

####  delayed passive abilities

**Delayed Passive Abilities**

- [[##rule 390.4|390.4.]] Delayed Passive Abilities are Passive Abilities that are applicable only during a speciﬁed window of time. The time that the Delayed Passive Ability applies will be recognized in the effect that initiates it.
- [[##rule 391|391.]] Delayed Abilities will resolve or be active just like the ability they augment, but only during the speciﬁed time in the effect that created the Delayed Ability.  Example: Ravenborn Tome reads “The next spell you play this turn deals 1 Bonus Damage” is a Delayed Passive Ability that passively adds 1 damage to just the next spell played. The next spell is a speciﬁc time, and the 1 Bonus Damage is a passive ability.  Example: Noxian Guillotine reads “Choose a unit. Kill it the next time it takes damage this turn.” When the chosen unit takes damage is the speciﬁed time, and killing it is the condition for a Delayed Triggered Ability.

####  delayed replacement effect

**Delayed Replacement Effect**

- [[##rule 437.7|437.7.]] Prevent is a Delayed Replacement Effect. See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information. See rule 389. Delayed Abilities for more information.

####  delayed replacements

**Delayed Replacements**

- [[##rule 390.3|390.3.]] Delayed Replacements are Replacement Effects that can be recognized by specifying the effect they are replacing at a speciﬁc time, or “the [Nth] time” in the description of the effect as it resolves.

####  delayed triggered ability

**Delayed Triggered Ability**

- [[##rule 391|391.]] Delayed Abilities will resolve or be active just like the ability they augment, but only during the speciﬁed time in the effect that created the Delayed Ability.  Example: Ravenborn Tome reads “The next spell you play this turn deals 1 Bonus Damage” is a Delayed Passive Ability that passively adds 1 damage to just the next spell played. The next spell is a speciﬁc time, and the 1 Bonus Damage is a passive ability.  Example: Noxian Guillotine reads “Choose a unit. Kill it the next time it takes damage this turn.” When the chosen unit takes damage is the speciﬁed time, and killing it is the condition for a Delayed Triggered Ability.

####  delayed triggers

**Delayed Triggers**

- [[##rule 390.2|390.2.]] Delayed Triggers are Triggered Abilities that can be recognized by describing a speciﬁc time of the turn, or by structuring a Triggered Ability with a speciﬁc frame of time as a restriction.

####  depend on

**Depend On**

- [[##rule 474|474.]] To determine which effect Depends on another, determine which of the prior criteria applies, and then also which effect’s evaluation is altered by the sequence of applications. That effect is said to Depend on the other.

####  dependency

**Dependency**

- [[##rule 473|473.]] If more than one effect applies to the same Game Object in the Same Layer, or to each other in the same layer, then both effects will apply but their order may be determined by Dependency.
- [[##rule 473.1|473.1.]] A Dependency is established if:

####  dependent ability

**Dependent Ability**

- [[##rule 727.1.b|727.1.b.]] The Dependent Ability associated with the Dependent Keyword is Inactive on the card with the Dependent Keyword until the Condition is met, when it becomes Active
- [[##rule 727.1.b.1|727.1.b.1.]] The Dependent Ability is present on the card for the sake of  or evaluation until the Condition is met See rule 720. Inactive for more information
- [[##rule 727.1.b.2|727.1.b.2.]] The Dependent Ability is Active exactly as written while the Condition is true Example: Gustwalker has “[Level3][>] I have +1 [M] and Ganking.” As long as its controller has 3 XP, Gustwalker’s Ganking is active.
- [[##rule 727.1.c|727.1.c.]] The Dependent Abilities of Dependent Keywords can be of any type
- [[##rule 812.1.b.2|812.1.b.2.]] The [Text] is the Dependent Ability.
- [[##rule 812.1.c|812.1.c.]] As long as a card different than the one with the Legion ability has been Finalized on the same turn then the Dependent Ability is Active on the card with Legion.
- [[##rule 824.1.b.2|824.1.b.2.]] The [Text] here is the Dependent Ability
- [[##rule 824.1.c|824.1.c.]] As long as the controlling player has [N] XP, then the Dependent Ability will be be Active on the card with Level
- [[##rule 824.1.c.1|824.1.c.1.]] If the controller of the card with Level changes, then the Dependent Ability will be rendered Active or Inactive based on the new controller’s XP.
- [[##rule 824.1.d|824.1.d.]] The Dependent Ability will be Inactive as soon as the controlling player has less than [N] XP.

####  dependent keywords

**Dependent Keywords**

- [[##rule 726|726.]] Dependent Keywords
- [[##rule 727|727.]] Keywords can be Dependent Keywords
- [[##rule 727.1|727.1.]] A Dependent Keyword is comprised of both a Condition that it is short for, and an ability of some format immediately after the Keyword itself. EXAMPLE: Noxus Hopeful has “[Legion][>] I cost [2] less.” [Legion] is short for the condition “if you have played another card this turn, this card gains [Text],” while “I cost [2] less” is the dependent ability.
- [[##rule 727.1.a|727.1.a.]] A Dependent Keyword will always be functionally short for a Condition.
- [[##rule 727.1.b|727.1.b.]] The Dependent Ability associated with the Dependent Keyword is Inactive on the card with the Dependent Keyword until the Condition is met, when it becomes Active
- [[##rule 727.1.c|727.1.c.]] The Dependent Abilities of Dependent Keywords can be of any type
- [[##rule 727.1.c.1|727.1.c.1.]] Triggered Abilities of Dependent Keywords must be Active for their trigger to be evaluated.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.2|727.1.c.2.]] Passive Abilities begin applying at the same time the Dependent Keyword becomes true.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.3|727.1.c.3.]] Activated Abilities that become Active from Dependent Keywords can be activated at their associated timing after that ability has been granted
- [[##rule 727.1.c.3.a|727.1.c.3.a.]] If the condition for the Dependent Keyword causes the Activated Ability to become Inactive after it has been added to the chain as a Pending Item, that chain item will not be affected and will proceed with being played as normal.
- [[##rule 812.1|812.1.]] Legion is a Dependent Keyword.
- [[##rule 824.1|824.1.]] Level is a Dependent Keyword.

####  depends on

**Depends On**

- [[##rule 474|474.]] To determine which effect Depends on another, determine which of the prior criteria applies, and then also which effect’s evaluation is altered by the sequence of applications. That effect is said to Depend on the other.
- [[##rule 474.1|474.1.]] To resolve a dependency, the effects within the same layer that created the dependency must be applied such that:  1. Identify which effect Depends on the other within the Layer.  2. Apply the effect that is depended on ﬁrst.  3. Immediately apply the effect that Depends on the ﬁrst effect next.

####  destination

**Destination**

- [[##rule 144.3.a|144.3.a.]] When a Move like this is declared by a player, the units' Destination must be the same.
- [[##rule 169.5.b|169.5.b.]] Battleﬁelds can be Destinations of moves.
- [[##rule 441.3.b|441.3.b.]] Permanents are either at their Origin before Moving or their Destination after Moving.
- [[##rule 442|442.]] Moving is deﬁned by the Origin and Destination of the Permanent that is changing locations.
- [[##rule 442.2|442.2.]] The Destination is where the Permanent is going to.
- [[##rule 444.1|444.1.]] The source of the Move will provide details on any restrictions on legality for Destination.
- [[##rule 445|445.]] The Destination becomes Contested if it is a Battleﬁeld not controlled by the controller of the Unit or Units that moved.

####  detach

**Detach**

- [[##rule 434.1.f|434.1.f.]] Attaching a card to a new Top-Most Card will cause it to Detach from the card to which it is currently Attached.
- [[##rule 435|435.]] Detach
- [[##rule 435.1|435.1.]] Detaching is the act of unlinking two cards that are currently linked through the act of Attaching. This causes one to cease being Attached, and potentially causes the other to cease being a Top-Most card.
- [[##rule 435.1.a|435.1.a.]] Detaching affects only cards that are currently Attached to another card.
- [[##rule 435.1.a.1|435.1.a.1.]] Game effects that instruct a player to Detach a card that is currently not Attached to anything will do nothing.
- [[##rule 435.1.b|435.1.b.]] When one or more cards become Detached, they cease to be in the Attached state.
- [[##rule 435.1.c|435.1.c.]] The card being Detached has its Effect Text become Inactive and its Rules Text cease being Inactive.
- [[##rule 435.1.d|435.1.d.]] The Top-Most Card ceases to have the Effect Text of the card being Detached appended to its Rules Text.
- [[##rule 435.1.e|435.1.e.]] The Top-Most Card ceases to have its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of the card being Detached.
- [[##rule 435.2|435.2.]] Detaching is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 435.2.a|435.2.a.]] Players may only Detach cards when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 435.3|435.3.]] Detaching cards does not inherently choose, or specify a target. However, Game Effects that Detach cards may.
- [[##rule 435.4|435.4.]] When a card Detaches from a Top-Most Card, its location is the same as the Top-Most Card from which it Detached.
- [[##rule 435.4.a|435.4.a.]] If the Detached card was a Gear and this causes it to become present at a Battleﬁeld, it will be Recalled during the next Cleanup.
- [[##rule 435.4.b|435.4.b.]] If the Attached card was Detached because the Top-Most Card changed zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, then the location that the Attached Card will Detach to is the last location the Top-Most Card was at before changing from a board zone to a non-board zone.
- [[##rule 718.1|718.1.]] A card remains in this state until Detached.
- [[##rule 719.5|719.5.]] When a Top-Most Card changes zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, all Attached cards Detach from it, remaining in their current zones.
- [[##rule 719.5.a|719.5.a.]] The player that controls the Top-Most Card that changed zones decides the order these cards Detach in, and thus the order of any relevant effects that occur due to the Detach occurring.
- [[##rule 725.2|725.2.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Detaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Detaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Detaches.

####  discard

**Discard**

- [[##rule 422|422.]] Discard
- [[##rule 422.1|422.1.]] Discarding a card is moving it from a player's hand directly into their trash without activating or executing its normal rules text.
- [[##rule 422.2|422.2.]] Discarding is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 422.2.a|422.2.a.]] A player must Discard cards when instructed to do so by game effects or costs.
- [[##rule 422.3|422.3.]] When Discarding is listed as a Cost, then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: A card has the ability "Discard 2: Deal 2 damage to a unit at a battleﬁeld." To activate the ability, the card's controller must have at least 2 cards in hand and must be able to discard them.
- [[##rule 422.4|422.4.]] When Discarding is part of an effect, then a player must Discard as many cards as possible from their hand. If instructed to discard more cards than they have in their hand, further discard instructions are ignored.  Example: Undercover Agent has the ability "[Deathknell][>] Discard 2, then draw 2. (When I die, get the effect.)" If Undercover Agent's controller has 2 or more cards in hand, they must discard 2. If they have 1 card in hand, they discard 1, and the rest of the discard instruction is ignored. If they have no cards in hand, the entire discard instruction is ignored. Regardless of how many cards they discard, they then draw 2.
- [[##rule 427.2.b|427.2.b.]] Banish is not a subset of Discard.

####  discretionary actions

**Discretionary Actions**

- [[##rule 305|305.]] When there are no items on the Chain and the Turn Player cannot or chooses not to perform any Discretionary Actions, the current phase or step of the turn ends and the next phase, step, or turn begins.
- [[##rule 312.1|312.1.]] Priority is the singular exclusive right to take Discretionary Actions. See rule 410.1. Discretionary Actions for more information.
- [[##rule 312.1.a|312.1.a.]] The player with Priority can take appropriately timed Discretionary Actions.
- [[##rule 312.1.b|312.1.b.]] If no player has Priority, no player can take Discretionary Actions.
- [[##rule 313.1|313.1.]] Focus is the permission to take appropriately timed Discretionary Actions when the turn is in a Showdown Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 313.1.a|313.1.a.]] The player with Focus must obey any additional restrictions on which Discretionary Actions may be performed.  Example: A player with Focus may not play spells or activate abilities that don't have the Action or Reaction keywords.
- [[##rule 316.2.a|316.2.a.]] A player may take any number of Discretionary Actions they are able to perform during this phase.  See rule 410.1. Discretionary Actions for more information.
- [[##rule 316.3|316.3.]] As a result of a player taking Discretionary Actions, one or more structured phases may occur.
- [[##rule 316.6|316.6.]] When a player has no more Discretionary Actions they wish to execute, they must indicate they are ending their turn.
- [[##rule 410.1|410.1.]] Discretionary Actions
- [[##rule 410.1.a|410.1.a.]] A Discretionary Action is a Game Action that may be performed at any time during a player's turn during a Neutral Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
