- [[##rule 410.1.b|410.1.b.]] A player may take any number of Discretionary Actions available to them during their turn.
- [[##rule 414.3.a|414.3.a.]] Most Exhaust actions will be costs for Activated Abilities or Discretionary Actions. Example: A unit's Standard Move exhausts the unit as a cost.
- [[##rule 419.2|419.2.]] This is a Discretionary Action.
- [[##rule 420.3|420.3.]] The Standard Move inherent to Units is a Discretionary Action.
- [[##rule 421.2|421.2.]] Hiding is a Discretionary Action.

####  disqualiﬁed

**Disqualiﬁed**

- [[##rule 315.2.b.3|315.2.b.3.]] Reminder: In Modes of Play with Teams, Battleﬁelds held by a Teammate of the Turn Player during this phase are disqualiﬁed from being scored this turn by the Turn Player.

####  disqualiﬁed from being scored

**Disqualiﬁed From Being Scored**

- [[##rule 484.8.b|484.8.b.]] Battleﬁelds controlled during the Beginning Phase of a player's turn by that player's teammate are disqualiﬁed from being scored by that Team, that turn. Example: A player may not induce their partner to retreat, and then conquer a Battleﬁeld their teammate was controlling.

####  domain

**Domain**

- [[##rule 103.1.b.3|103.1.b.3.]] If a card has a single Domain, then that card is permitted in the Domain Identity that corresponds to the same Domain.
- [[##rule 103.1.b.4|103.1.b.4.]] If a card has more than one Domain, then that card is permitted only in a Domain Identity that contains all of the indicated Domains on that card.
- [[##rule 134|134.]] Domain
- [[##rule 134.1|134.1.]] Most cards belong to one or more of six Domains, identiﬁed by one or more symbols in the lower right corner.
- [[##rule 135.2.e.4|135.2.e.4.]] Power of a speciﬁc Domain is represented by its domain symbol and the corresponding shorthand. See rule 134. Domain for more information.
- [[##rule 135.2.e.5|135.2.e.5.]] Power of any Domain is represented by a swirling rainbow symbol. Its shorthand is [A].
- [[##rule 135.2.e.5.a|135.2.e.5.a.]] When required as a cost, [A] can be paid by Power of any Domain.
- [[##rule 135.2.e.5.b|135.2.e.5.b.]] When Added to a player’s Rune Pool, [A] can be spent to pay a Power cost of any Domain.
- [[##rule 135.2.e.6|135.2.e.6.]] Power of a domain corresponding to a card’s own Domain is not represented by a symbol, but appears in these rules similarly to other symbols. Its shorthand is [C].
- [[##rule 135.2.e.6.a|135.2.e.6.a.]] When a [C] shorthand is printed on a card as reminder text, it assumes that card’s usual Domain, but it still means “one Power of this card’s Domain.”
- [[##rule 135.2.e.6.b|135.2.e.6.b.]] A [C] shorthand on a card with no Domain or with multiple Domains is processed as [A] instead.
- [[##rule 163.2.b.1|163.2.b.1.]] The Power added this way corresponds to the Domain of the Rune that is being Recycled.
- [[##rule 175|175.]] Legends may have one or more Domains.
- [[##rule 182.2.b|182.2.b.]] Tokens do not have domains.

####  domain identity

**Domain Identity**

- [[##rule 103.1.b|103.1.b.]] This will dictate the Domain Identity of the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 103.1.b.1|103.1.b.1.]] Cards included in your Deck must abide by your Domain Identity.
- [[##rule 103.1.b.2|103.1.b.2.]] Your deck’s Domain Identity is dictated by the domains of your Champion Legend. In the default card frame, these domains appear as symbols in the legend’s upper left corner.
- [[##rule 103.1.b.3|103.1.b.3.]] If a card has a single Domain, then that card is permitted in the Domain Identity that corresponds to the same Domain.
- [[##rule 103.1.b.4|103.1.b.4.]] If a card has more than one Domain, then that card is permitted only in a Domain Identity that contains all of the indicated Domains on that card.
- [[##rule 103.2.c|103.2.c.]] Subject to Domain Identity.
- [[##rule 103.3.a.1|103.3.a.1.]] Cards in this deck must be of the Domain Identity of your Champion Legend.
- [[##rule 103.4.b|103.4.b.]] Subject to Domain Identity if applicable.
- [[##rule 175.1|175.1.]] The Legend determines the Domain Identity of cards its owner can include. See rule 101. Deck Construction for more information.

####  double

**Double**

- [[##rule 432|432.]] Double
- [[##rule 432.1|432.1.]] Doubling is the act of increasing  a numeric attribute by an amount equal to that attribute’s current value.
- [[##rule 432.2|432.2.]] Doubling is a Limited Action.

####  drawn

**Drawn**

- [[##rule 108.7.b|108.7.b.]] This is the location cards go when Drawn.
- [[##rule 315.4.b.2|315.4.b.2.]] After completing the Burn Out the Turn Player still Draws 1.
- [[##rule 410.2.b|410.2.b.]] These actions can only be taken when a player is instructed to do so as the execution of an effect or during their speciﬁed occasion during the turn.  Example: A player may Draw during the Draw Step of the Beginning Phase of their turn or when instructed to do so by a spell or ability. They can't choose to Draw at any other time.
- [[##rule 413|413.]] Draw
- [[##rule 413.1|413.1.]] Drawing a card takes a single card from a zone and adding it to the player's Hand.
- [[##rule 413.2.a|413.2.a.]] Each player draws 1 during the Draw Step of their Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 413.4.c|413.4.c.]] Draw the remaining cards needed to complete the Draw action.
- [[##rule 431.1.a|431.1.a.]] If a player must Draw cards in excess to the number of cards in their deck, they will Draw as many as possible, perform this action, then Draw the remaining amount instructed.
- [[##rule 482.7|482.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 483.7|483.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 484.7|484.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.

####  duration

**Duration**

- [[##rule 727.1.a.1|727.1.a.1.]] This Condition may also have a determined Duration, Time, or Limitation as part of its deﬁnition. EXAMPLE: Legion speciﬁes the duration of its condition: “if you have played another card this turn.” This turn is the duration. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “Until you have spent [3] this turn” would include a limitation on its condition. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “After you’ve become an attacker this turn” would include a time after which the condition is active.

####  during a neutral open state

**During A Neutral Open State**

- [[##rule 410.1.a|410.1.a.]] A Discretionary Action is a Game Action that may be performed at any time during a player's turn during a Neutral Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.

###  group E

####  effect text

**Effect Text**

- [[##rule 136|136.]] Effect Text
- [[##rule 136.1|136.1.]] Some cards have a separate section of text below the Rules Text. This is referred to as the Effect Text.
- [[##rule 136.2|136.2.]] Effect Text can contain additional Abilities.
- [[##rule 136.2.a|136.2.a.]] Effect Text can be blank.
- [[##rule 136.2.b|136.2.b.]] Effect Text is inactive unless the card with the Effect Text is Attached to another card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 136.2.c|136.2.c.]] The abilities in the Effect Text section of a card are appended to the Rules Text of the card to which the card with the Effect Text is Attached.
- [[##rule 377.1|377.1.]] Activated Abilities are recognized by the presence of a ":" in the text of the card, preceded by a cost and succeeded by an effect.  Example: "[2]: Draw 1" is an activated ability. The cost is 2 energy. The effect is to draw 1 card.
- [[##rule 383.2|383.2.]] Triggered Abilities have a Condition and an Effect.
- [[##rule 383.2.b|383.2.b.]] The Effect is the Instruction that follows the comma after the Condition.
- [[##rule 383.3.a|383.3.a.]] If a Triggered Ability says “you may” as the ﬁrst part of its Effect, the controller of its source will choose whether or not to place the Triggered Ability on the chain when its trigger Condition is fulﬁlled.
- [[##rule 383.4|383.4.]] Some Conditions are commonly used and structured in a way that explicitly deﬁnes their use and other properties of the Effect that is associated with it.
- [[##rule 420.3.b|420.3.b.]] The Effect is Moving those Unit.
- [[##rule 434.1.b|434.1.b.]] This is represented by physically laying the Top-Most card on top of the other or others such that all Effect Texts and Might Bonuses are showing, but nothing else from the card or cards Attached.
- [[##rule 434.1.b.1|434.1.b.1.]] In the situation where there is more than one card attached to the Top-Most card, they should be stacked in such a way that all Effect Text boxes and Might Bonuses are readable. The order of the Attached cards has no bearing on the application of effects.
- [[##rule 434.1.c|434.1.c.]] The Top-Most card has all Effect Text of all cards Attached to it appended to its Rules Text.
- [[##rule 435.1.c|435.1.c.]] The card being Detached has its Effect Text become Inactive and its Rules Text cease being Inactive.
- [[##rule 435.1.d|435.1.d.]] The Top-Most Card ceases to have the Effect Text of the card being Detached appended to its Rules Text.
- [[##rule 472.2.c|472.2.c.]] Abilities of Effect Text of Attached cards are appended in this layer.
- [[##rule 718.3|718.3.]] While in this state, Abilities in the card’s Effect Text are appended to the Rules Text of the Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 718.5.g|718.5.g.]] An Attached card still appends the abilities in its Effect Text to the Rules Text of the Top-Most card and modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by its Might Bonus.
- [[##rule 719.1|719.1.]] The Effect Text of all cards Attached to this card are appended to the Rules Text of this card for as long as they remain Attached.
- [[##rule 724|724.]] Effect Text is Inactive unless the card with the Effect Text is Attached.

####  end of turn  process

**End Of Turn Process**

- [[##rule 334.1|334.1.]] Tasks include, but are not limited to: Cleanups, the actions performed during the Start of Turn Process, throughout Combat in its various steps, and the actions performed during the End of Turn  Process. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information on Cleanups See rule 315. Start of Turn for more information on the Start of Turn process See rule 454. Combat for more information on the steps of Combat See rule 317. Ending Phase for more information.

####  end of turn cleanup

**End Of Turn Cleanup**

- [[##rule 324.1|324.1.]] When a Special Cleanup is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a Combat Cleanup is invoked, the Combat section deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 461. The Resolution Step for more information. Example: When an End of Turn Cleanup is invoked, the End of Turn Phase subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 317. The Ending Phase for more information.

####  end of turn phase

**End Of Turn Phase**

- [[##rule 324.1|324.1.]] When a Special Cleanup is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a Combat Cleanup is invoked, the Combat section deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 461. The Resolution Step for more information. Example: When an End of Turn Cleanup is invoked, the End of Turn Phase subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 317. The Ending Phase for more information.

####  ending phase

**Ending Phase**

- [[##rule 316.6.b|316.6.b.]] Play proceeds to the Ending Phase.
- [[##rule 324.1|324.1.]] When a Special Cleanup is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a Combat Cleanup is invoked, the Combat section deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 461. The Resolution Step for more information. Example: When an End of Turn Cleanup is invoked, the End of Turn Phase subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 317. The Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 334.1|334.1.]] Tasks include, but are not limited to: Cleanups, the actions performed during the Start of Turn Process, throughout Combat in its various steps, and the actions performed during the End of Turn  Process. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information on Cleanups See rule 315. Start of Turn for more information on the Start of Turn process See rule 454. Combat for more information on the steps of Combat See rule 317. Ending Phase for more information.

####  ending step

**Ending Step**

- [[##rule 423.1.a.2|423.1.a.2.]] Stunned Units lose the Stunned status at the beginning of the next Ending Step.

####  enemies

**Enemies**

- [[##rule 740.2|740.2.]] Two Game Objects are enemies if one’s controller is an opponent of the other’s.

####  energy

**Energy**

- [[##rule 131.2|131.2.]] Energy Cost
- [[##rule 162|162.]] Runes produce Energy and Power.
- [[##rule 162.1|162.1.]] Energy is used to pay numeric Energy costs.
- [[##rule 162.1.a|162.1.a.]] Energy has no Domain.
- [[##rule 162.1.b|162.1.b.]] Energy has no type.
- [[##rule 165|165.]] The Rune Pool is a conceptual collection of a player's available Energy and Power available to pay Costs.
- [[##rule 165.1|165.1.]] When a card adds Energy or Power, it is added to the controlling player's Rune Pool.
- [[##rule 165.2|165.2.]] Players must ﬁrst add Energy and Power to their Rune Pool in order to be able to spend it to play cards or pay for Abilities with costs.
- [[##rule 165.3|165.3.]] Energy and Power do not have a physical marker or tracker, although players may wish to use a physical tracker if they are retaining unspent Energy and Power over the course of their turn.
- [[##rule 166.1|166.1.]] Any unspent Energy or Power are lost.
- [[##rule 167|167.]] All Abilities that include the action "Add" are abilities that are adding Energy or Power to the Rune Pool. See rule 429. Add for more information.
- [[##rule 306|306.]] The Turn Player changes when the current Turn Player reaches the End of all of the Phases of their Turn.
- [[##rule 315.4.d|315.4.d.]] 1. Each player's Rune Pool empties. Any unspent Energy and Power are lost. See rule 164. Rune Pools for more information.
- [[##rule 317.2.d|317.2.d.]] Insert “2e. Each player’s Rune Pool empties. Any unspent Energy and Power are lost.”
- [[##rule 356.1.b.1|356.1.b.1.]] If a card allows a player to play a card "ignoring its cost," its base Energy cost and base Power cost are set to zero.
- [[##rule 357.1|357.1.]] In total, pay the combined Energy cost (if any) and Power cost (if any).
- [[##rule 357.1.a|357.1.a.]] During this step, the card's controller can use activated abilities with the Reaction tag that Add resources to add Energy and Power to pay the card's costs.  See rule 164. Rune Pools and rule 429. Add for more information.

####  enter the board

**Enter The Board**

- [[##rule 188.3|188.3.]] For Permanents and Runes, when they Enter the Board, that player is assigned as that Game Object's Controller.

####  equip

**Equip**

- [[##rule 725.3|725.3.]] If an Attached card has an Equip ability, the Weaponmaster keyword can  that Equip ability and any abilities that passively modify that Equip ability.
- [[##rule 818|818.]] Equip
- [[##rule 818.1|818.1.]] Equip is an Activated Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 818.1.a|818.1.a.]] Equip is normally present on Gear with the tag Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.1.b|818.1.b.]] Equip has a cost to activate and Attaches the card with Equip to a chosen Unit when the cost is paid.
- [[##rule 818.1.b.1|818.1.b.1.]] Equip’s choice is a Target.
- [[##rule 818.1.c|818.1.c.]] Equip is formatted as “Equip [Cost]”
- [[##rule 818.1.c.2|818.1.c.2.]] Equip is functionally short for “[Cost]: Attach this gear to a unit you control.”
- [[##rule 818.1.c.3|818.1.c.3.]] Equip costs may include both resource costs and non-resource costs.
- [[##rule 818.1.c.4|818.1.c.4.]] Equip abilities may also include text that alters the Equip cost. Such text is taken into account when determining a card’s Equip cost for any reason.
- [[##rule 818.1.c.5|818.1.c.5.]] Equip abilities may include text that alters the timing or targeting of the Equip ability.
- [[##rule 818.2|818.2.]] When the Attach action completes from this keyword, the Unit that was chosen is considered to have been Equipped by the Gear with this ability.
- [[##rule 818.3|818.3.]] Equipped is the state of a Top-Most Card being Attached by one or more cards that are Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.3.a|818.3.a.]] The state of being Equipped is synchronous with that of the Attached state of the Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.3.b|818.3.b.]] A Top-Most Card is Equipped as long as one or more of its Attached cards are Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.3.c|818.3.c.]] The state of being Equipped corresponds to a Top-Most card having a card with Equip that is Attached to it.
- [[##rule 818.4|818.4.]] Multiple instances of Equip are equivalent to multiple Activated Abilities and can each be activated separately by paying the corresponding costs.
- [[##rule 818.5|818.5.]] Equip, and whether or not a Gear has Equip, is a characteristic of the Gear and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 818.5.a|818.5.a.]] Whether or not a Gear has Equip may be d even if the Rules Text of the Gear is Inactive. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 819.1.a|819.1.a.]] Quick-Draw is present on Gear with Equip abilities.
- [[##rule 821.1.b|821.1.b.]] Weaponmaster is a Play Effect that chooses an Equipment you control and allows you to pay its Equip cost at a discount, regardless of the usual timing of the Equip ability, to Attach that Equipment to the unit with Weaponmaster.
- [[##rule 821.1.c|821.1.c.]] Weaponmaster is functionally short for: “When you play me, you may choose a Card you control with the Equipment tag. Necessary portions of its Rules Text are no longer Inactive if they are currently Inactive. Pay the cost of its Equip ability, reduced by [A], to attach it to this unit.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 821.1.c.1|821.1.c.1.]] Weaponmaster can choose an Equipment whether it has an Equip ability or not.
- [[##rule 821.1.c.2|821.1.c.2.]] The cost of the Equip ability is determined as though that Equip ability was being activated choosing the unit with the Weaponmaster ability, as modulated by any abilities that alter Equip costs.
- [[##rule 821.1.c.3|821.1.c.3.]] If the chosen card’s Equip cost does not contain [A], it can still be paid, but will not be reduced.
- [[##rule 821.1.c.4|821.1.c.4.]] If the chosen card doesn’t have an Equip cost, it can’t be paid.
- [[##rule 821.1.c.5|821.1.c.5.]] If the chosen card’s Equip cost can’t be paid, if it can’t be detached from its current Top-Most card, or if it can’t be attached to the unit with the Weaponmaster ability, it stays in its current location, Attached to anything it was already Attached to.
- [[##rule 821.1.c.6|821.1.c.6.]] The Equip ability is not activated this way, and the unit with the Weaponmaster ability is not chosen.

####  establishes control

**Establishes Control**

- [[##rule 461.5|461.5.]] 1. If no Showdown or Combat is staged at this location, the player with Units remaining here Establishes Control.

####  establishing control

**Establishing Control**

- [[##rule 461.5.d|461.5.d.]] Establishing Control results in a Conquer if that player has not yet scored this Battleﬁeld this turn. See rule 185. Control for more information on Control.  See rule 464.1.for more information on Conquering.

####  everything else

**Everything Else**

- [[##rule 188|188.]] Everything Else

####  exhaust symbol

**Exhaust Symbol**

- [[##rule 414.5|414.5.]] In abilities, the Exhaust symbol represents the cost "Exhaust this" or "Exhaust me." It resembles a card turning sideways.

####  exhausted

**Exhausted**

- [[##rule 109.2|109.2.]] The State of all Game Objects in the Play Area is also Public Information.  Examples:   If a Unit is Buffed  If a Gear is Exhausted  Etc.
- [[##rule 135.2.e.2|135.2.e.2.]] The cost of Exhausting a Permanent is represented by the “exhaust symbol,” which resembles a card turning sideways. Its shorthand is [E]. (Some previous rules information has given its shorthand as [T].)
- [[##rule 144.2|144.2.]] Exhausting the Unit is the Cost for this action.
- [[##rule 144.3.c|144.3.c.]] The Costs of Exhausting the Units are also paid Simultaneously.
- [[##rule 414|414.]] Exhaust
- [[##rule 414.1|414.1.]] Exhausting is an action that marks a non-spell Game Object on the board as "spent."
- [[##rule 414.1.b|414.1.b.]] A Unit that is already Exhausted cannot be Exhausted again.
- [[##rule 414.1.c|414.1.c.]] If a Unit is instructed to be Exhausted while it is already Exhausted, nothing additional happens.
- [[##rule 414.2|414.2.]] "Exhausted" is a state for Game Objects on the board that other game effects and rules can .
- [[##rule 414.3.a|414.3.a.]] Most Exhaust actions will be costs for Activated Abilities or Discretionary Actions. Example: A unit's Standard Move exhausts the unit as a cost.
- [[##rule 414.4|414.4.]] When Exhausting is listed as a Cost, then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: A spell says "As an additional cost to play this, you may exhaust a friendly unit." An exhausted friendly unit may not be exhausted again as the additional cost for the spell, and the additional cost has not been paid.
- [[##rule 415.1.a|415.1.a.]] To mark it, rotate the card 90 degrees opposite of Exhausting, so that it is vertically oriented in front of you.
- [[##rule 420.3.a|420.3.a.]] The Cost is Exhausting one or more Units.
- [[##rule 719.4|719.4.]] The Exhausted and Ready state of the Top-Most card does not affect nor change the status of the Attached cards and vice versa.

###  group F

####  face up

**Face Up**

- [[##rule 130.5|130.5.]] The term face up is used to describe the state during regular play of having a card's front face presented

####  facedown zones

**Facedown Zones**

- [[##rule 107.3|107.3.]] Facedown Zones
- [[##rule 107.3.a|107.3.a.]] Each Battleﬁeld is associated with a sub-zone called a Facedown Zone, a single logical space that a card can be put facedown in through various Game Effects.
- [[##rule 107.3.b|107.3.b.]] Each Facedown Zone has a maximum occupancy of one card.
- [[##rule 107.3.b.1|107.3.b.1.]] The maximum occupancy of a Facedown Zone can increase or decrease.
- [[##rule 107.3.b.2|107.3.b.2.]] If the maximum occupancy of a Facedown Zone decreases to a number less than the number of cards currently located there, the controller of that Facedown Zone must put a number of cards equal to the difference in the trash from the Facedown Zone.
- [[##rule 107.3.c|107.3.c.]] Cards can only be placed in or occupy the Facedown Zone if the controller of the card also controls the associated Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 107.3.d|107.3.d.]] If a player loses Control of a Battleﬁeld, any cards in the Facedown Zone associated with that Battleﬁeld are removed during the next Cleanup. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information. See rule 421. Hide for more information.
- [[##rule 129.4|129.4.]] The term facedown is used to describe the state during regular play of having a card's back side presented on the Board. A facedown card’s front side is considered Private Information.

####  fepr

**Fepr**

- [[##rule 335.2|335.2.]] When all Outstanding Tasks are completed, all pending Chain Items will subsequently be processed by the FEPR process.
- [[##rule 336|336.]] When there are no outstanding Tasks and there are pending Chain Items on the Chain, players should refer to the FEPR process to proceed.
- [[##rule 336.1|336.1.]] In the sequence of resolving FEPR more Chain Items may become Pending Chain Items. These will be processed by the same FEPR process that produced them.
- [[##rule 460.3|460.3.]] 2. Skip the FEPR process and proceed to the Resolution Step.

####  final point

**Final Point**

- [[##rule 484.8.f|484.8.f.]] The Final Point has an adjustment to the criteria when scoring.
- [[##rule 484.8.f.1|484.8.f.1.]] When scoring the Final Point from Conquer, a player must Score each Battleﬁeld in the same turn, excepting any that were occupied by their ally during that turn’s Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 484.8.f.2|484.8.f.2.]] No other changes to Final Point restrictions.

####  finalize

**Finalize**

- [[##rule 419.1|419.1.]] A player Plays cards by placing them on the chain and queuing them to be ﬁnalized.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information on playing cards. See rule 337. Finalize for more information on ﬁnalizing cards.
- [[##rule 808.1.d.3|808.1.d.3.]] Before the card with Deathknell is moved to the Trash, note its location, its attributes, and any other details related to the effect of its Deathknell to process the trigger after it has been Finalized.
- [[##rule 812.1.c|812.1.c.]] As long as a card different than the one with the Legion ability has been Finalized on the same turn then the Dependent Ability is Active on the card with Legion.
- [[##rule 822.3|822.3.]] If there are no units at the location chosen before Finalization completes for any reason, then it is no longer a valid location by Ambush’s reasoning and cannot be played there

####  finalized chain items

**Finalized Chain Items**

- [[##rule 352.2|352.2.]] Near the end of the process cards will cease being Pending and become Finalized Chain Items.

####  finalized items

**Finalized Items**

- [[##rule 337.1|337.1.]] If one or more Items are Pending, their controllers must complete the steps of Playing those Pending Items until they are Finalized Items or leave the Chain.
- [[##rule 337.1.b|337.1.b.]] Each Item is Finalized in the order it was appended to the Chain.
- [[##rule 337.1.c|337.1.c.]] Units, Gear, and abilities that Add resources resolve immediately when Finalized and do not progress to Step 2: Execute.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.2|383.4.b.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after a spell or ability that targets an appropriate Game Object is Finalized.

####  first player

**First Player**

- [[##rule 116.1.a|116.1.a.]] The Mode of Play will specify how to determine a First Player.
- [[##rule 116.1.b|116.1.b.]] If not otherwise speciﬁed, Seating then determines the sequence, play proceeding clockwise from the First Player.
- [[##rule 116.1.b.1|116.1.b.1.]] The First Player is the player who becomes the Turn Player ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 119|119.]] Begin play with the First Player taking their turn.

####  first turn process

**First Turn Process**

- [[##rule 478.7|478.7.]] First Turn Process: Adjustments to each player's ﬁrst turn.
- [[##rule 480.7|480.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going second channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 481.7|481.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going second channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 482.7|482.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 483.7|483.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.
- [[##rule 484.7|484.7.]] First Turn Process: The player going ﬁrst does not draw a card during their ﬁrst Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their ﬁrst Channel Phase of the game.

####  flavor text

**Flavor Text**

- [[##rule 138|138.]] Flavor Text

####  focus

**Focus**

- [[##rule 312.2.b|312.2.b.]] When the turn is in a Showdown State and they gain Focus.
- [[##rule 313|313.]] At any given time, up to one player has Focus.
- [[##rule 313.1|313.1.]] Focus is the permission to take appropriately timed Discretionary Actions when the turn is in a Showdown Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 313.1.a|313.1.a.]] The player with Focus must obey any additional restrictions on which Discretionary Actions may be performed.  Example: A player with Focus may not play spells or activate abilities that don't have the Action or Reaction keywords.
- [[##rule 313.2|313.2.]] A player who gains Focus also gains Priority.
- [[##rule 313.3|313.3.]] A player who passes Priority retains Focus.
- [[##rule 313.4|313.4.]] A player may not make discretionary actions with Focus unless they also possess Priority.
- [[##rule 313.5|313.5.]] If the turn is in a Neutral State, no player has Focus.
- [[##rule 320.1|320.1.]] New Pending Items can be added, but Legal Items cannot be executed and Priority and Focus are not passed or awarded.
- [[##rule 337.1.c.1.a|337.1.c.1.a.]] If this occurs during a Showdown, the next player in turn order gains Focus.
- [[##rule 345|345.]] As a Showdown begins, the player who applied Contested status to the Battleﬁeld gains Focus.
- [[##rule 346|346.]] When the last item on the chain resolves and the turn returns to an Open State during a Showdown, Focus passes, and the next Player gains both Focus and Priority.
- [[##rule 347|347.]] During a Showdown, the player with Focus may do one of the following:
- [[##rule 347.4|347.4.]] Otherwise, Focus passes to the next Player in Turn Order.
- [[##rule 348|348.]] If all players pass Focus without playing a spell or activating an ability, then the Showdown Closes.
- [[##rule 429.2.a|429.2.a.]] Priority and Focus will not pass from Add abilities being ﬁnalized or resolving, and will resolve before any other outstanding items on the chain are ﬁnalized.
- [[##rule 459.2.c|459.2.c.]] 2. The Attacker gains Focus.
- [[##rule 459.2.d.1|459.2.d.1.]] The Attacking player, who has Focus, places Triggered Abilities on the Chain ﬁrst, followed by all non-Defender players in Turn Order, followed by the Defending Player.
- [[##rule 652.5.b.1|652.5.b.1.]] If the removed player had Focus in a Showdown, the next Player in order receives Focus.
- [[##rule 652.5.b.2|652.5.b.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have Passed their Focus, the Showdown ends and play proceeds as necessary, E.G. Combat is resolved or a Cleanup is completed.

####  format

**Format**

- [[##rule 478.6|478.6.]] Format: Conditions to win or additional rules added over play.
- [[##rule 480.6|480.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 481.6|481.6.]] Format: Best of 3. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the game. The winner of that game earns One Game Win. Players then reset the game state, remove the Battleﬁelds in play from the game, choose new Battleﬁelds from those set aside, and play again. The ﬁrst player to earn Two Game Wins wins the match.
- [[##rule 482.6|482.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 483.6|483.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 484.6|484.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst team to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.

####  formation of players

**Formation Of Players**

- [[##rule 478.2|478.2.]] Formation of Players: How the players are organized while playing.

####  friendly

**Friendly**

- [[##rule 484.8.d|484.8.d.]] Friendly describes controlled Game Objects by a player or their Teammate. Example: "When I am played, ready a friendly unit" could target a player's own Units or their teammate's Units.
- [[##rule 740.1|740.1.]] Two Game Objects are friendly if they share a controller, or if one’s controller is teammates with the other’s.

####  front face

**Front Face**

- [[##rule 130.2|130.2.]] This is also referred to as a front face.

####  front side

**Front Side**

- [[##rule 130|130.]] Front Side

####  fury

**Fury**

- [[##rule 134.2.a|134.2.a.]] Fury is associated with the color red and represented by a circular symbol with three projecting points. Its shorthand is [R].
- [[##rule 335|335.]] Whenever a Player takes one or more actions that incur Tasks they should refer to the process of HOT FEPR: Handle Outstanding Tasks; then Finalize, Execute, Pass, Resolve.

###  group G

####  gain xp

**Gain Xp**

- [[##rule 730.1|730.1.]] To Gain XP, increase the value of XP marked on the Player gaining it.

####  gaining

**Gaining**

- [[##rule 463.1|463.1.]] Every instance of Scoring is also an instance of Gaining points
- [[##rule 466.1|466.1.]] The player Gains up to one Point, depending on their current score.
- [[##rule 466.1.a.1|466.1.a.1.]] Notably, points Gained from sources that are not Conquer or Hold are not beholden to these restrictions.
- [[##rule 466.1.b|466.1.b.]] When a player tries to Gain a Point through a Score, and their current Point Total is 1 point from the Victory Score of the Mode of Play or higher, the following occurs:
- [[##rule 466.1.b.1|466.1.b.1.]] If the player has Scored through Hold, that player Gains the Winning Point.
- [[##rule 466.1.b.2|466.1.b.2.]] If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has Scored every Battleﬁeld through either method this turn, that player Gains the Winning Point. If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has not Scored every Battleﬁeld this turn, that player draws a card.
- [[##rule 730|730.]] XP can be Gained and Spent.

####  game actions

**Game Actions**

- [[##rule 121|121.]] A Game Object is any game piece that can produce one or more Game Effects or grant prerequisites for players to take Game Actions.
- [[##rule 122|122.]] A Game Object does not include nor preclude any inherent properties beyond the ability to produce, or act as the prerequisite for, Game Effects and Game Actions.
- [[##rule 303.1|303.1.]] Game Actions of any nature are performed one at a time and are executed completely.
- [[##rule 303.2|303.2.]] Game Actions cannot be performed simultaneously for any reason.
- [[##rule 355.12|355.12.]] If a spell speciﬁes that a player may perform a Game Action on some number of Game Objects, then all choices are considered targeted and chosen independently of the decision to perform the Game Action.
- [[##rule 369.2|369.2.]] Some Game Actions are themselves Replacement Effects. Example: Burning Out is a replacement effect. Example: Preventing Damage is a replacement effect.
- [[##rule 370.1.a|370.1.a.]] When a Replacement Effect applies, it replaces the qualifying event with one or more Game Actions or events, or the qualifying instruction with another instruction.
- [[##rule 370.2|370.2.]] A Replacement Effect can only be applied once to an event, or to any Game Actions or events that replace that event. Example: A player plays a spell that reads “gear you control become 1 [M] gear units this turn.” They control two copies of Zhonya’s Hourglass when the spell resolves. If one of those copies is killed, both of their Replacement Effects will be applied. Whichever is applied ﬁrst, that Replacement Effect can’t be applied again. When it is applied, it kills its source, which creates an event the other can apply its Replacement Effect to. Once they’ve both applied their Replacement Effect to the original death event and the event that replaced it, they cannot go any further. At that point, whichever Zhonya’s Hourglass applied its Replacement Effect last will die.
- [[##rule 375|375.]] If an event that a Replacement Effect applies to would be modiﬁed by a Game Effect, or the results of that event would be modiﬁed by a Game Action, the Replacement Effect will inherit those modiﬁcations. Example: Treasure Hunter reads “When I move, play a Gold gear token exhausted.” A Replacement Effect that says “if you would play a token gear, play that token and an additional copy instead” is applied to the event of the Gold gear token being played. The additional copy will also be exhausted, as it inherits the “exhausted” modiﬁcation. Example: Another Replacement Effect says “if you would play a token, draw 1 instead.” The modiﬁcation cannot apply, so we ignore it. Example: A spell reads “play a ready 3 [M] Mech token. Then do this: Give it Temporary.” A Replacement Effect that says “if you would play a unit token, play that token and a 1 [M] Recruit token instead” is applied to the event of the Mech token being made. The Recruit token enters ready and is given Temporary.
- [[##rule 407|407.]] Game Actions
- [[##rule 408|408.]] Game Actions are actions players may perform at any given time during the game.
- [[##rule 410|410.]] There are two types of Game Actions:
- [[##rule 410.1.a|410.1.a.]] A Discretionary Action is a Game Action that may be performed at any time during a player's turn during a Neutral Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 411.1|411.1.]] Game Actions may be the responsibility of up to one player. The player that performs the Game Action is responsible for it.
- [[##rule 411.2|411.2.]] In the case where a Game Action is performed by procedures of the game and not by any player, that Game Action is not the responsibility of any player.
- [[##rule 411.3|411.3.]] Certain rules assign responsibility to players for Game Actions that they are not normally responsible for.
- [[##rule 411.4|411.4.]] If an ability triggers when “you” do something, it triggers when a Game Action that you are responsible for occurs. Example: A gear reads “When you move an enemy unit, you may exhaust this to [Stun] it.” It will trigger whenever a move game action that you are responsible for causes an enemy unit to move. If an opponent plays a spell that reads “choose a Battleﬁeld. Each player may move a unit they don’t control to that battleﬁeld,” and a player that controls the gear chooses to move an enemy unit, their gear will trigger.
- [[##rule 411.5|411.5.]] Note that certain Game Actions, speciﬁcally Kill, can be attributed to spells and abilities. This attribution is not the same as the responsibility a given player has for the kill game action.

####  game effects

**Game Effects**

- [[##rule 107.3.a|107.3.a.]] Each Battleﬁeld is associated with a sub-zone called a Facedown Zone, a single logical space that a card can be put facedown in through various Game Effects.
- [[##rule 121|121.]] A Game Object is any game piece that can produce one or more Game Effects or grant prerequisites for players to take Game Actions.
- [[##rule 122|122.]] A Game Object does not include nor preclude any inherent properties beyond the ability to produce, or act as the prerequisite for, Game Effects and Game Actions.
- [[##rule 145.1|145.1.]] Activated Abilities are Game Effects that are written as Costs followed by a ":", and then succeeded by an effect.  See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 150.1|150.1.]] Activated Abilities are Game Effects that are written as Costs followed by a ":", and then succeeded by an effect.  See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 187.3.d|187.3.d.]] At this time Game Effects cannot  this status.
- [[##rule 316.4.b|316.4.b.]] This could be the result of a Standard Move Standard Action, a Spell, or other Game Effect.
- [[##rule 317.1.a|317.1.a.]] At the end of the turn Game Effects take place.
- [[##rule 355.2.b|355.2.b.]] Some Game Effects may grant players permission to play Units to locations that are not normally Valid. Such locations become Valid for the purposes of Playing the Unit.
- [[##rule 375|375.]] If an event that a Replacement Effect applies to would be modiﬁed by a Game Effect, or the results of that event would be modiﬁed by a Game Action, the Replacement Effect will inherit those modiﬁcations. Example: Treasure Hunter reads “When I move, play a Gold gear token exhausted.” A Replacement Effect that says “if you would play a token gear, play that token and an additional copy instead” is applied to the event of the Gold gear token being played. The additional copy will also be exhausted, as it inherits the “exhausted” modiﬁcation. Example: Another Replacement Effect says “if you would play a token, draw 1 instead.” The modiﬁcation cannot apply, so we ignore it. Example: A spell reads “play a ready 3 [M] Mech token. Then do this: Give it Temporary.” A Replacement Effect that says “if you would play a unit token, play that token and a 1 [M] Recruit token instead” is applied to the event of the Mech token being made. The Recruit token enters ready and is given Temporary.
- [[##rule 423.2.a|423.2.a.]] Players may only Stun Units when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 424.2.a|424.2.a.]] Players may only Reveal cards from Private or Secret zones when instructed to do so by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 424.4|424.4.]] Game Effects can manipulate or modify the cards Revealed while they are Revealed
- [[##rule 425.2.a|425.2.a.]] Players may only Counter cards and abilities when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 426.2.a|426.2.a.]] Players may only Buff units when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 427.4.a|427.4.a.]] Players may only Banish cards or permanents when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 428.3.a|428.3.a.]] Players may only Kill units when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 429.4.a|429.4.a.]] Players may only Add resources when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 430.2|430.2.]] The Game Effect that instructs a player to channel 1 or more runes may specify the conditions or circumstances under which those runes enter the board. Example: A spell reads "Channel 1 rune exhausted." As that spell resolves, its controller puts the top rune of their rune deck onto the board and that rune enters the board exhausted rather than ready.
- [[##rule 430.3.a|430.3.a.]] Players may only channel runes when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 431.4.a|431.4.a.]] Players may only burn out when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 432.1.a|432.1.a.]] This creates an effect that modulates that attribute by that speciﬁc amount for the duration speciﬁed by the Game Effect that instructed the player to perform this action. Example: A unit with 3 base Might and Shield 2 is in combat as a Defender. Since Shield applies, its current Might is 5. A player chooses it as the target for Last Stand, a spell that reads in part “Double a friendly unit's Might this turn.” Its current Might is 5, so it gets +5 Might this turn, for a current Might of 10. After combat, Shield no longer applies, but the +5 Might from Last Stand does, so the unit’s Might is 8.
- [[##rule 432.2.a|432.2.a.]] Players may only Double when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 433.2.a|433.2.a.]] Players may only swap when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 434.1.h|434.1.h.]] If a Game Effect instructs a player to Attach a card to its current Top-Most Card, nothing additional happens.
- [[##rule 434.2.a|434.2.a.]] Players may only Attach cards when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 434.3|434.3.]] Attaching cards does not inherently choose or specify a target. However, Game Effects that Attach cards may do so.
- [[##rule 435.2.a|435.2.a.]] Players may only Detach cards when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 437.6.a|437.6.a.]] Players may only Prevent Damage when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 439.4|439.4.]] Unless speciﬁed otherwise by the Game Effect that Creates a Game Object, any such Game Object is owned by the player who Created it. Control is established as usual for Game Objects of the appropriate type.
- [[##rule 439.6.a|439.6.a.]] Players may only Create Game Objects when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 451.3|451.3.]] A Recall cannot be prevented by actions and Game Effects that restrict or block Movement.
- [[##rule 469|469.]] Layers are the mechanism in which Game Effects alter the Traits, Intrinsic Abilities, or other properties of Game Objects.
- [[##rule 470.1|470.1.]] Layers only serve to structure the application and order that Game Effects apply to Game Objects to maintain consistency.
- [[##rule 472.1.b.1|472.1.b.1.]] When one Game Object becomes a copy of another, all Traits, including the Rules Text, replace or are added to those of the original Game Object as speciﬁed by the Game Effect directing the Copy. This is applied in this layer.
- [[##rule 472.1.b.2|472.1.b.2.]] Some Game Effects may specify copying certain traits of a card - only the traits speciﬁed by the Game Effect will be copied.
- [[##rule 735|735.]] Certain Game Effects will instruct a player to “take a turn after this.” These effects create a temporary Additional Turn owned by that player that is inserted into the turn queue after the current turn.
- [[##rule 738|738.]] If multiple Additional Turns are queued, they are added to the queue in the order the Game Effects that generated them occurred. Example: The First Player plays, through some means, two Time Warps during their turn. The Time Warps create two Additional Turns for their controller and insert them into the turn queue after the current turn. If the turn queue is represented as [> A > B > C > D >], then these Additional Turns will appear as [> A > A* > A* > B > C > D >]. After the last Additional Turn is played, the queue returns to its previously queued turns. The “*” denotes that a turn is an Additional Turn. Example: The First Player plays Promising Future during their turn, during the resolution of which the Second and Fourth Player choose, banish, and play one Time Warp each. The Fourth Player’s Time Warp resolves ﬁrst, inserting an Additional Turn for them in the queue as such: [> A > D* > B > C > D >]. The Second Player’s Time Warp resolves afterwards, inserting that turn: [> A > B* > D* > B > C > D >]. When the First Player passes the turn, the Second Player will take their turn, followed by the Fourth Player, after which the queue returns to its previously queued turns.
- [[##rule 801.3|801.3.]] Keywords can be d or speciﬁed by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 805.5|805.5.]] Accelerate, and whether or not a unit has Accelerate, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 806.5.a|806.5.a.]] Whether or not a Game Object has Action is a characteristic of that Game Object and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 806.5.b|806.5.b.]] Whether or not a Spell has Action is a characteristic of that Spell and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 806.5.c|806.5.c.]] Whether or not an Ability has Action is a characteristic of that Ability and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 807.3|807.3.]] Assault, and whether or not a unit has Assault, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 808.3|808.3.]] Deathknell, and whether or not a permanent has Deathknell, is a characteristic of the permanent and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 809.3|809.3.]] Deflect, and whether or not a permanent has Deflect, is a characteristic of the permanent and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 810.3|810.3.]] Ganking, and whether or not a unit has Ganking, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 811.5|811.5.]] Hidden, and whether or not a card has Hidden, is a characteristic of the card and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 812.3|812.3.]] Legion, and whether or not a card has Legion, is a characteristic of the card and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 813.5.a|813.5.a.]] Whether or not a Game Object has Reaction is a characteristic of that Game Object and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 813.5.b|813.5.b.]] Whether or not a Spell has Reaction is a characteristic of that Spell and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 813.5.c|813.5.c.]] Whether or not an Ability has Reaction is a characteristic of that Ability and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 814.3|814.3.]] Shield, and whether or not a unit has Shield, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 815.3|815.3.]] Tank, and whether or not a unit has Tank, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 816.3|816.3.]] Temporary, and whether or not a permanent has Temporary, is a characteristic of the permanent and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 817.3|817.3.]] Vision, and whether or not a permanent has Vision, is a characteristic of the permanent and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 818.2.a|818.2.a.]] This is an event other Game Effects and Triggered Abilities can .
- [[##rule 818.5|818.5.]] Equip, and whether or not a Gear has Equip, is a characteristic of the Gear and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 819.3|819.3.]] Quick-Draw, and whether or not a gear has Quick-Draw, is a characteristic of the Gear and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 820.4|820.4.]] Repeat, and whether or not a spell has Repeat, is a characteristic of the Spell and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 821.3|821.3.]] Weaponmaster, and whether or not a unit has Weaponmaster, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 822.4|822.4.]] Ambush, and whether or not a unit has Ambush, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 823.3|823.3.]] Hunt, and whether or not a unit has Hunt, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 824.2|824.2.]] Level, and whether or not a card has Level is a characteristic of the card and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 825.4|825.4.]] Unique, and whether or not a Card has Unique, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 826.6|826.6.]] Backline, and whether or not a unit has Backline, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

####  game modes

**Game Modes**

- [[##rule 732|732.]] XP is not shared between Allies in Game Modes with Teammates.

####  game object

**Game Object**

- [[##rule 107.4.c|107.4.c.]] The Champion Legend here is a Game Object. See rule 120. Game Objects for more information.
- [[##rule 109|109.]] All Game Objects in the collective Play Areas are Public Information.
- [[##rule 109.2|109.2.]] The State of all Game Objects in the Play Area is also Public Information.  Examples:   If a Unit is Buffed  If a Gear is Exhausted  Etc.
- [[##rule 110|110.]] Whenever a Game Object changes zones to or from a Non-Board Zone, all Temporary Modiﬁcations of all kinds cease to be tracked on it in all capacities.  Examples:  Damage is cleared.  Buffs are removed.  Granted Keywords are no longer granted.
- [[##rule 120|120.]] Game Objects
- [[##rule 121|121.]] A Game Object is any game piece that can produce one or more Game Effects or grant prerequisites for players to take Game Actions.
- [[##rule 122|122.]] A Game Object does not include nor preclude any inherent properties beyond the ability to produce, or act as the prerequisite for, Game Effects and Game Actions.
- [[##rule 123|123.]] A Game Object can be a literal object or a logical object.
- [[##rule 124|124.]] Game Objects include, but are not limited to, the following:  Main Deck cards in any zone  Runes in any zone  Legends  Battleﬁelds  Tokens in any zone Abilities of any type on the chain  Buffs and other status markers
- [[##rule 141.1|141.1.]] A Game Object
- [[##rule 142.1|142.1.]] Damage is not a Game Object.
- [[##rule 148.1|148.1.]] A Game Object
- [[##rule 148.1.b.1|148.1.b.1.]] Gear are treated as Cards before Game Objects, similar to the Hand.
- [[##rule 169|169.]] Battleﬁelds are Game Objects.
- [[##rule 173|173.]] Legends are Game Objects.
- [[##rule 177|177.]] Tokens are Game Objects created by spells and abilities during play.
- [[##rule 186|186.]] Control is the concept of a player having influence of a Game Object and applies differently to different card types.
- [[##rule 188.1|188.1.]] When a player Plays a Card or other Game Object, they are established as that Game Object's Controller.
- [[##rule 188.3|188.3.]] For Permanents and Runes, when they Enter the Board, that player is assigned as that Game Object's Controller.
- [[##rule 188.3.a|188.3.a.]] That player may make decisions about the Game Object's Inherent Abilities.
- [[##rule 188.3.b|188.3.b.]] That player may make decisions about the Game Object's Unique Abilities.
- [[##rule 189.1|189.1.]] The method of assignment of control is different, but the status of Control is the same across all Game Objects.
- [[##rule 315.1.b|315.1.b.]] 1. The Turn Player readies all Game Objects they control that are able to be readied.  See rule 415. Ready for more information.
- [[##rule 319.6|319.6.]] After any number of Game Objects enter or leave the Board
- [[##rule 319.7|319.7.]] After the status of any number of Game Objects changes for any reason
- [[##rule 338.1.b|338.1.b.]] Activate Abilities of Game Objects that are legally timed.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 347.2|347.2.]] Activate Abilities of Game Objects that are legally timed.  See rule 360. Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 351.1|351.1.]] Permanents become Game Objects when Played.
- [[##rule 355.5|355.5.]] If a card requires you to speciﬁcally choose one or more Game Objects, that choice is made now.
- [[##rule 355.5.a|355.5.a.]] This does not include cards that affect one or more Game Objects based on criteria.  Example: "Stun a unit at a battleﬁeld" is a Choice.  Example: "Kill all gear" is not a Choice.
- [[##rule 355.7|355.7.]] When a card Chooses one or more speciﬁc Game Objects to affect, it is Targeted unless indicated otherwise by the rules in this section.
- [[##rule 355.12|355.12.]] If a spell speciﬁes that a player may perform a Game Action on some number of Game Objects, then all choices are considered targeted and chosen independently of the decision to perform the Game Action.
- [[##rule 355.13|355.13.]] If a card speciﬁes that a player chooses “any number” or “up to” some number of Game Objects to be affected, they may choose any number of available targets, including zero. If they choose zero, the spell or ability can be played without any targets.
- [[##rule 355.14.i|355.14.i.]] Any costs that were paid, or effects that were triggered as a result of those Game Objects being chosen as Targets remain in effect, paid, or otherwise triggered.
- [[##rule 359.2|359.2.]] A Permanent leaves the Chain and becomes a Game Object.
- [[##rule 361|361.]] An Ability is the structured rules and capabilities of Game Objects or Spells.
- [[##rule 370.3|370.3.]] If a Game Object has a Replacement Effect that is active in a speciﬁc zone, it is evaluated and subsequently applied if it enters that zone before an event occurs that it could replace.  Example: A unit that reads “if a unit you control would die, you may banish me from your trash instead. If you do, heal that unit, exhaust it and recall it.” The ﬁrst unit dies simultaneously with a 1 [M] Recruit token. It does not enter the trash before the Recruit dies, so it will not be able to replace its death.
- [[##rule 379|379.]] Activated abilities are present on Game Objects and some Spells.
- [[##rule 383.2.c.1|383.2.c.1.]] If a Game Object with a Triggered Ability that is active in a speciﬁc zone, it is evaluated and subsequently triggered if it enters that zone at the same time that its Trigger’s condition is met.  Example: Immortal Phoenix says “When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.” This ability triggers if Immortal Phoenix is in your trash immediately after you kill a unit with a spell, even if the unit you killed with a spell was that Immortal Phoenix.
- [[##rule 383.2.c.2|383.2.c.2.]] A Game Object will not be able to successfully be able to evaluate its Trigger Condition, however, if it leaves the zone that its Trigger is active from at the same time that its Trigger is satisﬁed.  Example: Viktor, Leader says “When another non-Recruit unit you control dies, play a 1 [M] Recruit unit token into your base.” This ability triggers if Viktor is on the board immediately after another non-Recruit unit you control dies. It does not trigger if Viktor and another non-Recruit unit you control die during the same game action (for instance, if they are both killed in the same Cleanup due to the damage dealt by Unchecked Power).
- [[##rule 383.4.b|383.4.b.]] Targeting Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that a Game Object becomes targeted.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.2|383.4.b.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after a spell or ability that targets an appropriate Game Object is Finalized.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.3|383.4.b.3.]] Although these abilities say “choose” in their Condition, they trigger speciﬁcally when an appropriate Game Object is Targeted. See rule 355.6. Targeting for more information on what counts as Targeting.
- [[##rule 390.5|390.5.]] Delayed Linked Abilities are Linked Abilities that are generated by another Ability and  that Ability or Game Objects it affects. Delayed Linked Abilities don’t necessarily identify a speciﬁc window of time, and instead are deﬁned by the Ability they are linked with.
- [[##rule 390.5.a|390.5.a.]] If that Ability affects a Game Object, the Delayed Linked Ability’s window will be as long as that Game Object is in an appropriate zone.
- [[##rule 397|397.]] A component Linked Ability that s a Game Object affected by another Ability in the set may only interact with Game Objects affected by the Abilities it is Linked with.
- [[##rule 414.1|414.1.]] Exhausting is an action that marks a non-spell Game Object on the board as "spent."
- [[##rule 414.2|414.2.]] "Exhausted" is a state for Game Objects on the board that other game effects and rules can .
- [[##rule 415.1|415.1.]] Readying is an action that marks a non-spell Game Object on the board as available for action.
- [[##rule 415.2|415.2.]] "Ready" is a state for Game Objects on the board that other game effects and rules can .
- [[##rule 415.3.a|415.3.a.]] A player Readies all non-spell Game Objects they Control during the Ready Step of the Beginning Phase on their turn.
- [[##rule 420.1|420.1.]] Moving is the act of a Game Object moving between two Locations on The Board. See rule 440. Movement for more information on movement.
- [[##rule 420.2.a|420.2.a.]] Players may only move Game Objects when instructed to do so by Game Effects or costs.
- [[##rule 428.5|428.5.]] Killing can be attributed to one or more Game Objects.
- [[##rule 428.5.a|428.5.a.]] The Killed Unit or Gear is said to be Killed by that Game Object.
- [[##rule 428.5.d|428.5.d.]] Abilities originating from Game Objects that are  attributed Kill Actions are attributed in addition to the Game Object that created them.  Example: There is a spell that says “Do this twice: Deal 3 to a unit.” Immortal Phoenix is a unit that says “When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.” A player plays the spell while Immortal Phoenix is in their trash. The “do this” phrasing means that it has a reflexive triggered ability, which places two triggered abilities on the chain. As each of those triggered abilities resolve, it deals damage to the unit chosen for that ability. If one of these abilities deals lethal damage to a unit, both the spell and its ability are considered sources of the damage, and so both the spell and its ability receive attribution for killing the unit. This means that the spell’s controller killed a unit with a spell, so Immortal Phoenix’s ability will trigger.
- [[##rule 433.1|433.1.]] Swapping is the act of increasing one numeric value and decreasing another numeric value on some number of Game Objects such that their values are reversed.
- [[##rule 439.1|439.1.]] Creating is the act of producing a Game Object that previously did not exist in the game.
- [[##rule 439.2|439.2.]] Effects that Create one or more Game Objects will direct where those Game Objects must go - the Game Objects are Created directly to the zones in question.
- [[##rule 439.2.a|439.2.a.]] Prior to being Created, these Game Objects did not exist outside of the zone they were Created to. After being Created, they may change zones as appropriate for Game Objects of their type.
- [[##rule 439.2.b|439.2.b.]] If a zone is not speciﬁed by the effect, the Game Object will be created to the appropriate zone for its type. Permanents will be Created to any location on the Board that they can be played to.
- [[##rule 439.3|439.3.]] An effect that Creates a Game Object will specify the nature of the Game Object created.
- [[##rule 439.3.a|439.3.a.]] If the Game Object is a token, it will follow the normal rules for tokens. See rule 176. Tokens for more information.
- [[##rule 439.4|439.4.]] Unless speciﬁed otherwise by the Game Effect that Creates a Game Object, any such Game Object is owned by the player who Created it. Control is established as usual for Game Objects of the appropriate type.
- [[##rule 469|469.]] Layers are the mechanism in which Game Effects alter the Traits, Intrinsic Abilities, or other properties of Game Objects.
- [[##rule 470.1|470.1.]] Layers only serve to structure the application and order that Game Effects apply to Game Objects to maintain consistency.
- [[##rule 472.1.a|472.1.a.]] This layer deals with effects that grant, remove, or replace inherent traits of Game Objects.  Name Super Type Type Tags Controller Cost Domain
- [[##rule 472.1.b.1|472.1.b.1.]] When one Game Object becomes a copy of another, all Traits, including the Rules Text, replace or are added to those of the original Game Object as speciﬁed by the Game Effect directing the Copy. This is applied in this layer.
- [[##rule 472.1.b.3|472.1.b.3.]] Copy effects will copy the copyable traits of a Game Object: by default, those are the printed traits of the Game Object. When a Game Object becomes a copy of something, its copyable traits are updated to the new traits it has received. Example: A player triggers Leblanc, Deceiver’s hold effect and plays a Reflection token, making it a copy of Honest Broker. That player then plays Mirror Image, targeting the Reflection token. When the Mirror Image Reflection token is played, it copies all of the copyable traits of the original Reflection token - which are currently those of Honest Broker which it is a copy of. That player will have three units named Honest Broker in play, two of which are token Copies with Temporary.
- [[##rule 472.2.a|472.2.a.]] This layer deals with effects that grant, remove, or replace the abilities or rules text of Game Objects.  Keywords Passive Abilities Appending rules text Removing rules text Duplicating Rules Text from one Game Object to another
- [[##rule 472.3.a|472.3.a.]] This layer deals with the mathematics of increasing and decreasing the numeric values of the traits of Game Objects.  Might Energy Cost Power Cost
- [[##rule 473|473.]] If more than one effect applies to the same Game Object in the Same Layer, or to each other in the same layer, then both effects will apply but their order may be determined by Dependency.
- [[##rule 484.8.d|484.8.d.]] Friendly describes controlled Game Objects by a player or their Teammate. Example: "When I am played, ready a friendly unit" could target a player's own Units or their teammate's Units.
- [[##rule 704|704.]] Buffs are Game Objects and may be d, counted, or targeted by other effects as speciﬁed.
- [[##rule 731|731.]] XP is not a Game Object.
- [[##rule 740|740.]] Some card text refers to Game Objects in particular ways:
- [[##rule 740.1|740.1.]] Two Game Objects are friendly if they share a controller, or if one’s controller is teammates with the other’s.
- [[##rule 740.2|740.2.]] Two Game Objects are enemies if one’s controller is an opponent of the other’s.
- [[##rule 801.3.a.3|801.3.a.3.]] If an effect that grants a Keyword does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that Game Object remains on the Board or in its current Non-Board Zone.
- [[##rule 801.3.b.2|801.3.b.2.]] If an effect that removes a Keyword does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that Game Object remains on the Board or in its current Non-Board Zone.
- [[##rule 806.5.a|806.5.a.]] Whether or not a Game Object has Action is a characteristic of that Game Object and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 813.5.a|813.5.a.]] Whether or not a Game Object has Reaction is a characteristic of that Game Object and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

####  game object, or be granted by the same source to another game object

**Game Object, Or Be Granted By The Same Source To Another Game Object**

- [[##rule 395|395.]] In order for a set of Abilities to be Linked, they must be present in the printed Effect or Rules Text of the same Game Object, or be granted by the same source to another Game Object.

####  ganking

**Ganking**

- [[##rule 144.4.c|144.4.c.]] Ganking is a unique ability that affects a Unit's Standard Move
- [[##rule 144.4.c.1|144.4.c.1.]] Units with Ganking may use their Standard Move to Move from Battleﬁeld to Battleﬁeld.  See rule 810. Ganking for more information.
- [[##rule 810|810.]] Ganking

####  gear

**Gear**

- [[##rule 109.2|109.2.]] The State of all Game Objects in the Play Area is also Public Information.  Examples:   If a Unit is Buffed  If a Gear is Exhausted  Etc.
- [[##rule 133.4.a.2|133.4.a.2.]] Unit and Gear are permanent types.
- [[##rule 147|147.]] Gear
- [[##rule 148|148.]] Gear are:
- [[##rule 148.1.a.1|148.1.a.1.]] Gear can only be played to a player's Base unless an effect speciﬁes otherwise.
- [[##rule 148.1.a.2|148.1.a.2.]] Gear and their details are Public Information while on the Board.
- [[##rule 148.1.a.3|148.1.a.3.]] Gear can be chosen, affected, or manipulated by spells, effects, or game actions that specify Gear.
- [[##rule 148.1.a.4|148.1.a.4.]] Gear can be Killed. See rule 428. Kill for more information.
- [[##rule 148.1.b.1|148.1.b.1.]] Gear are treated as Cards before Game Objects, similar to the Hand.
- [[##rule 148.1.b.2|148.1.b.2.]] They retain the properties of being Gear, but are not on the Board and thus cannot take actions or be affected by spells, abilities, or game actions that affect Gear on the Board.
- [[##rule 148.1.b.3|148.1.b.3.]] Gear can be affected by spells and game effects that affect Gear in the Trash.
- [[##rule 149|149.]] Gear have several Intrinsic Properties unique to them.
- [[##rule 149.1|149.1.]] Gear enter play Ready.
- [[##rule 149.2|149.2.]] Gear can only be played to a player's Base unless an effect speciﬁes otherwise.
- [[##rule 149.3|149.3.]] If an unattached Gear is at a Battleﬁeld for any reason during a cleanup, then it is recalled to its controller's Base as a corrective action.  See rule 449. Recalls for more information. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 150|150.]] Gear may have Activated Abilities.
- [[##rule 150.2|150.2.]] The Activated Ability of Gear may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 151|151.]] Gear have a Location.
- [[##rule 151.2|151.2.]] Gear cannot normally become located at a Battleﬁeld unless by some special means. Example: Gear are always played to Base. The only exception is a gear played from Facedown, which is played to the Battleﬁeld it was played from. Gear can also become located at a Battleﬁeld if they are attached to a unit who becomes located at a Battleﬁeld. See rule 811. Hidden for more information. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 359.2.d|359.2.d.]] If it is a Gear, it enters the Board Ready at the player's Base.
- [[##rule 383.4.a.1|383.4.a.1.]] These are commonly structured as “When you play me…” for Units and “When you play this…” for Gear.
- [[##rule 392|392.]] Delayed Abilities are not associated with Units or Gear; they are created by other Abilities or Spells. As such they are executed when their condition and/or speciﬁed time occurs regardless of whether the source of the Delayed Ability is still on the board or not.
- [[##rule 400.2|400.2.]] When an Ability with the [Add] action is ﬁnalized it resolves immediately instead of becoming a Chain Item, like a Unit or Gear.
- [[##rule 428.5.a|428.5.a.]] The Killed Unit or Gear is said to be Killed by that Game Object.
- [[##rule 428.5.b|428.5.b.]] A spell or ability that contains a Kill instruction is responsible for Killing the Unit or Gear.
- [[##rule 435.4.a|435.4.a.]] If the Detached card was a Gear and this causes it to become present at a Battleﬁeld, it will be Recalled during the next Cleanup.
- [[##rule 452.1|452.1.]] When an un-attached Gear is created or played at a battleﬁeld, or is at a battleﬁeld for any other reason, it is Recalled to its controller's base during the next Cleanup.  Example: An Equipment is attached to a unit at a battleﬁeld, so the Equipment is present at that battleﬁeld. If the unit dies, the Equipment will be recalled during the next cleanup.
- [[##rule 818.1.a|818.1.a.]] Equip is normally present on Gear with the tag Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.2|818.2.]] When the Attach action completes from this keyword, the Unit that was chosen is considered to have been Equipped by the Gear with this ability.
- [[##rule 818.5|818.5.]] Equip, and whether or not a Gear has Equip, is a characteristic of the Gear and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 818.5.a|818.5.a.]] Whether or not a Gear has Equip may be d even if the Rules Text of the Gear is Inactive. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 819.1.a|819.1.a.]] Quick-Draw is present on Gear with Equip abilities.

####  gear’s location

**Gear’s Location**

- [[##rule 151.1|151.1.]] A Gear’s Location is the Base or Battleﬁeld it currently occupies.

####  gold gear token

**Gold Gear Token**

- [[##rule 184.5|184.5.]] A Gold gear token is a domainless gear token with “[Reaction][>] Kill this, [E]: [Add] [A].”

####  golden rule

**Golden Rule**

- [[##rule 001|001.]] Golden Rule

###  group H

####  hand

**Hand**

- [[##rule 108|108.7.]] The Hand
- [[##rule 108.7.a|108.7.a.]] Each player has their own Hand.
- [[##rule 141.1.b.1|141.1.b.1.]] Units are treated as Cards, similar to when in the Hand.
- [[##rule 148.1.b.1|148.1.b.1.]] Gear are treated as Cards before Game Objects, similar to the Hand.
- [[##rule 413.1|413.1.]] Drawing a card takes a single card from a zone and adding it to the player's Hand.

####  healed

**Healed**

- [[##rule 142.4|142.4.]] Damage can be Healed.  See rule 418. Heal for more information.
- [[##rule 143.3.b|143.3.b.]] Damage is Healed from Units at two speciﬁc times:
- [[##rule 317.2.b|317.2.b.]] Insert “2c. Heal all Units.”
- [[##rule 418|418.]] Heal
- [[##rule 418.1|418.1.]] Damage being cleared from Units is Healing.
- [[##rule 418.1.a|418.1.a.]] If Damage is cleared for any reason it is considered Healing.
- [[##rule 418.2|418.2.]] More than one Unit can be Healed at the same time.
- [[##rule 418.3|418.3.]] Healing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 418.3.a|418.3.a.]] Players may only Heal units when game effects instruct them to, or at speciﬁc points in the turn.
- [[##rule 461.1.a.1|461.1.a.1.]] Insert “3c. Heal  all Units.”

####  held

**Held**

- [[##rule 466.2.b|466.2.b.]] Hold abilities trigger at a Battleﬁeld that was Held.

####  hide

**Hide**

- [[##rule 107.3.d|107.3.d.]] If a player loses Control of a Battleﬁeld, any cards in the Facedown Zone associated with that Battleﬁeld are removed during the next Cleanup. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information. See rule 421. Hide for more information.
- [[##rule 151.2|151.2.]] Gear cannot normally become located at a Battleﬁeld unless by some special means. Example: Gear are always played to Base. The only exception is a gear played from Facedown, which is played to the Battleﬁeld it was played from. Gear can also become located at a Battleﬁeld if they are attached to a unit who becomes located at a Battleﬁeld. See rule 811. Hidden for more information. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 323.7|323.7.]] 5. Recall all Unattached non-Unit Gear at Battleﬁelds, and all Permanents and Runes in Bases other than their controller’s. Remove all Hidden cards from all Battleﬁelds that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's Trash.
- [[##rule 421|421.]] Hide
- [[##rule 421.1|421.1.]] Hiding a card is the act of placing a card facedown at a Battleﬁeld you control.
- [[##rule 421.2|421.2.]] Hiding is a Discretionary Action.
- [[##rule 421.2.a|421.2.a.]] The Hidden keyword allows a player to pay a cost to Hide a card any time they have a Hidden card in their hand or Champion Zone and meet the prerequisites.  See rule 811. Hidden for more information.
- [[##rule 421.3|421.3.]] Cards that are facedown at Battleﬁelds have their gameplay properties and permissions deﬁned by the effect that put them there.  Example: Cards that players Hide with the Hidden keyword can be Played for [0] on any subsequent turn as a property of the Hidden keyword.
- [[##rule 461.5.c|461.5.c.]] Remove all Hidden cards from this Battleﬁeld that do not share a controller with the Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 484.8.c.1|484.8.c.1.]] Players may not Hide cards at Battleﬁelds controlled by their Teammate.
- [[##rule 811|811.]] Hidden
- [[##rule 811.1|811.1.]] Hidden is a keyword that acts as a prerequisite to perform the Hide Discretionary Action.
- [[##rule 811.1.c|811.1.c.]] It allows the player to take the Discretionary Action Hide.
- [[##rule 811.6|811.6.]] A card that is Hidden gains Reaction while facedown or played from facedown, and may be played any time a card with Reaction may be played as a result.

####  hold abilities

**Hold Abilities**

- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.a|383.4.d.2.a.]] The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.b|383.4.d.2.b.]] The Hold Abilities of anything that s the player Holding is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Hold and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 466.2.b|466.2.b.]] Hold abilities trigger at a Battleﬁeld that was Held.

####  hold effects

**Hold Effects**

- [[##rule 383.4.d|383.4.d.]] Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battleﬁeld during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.c|383.4.d.2.c.]] If the act of gaining one point from Holding is negated or replaced in any way, the Hold Effect will still trigger.

####  holding

**Holding**

- [[##rule 383.4.d|383.4.d.]] Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battleﬁeld during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2|383.4.d.2.]] This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Hold action, or Abilities that  the player that performed the Hold action.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.a|383.4.d.2.a.]] The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.b|383.4.d.2.b.]] The Hold Abilities of anything that s the player Holding is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Hold and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.c|383.4.d.2.c.]] If the act of gaining one point from Holding is negated or replaced in any way, the Hold Effect will still trigger.
- [[##rule 464.2|464.2.]] Hold: A player maintains Control of a Battleﬁeld during their Beginning Phase.
- [[##rule 466.1.a.1|466.1.a.1.]] Notably, points Gained from sources that are not Conquer or Hold are not beholden to these restrictions.
- [[##rule 466.1.b.1|466.1.b.1.]] If the player has Scored through Hold, that player Gains the Winning Point.
- [[##rule 823.1.b|823.1.b.]] Hunt is both a Conquer and a Hold effect.
- [[##rule 823.1.c.1|823.1.c.1.]] Hunt is functionally short for: “When I Conquer or Hold, my controller gains X XP.” See rule 728. XP for more information

####  hot fepr: h

**Hot Fepr: H**

- [[##rule 335|335.]] Whenever a Player takes one or more actions that incur Tasks they should refer to the process of HOT FEPR: Handle Outstanding Tasks; then Finalize, Execute, Pass, Resolve.

####  hunt

**Hunt**

- [[##rule 823|823.]] Hunt
- [[##rule 823.1|823.1.]] Hunt is a Triggered Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 823.1.a|823.1.a.]] Hunt is present on Units.
- [[##rule 823.1.b|823.1.b.]] Hunt is both a Conquer and a Hold effect.
- [[##rule 823.1.c|823.1.c.]] Hunt is formatted as “Hunt X”
- [[##rule 823.1.c.1|823.1.c.1.]] Hunt is functionally short for: “When I Conquer or Hold, my controller gains X XP.” See rule 728. XP for more information
- [[##rule 823.2|823.2.]] If a Unit has Hunt, or has been granted Hunt, and is granted Hunt by an additional source, the Hunt Value of all granted Hunt keywords is summed.
- [[##rule 823.3|823.3.]] Hunt, and whether or not a unit has Hunt, is a characteristic of the Unit and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

###  group I

####  identiﬁer

**Identiﬁer**

- [[##rule 187.2|187.2.]] Control is a binary state for Battleﬁelds and an Identiﬁer for players.

####  illustration

**Illustration**

- [[##rule 139|139.]] Illustration

####  in combat

**In Combat**

- [[##rule 741.3|741.3.]] A unit is in combat if it is occupying a battleﬁeld where combat is ongoing and has a combat designation.

####  inactive

**Inactive**

- [[##rule 135.4|135.4.]] A card’s printed Rules Text is Inactive while that card is Attached to another card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 135.4.a|135.4.a.]] The presence of text, rules, Keywords, and other effects can still be d and detected by other game effects, even while Rules Text is Inactive.
- [[##rule 136.2.b|136.2.b.]] Effect Text is inactive unless the card with the Effect Text is Attached to another card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 434.1.e|434.1.e.]] Attaching one or more cards will cause those cards’ Rules Text to become Inactive for as long as they remain Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 435.1.c|435.1.c.]] The card being Detached has its Effect Text become Inactive and its Rules Text cease being Inactive.
