- [[##rule 475.2|475.2.]] When Rules Text becomes Inactive for any reason, it loses its Timestamp. When it ceases to be Inactive, a new Timestamp is established.
- [[##rule 718.2|718.2.]] While in this state, the card’s printed Rules Text is Inactive. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 720|720.]] Inactive
- [[##rule 721|721.]] Card text can occasionally be assigned to be ignored, disregarded, or otherwise rendered as not applicable during the course of play. This state is referred to as Inactive.
- [[##rule 721.2|721.2.]] Inactive Abilities do not trigger, do not apply, and cannot be activated. Inactive instructions are not processed.
- [[##rule 722|722.]] Inactive text is still present on cards.
- [[##rule 722.1|722.1.]] Cards with Inactive text still have keywords for the sake of Game Effects that want to  or see if a card has a keyword.
- [[##rule 722.2|722.2.]] Game Effects that parse or interpret text to determine target eligibility may still parse Inactive text for the sake of eligibility. Example: Spinning Axe is a gear with [Temporary]. While it’s attached and its rules text is inactive, its [Temporary] ability doesn’t trigger. However, a spell that reads “Destroy a gear with [Temporary]” could still choose and destroy Spinning Axe.
- [[##rule 723|723.]] Rules Text is never Inactive by default.
- [[##rule 724|724.]] Effect Text is Inactive unless the card with the Effect Text is Attached.
- [[##rule 725|725.]] Inactive text can partially cease to be Inactive under speciﬁc circumstances and exceptions.
- [[##rule 727.1.b|727.1.b.]] The Dependent Ability associated with the Dependent Keyword is Inactive on the card with the Dependent Keyword until the Condition is met, when it becomes Active
- [[##rule 727.1.b.1|727.1.b.1.]] The Dependent Ability is present on the card for the sake of  or evaluation until the Condition is met See rule 720. Inactive for more information
- [[##rule 727.1.c.3.a|727.1.c.3.a.]] If the condition for the Dependent Keyword causes the Activated Ability to become Inactive after it has been added to the chain as a Pending Item, that chain item will not be affected and will proceed with being played as normal.
- [[##rule 818.5.a|818.5.a.]] Whether or not a Gear has Equip may be d even if the Rules Text of the Gear is Inactive. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 821.1.c|821.1.c.]] Weaponmaster is functionally short for: “When you play me, you may choose a Card you control with the Equipment tag. Necessary portions of its Rules Text are no longer Inactive if they are currently Inactive. Pay the cost of its Equip ability, reduced by [A], to attach it to this unit.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 824.1.c.1|824.1.c.1.]] If the controller of the card with Level changes, then the Dependent Ability will be rendered Active or Inactive based on the new controller’s XP.
- [[##rule 824.1.d|824.1.d.]] The Dependent Ability will be Inactive as soon as the controlling player has less than [N] XP.

####  increasing

**Increasing**

- [[##rule 432.1|432.1.]] Doubling is the act of increasing  a numeric attribute by an amount equal to that attribute’s current value.
- [[##rule 433.1.a|433.1.a.]] Swapping creates two different effects that apply to each attribute. One that Increases one value and one that Decreases the other.
- [[##rule 433.1.b|433.1.b.]] To accomplish this, determine the difference between these values and then apply an Increase for that amount to the lower value  of the two attributes, and a Decrease of that amount to the higher value of the two attributes.

####  information

**Information**

- [[##rule 108.2.d|108.2.d.]] Cards in a player's Trash are Public Information. See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 108.6.e|108.6.e.]] The cards in any player's Banishment are Public Information. See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 385.1|385.1.]] Triggered Abilities on cards outside of the Board rely on the Information Level of the zone they are in.

####  inherent ability

**Inherent Ability**

- [[##rule 144|144.]] Units have the Inherent Ability to perform a Standard Move.
- [[##rule 188.3.a|188.3.a.]] That player may make decisions about the Game Object's Inherent Abilities.

####  instructions

**Instructions**

- [[##rule 135.2.b|135.2.b.]] Instructions
- [[##rule 383.2.b|383.2.b.]] The Effect is the Instruction that follows the comma after the Condition.

####  intrinsic properties

**Intrinsic Properties**

- [[##rule 143|143.]] Units have multiple Intrinsic Properties unique to them:
- [[##rule 149|149.]] Gear have several Intrinsic Properties unique to them.

####  invalid

**Invalid**

- [[##rule 359.3.e.7|359.3.e.7.]] If all of an instruction's Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is ﬁnished being played, that instruction will not execute.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.8|359.3.e.8.]] If an instruction has more than one Target and fewer than all of the Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is ﬁnished being played, the instruction will execute, with only the Targets available and valid being operated on.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.10|359.3.e.10.]] It is possible for none of a spell's instructions to be executed as it resolves, due to all of them requiring targets to act on and all of those targets becoming Invalid or Unavailable. In this case, the spell has no effect but is still considered played.  Example: A player plays a spell that reads "Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld" with no other instructions, and chooses an enemy unit at a battleﬁeld. They also control a unit with the ability "When you play a spell, give me +1 [M] this turn." Before the spell resolves, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The spell resolves and its only instruction cannot be executed, but the unit's ability still triggers as the spell resolves and gives it +1 [M].
- [[##rule 364.3.a|364.3.a.]] Conditional Passive Abilities can be recognized by the occurrence of "if" or "while" as part of the statement of the ability.  Example: "While I'm attacking or defending alone, I have +2 [M]."  Example: "If an opponent controls a battleﬁeld, I enter ready."
- [[##rule 457.2|457.2.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid to be chosen as a location to play one or more Units by a player not involved in that Combat by any means,

####  invalid destinations

**Invalid Destinations**

- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 442.2.b|442.2.b.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds Controlled by a player’s teammates are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units that player controls.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.

###  group K

####  keywords

**Keywords**

- [[##rule 110|110.]] Whenever a Game Object changes zones to or from a Non-Board Zone, all Temporary Modiﬁcations of all kinds cease to be tracked on it in all capacities.  Examples:  Damage is cleared.  Buffs are removed.  Granted Keywords are no longer granted.
- [[##rule 135.2.c|135.2.c.]] Keywords
- [[##rule 135.2.c.1|135.2.c.1.]] Keywords are short words or phrases that represent longer abilities or instructions. See rule 800. Keywords for more information.
- [[##rule 135.4.a|135.4.a.]] The presence of text, rules, Keywords, and other effects can still be d and detected by other game effects, even while Rules Text is Inactive.
- [[##rule 158|158.]] Certain Keywords on spells are not executable rules text, but instead intrinsic properties of the spell.
- [[##rule 727|727.]] Keywords can be Dependent Keywords
- [[##rule 727.1|727.1.]] A Dependent Keyword is comprised of both a Condition that it is short for, and an ability of some format immediately after the Keyword itself. EXAMPLE: Noxus Hopeful has “[Legion][>] I cost [2] less.” [Legion] is short for the condition “if you have played another card this turn, this card gains [Text],” while “I cost [2] less” is the dependent ability.
- [[##rule 800|800.]] Keywords
- [[##rule 801|801.]] A Keyword is a speciﬁc term that appears on Cards that acts as a shorthand for a speciﬁc game effect, or ability of any variety.
- [[##rule 801.1|801.1.]] A Keyword can be an ability.
- [[##rule 801.2|801.2.]] Keywords can be identiﬁed by having a colored highlight behind them.
- [[##rule 801.3|801.3.]] Keywords can be d or speciﬁed by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 801.3.a|801.3.a.]] Other effects may grant Keywords.
- [[##rule 801.3.a.1|801.3.a.1.]] The deﬁnition and rules of the speciﬁc Keyword will determine the behavior if a Keyword is granted while it is already present.
- [[##rule 801.3.a.2|801.3.a.2.]] The effect that granted the Keyword will specify the duration for which it is granted.
- [[##rule 801.3.a.3|801.3.a.3.]] If an effect that grants a Keyword does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that Game Object remains on the Board or in its current Non-Board Zone.
- [[##rule 801.3.b|801.3.b.]] Other effects may remove Keywords.
- [[##rule 801.3.b.1|801.3.b.1.]] The effect that removed the Keyword will specify the duration it is removed.
- [[##rule 801.3.b.2|801.3.b.2.]] If an effect that removes a Keyword does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that Game Object remains on the Board or in its current Non-Board Zone.
- [[##rule 802|802.]] A card can have any number of Keywords.
- [[##rule 803|803.]] Similar to other rules text, execute any effects of Keywords in the order listed when reading the card from top to bottom of the rules text.

####  kill actions

**Kill Actions**

- [[##rule 428.5.d|428.5.d.]] Abilities originating from Game Objects that are  attributed Kill Actions are attributed in addition to the Game Object that created them.  Example: There is a spell that says “Do this twice: Deal 3 to a unit.” Immortal Phoenix is a unit that says “When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.” A player plays the spell while Immortal Phoenix is in their trash. The “do this” phrasing means that it has a reflexive triggered ability, which places two triggered abilities on the chain. As each of those triggered abilities resolve, it deals damage to the unit chosen for that ability. If one of these abilities deals lethal damage to a unit, both the spell and its ability are considered sources of the damage, and so both the spell and its ability receive attribution for killing the unit. This means that the spell’s controller killed a unit with a spell, so Immortal Phoenix’s ability will trigger.

####  kill instruction

**Kill Instruction**

- [[##rule 428.1.a.1.a|428.1.a.1.a.]] This is referred to as a Kill Instruction.
- [[##rule 428.1.a.1.b|428.1.a.1.b.]] When a unit with a Deathknell  is to be put in the Trash due to a Kill Instruction, it ﬁrst has its Deathknell added to the chain as a Pending Item. Note the unit’s location, attributes, and other relevant information to process its Deathknell when ﬁnalized before completing this Kill Instruction.

####  killed

**Killed**

- [[##rule 141.1.a.4|141.1.a.4.]] Units can be Killed.  See rule 428. Kill for more information.
- [[##rule 142.3|142.3.]] Damage tracks how close a Unit is to being Killed.  See rule 428. Kill for more information.
- [[##rule 143.2|143.2.]] Might: The combat statistic of a Unit. Used to determine a Unit's contribution to Combat, as well as when it is Killed by damaging effects.
- [[##rule 143.2.a|143.2.a.]] If a Unit ever has nonzero damage marked on it equalling or exceeding its Might, it is Killed.
- [[##rule 148.1.a.4|148.1.a.4.]] Gear can be Killed. See rule 428. Kill for more information.
- [[##rule 169.3|169.3.]] Battleﬁelds cannot be Killed during the course of regular play.
- [[##rule 173.3|173.3.]] Legends cannot be Killed during the course of regular play.
- [[##rule 427.2.a|427.2.a.]] Banish is not a subset of Kill.
- [[##rule 428|428.]] Kill
- [[##rule 428.1|428.1.]] Killing is the action of a Permanent going to the trash from the board.
- [[##rule 428.2|428.2.]] When a permanent is killed it is placed directly in the trash from its place of origin.
- [[##rule 428.2.a|428.2.a.]] It is only considered Killed if its origin was any zone on the board.
- [[##rule 428.3|428.3.]] Killing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 428.3.a|428.3.a.]] Players may only Kill units when Game Effects direct them to do so.
- [[##rule 428.4|428.4.]] Killing can also be the result of resolving a Cleanup.
- [[##rule 428.5|428.5.]] Killing can be attributed to one or more Game Objects.
- [[##rule 428.5.a|428.5.a.]] The Killed Unit or Gear is said to be Killed by that Game Object.
- [[##rule 428.5.b|428.5.b.]] A spell or ability that contains a Kill instruction is responsible for Killing the Unit or Gear.
- [[##rule 428.5.e|428.5.e.]] In order to Kill something “with” a spell or ability, the Kill action must be attributed to the spell or ability, the player must control that spell or ability, and the player must be responsible for the Kill action.
- [[##rule 808.1.d|808.1.d.]] The Trigger for this effect is the Permanent being Killed and sent to the Trash.
- [[##rule 808.1.d.2|808.1.d.2.]] The trigger will be added to the chain as a Pending Item before the card with Deathknell is moved to the trash due to a Kill instruction or a Cleanup.

###  group L

####  layers

**Layers**

- [[##rule 468|468.]] Layers

####  legal item

**Legal Item**

- [[##rule 319.4|319.4.]] After a Pending Item becomes a Legal Item on the Chain
- [[##rule 320.1|320.1.]] New Pending Items can be added, but Legal Items cannot be executed and Priority and Focus are not passed or awarded.

####  legally timed

**Legally Timed**

- [[##rule 338.1.a|338.1.a.]] Play a Card that is legally timed.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.2|338.1.a.2.]] A Legally Timed Card would be a Card with Reaction or a card that will have Reaction when played under appropriate circumstances.
- [[##rule 338.1.b|338.1.b.]] Activate Abilities of Game Objects that are legally timed.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 338.1.b.1|338.1.b.1.]] All rules for legally timed cards apply to legally timed abilities.
- [[##rule 347.1|347.1.]] Play a card that is legally timed.
- [[##rule 347.2|347.2.]] Activate Abilities of Game Objects that are legally timed.  See rule 360. Abilities for more information.

####  legend zone

**Legend Zone**

- [[##rule 103.1.a|103.1.a.]] This is placed in the Legend Zone at the start of the game.
- [[##rule 107.4|107.4.]] Legend Zone
- [[##rule 112|112.]] Each player separates their Champion Legend and places it in the Legend Zone.
- [[##rule 133.6.b|133.6.b.]] Legends
- [[##rule 133.8.b|133.8.b.]] Tags used to link Legends, Champion Units, and Signature cards are known as Champion Tags.
- [[##rule 172|172.]] Legends
- [[##rule 173|173.]] Legends are Game Objects.
- [[##rule 173.1|173.1.]] Legends are Owned by a player.
- [[##rule 173.2|173.2.]] Legends are not shuffled into Decks at the start of a game.
- [[##rule 173.2.a|173.2.a.]] Legends are not played during the course of regular play.
- [[##rule 173.2.b|173.2.b.]] Legends are established at the start of a game, and remain in place for the duration of regular play.
- [[##rule 173.3|173.3.]] Legends cannot be Killed during the course of regular play.
- [[##rule 173.4|173.4.]] Legends cannot be Moved.
- [[##rule 173.5|173.5.]] Legends can be targeted by spells or game effects.
- [[##rule 173.6|173.6.]] Legends can have Passive Abilities. See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 173.7|173.7.]] Legends can have Triggered Abilities. See rule 382. Triggered Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 173.8|173.8.]] Legends can have Activated Abilities. See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 174|174.]] Legends are not Permanents.
- [[##rule 175|175.]] Legends may have one or more Domains.
- [[##rule 175.1|175.1.]] The Legend determines the Domain Identity of cards its owner can include. See rule 101. Deck Construction for more information.

####  legion

**Legion**

- [[##rule 812|812.]] Legion
- [[##rule 812.1.b.1|812.1.b.1.]] Legion is functionally short for “If you have played another card this turn, this card gains [Text].”
- [[##rule 812.1.c|812.1.c.]] As long as a card different than the one with the Legion ability has been Finalized on the same turn then the Dependent Ability is Active on the card with Legion.
- [[##rule 812.2|812.2.]] All instances of Legion on cards a player controls are satisﬁed by that player playing a single card.  Example: One card has three different Legion Abilities. The Legion Text of all three abilities will be active as long as one card has been played by the card's controller earlier in the same turn.
- [[##rule 812.3|812.3.]] Legion, and whether or not a card has Legion, is a characteristic of the card and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

####  legion ability

**Legion Ability**

- [[##rule 812.1.b|812.1.b.]] Starting from the Keyword to the end of the clause, the entire statement is the Legion Ability.

####  lethal

**Lethal**

- [[##rule 437.5.a|437.5.a.]] Damage can be assigned to a Unit up to a value that would be Lethal considering the Prevent Value of all Prevent Actions on a Unit. Example:  A unit with 2 [M] is being assigned damage in the combat damage step. The unit has “prevent the ﬁrst 3 damage I would take each combat.” The unit would need to be assigned 5 damage in order to have lethal damage assigned to it.

####  lethal damage

**Lethal Damage**

- [[##rule 428.1.a.2|428.1.a.2.]] Passive Kill is when the action is taken as a result of Lethal Damage or as a consequence for any other state.

####  level

**Level**

- [[##rule 824|824.]] Level
- [[##rule 824.1|824.1.]] Level is a Dependent Keyword.
- [[##rule 824.1.c|824.1.c.]] As long as the controlling player has [N] XP, then the Dependent Ability will be be Active on the card with Level
- [[##rule 824.1.c.1|824.1.c.1.]] If the controller of the card with Level changes, then the Dependent Ability will be rendered Active or Inactive based on the new controller’s XP.
- [[##rule 824.2|824.2.]] Level, and whether or not a card has Level is a characteristic of the card and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

####  level ability

**Level Ability**

- [[##rule 824.1.b|824.1.b.]] Starting from the Keyword to the end of the clause, the entire statement is the Level Ability.

####  limitation

**Limitation**

- [[##rule 727.1.a.1|727.1.a.1.]] This Condition may also have a determined Duration, Time, or Limitation as part of its deﬁnition. EXAMPLE: Legion speciﬁes the duration of its condition: “if you have played another card this turn.” This turn is the duration. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “Until you have spent [3] this turn” would include a limitation on its condition. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “After you’ve become an attacker this turn” would include a time after which the condition is active.

####  limited actions

**Limited Actions**

- [[##rule 312.1.b.1|312.1.b.1.]] Players can always take and make choices for Limited Actions when instructed, regardless of Priority.
- [[##rule 410.2|410.2.]] Limited Actions
- [[##rule 410.2.a|410.2.a.]] A Limited Action is a game action that a spell, ability, or circumstance of the turn's progression causes the player to perform. A player cannot perform these actions at-will.
- [[##rule 413.2|413.2.]] This is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 414.3|414.3.]] This is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 415.3|415.3.]] This is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 416.2|416.2.]] This is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 417.3|417.3.]] Dealing Damage is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 418.3|418.3.]] Healing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 419.3.a|419.3.a.]] This treats Play as a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 420.2|420.2.]] Moving is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 422.2|422.2.]] Discarding is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 423.2|423.2.]] Stunning is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 424.2|424.2.]] Revealing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 425.2|425.2.]] Countering is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 426.2|426.2.]] Bufﬁng is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 427.4|427.4.]] Banishing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 428.3|428.3.]] Killing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 429.4|429.4.]] Adding is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 430.3|430.3.]] Channeling is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 431.4|431.4.]] Burning Out is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 432.2|432.2.]] Doubling is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 433.2|433.2.]] Swapping is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 435.2|435.2.]] Detaching is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 436.2|436.2.]] Predicting is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 437.6|437.6.]] Prevent is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 438.2|438.2.]] Replacing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 439.6|439.6.]] Creating is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 441|441.]] Moving is a Limited Action.

####  limited play effect

**Limited Play Effect**

- [[##rule 419.3.b|419.3.b.]] Treat all steps of Play as normal, except as noted by the game effect creating this Limited Play Effect.

####  linked

**Linked**

- [[##rule 395|395.]] In order for a set of Abilities to be Linked, they must be present in the printed Effect or Rules Text of the same Game Object, or be granted by the same source to another Game Object.
- [[##rule 397|397.]] A component Linked Ability that s a Game Object affected by another Ability in the set may only interact with Game Objects affected by the Abilities it is Linked with.

####  linked abilities

**Linked Abilities**

- [[##rule 390.5|390.5.]] Delayed Linked Abilities are Linked Abilities that are generated by another Ability and  that Ability or Game Objects it affects. Delayed Linked Abilities don’t necessarily identify a speciﬁc window of time, and instead are deﬁned by the Ability they are linked with.
- [[##rule 394|394.]] Linked Abilities are a set of Abilities with one or more of the component Abilities referencing the other Abilities in the set.
- [[##rule 396|396.]] Linked Abilities can contain component Abilities of any type.
- [[##rule 397|397.]] A component Linked Ability that s a Game Object affected by another Ability in the set may only interact with Game Objects affected by the Abilities it is Linked with.
- [[##rule 427.3.a|427.3.a.]] Separate instances of an object or effect banishing cards do not  other banished cards by objects of the same name or effects originating from cards of the same name.  Example: A spell reads "Banish the top card of your Main Deck. When you conquer this turn, draw it." This card effect allows you to draw the banished card from banishment if a condition is met. If more than one of these effects is played, each one triggers separately. Each card will be drawn separately. If the turn player passes the turn without playing the card, the card remains in banishment indeﬁnitely. If the same player plays another copy of the same spell, banishes another card, and satisﬁes its condition, they could play the new banished card, but not the original banished card. See rule 393. Linked Abilities for more information.

####  location

**Location**

- [[##rule 107.1.b|107.1.b.]] Each Base is a Location.
- [[##rule 107.2.b|107.2.b.]] Each Battleﬁeld is individually a Location.
- [[##rule 141.1.a.1|141.1.a.1.]] Units are at one of several Locations while on the Board: a Battleﬁeld or their Base.
- [[##rule 146|146.]] Units have a Location.
- [[##rule 151|151.]] Gear have a Location.
- [[##rule 169.5|169.5.]] Battleﬁelds are Locations.
- [[##rule 355.2|355.2.]] For Units, choose a valid Location where that Unit will be placed upon being Played.
- [[##rule 355.4|355.4.]] For Spells and Abilities that Move one or more Units, choose a valid Location as the Move Destination for each Move that will be performed.
- [[##rule 355.4.a|355.4.a.]] A valid Location is one other than the Units’ current Location where they are allowed to be present.
- [[##rule 359.2.c|359.2.c.]] If it is a Unit, it enters the Board exhausted at the Location that was chosen.
- [[##rule 420.1|420.1.]] Moving is the act of a Game Object moving between two Locations on The Board. See rule 440. Movement for more information on movement.
- [[##rule 442.2.c|442.2.c.]] If an action would require a Move that would cause a Unit to become present in a Location where it cannot move for any reason, such as a Battleﬁeld with two players that are not the controller of the Unit performing this Move action are in a Combat or such a Combat is Staged, it instead Recalls. See rule 449. Recalls for more information.

####  loses

**Loses**

- [[##rule 484.6.a.2|484.6.a.2.]] If one player Loses, then the entire team loses.

###  group M

####  main deck

**Main Deck**

- [[##rule 052|052.]] Card, when written in card effects, is shorthand for "Main Deck card." Runes, legends, and battleﬁelds are not considered cards when executing the abilities and effects of game objects. They are considered cards for the purposes of these rules.
- [[##rule 103.1.b|103.1.b.]] This will dictate the Domain Identity of the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 103.2.b|103.2.b.]] Your Main Deck can include up to 3 copies of the same named card.
- [[##rule 103.2.e|103.2.e.]] During Gameplay, the Main Deck is Secret Information.
- [[##rule 103.3.b|103.3.b.]] Must be shuffled and kept separate from the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 108.4|108.4.]] Main Deck Zones
- [[##rule 108.4.a|108.4.a.]] Each player has their own Main Deck Zone.
- [[##rule 108.4.b|108.4.b.]] The space for the player's Main Deck.
- [[##rule 115.1|115.1.]] The Main Deck is placed in the Main Deck Zone.
- [[##rule 127.1|127.1.]] For gameplay purposes, a card's Owner is the player who brought it into the game, either as their Champion Legend, one of their Battleﬁelds, or part of their Main Deck or Rune Deck. The legal owner of a card doesn't matter during gameplay.  Example: Bo didn't bring a deck, so Alice loans him a deck. During the game, Bo is considered the owner of those cards, even though legally they belong to Alice.
- [[##rule 129.2|129.2.]] There is a unique pattern of back side for each of the three categories of card: Main Deck cards, Rune Deck cards, and Battleﬁelds and Champion Legends.
- [[##rule 129.3|129.3.]] The back side of a card is presented to conceal information for Private and Secret information cards. For example, cards in the Main Deck and cards in hand have their back side presented.
- [[##rule 131.1|131.1.]] Main Deck cards have a Cost, listed in the upper left corner of the front face of the card. See rule 164. Rune Pools for more information.
- [[##rule 133.4|133.4.]] Main Deck Cards begin the game in the Main Deck or (in the case of a Chosen Champion) the Champion Zone.
- [[##rule 133.4.a.1|133.4.a.1.]] An umbrella sub-category encompassing Main Deck Game Objects that remain on the board after being played.
- [[##rule 133.5.a.1|133.5.a.1.]] A sub-category encompassing cards with the rune type. These are channeled rather than played. They remain on the board after being channeled, but they are not permanents, as they are not Main Deck cards.
- [[##rule 160.1|160.1.]] A Rune is not a Main Deck card.
- [[##rule 160.2.b|160.2.b.]] When a Rune is Recycled it is returned to the Rune Deck, not the Main Deck.  See rule 416. Recycle for more information.
- [[##rule 315.4.b.1|315.4.b.1.]] If there are no cards remaining in their Main Deck to draw, the Turn Player has been Burned Out.  See rule 431. Burn Out for more information.
- [[##rule 413.1.a|413.1.a.]] Unless speciﬁed otherwise, drawing takes cards from the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 413.4|413.4.]] If a player attempts to draw more cards than are available in their Main Deck, they do the following:
- [[##rule 416.1.a|416.1.a.]] Main Deck cards are Recycled to the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 416.1.c|416.1.c.]] Each player Recycles cards to their own Main Deck and Rune Deck, regardless of which player is instructed to perform the Recycle action.
- [[##rule 416.5|416.5.]] If 2 or more cards are Recycled to the Main Deck simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in a random order.  Example: Garbage Grabber has the ability "Recycle 3 from your trash, [1], [E]: Draw " To pay the cost of activating this ability, its controller chooses 3 cards from their trash and places them on the bottom of their Main Deck in a random order.
- [[##rule 424.1.a.2|424.1.a.2.]] Cards remain in the zone they are being Revealed from. Example: If a card is being Revealed from the top of a player's Main Deck, it is still the top card of that player's Main Deck.
- [[##rule 424.4.a|424.4.a.]] While cards are Revealed, those cards can be further manipulated, or accessed. They can even have their destination modiﬁed for when the Reveal ends.  Example: "Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck. Put one into your hand and Recycle the other" would be executed by taking the top two cards from your Main Deck to the table, and once every player present has had a chance to understand them you would make the selection of one of them to add to your hand. The one you did not select would then be Recycled to the bottom of the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 431.1|431.1.]] Burning Out is an action a player must perform if they attempt to move one or more cards from their Main Deck to any other zone in excess of the number of cards remaining in their Main Deck:
- [[##rule 431.1.b|431.1.b.]] If a player must put one or more cards from their Main Deck in any other zone, such as the Trash, in excess of the number of cards in their deck they will do so as much as possible, perform this action, and then complete the remaining number required by the instruction.
- [[##rule 431.1.c|431.1.c.]] If an instruction directs a player to look at or reveal cards in excess to the number of cards in a player’s Main Deck, that player looks at or Reveals as many as possible, but does not Burn Out, then proceeds with the rest of the instruction.
- [[##rule 431.1.c.1|431.1.c.1.]] If there are insufﬁcient cards among the looked at or revealed cards to perform subsequent actions to the revealed or looked at cards, any further instructions are ignored. This does not cause a Burn Out, even if those instructions would cause those cards to change zones.  Reminder: Cards are considered in the zone of origin while being looked at or revealed, in this case the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 431.2.b|431.2.b.]] Recycles their trash into their Main Deck.  Reminder: When multiple cards are Recycled to the Main Deck at the same time, those cards must be randomized
- [[##rule 436.1|436.1.]] Predicting a card is the act of looking at a single card from the top of the Main Deck and choosing whether or not to Recycle it.
- [[##rule 436.4|436.4.]] If a player attempts to Predict more cards than are available in their Main Deck, they will Predict as many as possible instead.

####  main phase

**Main Phase**

- [[##rule 144.1.a|144.1.a.]] This action can be done any time during a player's Main Phase.
- [[##rule 145.2|145.2.]] The Activated Ability of Units may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 150.2|150.2.]] The Activated Ability of Gear may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 312.2.a|312.2.a.]] When the turn is in a Neutral Open State during their Main Phase.
- [[##rule 316|316.]] Main Phase
- [[##rule 316.1|316.1.]] When all steps of the Start of Turn have been completed, the Main Phase begins.
- [[##rule 316.2|316.2.]] The Main Phase has no deﬁned structure.
- [[##rule 316.6.a|316.6.a.]] This ends the Main Phase.
- [[##rule 335.3|335.3.]] If there are no Outstanding Tasks, no pending Chain Items, and it is the Main Phase, the Turn Player receives priority. If there are no Outstanding Tasks, no pending items, and it is any other phase of the turn, proceed to the next substep, step, phase, or turn.

####  make relevant choices

**Make Relevant Choices**

- [[##rule 820.2|820.2.]] When a spell’s effect is performed an additional time with Repeat, choices must be made at the usual time during the Make Relevant Choices step of Playing a Card. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.

####  mandatory

**Mandatory**

- [[##rule 356.2.a.1|356.2.a.1.]] Some Additional Costs speciﬁed by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Mandatory, and must be paid to complete playing the card. They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and don't include the word "may."  Example: A unit has the passive ability "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." To play that unit, a player must kill a friendly unit.  See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.

####  mandatory additional costs

**Mandatory Additional Costs**

- [[##rule 356.2.a|356.2.a.]] Mandatory Additional Costs
- [[##rule 356.2.a.2|356.2.a.2.]] The cost imposed by the Deflect keyword is a Mandatory Additional Cost.  See rule 809. Deflect for more information.

####  match

**Match**

- [[##rule 480.6|480.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 481.5|481.5.]] Setup: Each player selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are set aside and will not be used for this round of play. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously in the Battleﬁeld Zone. After this game, the Battleﬁelds that were used are to be removed and not selected again for this Match. One of the remaining Battleﬁelds that were set aside must be chosen instead.
- [[##rule 482.6|482.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 483.6|483.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 484.6|484.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst team to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.

####  mech token

**Mech Token**

- [[##rule 184.4|184.4.]] A 3 [M] Mech token is a domainless unit token with 3 Might and the Mech tag.

####  might

**Might**

- [[##rule 135.2.e.3|135.2.e.3.]] Might is represented by the “Might symbol,” which resembles a sword and shield. Its shorthand is [M]. (Some previous rules information has given its shorthand as [S].)
- [[##rule 137.3|137.3.]] A card’s Might Bonus modulates the Might of the card to which the card that has the Might Bonus is Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 137.3.b|137.3.b.]] If the card to which a card with a Might Bonus is Attached has no Might value, the Might Bonus is ignored.
- [[##rule 143.2|143.2.]] Might: The combat statistic of a Unit. Used to determine a Unit's contribution to Combat, as well as when it is Killed by damaging effects.
- [[##rule 143.2.a|143.2.a.]] If a Unit ever has nonzero damage marked on it equalling or exceeding its Might, it is Killed.
- [[##rule 182.1.b|182.1.b.]] Token units have a Might.
- [[##rule 323.4|323.4.]] 3a. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might that have Deathknell abilities will trigger their Deathknell ability now, making note of their current location, attributes, and other information relevant to add the trigger as a Pending Item See rule 808 Deathknell for more information.
- [[##rule 323.5|323.5.]] 3b. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might are killed and placed in their owners' Trash.
- [[##rule 434.1.d|434.1.d.]] The Top-Most Card has its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of all cards Attached to it.
- [[##rule 435.1.e|435.1.e.]] The Top-Most Card ceases to have its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of the card being Detached.
- [[##rule 460.2|460.2.]] 1. When the Showdown closes, Attackers and Defenders resolve Combat Damage at the Battleﬁeld that was attacked, using their current Might.
- [[##rule 460.2.a|460.2.a.]] Sum the Might of all Attacking Units.
- [[##rule 460.2.b|460.2.b.]] Sum the Might of all Defending Units.
- [[##rule 460.2.c|460.2.c.]] Starting with the Attacker, each player assigns an amount of damage equal to their summed Might among the other's Units.
- [[##rule 703|703.]] Each Buff individually contributes +1 Might to a Unit.
- [[##rule 706|706.]] Mighty
- [[##rule 707|707.]] Mighty is a description that applies to some units. Other game effects can check whether a unit is Mighty.
- [[##rule 709|709.]] A Unit "becomes Mighty" at the moment its Might changes from being less than 5 to being 5 or greater.  Example: A Unit with Might 4 that gets +1 [M] becomes Mighty.  Example: A Unit with Might 5 that gets +1 [M] does not become Mighty, because it was already Mighty.
- [[##rule 710|710.]] Units on the board are evaluated according to their current Might.  Example: A unit with a base Might of 3 is targeted by a spell that reads "A unit gets +3 [M] this turn." As that spell resolves, its Might changes from 3 to 6, and it becomes Mighty. When that effect expires at the end of the turn, it will no longer be Mighty.
- [[##rule 711|711.]] Units in Non-Board Zones are evaluated according to their inherent Might.  Example: A unit in the trash is Mighty if its printed Might is 5 or greater. It doesn't matter if there were effects raising or lowering its might while it was on the board.
- [[##rule 718.4|718.4.]] While in this state, the card’s Might Bonus modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by the value listed.
- [[##rule 718.5.g|718.5.g.]] An Attached card still appends the abilities in its Effect Text to the Rules Text of the Top-Most card and modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by its Might Bonus.

####  might bonus

**Might Bonus**

- [[##rule 137|137.]] Might Bonus
- [[##rule 137.1|137.1.]] Some cards have a Might Bonus in their lower right corner, expressed as an operator plus an integer.
- [[##rule 137.2|137.2.]] A card’s Might Bonus can be +0.
- [[##rule 137.3|137.3.]] A card’s Might Bonus modulates the Might of the card to which the card that has the Might Bonus is Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 137.3.a|137.3.a.]] The Might Bonus is applied while Attached and stops applying as soon as the card with the Might Bonus is no longer Attached.
- [[##rule 137.3.b|137.3.b.]] If the card to which a card with a Might Bonus is Attached has no Might value, the Might Bonus is ignored.
- [[##rule 434.1.b|434.1.b.]] This is represented by physically laying the Top-Most card on top of the other or others such that all Effect Texts and Might Bonuses are showing, but nothing else from the card or cards Attached.
- [[##rule 434.1.b.1|434.1.b.1.]] In the situation where there is more than one card attached to the Top-Most card, they should be stacked in such a way that all Effect Text boxes and Might Bonuses are readable. The order of the Attached cards has no bearing on the application of effects.
- [[##rule 434.1.d|434.1.d.]] The Top-Most Card has its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of all cards Attached to it.
- [[##rule 435.1.e|435.1.e.]] The Top-Most Card ceases to have its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of the card being Detached.
- [[##rule 472.3.c|472.3.c.]] Might Bonuses of Attached cards are applied in this layer.
- [[##rule 718.4|718.4.]] While in this state, the card’s Might Bonus modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by the value listed.
- [[##rule 718.5.g|718.5.g.]] An Attached card still appends the abilities in its Effect Text to the Rules Text of the Top-Most card and modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by its Might Bonus.

####  mind

**Mind**

- [[##rule 134.2.c|134.2.c.]] Mind is associated with the color blue and represented by a symbol resembling a sun and moon. Its shorthand is [B].

####  mistargeting

**Mistargeting**

- [[##rule 359.3.e.9|359.3.e.9.]] The process for a card's choice becoming Invalid or Unavailable is referred to as mistargeting.  Example: A spell has the instruction "Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld." Before that instruction can execute, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The instruction will not be executed, because it speciﬁes that the unit it chooses must be at a Battleﬁeld, and by the time it attempted to execute, the unit was no longer valid as a choice.
- [[##rule 457.2.b|457.2.b.]] Any subsequent  to "here" in the corresponding effect is reassigned to the Controller's Base, where the Unit was played. Any further effects that may be invalidated are invalidated as if the effect was mistargeted. See rule 355.6. Targeting for more information on Mistargeting.

####  mode of play

**Mode Of Play**

- [[##rule 103|103.]] To play Riftbound, a player must have two Decks, a Champion Legend, and a number of Battleﬁelds determined by the Mode of Play.
- [[##rule 103.4.a|103.4.a.]] The number will be dictated by your Mode of Play.
- [[##rule 114.1|114.1.]] Your Mode of Play will dictate how these are used and placed into the Battleﬁeld Zone.  See rule 476. Modes of Play for more information.
- [[##rule 116.1.a|116.1.a.]] The Mode of Play will specify how to determine a First Player.
- [[##rule 116.2|116.2.]] See the selected Mode of Play for any adjustments to each player's ﬁrst turn.  See rule 476. Modes of Play for more information.
- [[##rule 171|171.]] The number of Battleﬁelds on the Board is determined by the Mode of Play.
- [[##rule 466.1.b|466.1.b.]] When a player tries to Gain a Point through a Score, and their current Point Total is 1 point from the Victory Score of the Mode of Play or higher, the following occurs:
- [[##rule 467|467.]] When a cleanup occurs and a player has accrued Points greater than or equal to the Victory Score for their Mode of Play, and if they have more points than any opponent, they Win the Game.
- [[##rule 478|478.]] A Mode of Play must deﬁne several variables for the game.
- [[##rule 651.4|651.4.]] If the player has Teammates due to the Mode of Play, that player’s Teammates also lose and are removed from the game.

####  modes of play

**Modes Of Play**

- [[##rule 114.1|114.1.]] Your Mode of Play will dictate how these are used and placed into the Battleﬁeld Zone.  See rule 476. Modes of Play for more information.
- [[##rule 116.2|116.2.]] See the selected Mode of Play for any adjustments to each player's ﬁrst turn.  See rule 476. Modes of Play for more information.
- [[##rule 315.2.b.3|315.2.b.3.]] Reminder: In Modes of Play with Teams, Battleﬁelds held by a Teammate of the Turn Player during this phase are disqualiﬁed from being scored this turn by the Turn Player.
- [[##rule 316.2.b.1|316.2.b.1.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, the Turn Player's teammates may play spells and activate abilities, including ones without Action or Reaction. They can only do so when the Turn Player invites them to do so with their own Priority.
- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 442.2.b|442.2.b.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds Controlled by a player’s teammates are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units that player controls.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.
- [[##rule 457.2|457.2.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid to be chosen as a location to play one or more Units by a player not involved in that Combat by any means,
- [[##rule 464.1.a|464.1.a.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds under the Control of a teammate during the Beginning Phase are also disqualiﬁed from being Scored through Conquer by any means.
- [[##rule 476|476.]] Modes of Play

####  move

**Move**

- [[##rule 144.3.a|144.3.a.]] When a Move like this is declared by a player, the units' Destination must be the same.
- [[##rule 144.3.b|144.3.b.]] When a Move like this is declared by a player, the Origins do not need to be the same.
- [[##rule 144.4|144.4.]] The Destinations where Units can Move to with their Standard Move are restricted:
- [[##rule 144.4.c.1|144.4.c.1.]] Units with Ganking may use their Standard Move to Move from Battleﬁeld to Battleﬁeld.  See rule 810. Ganking for more information.
- [[##rule 169.4|169.4.]] Battleﬁelds cannot be Moved.
- [[##rule 173.4|173.4.]] Legends cannot be Moved.
- [[##rule 319.8|319.8.]] After a Move is completed
- [[##rule 355.4|355.4.]] For Spells and Abilities that Move one or more Units, choose a valid Location as the Move Destination for each Move that will be performed.
- [[##rule 420|420.]] Move
- [[##rule 420.1|420.1.]] Moving is the act of a Game Object moving between two Locations on The Board. See rule 440. Movement for more information on movement.
- [[##rule 420.2|420.2.]] Moving is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 420.2.b|420.2.b.]] The Standard Move inherent to Units may also cause Movement.  See rule 144.for more information on the Standard Move.
- [[##rule 420.3.b|420.3.b.]] The Effect is Moving those Unit.
- [[##rule 428.2.b|428.2.b.]] This is not a subset of Move.
- [[##rule 434.4.a|434.4.a.]] This is not a Move.
- [[##rule 440|440.]] Movement
- [[##rule 441|441.]] Moving is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 441.1|441.1.]] A Permanent changing its position from any space on the Board to another space on the Board is a Move, unless it is caused by a corrective Recall.  See rule 420. Move for more information.
- [[##rule 441.2|441.2.]] A card changing game zones does not in itself constitute a Move.
- [[##rule 441.3|441.3.]] Moving is instantaneous.
- [[##rule 441.3.b|441.3.b.]] Permanents are either at their Origin before Moving or their Destination after Moving.
- [[##rule 441.3.c|441.3.c.]] Moving does not use the Chain, nor is it able to be Reacted to.
- [[##rule 442|442.]] Moving is deﬁned by the Origin and Destination of the Permanent that is changing locations.
- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 442.2.b|442.2.b.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds Controlled by a player’s teammates are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units that player controls.
- [[##rule 442.2.c|442.2.c.]] If an action would require a Move that would cause a Unit to become present in a Location where it cannot move for any reason, such as a Battleﬁeld with two players that are not the controller of the Unit performing this Move action are in a Combat or such a Combat is Staged, it instead Recalls. See rule 449. Recalls for more information.
- [[##rule 442.3|442.3.]] Units are the only Permanents that can Move.
- [[##rule 444|444.]] Spells, Abilities, or other effects may cause a Move to occur.
- [[##rule 444.1|444.1.]] The source of the Move will provide details on any restrictions on legality for Destination.
- [[##rule 446|446.]] Units may cause a Showdown without a Combat when they Move.
- [[##rule 446.1|446.1.]] A Showdown is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested while it has no Units present from any player other than those that just moved.
- [[##rule 447|447.]] Units may cause Combat when they Move.
- [[##rule 447.1|447.1.]] A Combat is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested and Units controlled by opposing players, or when a Move causes Units controlled by opposing players to become present in the same Battleﬁeld where a Showdown is ongoing. See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 448|448.]] When a Move action is complete, perform a Cleanup.
- [[##rule 450|450.]] A Recall is when a Permanent is relocated from anywhere to its Base without it being a Move.
- [[##rule 451|451.]] Recalls are not Moves.
- [[##rule 451.1|451.1.]] They do not cause Triggered Abilities to trigger that are triggered by Move actions.
- [[##rule 451.3|451.3.]] A Recall cannot be prevented by actions and Game Effects that restrict or block Movement.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.

####  move destination

**Move Destination**

- [[##rule 355.4|355.4.]] For Spells and Abilities that Move one or more Units, choose a valid Location as the Move Destination for each Move that will be performed.

####  mulligan

**Mulligan**

- [[##rule 118|118.]] In turn order, players perform their Mulligan.

###  group N

####  name

**Name**

- [[##rule 132|132.]] Name
- [[##rule 132.3|132.3.]] Cards that are printed in different languages but represent the same card are considered to have the same name for the purposes of deckbuilding and gameplay.  Example: Chemtech Enforcer in English and its counterpart in Chinese are considered the same card, despite the Name element on the card reading differently.
- [[##rule 442.2.c|442.2.c.]] If an action would require a Move that would cause a Unit to become present in a Location where it cannot move for any reason, such as a Battleﬁeld with two players that are not the controller of the Unit performing this Move action are in a Combat or such a Combat is Staged, it instead Recalls. See rule 449. Recalls for more information.

####  neutral closed

**Neutral Closed**

- [[##rule 310.2|310.2.]] Neutral Closed: There is no Showdown or Combat in progress and a Chain exists.

####  neutral open

**Neutral Open**

- [[##rule 310.1|310.1.]] Neutral Open: There is no Showdown or Combat in progress and no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.1.a|310.1.a.]] By default, cards can be played and abilities activated only when a player has priority on their turn in a Neutral Open state.
- [[##rule 312.2.a|312.2.a.]] When the turn is in a Neutral Open State during their Main Phase.
- [[##rule 316.2.b|316.2.b.]] This is denoted as a Neutral Open State, and only the Turn Player has the ability to play spells or activate abilities.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 323.11|323.11.]] 8. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and one or more Showdowns are Staged, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. A Showdown begins there.
- [[##rule 323.13|323.13.]] 9. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and Combat is Staged at one or more Battleﬁelds, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. Combat begins there.
- [[##rule 344|344.]] A Showdown begins when Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the turn is in a Neutral Open State.

####  neutral state

**Neutral State**

- [[##rule 308|308.]] At any given time, the turn is in either a Neutral State or a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 308.2|308.2.]] If no Showdown or Combat is in progress, the turn is in a Neutral State.
- [[##rule 313.5|313.5.]] If the turn is in a Neutral State, no player has Focus.
- [[##rule 343.2|343.2.]] The turn is said to be in a Neutral State if no Showdown or Combat is in progress.

####  no changes have been processed

**No Changes Have Been Processed**

- [[##rule 471|471.]] The layers are applied repeatedly until all effects operating on objects have been applied once and no changes have been processed.

####  non-board zones

**Non-board Zones**

- [[##rule 106|106.]] The Play Area is a collection of logical Zones that are deﬁned by their behaviors and relationships to Players. These Zones are grouped into The Board and Non-Board Zones.
- [[##rule 108|108.]] Non-Board Zones.
- [[##rule 110|110.]] Whenever a Game Object changes zones to or from a Non-Board Zone, all Temporary Modiﬁcations of all kinds cease to be tracked on it in all capacities.  Examples:  Damage is cleared.  Buffs are removed.  Granted Keywords are no longer granted.
- [[##rule 183.1|183.1.]] If a token is put into any Non-Board Zone besides the chain, it ceases to exist immediately after moving to its new zone.
- [[##rule 328|328.]] The Chain is a Non-Board Zone that temporarily exists whenever a card is played or an ability is activated.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.2|359.3.e.2.]] A target is illegal as the spell resolves if it no longer meets the targeting requirements of the spell, or if it has changed Zones to or from a Non-Board Zone.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.4|359.3.e.4.]] If a target changes Zones to or from a Non-Board Zone and then returns to its original zone, it is no longer a legal target, because it's not treated as the same object.  Examples:  An enemy unit at a battleﬁeld is no longer a legal target if it is no longer an enemy, no longer a unit, or no longer at a battleﬁeld.  A unit with 3 or less Might is no longer a legal target if it is no longer a unit or if its Might is greater than 3.  Something that's exhausted is no longer a legal target if it is no longer exhausted. (It can't stop being "something.")  A spell that's played from hidden can normally only target its own battleﬁeld or something at that battleﬁeld. A target for such a spell may cease to be a legal target if it moves from the battleﬁeld where that spell was played, even if the spell has no location targeting requirement otherwise.
- [[##rule 711|711.]] Units in Non-Board Zones are evaluated according to their inherent Might.  Example: A unit in the trash is Mighty if its printed Might is 5 or greater. It doesn't matter if there were effects raising or lowering its might while it was on the board.
- [[##rule 801.3.a.3|801.3.a.3.]] If an effect that grants a Keyword does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that Game Object remains on the Board or in its current Non-Board Zone.
- [[##rule 801.3.b.2|801.3.b.2.]] If an effect that removes a Keyword does not specify a duration, the duration is as long as that Game Object remains on the Board or in its current Non-Board Zone.

####  non-combat showdown

**Non-combat Showdown**

- [[##rule 187.3.c|187.3.c.]] The state of a Battleﬁeld being Contested is used to determine when Combat should occur, when a Non-Combat Showdown should occur, and when Control will change.
- [[##rule 316.5.b.1.a|316.5.b.1.a.]] These Showdowns are called Non-Combat Showdowns. During the proceedings of a Non-Combat Showdown, units controlled by a different player may become present at the Battleﬁeld where the Showdown is ongoing. This will cause the Showdown to become a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 323.14|323.14.]] 9a. If the current state is Showdown Open State and Combat is Staged at a Battleﬁeld where there is a Non-Combat Showdown ongoing, that Showdown becomes a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 348.2|348.2.]] If it is a Non-Combat Showdown, do the following:

####  non-deck cards

**Non-deck Cards**

- [[##rule 133.6|133.6.]] Non-Deck Cards are not part of any deck and begin the game in a zone determined by their type.

####  non-mandatory

**Non-mandatory**

- [[##rule 356.2.b.1|356.2.b.1.]] Some Optional Costs speciﬁed by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Non-Mandatory, and must be paid only if the player made the choice to pay them in step 2. They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and the word "may."  Example: A unit has the ability "As you play me, you may discard 1 as an additional cost. If you do, reduce my cost by [2]." While playing the unit, its controller declares their intention to pay the additional cost in step 2, applies that additional cost in rule 356.2, applies the discount granted by paying that cost in rule 356.4, and discards a card to pay that additional cost in rule 357.2.See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.

####  number of players

**Number Of Players**

- [[##rule 478.1|478.1.]] Number of Players: How many people are playing the game.

###  group O

####  one game win

**One Game Win**

- [[##rule 481.6|481.6.]] Format: Best of 3. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the game. The winner of that game earns One Game Win. Players then reset the game state, remove the Battleﬁelds in play from the game, choose new Battleﬁelds from those set aside, and play again. The ﬁrst player to earn Two Game Wins wins the match.

####  one on one

**One On One**

- [[##rule 741.2|741.2.]] A unit is one on one when it and the enemy unit at the same location are both alone.

####  open state

**Open State**

- [[##rule 145.2|145.2.]] The Activated Ability of Units may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 150.2|150.2.]] The Activated Ability of Gear may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 154|154.]] A spell can be played during an Open State outside of Showdowns on its controller's turn.
- [[##rule 158.2.a.1|158.2.a.1.]] This indicates that, in addition to being able to be played during an Open State, this spell may also be played during Open States during Showdowns. See rule 806. Action for more information.
- [[##rule 187.4.c|187.4.c.]] If a player has no Units at a Battleﬁeld and the turn is in an Open state, they lose Control of that Battleﬁeld in the following cleanup, unless there is a Combat or Showdown ongoing there.
- [[##rule 309|309.]] At any given time, the turn is in either an Open State or a Closed State.
- [[##rule 309.2|309.2.]] If no Chain exists, the turn is in an Open State.
- [[##rule 319.1|319.1.]] After the game transitions to or from an Open or Closed state
- [[##rule 331.2|331.2.]] The turn is said to be in an Open State if no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 337.1.c.1|337.1.c.1.]] If the Chain is empty, play proceeds in an Open State.
- [[##rule 340.2|340.2.]] If the Chain is empty, play proceeds in an Open State.
- [[##rule 342|342.]] A Showdown is a Window of Opportunity in which Players have an Open State in which they may play Spells in an alternating fashion.
- [[##rule 346|346.]] When the last item on the chain resolves and the turn returns to an Open State during a Showdown, Focus passes, and the next Player gains both Focus and Priority.
- [[##rule 381|381.]] All Activated Abilities can only be activated on the Controlling Player's Turn and during an Open State.
- [[##rule 383.3.c|383.3.c.]] Triggered Abilities can be put on the Chain during Closed States or Open States on any player's turn.

####  open state, battleﬁelds

**Open State, Battleﬁelds**

- [[##rule 323.6|323.6.]] 4. If the turn is in an Open State, Battleﬁelds with no Units occupying them and no Showdown or Combat ongoing become Uncontrolled.

They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and the word "may."  Example: A unit has the ability "As you play me, you may discard 1 as an additional cost. If you do, reduce my cost by [2]." While playing the unit, its controller declares their intention to pay the additional cost in step 2, applies that additional cost in rule 356.2, applies the discount granted by paying that cost in rule 356.4, and discards a card to pay that additional cost in rule 357.2.See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.

####  order

**Order**

- [[##rule 134.2.f|134.2.f.]] Order is associated with the color yellow and represented by an angular winged symbol. Its shorthand is [Y].

####  origins

**Origins**

- [[##rule 144.3.b|144.3.b.]] When a Move like this is declared by a player, the Origins do not need to be the same.
- [[##rule 169.5.a|169.5.a.]] Battleﬁelds can be Origins of moves.
- [[##rule 441.3.b|441.3.b.]] Permanents are either at their Origin before Moving or their Destination after Moving.
- [[##rule 442|442.]] Moving is deﬁned by the Origin and Destination of the Permanent that is changing locations.
- [[##rule 442.1|442.1.]] The Origin is where the Permanent is starting from.

####  ownership

**Ownership**

- [[##rule 127|127.]] Ownership
- [[##rule 127.1|127.1.]] For gameplay purposes, a card's Owner is the player who brought it into the game, either as their Champion Legend, one of their Battleﬁelds, or part of their Main Deck or Rune Deck. The legal owner of a card doesn't matter during gameplay.  Example: Bo didn't bring a deck, so Alice loans him a deck. During the game, Bo is considered the owner of those cards, even though legally they belong to Alice.
- [[##rule 169.1|169.1.]] Battleﬁelds are Owned by a player.
- [[##rule 173.1|173.1.]] Legends are Owned by a player.
- [[##rule 180|180.]] A token's owner is the player who controlled the effect that created it.

###  group P

####  pass priority

**Pass Priority**

- [[##rule 338.1.c|338.1.c.]] Pass Priority

####  passive

**Passive**

- [[##rule 428.1.a|428.1.a.]] This can be Active or Passive.
- [[##rule 428.1.a.2|428.1.a.2.]] Passive Kill is when the action is taken as a result of Lethal Damage or as a consequence for any other state.
- [[##rule 652.5.b.2|652.5.b.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have Passed their Focus, the Showdown ends and play proceeds as necessary, E.G. Combat is resolved or a Cleanup is completed.
- [[##rule 725.1|725.1.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Attaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Attaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Attaches.
- [[##rule 725.2|725.2.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Detaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Detaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Detaches.

####  passive abilities

**Passive Abilities**

- [[##rule 169.8|169.8.]] Battleﬁelds can have Passive Abilities. See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 173.6|173.6.]] Legends can have Passive Abilities. See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 356.2.a.1|356.2.a.1.]] Some Additional Costs speciﬁed by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Mandatory, and must be paid to complete playing the card. They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and don't include the word "may."  Example: A unit has the passive ability "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." To play that unit, a player must kill a friendly unit.  See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 356.2.b.1|356.2.b.1.]] Some Optional Costs speciﬁed by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Non-Mandatory, and must be paid only if the player made the choice to pay them in step 2. They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and the word "may."  Example: A unit has the ability "As you play me, you may discard 1 as an additional cost. If you do, reduce my cost by [2]." While playing the unit, its controller declares their intention to pay the additional cost in step 2, applies that additional cost in rule 356.2, applies the discount granted by paying that cost in rule 356.4, and discards a card to pay that additional cost in rule 357.2.See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 361.1|361.1.]] An Ability has multiple structures.  -Passive Abilities  -Replacement Effects  -Activated Abilities  -Triggered Abilities  -Delayed Abilities
- [[##rule 364.3|364.3.]] Passive Abilities can be conditional.
- [[##rule 366.1|366.1.]] Passive Abilities of cards in zones that are outside of the Board will self-describe their context.  Example: The passive ability "Play me only during an opponent's turn." applies in any zone from which that card can be played.
- [[##rule 366.2|366.2.]] Passive Abilities can alter the costs of cards as they are played.
- [[##rule 368.1|368.1.]] Passive Abilities can be Replacement Effects.
- [[##rule 390.4|390.4.]] Delayed Passive Abilities are Passive Abilities that are applicable only during a speciﬁed window of time. The time that the Delayed Passive Ability applies will be recognized in the effect that initiates it.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.2|727.1.c.2.]] Passive Abilities begin applying at the same time the Dependent Keyword becomes true.
- [[##rule 807.1|807.1.]] Assault is a Passive Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 809.1|809.1.]] Deflect is a Passive Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 810.1|810.1.]] Ganking is a Passive Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 814.1|814.1.]] Shield is a Passive Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 815.1|815.1.]] Tank is a Passive Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 822.1|822.1.]] Ambush is a Passive Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 826.1|826.1.]] Backline is a Passive Ability keyword.

####  pending chain items

**Pending Chain Items**

- [[##rule 329|329.]] Cards and abilities added to the chain are added as Pending Chain Items that become Finalized Chain Items.
- [[##rule 329.3|329.3.]] When a Pending Chain Item is no longer Pending it is ﬁnalized and becomes a Finalized Chain Item.
- [[##rule 336.1|336.1.]] In the sequence of resolving FEPR more Chain Items may become Pending Chain Items. These will be processed by the same FEPR process that produced them.
- [[##rule 352.1|352.1.]] When initially being played cards are Pending, as Pending Chain Items.
- [[##rule 377.3.b.1|377.3.b.1.]] Follow the steps of “Playing or Activating Abilities” in rule 398. This ability will become a Pending Chain Item.

####  pending item

**Pending Item**

- [[##rule 319.3|319.3.]] After a Pending Item is added to the Chain
- [[##rule 319.4|319.4.]] After a Pending Item becomes a Legal Item on the Chain
- [[##rule 320.1|320.1.]] New Pending Items can be added, but Legal Items cannot be executed and Priority and Focus are not passed or awarded.
- [[##rule 323.4|323.4.]] 3a. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might that have Deathknell abilities will trigger their Deathknell ability now, making note of their current location, attributes, and other information relevant to add the trigger as a Pending Item See rule 808 Deathknell for more information.
- [[##rule 329.1|329.1.]] Pending Items are on the Chain.
- [[##rule 329.2|329.2.]] Chain Items are Pending until the “Check Legality” step of playing a card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 329.3|329.3.]] When a Pending Chain Item is no longer Pending it is ﬁnalized and becomes a Finalized Chain Item.
- [[##rule 337.1|337.1.]] If one or more Items are Pending, their controllers must complete the steps of Playing those Pending Items until they are Finalized Items or leave the Chain.
- [[##rule 337.1.c.2|337.1.c.2.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are one or more Pending Items, repeat Step 1.
- [[##rule 337.1.c.3|337.1.c.3.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are no Pending Items, the controller of the newest item on the chain gains Priority and becomes the Active Player. Proceed to Step 2: Execute.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.4|338.1.a.4.]] The card will be added to the chain as a Pending Item, following the steps of playing a card.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.7|338.1.a.7.]] Playing a card will create one or more Pending Items. Return to Step 1: Finalize.
- [[##rule 338.1.b.2|338.1.b.2.]] Activating abilities will create one or more Pending Items. Return to Step 1: Finalize.
- [[##rule 340.3|340.3.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are one or more Pending Items, return to Step 1: Finalize.
- [[##rule 340.4|340.4.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are no Pending Items, the controller of the newest item on the chain gains Priority. Return to Step 2: Execute.
- [[##rule 352.1|352.1.]] When initially being played cards are Pending, as Pending Chain Items.
- [[##rule 352.2|352.2.]] Near the end of the process cards will cease being Pending and become Finalized Chain Items.
- [[##rule 354.2|354.2.]] This item becomes Pending, awaiting the ﬁnalization process (steps 2 - 5)
- [[##rule 359.1|359.1.]] This card is no longer Pending.
- [[##rule 359.3.b|359.3.b.]] If there are other Pending Items on the Chain, then the controller of those Pending Items completes Steps 2 through 5 of Playing Cards for those items before continuing.  See rule 327. Chains for more information.
- [[##rule 383.4.a.2|383.4.a.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Permanent these effects correspond to is ﬁnalized and enters the board.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.2|383.4.b.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after a spell or ability that targets an appropriate Game Object is Finalized.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.a|383.4.c.2.a.]] The Conquer Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit(s) these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from Conquering.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.b|383.4.c.2.b.]] The Conquer Abilities of anything that s the player Conquering is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Conquer and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.a|383.4.d.2.a.]] The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.b|383.4.d.2.b.]] The Hold Abilities of anything that s the player Holding is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Hold and gained 1 Victory Point.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2|383.4.e.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Attacker designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2|383.4.f.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Defender designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 388.1|388.1.]] A new ability is created and added to the chain as a Pending Item. See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 388.2|388.2.]] If a Reflexive Trigger creates more than one Pending Item it creates them all in order, but does not go beyond the ﬁrst step of adding them to the Chain.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 400|400.]] Abilities when added to the Chain become Pending Items until they complete the steps of Playing.
- [[##rule 401.1|401.1.]] Add a Pending Item to the chain representing the Ability that is either being Activated or Triggered. Notably, although this Chain Item will not have a card representing it, this will create a Closed State.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 402.3|402.3.]] If there are not enough options to make legal choices for a Triggered Ability that has been put on the chain, remove it from the Chain now. It ceases to be a Pending Item but never becomes a Chain Item.
- [[##rule 404.2|404.2.]] At this stage, players may decline to pay for Triggered Abilities that have incurred a cost. If they do, the ability will cease being a Pending Item and be removed from the Chain. It never becomes a Chain Item.
- [[##rule 406.1|406.1.]] This Ability is no longer Pending.
- [[##rule 406.3|406.3.]] If there are other Pending Items on the Chain, their controllers perform the remaining steps of playing now.
- [[##rule 428.1.a.1.b|428.1.a.1.b.]] When a unit with a Deathknell  is to be put in the Trash due to a Kill Instruction, it ﬁrst has its Deathknell added to the chain as a Pending Item. Note the unit’s location, attributes, and other relevant information to process its Deathknell when ﬁnalized before completing this Kill Instruction.
- [[##rule 459.2.d|459.2.d.]] 3. Add items to the Combat Chain if establishing Attacker and Defender has caused Triggered Abilities to become Pending.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.3.a|727.1.c.3.a.]] If the condition for the Dependent Keyword causes the Activated Ability to become Inactive after it has been added to the chain as a Pending Item, that chain item will not be affected and will proceed with being played as normal.
- [[##rule 808.1.d.2|808.1.d.2.]] The trigger will be added to the chain as a Pending Item before the card with Deathknell is moved to the trash due to a Kill instruction or a Cleanup.
- [[##rule 818.1.c.1|818.1.c.1.]] If paying costs or making choices for this ability causes triggered abilities to trigger, they will be placed on the chain above this ability in a Pending state. See rule 376. Activated Abilities for more information.

####  permanent abilities

**Permanent Abilities**

- [[##rule 806.1.a|806.1.a.]] It can be present on Cards, Rune Abilities, Legend Abilities or Permanent Abilities.
- [[##rule 813.1.a|813.1.a.]] It can be present on Cards, Rune Abilities, Legend Abilities and Permanent Abilities.

####  permanents

**Permanents**

- [[##rule 107.1.c|107.1.c.]] Permanents and Runes controlled by a player reside in that player's Base.
- [[##rule 107.1.c.1|107.1.c.1.]] Permanents attached to Permanents controlled by a player may also be found in that player’s Base.
- [[##rule 107.1.d|107.1.d.]] Permanents and Runes in Bases are Public Information.
- [[##rule 133.4.a|133.4.a.]] Permanents
- [[##rule 135.2.e.2|135.2.e.2.]] The cost of Exhausting a Permanent is represented by the “exhaust symbol,” which resembles a card turning sideways. Its shorthand is [E]. (Some previous rules information has given its shorthand as [T].)
- [[##rule 160.1.a|160.1.a.]] This means, despite remaining on the Board until Recycled or otherwise removed from the board, it is not a Permanent.
- [[##rule 170|170.]] Battleﬁelds are not Permanents.
- [[##rule 174|174.]] Legends are not Permanents.
- [[##rule 188.3|188.3.]] For Permanents and Runes, when they Enter the Board, that player is assigned as that Game Object's Controller.
- [[##rule 188.3.d|188.3.d.]] That player may make decisions about any game effects created from "When you play me" effects of Permanents.
- [[##rule 323.7|323.7.]] 5. Recall all Unattached non-Unit Gear at Battleﬁelds, and all Permanents and Runes in Bases other than their controller’s. Remove all Hidden cards from all Battleﬁelds that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's Trash.
- [[##rule 351.1|351.1.]] Permanents become Game Objects when Played.
- [[##rule 359.2|359.2.]] A Permanent leaves the Chain and becomes a Game Object.
- [[##rule 365|365.]] Presence on Permanents
- [[##rule 365.1|365.1.]] Passive Abilities of Permanents are typically only active while on the Board.
- [[##rule 383.4.a|383.4.a.]] Play Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that the Permanent that has the Play Effect being played to the board.
- [[##rule 383.4.a.2|383.4.a.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Permanent these effects correspond to is ﬁnalized and enters the board.
- [[##rule 384|384.]] Presence on Permanents
- [[##rule 384.2|384.2.]] Triggered Abilities of Permanents are only able to have their Conditions evaluated while on the Board.
- [[##rule 428.1|428.1.]] Killing is the action of a Permanent going to the trash from the board.
- [[##rule 428.2|428.2.]] When a permanent is killed it is placed directly in the trash from its place of origin.
- [[##rule 441.1|441.1.]] A Permanent changing its position from any space on the Board to another space on the Board is a Move, unless it is caused by a corrective Recall.  See rule 420. Move for more information.
- [[##rule 441.3.a|441.3.a.]] There is no state for Permanents between locations.
- [[##rule 441.3.b|441.3.b.]] Permanents are either at their Origin before Moving or their Destination after Moving.
- [[##rule 442|442.]] Moving is deﬁned by the Origin and Destination of the Permanent that is changing locations.
- [[##rule 442.1|442.1.]] The Origin is where the Permanent is starting from.
- [[##rule 442.2|442.2.]] The Destination is where the Permanent is going to.
- [[##rule 442.3|442.3.]] Units are the only Permanents that can Move.
- [[##rule 450|450.]] A Recall is when a Permanent is relocated from anywhere to its Base without it being a Move.
- [[##rule 451.2|451.2.]] A Recall causes a Permanent to change locations.
- [[##rule 453|453.]] Recalls do not affect the state of the Permanent being recalled.
- [[##rule 808.1.a|808.1.a.]] It is present on Permanents.

####  permissive

**Permissive**

- [[##rule 806.1|806.1.]] Action is a Permissive keyword.
- [[##rule 813.1|813.1.]] Reaction is a Permissive keyword.
- [[##rule 819.1|819.1.]] Quick-Draw is a Triggered Ability keyword. It is also a Permissive keyword.

####  phases

**Phases**

- [[##rule 306|306.]] The Turn Player changes when the current Turn Player reaches the End of all of the Phases of their Turn.
- [[##rule 316.5.b.1|316.5.b.1.]] Showdowns that occur as a result of a player moving to an empty Battleﬁeld are a stand-alone Phase and do not create a Combat.
- [[##rule 319.2|319.2.]] After the game transitions between Phases, unless speciﬁed otherwise

####  play

**Play**

- [[##rule 188.1|188.1.]] When a player Plays a Card or other Game Object, they are established as that Game Object's Controller.
- [[##rule 335|335.]] Whenever a Player takes one or more actions that incur Tasks they should refer to the process of HOT FEPR: Handle Outstanding Tasks; then Finalize, Execute, Pass, Resolve.
- [[##rule 338.1.a|338.1.a.]] Play a Card that is legally timed.
- [[##rule 347.1|347.1.]] Play a card that is legally timed.
- [[##rule 359|359.]] 6. Finish ﬁnalizing this card and proceed with the card's category of Play.
- [[##rule 419|419.]] Play
- [[##rule 419.1|419.1.]] A player Plays cards by placing them on the chain and queuing them to be ﬁnalized.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information on playing cards. See rule 337. Finalize for more information on ﬁnalizing cards.
- [[##rule 419.1.a|419.1.a.]] By default, a player can only Play cards from their hand or their Chosen Champion zone.
- [[##rule 419.2.a|419.2.a.]] As long as a player has the resources to pay the costs associated with the card and legal choices to make for their cards, they may Play cards.
- [[##rule 419.3.a|419.3.a.]] This treats Play as a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 419.3.b|419.3.b.]] Treat all steps of Play as normal, except as noted by the game effect creating this Limited Play Effect.
- [[##rule 419.3.c|419.3.c.]] If there are no eligible cards to Play when instructed to Play in this manner like this, then nothing happens and resolution continues.
