- [[##rule 811.1.c.1|811.1.c.1.]] Hide is not a subset of Play.

####  play area

**Play Area**

- [[##rule 106|106.]] The Play Area is a collection of logical Zones that are deﬁned by their behaviors and relationships to Players. These Zones are grouped into The Board and Non-Board Zones.
- [[##rule 109|109.]] All Game Objects in the collective Play Areas are Public Information.
- [[##rule 109.1|109.1.]] Any player may view, or be provided with the details of the face-up information printed on the cards in the Play Area.
- [[##rule 109.2|109.2.]] The State of all Game Objects in the Play Area is also Public Information.  Examples:   If a Unit is Buffed  If a Gear is Exhausted  Etc.

####  play cost

**Play Cost**

- [[##rule 130.3|130.3.]] This can be identiﬁed in situations where the back is not easily discernible by the presence of the Play Cost in the upper left corner of the card.

####  play effect

**Play Effect**

- [[##rule 383.4.a|383.4.a.]] Play Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that the Permanent that has the Play Effect being played to the board.
- [[##rule 821.1.b|821.1.b.]] Weaponmaster is a Play Effect that chooses an Equipment you control and allows you to pay its Equip cost at a discount, regardless of the usual timing of the Equip ability, to Attach that Equipment to the unit with Weaponmaster.

####  played

**Played**

- [[##rule 108.1.a|108.1.a.]] Cards and abilities are placed here as part of the process of being played. See rule 327. Chains for more information.
- [[##rule 182.1.a|182.1.a.]] Tokens are played by their owner if their card type is played, following all the applicable steps for playing a card plus any restrictions or modiﬁcations from the effect that created the token.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 350.1|350.1.]] A card is Played when it has ﬁnished this process in its entirety.
- [[##rule 350.2|350.2.]] Tokens are not cards, but can still be Played.  See rule 176. Tokens for more information.
- [[##rule 351.1|351.1.]] Permanents become Game Objects when Played.
- [[##rule 351.2|351.2.]] Spells create game effects that are executed, then the card is placed in the trash when Played.
- [[##rule 355.2|355.2.]] For Units, choose a valid Location where that Unit will be placed upon being Played.
- [[##rule 419.3|419.3.]] Game effects may result in cards being played as part of their resolution.
- [[##rule 421.3|421.3.]] Cards that are facedown at Battleﬁelds have their gameplay properties and permissions deﬁned by the effect that put them there.  Example: Cards that players Hide with the Hidden keyword can be Played for [0] on any subsequent turn as a property of the Hidden keyword.
- [[##rule 820.3.a|820.3.a.]] Regardless of the number of times a spell's instructions are executed with this keyword, the spell is only Played once.

####  player

**Player**

- [[##rule 106|106.]] The Play Area is a collection of logical Zones that are deﬁned by their behaviors and relationships to Players. These Zones are grouped into The Board and Non-Board Zones.
- [[##rule 187.3.a|187.3.a.]] Contested is a temporary status applied to the battleﬁeld when a Unit controlled by a Player who does not currently Control that Battleﬁeld Moves or otherwise becomes present there.
- [[##rule 312.2.d|312.2.d.]] When the turn is in a Closed State, they are the next Player in Turn Order, and the player with Priority passes.
- [[##rule 316.5.c|316.5.c.]] A Showdown is a structured Window of Opportunity where Players may play cards and activate abilities with Action or Reaction. See rule 341. Showdowns for more information.
- [[##rule 334|334.]] A Task is one or more steps or processes that one or more Players must perform before continuing with any other actions.
- [[##rule 335|335.]] Whenever a Player takes one or more actions that incur Tasks they should refer to the process of HOT FEPR: Handle Outstanding Tasks; then Finalize, Execute, Pass, Resolve.
- [[##rule 338.1.c.1|338.1.c.1.]] The player with Priority passes Priority to the next Player in Turn Order. Proceed to Step 3: Pass.
- [[##rule 339.2|339.2.]] Otherwise, the player with Priority passes Priority to the next Player in Turn Order. Return to Step 3: Execute.
- [[##rule 342|342.]] A Showdown is a Window of Opportunity in which Players have an Open State in which they may play Spells in an alternating fashion.
- [[##rule 346|346.]] When the last item on the chain resolves and the turn returns to an Open State during a Showdown, Focus passes, and the next Player gains both Focus and Priority.
- [[##rule 347.3.a|347.3.a.]] If all Players have passed once in sequence, the Showdown ends.
- [[##rule 347.4|347.4.]] Otherwise, Focus passes to the next Player in Turn Order.
- [[##rule 435.2.a|435.2.a.]] Players may only Detach cards when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 436.1.b|436.1.b.]] The Player who performs the game action may rearrange any cards not Recycled in this way.
- [[##rule 436.2.a|436.2.a.]] Players may only Predict cards when instructed to do so by game effects.
- [[##rule 436.4.a|436.4.a.]] The Player will not perform a Burn Out as a result of Predicting with too few cards in their deck.
- [[##rule 437.6.a|437.6.a.]] Players may only Prevent Damage when directed to by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.
- [[##rule 461.3.a|461.3.a.]] A Player has won a combat if they received either the attacker or defender designation and are the only Player that has units remaining at this battleﬁeld during this step.
- [[##rule 461.3.b|461.3.b.]] A Player has lost a combat if they received either the attacker or defender designation and are the only Player that does not have any units remaining at this battleﬁeld during this step.
- [[##rule 461.3.d|461.3.d.]] There is “No Result” if either both Players have units present during this step, or neither player has units present during this step.
- [[##rule 461.7.a|461.7.a.]] Remove Attacker and Defender Designation from all Units and Players.
- [[##rule 463|463.]] Scoring is the act of a Player gaining a point through the process of seizing or maintaining control over Battleﬁelds.
- [[##rule 652.5.b.1|652.5.b.1.]] If the removed player had Focus in a Showdown, the next Player in order receives Focus.
- [[##rule 652.5.b.2|652.5.b.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have Passed their Focus, the Showdown ends and play proceeds as necessary, E.G. Combat is resolved or a Cleanup is completed.
- [[##rule 652.5.c.1|652.5.c.1.]] If the removed player had Priority during a Chain, the next Player in order receives Priority.
- [[##rule 652.5.c.2|652.5.c.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have passed Priority, then the most recent spell or ability on the Chain will resolve with Priority being re-established as appropriate for the state after the resolution of that spell or ability.
- [[##rule 729|729.]] XP is a resource that is accrued, spent, or otherwise modiﬁed by Players through the course of play.
- [[##rule 729.1.a|729.1.a.]] XP is a value that can be tracked by counters, dice, cards, or any method that clearly displays the speciﬁc value of XP that is currently on a Player.
- [[##rule 729.2|729.2.]] The amount of XP a Player has is Public Information.
- [[##rule 730.1|730.1.]] To Gain XP, increase the value of XP marked on the Player gaining it.
- [[##rule 730.2|730.2.]] To Spend XP, reduce the value of XP marked on the Player spending it.

####  players must still assign lethal damage to a unit before moving to the next when assigning their damage

**Players Must Still Assign Lethal Damage To A Unit Before Moving To The Next When Assigning Their Damage**

- [[##rule 826.4.a|826.4.a.]] Players must still assign lethal damage to a unit before moving to the next when assigning their damage.

####  playing

**Playing**

- [[##rule 337.1|337.1.]] If one or more Items are Pending, their controllers must complete the steps of Playing those Pending Items until they are Finalized Items or leave the Chain.
- [[##rule 355.2.b|355.2.b.]] Some Game Effects may grant players permission to play Units to locations that are not normally Valid. Such locations become Valid for the purposes of Playing the Unit.
- [[##rule 400|400.]] Abilities when added to the Chain become Pending Items until they complete the steps of Playing.

####  playing a card

**Playing A Card**

- [[##rule 108.3.d|108.3.d.]] The Chosen Champion can be played from here as normal, following the rules of Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.6|338.1.a.6.]] Whether a Card is legally timed is evaluated during the “Check Legality” step of Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 377|377.]] Activated Abilities are repeatable effects with a cost. They follow a process of going onto the chain and resolving, similar to Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 820.2|820.2.]] When a spell’s effect is performed an additional time with Repeat, choices must be made at the usual time during the Make Relevant Choices step of Playing a Card. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.

####  playing cards

**Playing Cards**

- [[##rule 108.3.d|108.3.d.]] The Chosen Champion can be played from here as normal, following the rules of Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 145.2.a|145.2.a.]] This follows the same process as playing a card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 150.2.a|150.2.a.]] This follows the same process as playing a card. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 182.1.a|182.1.a.]] Tokens are played by their owner if their card type is played, following all the applicable steps for playing a card plus any restrictions or modiﬁcations from the effect that created the token.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 329.2|329.2.]] Chain Items are Pending until the “Check Legality” step of playing a card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 337.1.c|337.1.c.]] Units, Gear, and abilities that Add resources resolve immediately when Finalized and do not progress to Step 2: Execute.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.6|338.1.a.6.]] Whether a Card is legally timed is evaluated during the “Check Legality” step of Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 340.1|340.1.]] The newest item on the Chain resolves. Execute its game effects in their entirety. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information on resolving spells.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information on resolving abilities.
- [[##rule 349|349.]] Playing Cards
- [[##rule 377|377.]] Activated Abilities are repeatable effects with a cost. They follow a process of going onto the chain and resolving, similar to Playing a Card.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 401.1|401.1.]] Add a Pending Item to the chain representing the Ability that is either being Activated or Triggered. Notably, although this Chain Item will not have a card representing it, this will create a Closed State.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 402.1|402.1.]] Make all choices required for this ability, such as targets, modes, or other relevant decisions.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information
- [[##rule 403.2|403.2.]] Apply cost increases and decreases as a result of choices made in the prior step.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 403.3|403.3.]] Apply any other cost increases or decreases as necessary.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 404.1|404.1.]] Pay costs as determined in the prior step.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 405.2|405.2.]] Ensure that the Ability’s effect would not create an illegal state. If it would, resolve in the same way you would resolve a Card that creates an illegal state. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 419.1|419.1.]] A player Plays cards by placing them on the chain and queuing them to be ﬁnalized.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information on playing cards. See rule 337. Finalize for more information on ﬁnalizing cards.
- [[##rule 809.1.d|809.1.d.]] It is an effect that imposes a Mandatory Additional Cost on Spells and Abilities that choose the permanent that has this ability.  See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 820.2|820.2.]] When a spell’s effect is performed an additional time with Repeat, choices must be made at the usual time during the Make Relevant Choices step of Playing a Card. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 822.1.c|822.1.c.]] It is a passive ability that adds options to locations that are valid for a Unit to be played to during the Make Relevant Choices step of Playing a Card See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information

####  playing or activating abilities

**Playing Or Activating Abilities**

- [[##rule 338.1.b|338.1.b.]] Activate Abilities of Game Objects that are legally timed.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 340.1|340.1.]] The newest item on the Chain resolves. Execute its game effects in their entirety. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information on resolving spells.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information on resolving abilities.
- [[##rule 388.1|388.1.]] A new ability is created and added to the chain as a Pending Item. See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 388.2|388.2.]] If a Reflexive Trigger creates more than one Pending Item it creates them all in order, but does not go beyond the ﬁrst step of adding them to the Chain.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.

####  point

**Point**

- [[##rule 466.1|466.1.]] The player Gains up to one Point, depending on their current score.
- [[##rule 466.1.b|466.1.b.]] When a player tries to Gain a Point through a Score, and their current Point Total is 1 point from the Victory Score of the Mode of Play or higher, the following occurs:
- [[##rule 467|467.]] When a cleanup occurs and a player has accrued Points greater than or equal to the Victory Score for their Mode of Play, and if they have more points than any opponent, they Win the Game.
- [[##rule 480.6|480.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 481.6|481.6.]] Format: Best of 3. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the game. The winner of that game earns One Game Win. Players then reset the game state, remove the Battleﬁelds in play from the game, choose new Battleﬁelds from those set aside, and play again. The ﬁrst player to earn Two Game Wins wins the match.
- [[##rule 482.6|482.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 483.6|483.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.
- [[##rule 484.6|484.6.]] Format: Best of 1. The ﬁrst team to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.

####  power

**Power**

- [[##rule 131.3|131.3.]] Power cost
- [[##rule 135.2.e.4|135.2.e.4.]] Power of a speciﬁc Domain is represented by its domain symbol and the corresponding shorthand. See rule 134. Domain for more information.
- [[##rule 135.2.e.5.a|135.2.e.5.a.]] When required as a cost, [A] can be paid by Power of any Domain.
- [[##rule 135.2.e.5.b|135.2.e.5.b.]] When Added to a player’s Rune Pool, [A] can be spent to pay a Power cost of any Domain.
- [[##rule 162|162.]] Runes produce Energy and Power.
- [[##rule 162.2|162.2.]] Power is used to pay Domain-associated Power Costs.
- [[##rule 162.2.a|162.2.a.]] Power has a Domain.
- [[##rule 162.2.a.1|162.2.a.1.]] Power's Domain usually corresponds to the Domain of the Rune that produced it.
- [[##rule 162.2.b|162.2.b.]] Some Power is Universal and can be used to pay for costs of any Domain.
- [[##rule 163.2.b.1|163.2.b.1.]] The Power added this way corresponds to the Domain of the Rune that is being Recycled.
- [[##rule 165|165.]] The Rune Pool is a conceptual collection of a player's available Energy and Power available to pay Costs.
- [[##rule 165.1|165.1.]] When a card adds Energy or Power, it is added to the controlling player's Rune Pool.
- [[##rule 165.2|165.2.]] Players must ﬁrst add Energy and Power to their Rune Pool in order to be able to spend it to play cards or pay for Abilities with costs.
- [[##rule 165.3|165.3.]] Energy and Power do not have a physical marker or tracker, although players may wish to use a physical tracker if they are retaining unspent Energy and Power over the course of their turn.
- [[##rule 166.1|166.1.]] Any unspent Energy or Power are lost.
- [[##rule 167|167.]] All Abilities that include the action "Add" are abilities that are adding Energy or Power to the Rune Pool. See rule 429. Add for more information.
- [[##rule 315.4.d|315.4.d.]] 1. Each player's Rune Pool empties. Any unspent Energy and Power are lost. See rule 164. Rune Pools for more information.
- [[##rule 317.2.d|317.2.d.]] Insert “2e. Each player’s Rune Pool empties. Any unspent Energy and Power are lost.”
- [[##rule 356.1.b.1|356.1.b.1.]] If a card allows a player to play a card "ignoring its cost," its base Energy cost and base Power cost are set to zero.
- [[##rule 357.1|357.1.]] In total, pay the combined Energy cost (if any) and Power cost (if any).
- [[##rule 357.1.a|357.1.a.]] During this step, the card's controller can use activated abilities with the Reaction tag that Add resources to add Energy and Power to pay the card's costs.  See rule 164. Rune Pools and rule 429. Add for more information.

####  predict

**Predict**

- [[##rule 436|436.]] Predict
- [[##rule 436.1|436.1.]] Predicting a card is the act of looking at a single card from the top of the Main Deck and choosing whether or not to Recycle it.
- [[##rule 436.1.a|436.1.a.]] When more than one card is Predicted, the Predicting player looks at that many cards and Recycles any number of them.
- [[##rule 436.2|436.2.]] Predicting is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 436.2.a|436.2.a.]] Players may only Predict cards when instructed to do so by game effects.
- [[##rule 436.4|436.4.]] If a player attempts to Predict more cards than are available in their Main Deck, they will Predict as many as possible instead.
- [[##rule 436.4.a|436.4.a.]] The Player will not perform a Burn Out as a result of Predicting with too few cards in their deck.

####  prevent

**Prevent**

- [[##rule 437|437.]] Prevent
- [[##rule 437.1|437.1.]] Preventing damage is the act of reducing the Damage a set of game objects would take.
- [[##rule 437.1.a|437.1.a.]] Prevent is an action that interacts with Damage.
- [[##rule 437.1.b|437.1.b.]] Prevent appears in statements that deﬁne an amount of damage and the source of the damage it will affect, as well as the timespan it will be relevant for.
- [[##rule 437.1.b.1|437.1.b.1.]] Prevent actions are usually formatted as “Prevent the next X [source] damage that would be dealt to a [unit] this turn.”
- [[##rule 437.1.b.2|437.1.b.2.]] Prevent will always apply to the next damage that would be dealt to a unit affected by the Prevent action.
- [[##rule 437.2|437.2.]] When damage is Prevented, it is replaced with an event where it deals that much damage reduced by the Prevent Value tracked on the Unit speciﬁcally.
- [[##rule 437.2.a|437.2.a.]] The damage being dealt as a result of Preventing can never be less than 0, but can be 0. This is equivalent to not dealing damage.
- [[##rule 437.3|437.3.]] When damage is dealt this way, reduce the Prevent Value being tracked on the Unit affected by the Prevent action by the prevented amount.
- [[##rule 437.3.a|437.3.a.]] If the Prevent Value is 0 or less, then Prevent is no longer being tracked on the Unit in question, and the effect expires.
- [[##rule 437.4|437.4.]] Damage dealt to a Unit that has that all of that damage Prevented is not considered to have been dealt to it at all.
- [[##rule 437.5|437.5.]] Damage can still be assigned to Units in combat that are affected by Prevent. The damage dealt as a result of that assignment will be affected by the Prevent action.
- [[##rule 437.6|437.6.]] Prevent is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 437.7|437.7.]] Prevent is a Delayed Replacement Effect. See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information. See rule 389. Delayed Abilities for more information.

####  prevent actions

**Prevent Actions**

- [[##rule 437.5.a|437.5.a.]] Damage can be assigned to a Unit up to a value that would be Lethal considering the Prevent Value of all Prevent Actions on a Unit. Example:  A unit with 2 [M] is being assigned damage in the combat damage step. The unit has “prevent the ﬁrst 3 damage I would take each combat.” The unit would need to be assigned 5 damage in order to have lethal damage assigned to it.

####  prevent damage

**Prevent Damage**

- [[##rule 437.6.a|437.6.a.]] Players may only Prevent Damage when directed to by Game Effects.

####  priority

**Priority**

- [[##rule 312|312.]] At any given time, up to one player has Priority.
- [[##rule 312.1|312.1.]] Priority is the singular exclusive right to take Discretionary Actions. See rule 410.1. Discretionary Actions for more information.
- [[##rule 312.1.a|312.1.a.]] The player with Priority can take appropriately timed Discretionary Actions.
- [[##rule 312.1.b|312.1.b.]] If no player has Priority, no player can take Discretionary Actions.
- [[##rule 312.1.b.1|312.1.b.1.]] Players can always take and make choices for Limited Actions when instructed, regardless of Priority.
- [[##rule 312.2|312.2.]] A player receives Priority at the following times:
- [[##rule 312.2.d|312.2.d.]] When the turn is in a Closed State, they are the next Player in Turn Order, and the player with Priority passes.
- [[##rule 312.3|312.3.]] When a player is granted Priority, it is either created if no player has it or taken from the player with Priority.
- [[##rule 313.2|313.2.]] A player who gains Focus also gains Priority.
- [[##rule 313.3|313.3.]] A player who passes Priority retains Focus.
- [[##rule 313.4|313.4.]] A player may not make discretionary actions with Focus unless they also possess Priority.
- [[##rule 316.2.b.1|316.2.b.1.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, the Turn Player's teammates may play spells and activate abilities, including ones without Action or Reaction. They can only do so when the Turn Player invites them to do so with their own Priority.
- [[##rule 320.1|320.1.]] New Pending Items can be added, but Legal Items cannot be executed and Priority and Focus are not passed or awarded.
- [[##rule 333.1|333.1.]] The player that created the chain becomes the ﬁrst player with Priority.
- [[##rule 337.1.a|337.1.a.]] This process does not pass Priority.
- [[##rule 337.1.c.3|337.1.c.3.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are no Pending Items, the controller of the newest item on the chain gains Priority and becomes the Active Player. Proceed to Step 2: Execute.
- [[##rule 338.1|338.1.]] The player with Priority may do any the following:
- [[##rule 338.1.a.5|338.1.a.5.]] This can be an additional card to the item that Started the Chain in the case of the ﬁrst player with Priority after creating the Chain.
- [[##rule 338.1.c.1|338.1.c.1.]] The player with Priority passes Priority to the next Player in Turn Order. Proceed to Step 3: Pass.
- [[##rule 339.1|339.1.]] If all players have passed Priority without adding any items to the Chain, proceed to Step 4: Resolve.
- [[##rule 339.2|339.2.]] Otherwise, the player with Priority passes Priority to the next Player in Turn Order. Return to Step 3: Execute.
- [[##rule 340.4|340.4.]] If the Chain is not empty and there are no Pending Items, the controller of the newest item on the chain gains Priority. Return to Step 2: Execute.
- [[##rule 346|346.]] When the last item on the chain resolves and the turn returns to an Open State during a Showdown, Focus passes, and the next Player gains both Focus and Priority.
- [[##rule 429.2.a|429.2.a.]] Priority and Focus will not pass from Add abilities being ﬁnalized or resolving, and will resolve before any other outstanding items on the chain are ﬁnalized.
- [[##rule 484.8.a|484.8.a.]] Players may play spells or activate abilities during their Teammate's Turn.In order to do so, their Teammate will invite them to play a spell or activate an ability using their own Priority.
- [[##rule 652.5.c.1|652.5.c.1.]] If the removed player had Priority during a Chain, the next Player in order receives Priority.
- [[##rule 652.5.c.2|652.5.c.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have passed Priority, then the most recent spell or ability on the Chain will resolve with Priority being re-established as appropriate for the state after the resolution of that spell or ability.

####  privacy

**Privacy**

- [[##rule 108.2.d|108.2.d.]] Cards in a player's Trash are Public Information. See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 108.4.d|108.4.d.]] The order of cards in the deck is Secret Information during the course of play.  See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 108.5.d|108.5.d.]] The order of runes in the deck is Secret Information during the course of play.  See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 108.6.e|108.6.e.]] The cards in any player's Banishment are Public Information. See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 128|128.]] Privacy
- [[##rule 128.2|128.2.]] A card will have a different level of Privacy based on where it resides at a given time
- [[##rule 421.4|421.4.]] If a facedown card would change zones or if the game ends, its owner reveals it to all players.  See rule 128. Privacy for more information.

####  private

**Private**

- [[##rule 128.4|128.4.]] Private: This level of Privacy indicates that only the controller of a card on the board or the owner of a card in any other zone may read or look at the face of the card.  Example: Cards in a player's hand are owned by that player. Only that player may read or look at their faces.  Example: If a player controls a facedown card at a battleﬁeld, that player and only that player may read or look at that card's face, regardless of who owns that card.
- [[##rule 129.3|129.3.]] The back side of a card is presented to conceal information for Private and Secret information cards. For example, cards in the Main Deck and cards in hand have their back side presented.
- [[##rule 424.2.a|424.2.a.]] Players may only Reveal cards from Private or Secret zones when instructed to do so by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 424.2.b|424.2.b.]] During the course of a game of Riftbound, a player may choose to show Private information to one or more other players. This does not count as revealing and does not trigger any effects that trigger when cards are revealed.

####  private information

**Private Information**

- [[##rule 108.7.c|108.7.c.]] The cards in a player's hand are Private Information.
- [[##rule 129.4|129.4.]] The term facedown is used to describe the state during regular play of having a card's back side presented on the Board. A facedown card’s front side is considered Private Information.
- [[##rule 422.1.a|422.1.a.]] The player who is performing the action chooses which cards to send to their Trash, and may use Private Information to do so.
- [[##rule 484.8.e|484.8.e.]] Hands are Private Information. Players may show their Private Information to one or more players at any time during play, including their teammate.

####  process of play

**Process Of Play**

- [[##rule 353|353.]] The Process of Play

####  public

**Public**

- [[##rule 128.5|128.5.]] Public: This level of Privacy indicates that any player may read or look at the face of the card.

####  public information

**Public Information**

- [[##rule 107.1.d|107.1.d.]] Permanents and Runes in Bases are Public Information.
- [[##rule 107.2.c|107.2.c.]] Battleﬁelds and permanents at Battleﬁelds are Public Information.
- [[##rule 108.1.b|108.1.b.]] Cards and abilities on the Chain are Public Information.
- [[##rule 108.3.e|108.3.e.]] Cards in a player’s Champion Zone are Public Information.
- [[##rule 108.7.d|108.7.d.]] The number of cards in a player's hand is Public Information.
- [[##rule 109|109.]] All Game Objects in the collective Play Areas are Public Information.
- [[##rule 109.2|109.2.]] The State of all Game Objects in the Play Area is also Public Information.  Examples:   If a Unit is Buffed  If a Gear is Exhausted  Etc.
- [[##rule 130.6|130.6.]] Cards are considered to be Public Information while in this state, even if obscured by other cards in a pile. Example: The Trash is Public Information because all cards there have their front face presented even while stacked.
- [[##rule 729.2|729.2.]] The amount of XP a Player has is Public Information.

###  group Q

####  quick-draw

**Quick-draw**

- [[##rule 819|819.]] Quick-Draw
- [[##rule 819.1|819.1.]] Quick-Draw is a Triggered Ability keyword. It is also a Permissive keyword.
- [[##rule 819.1.a|819.1.a.]] Quick-Draw is present on Gear with Equip abilities.
- [[##rule 819.1.b|819.1.b.]] Cards with Quick-Draw have Reaction inherently.
- [[##rule 819.1.c|819.1.c.]] Quick-Draw allows cards to be played and Attached using Reaction timing.
- [[##rule 819.1.d|819.1.d.]] Quick-Draw is functionally short for “[Reaction]” and “When you play this, attach it to a Unit you control.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 819.2|819.2.]] Multiple instances of Quick-Draw do not trigger separately and have no effect beyond the ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 819.3|819.3.]] Quick-Draw, and whether or not a gear has Quick-Draw, is a characteristic of the Gear and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

###  group R

####  reaction

**Reaction**

- [[##rule 158.2.b|158.2.b.]] Reaction
- [[##rule 158.2.b.3|158.2.b.3.]] This will result in this spell resolving before spells and abilities that are already on the chain. See rule 813. Reaction for more information.
- [[##rule 308.1.a|308.1.a.]] Only cards and abilities with the Action or Reaction keywords can be played or activated in a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 309.1.a|309.1.a.]] Only cards and abilities with the Reaction keyword can be played or activated in a Closed State.
- [[##rule 313.1.a|313.1.a.]] The player with Focus must obey any additional restrictions on which Discretionary Actions may be performed.  Example: A player with Focus may not play spells or activate abilities that don't have the Action or Reaction keywords.
- [[##rule 316.2.b.1|316.2.b.1.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, the Turn Player's teammates may play spells and activate abilities, including ones without Action or Reaction. They can only do so when the Turn Player invites them to do so with their own Priority.
- [[##rule 316.5.c|316.5.c.]] A Showdown is a structured Window of Opportunity where Players may play cards and activate abilities with Action or Reaction. See rule 341. Showdowns for more information.
- [[##rule 338.1.a.2|338.1.a.2.]] A Legally Timed Card would be a Card with Reaction or a card that will have Reaction when played under appropriate circumstances.
- [[##rule 357.1.a|357.1.a.]] During this step, the card's controller can use activated abilities with the Reaction tag that Add resources to add Energy and Power to pay the card's costs.  See rule 164. Rune Pools and rule 429. Add for more information.
- [[##rule 359.3.c|359.3.c.]] Other players have an opportunity to play Reactions before the resolution of spells.  See rule 327. Chains for more information.
- [[##rule 406.4|406.4.]] Other players have an opportunity to play Reactions before the resolution of spells.  See rule 327. Chains for more information.
- [[##rule 429.3|429.3.]] Activated abilities that Add resources and have the Reaction tag can be activated during the playing or resolution of other spells and abilities, any time that those spells or abilities require resources be paid.  Example: A player can add Energy and Power through any means before initiating the process of playing a spell. After initiating that process, in the Pay Costs step, they may activate Add Reactions to add Energy or Power to pay costs.
- [[##rule 441.3.c|441.3.c.]] Moving does not use the Chain, nor is it able to be Reacted to.
- [[##rule 811.6|811.6.]] A card that is Hidden gains Reaction while facedown or played from facedown, and may be played any time a card with Reaction may be played as a result.
- [[##rule 813|813.]] Reaction
- [[##rule 813.1.b|813.1.b.]] Reaction grants the corresponding card or effect all abilities and permissions of Action.
- [[##rule 813.1.c|813.1.c.]] Reaction, additionally, is functionally short for the following:
- [[##rule 819.1.b|819.1.b.]] Cards with Quick-Draw have Reaction inherently.
- [[##rule 819.1.c|819.1.c.]] Quick-Draw allows cards to be played and Attached using Reaction timing.
- [[##rule 819.1.d|819.1.d.]] Quick-Draw is functionally short for “[Reaction]” and “When you play this, attach it to a Unit you control.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 822.1.b|822.1.b.]] It is functionally short for "I may be played to a battleﬁeld where you control Units" and “I have [Reaction] as long as I’m being played to a battleﬁeld where you control Units.”

####  ready

**Ready**

- [[##rule 149.1|149.1.]] Gear enter play Ready.
- [[##rule 315.1.b|315.1.b.]] 1. The Turn Player readies all Game Objects they control that are able to be readied.  See rule 415. Ready for more information.
- [[##rule 414.1.a|414.1.a.]] To mark it, rotate the card 90 degrees opposite of Readying, so that the orientation of the card is lengthwise in front of you.
- [[##rule 415|415.]] Ready
- [[##rule 415.1|415.1.]] Readying is an action that marks a non-spell Game Object on the board as available for action.
- [[##rule 415.1.b|415.1.b.]] A Unit that is already Ready cannot be Readied again.
- [[##rule 415.1.c|415.1.c.]] If a Unit is instructed to be Readied while it is already Ready, nothing additional happens.
- [[##rule 415.2|415.2.]] "Ready" is a state for Game Objects on the board that other game effects and rules can .
- [[##rule 415.3.a|415.3.a.]] A player Readies all non-spell Game Objects they Control during the Ready Step of the Beginning Phase on their turn.
- [[##rule 719.4|719.4.]] The Exhausted and Ready state of the Top-Most card does not affect nor change the status of the Attached cards and vice versa.

####  ready game objects

**Ready Game Objects**

- [[##rule 415.3.b|415.3.b.]] Players may also Ready Game Objects on the board when effects or spells instruct them to do so.

####  recalls

**Recalls**

- [[##rule 149.3|149.3.]] If an unattached Gear is at a Battleﬁeld for any reason during a cleanup, then it is recalled to its controller's Base as a corrective action.  See rule 449. Recalls for more information. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 435.4.a|435.4.a.]] If the Detached card was a Gear and this causes it to become present at a Battleﬁeld, it will be Recalled during the next Cleanup.
- [[##rule 441.1|441.1.]] A Permanent changing its position from any space on the Board to another space on the Board is a Move, unless it is caused by a corrective Recall.  See rule 420. Move for more information.
- [[##rule 442.2.c|442.2.c.]] If an action would require a Move that would cause a Unit to become present in a Location where it cannot move for any reason, such as a Battleﬁeld with two players that are not the controller of the Unit performing this Move action are in a Combat or such a Combat is Staged, it instead Recalls. See rule 449. Recalls for more information.
- [[##rule 450|450.]] A Recall is when a Permanent is relocated from anywhere to its Base without it being a Move.
- [[##rule 451|451.]] Recalls are not Moves.
- [[##rule 451.2|451.2.]] A Recall causes a Permanent to change locations.
- [[##rule 451.3|451.3.]] A Recall cannot be prevented by actions and Game Effects that restrict or block Movement.
- [[##rule 452|452.]] Gear can be Recalled.
- [[##rule 452.1|452.1.]] When an un-attached Gear is created or played at a battleﬁeld, or is at a battleﬁeld for any other reason, it is Recalled to its controller's base during the next Cleanup.  Example: An Equipment is attached to a unit at a battleﬁeld, so the Equipment is present at that battleﬁeld. If the unit dies, the Equipment will be recalled during the next cleanup.
- [[##rule 453.1|453.1.]] Unless otherwise stated by the source of the Recall, Damage, Exhausted Status, Buffed Status, and applied Layer alterations will all remain unaffected by a Recall.
- [[##rule 461.1.a.2|461.1.a.2.]] Insert “3d. Recall Attackers present at the Battleﬁeld if Defenders are still present.” See rule 449. Recalls for more information.

####  recruit token

**Recruit Token**

- [[##rule 184.1|184.1.]] A 1 [M] Recruit token is a domainless unit token with 1 Might and the Recruit tag.

####  recycled

**Recycled**

- [[##rule 160.1.a|160.1.a.]] This means, despite remaining on the Board until Recycled or otherwise removed from the board, it is not a Permanent.
- [[##rule 160.2.b|160.2.b.]] When a Rune is Recycled it is returned to the Rune Deck, not the Main Deck.  See rule 416. Recycle for more information.
- [[##rule 163.2.b.1|163.2.b.1.]] The Power added this way corresponds to the Domain of the Rune that is being Recycled.
- [[##rule 416|416.]] Recycle
- [[##rule 416.1|416.1.]] Recycling cards is the action in which a player takes one or more cards from a speciﬁc zone and then puts it on the bottom of the corresponding deck.
- [[##rule 416.1.a|416.1.a.]] Main Deck cards are Recycled to the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 416.1.b|416.1.b.]] Runes are Recycled to the Rune Deck.
- [[##rule 416.1.c|416.1.c.]] Each player Recycles cards to their own Main Deck and Rune Deck, regardless of which player is instructed to perform the Recycle action.
- [[##rule 416.2.a|416.2.a.]] The player must Recycle cards from the speciﬁed zones when instructed to do so by game effects or costs.
- [[##rule 416.3|416.3.]] When Recycling is listed as a Cost, the action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid.  Example: Vi, Destructive has the ability "Recycle 1 from your trash: Give me +1 [M] this turn." Each time a player activates the ability, they must recycle 1 card from their trash to pay its cost. If they have no cards in their trash, they can't activate the ability, because they can't pay its cost.
- [[##rule 416.4|416.4.]] When Recycling is part of an effect, a player must Recycle as many cards as possible from the speciﬁed zone or zones.
- [[##rule 416.5|416.5.]] If 2 or more cards are Recycled to the Main Deck simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in a random order.  Example: Garbage Grabber has the ability "Recycle 3 from your trash, [1], [E]: Draw " To pay the cost of activating this ability, its controller chooses 3 cards from their trash and places them on the bottom of their Main Deck in a random order.
- [[##rule 416.5.a|416.5.a.]] If 2 or more cards are Recycled to the Rune Deck simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in the order of their owner's choosing.
- [[##rule 416.6|416.6.]] This action, when instructed, is sometimes formatted as "Recycle X from [Zone]." That means to take X cards of the instructed player's choice from the relevant zone and recycle them.  Example: Dr. Mundo, Expert has the ability "At the start of your Beginning Phase, recycle 3 from your trash." As that ability resolves, its controller recycles 3 cards from their trash. If there are fewer than 3 cards in that player's trash, they recycle as many as they can.
- [[##rule 424.4.a|424.4.a.]] While cards are Revealed, those cards can be further manipulated, or accessed. They can even have their destination modiﬁed for when the Reveal ends.  Example: "Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck. Put one into your hand and Recycle the other" would be executed by taking the top two cards from your Main Deck to the table, and once every player present has had a chance to understand them you would make the selection of one of them to add to your hand. The one you did not select would then be Recycled to the bottom of the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 431.2.b|431.2.b.]] Recycles their trash into their Main Deck.  Reminder: When multiple cards are Recycled to the Main Deck at the same time, those cards must be randomized
- [[##rule 436.1|436.1.]] Predicting a card is the act of looking at a single card from the top of the Main Deck and choosing whether or not to Recycle it.
- [[##rule 436.1.b|436.1.b.]] The Player who performs the game action may rearrange any cards not Recycled in this way.

####  recycles

**Recycles**

- [[##rule 118.3|118.3.]] Finally, that player Recycles the cards that were set aside.  See rule 416. Recycle for more information.
- [[##rule 416.1.c|416.1.c.]] Each player Recycles cards to their own Main Deck and Rune Deck, regardless of which player is instructed to perform the Recycle action.
- [[##rule 436.1.a|436.1.a.]] When more than one card is Predicted, the Predicting player looks at that many cards and Recycles any number of them.

####  reflection token

**Reflection Token**

- [[##rule 184.6|184.6.]] A 0 [M] Reflection token is a domainless unit token with 0 Might.

####  reflexive triggers

**Reflexive Triggers**

- [[##rule 387|387.]] Reflexive Triggers are a type of Triggered Ability that create one or more Chain Items when their condition is met.
- [[##rule 387.1|387.1.]] Reflexive Triggers can be recognized by the phrase “Do this:” or “Do one of the following:”.
- [[##rule 387.1.a|387.1.a.]] “Do this” can be followed by “N times.” The Reflexive Trigger will thus be added to the chain N times when its condition is met.
- [[##rule 387.2|387.2.]] Reflexive Triggers will be preceded by their conditions, if any. If no condition is present in the ability then the Reflexive Trigger will always be added to the Chain.
- [[##rule 387.3|387.3.]] If present, the Condition of a Reflexive Trigger will follow the same format as a Triggered Ability.
- [[##rule 388|388.]] Reflexive Triggers use the Chain.
- [[##rule 388.2|388.2.]] If a Reflexive Trigger creates more than one Pending Item it creates them all in order, but does not go beyond the ﬁrst step of adding them to the Chain.  See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.

####  reminder text

**Reminder Text**

- [[##rule 135.2.d|135.2.d.]] Reminder Text

####  reminder: lethal damage is non-zero damage equaling or exceeding the might of a unit

**Reminder: Lethal Damage Is Non-zero Damage Equaling Or Exceeding The Might Of A Unit**

- [[##rule 460.2.c.2|460.2.c.2.]] Abilities or effects may influence the order in which damage is assigned. Reminder: Lethal Damage is non-zero damage equaling or exceeding the Might of a Unit.

####  removal of a player

**Removal Of A Player**

- [[##rule 651.2|651.2.]] If more than one player remains after a concession, follow the steps for the Removal of a Player.
- [[##rule 652|652.]] If the game continues, follow these steps for Removal of a Player.

####  repeat

**Repeat**

- [[##rule 820|820.]] Repeat
- [[##rule 820.1|820.1.]] Repeat is an Optional Additional Cost keyword.
- [[##rule 820.1.a|820.1.a.]] Repeat is present on Spells.
- [[##rule 820.1.b|820.1.b.]] Repeat is an optional cost that a player may pay to execute the effect of their spells a second time.
- [[##rule 820.1.c|820.1.c.]] Repeat is formatted as “Repeat [Cost]”
- [[##rule 820.1.c.2|820.1.c.2.]] If a spell has more than one instance of Repeat, each Cost may be paid or not paid individually.
- [[##rule 820.1.c.3|820.1.c.3.]] Each Repeat Cost can be paid only a single time.
- [[##rule 820.1.d|820.1.d.]] Repeat is functionally short for “You may pay [Cost] as an additional cost as you play this spell. If you do, execute the instructions of this spell one additional time.”
- [[##rule 820.2|820.2.]] When a spell’s effect is performed an additional time with Repeat, choices must be made at the usual time during the Make Relevant Choices step of Playing a Card. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.
- [[##rule 820.3|820.3.]] Multiple instances of Repeat can be paid for separately. The spell’s instructions  will be executed an additional time for each instance of Repeat that is paid for.
- [[##rule 820.4|820.4.]] Repeat, and whether or not a spell has Repeat, is a characteristic of the Spell and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.

####  repeatedly

**Repeatedly**

- [[##rule 471|471.]] The layers are applied repeatedly until all effects operating on objects have been applied once and no changes have been processed.

####  replace

**Replace**

- [[##rule 438|438.]] Replace
- [[##rule 438.1|438.1.]] Replacing is the act of Creating a token in the place of another card or token without playing it while inheriting all effects or statuses of the game object it replaced.
- [[##rule 438.2|438.2.]] Replacing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 438.2.a|438.2.a.]] The player may Replace cards and tokens when instructed to do so by other game effects.
- [[##rule 438.3.a|438.3.a.]] The [X] is the target to be Replaced.
- [[##rule 438.3.b|438.3.b.]] The [Y] is the object that will Replace the target.
- [[##rule 438.4|438.4.]] Replacing is not a subset of Banishing.
- [[##rule 438.5|438.5.]] The card or token that is Replaced is placed in Banishment.
- [[##rule 438.5.a|438.5.a.]] While it resides in Banishment, it is considered to have been Replaced and not Banished.
- [[##rule 438.6|438.6.]] If a token is Replaced it will stop existing once it begins its occupancy in Banishment.
- [[##rule 438.6.a|438.6.a.]] This does not invalidate the token created, or the act of Replacement.
- [[##rule 438.7|438.7.]] Tokens that have been Created through a Replace action can be instructed to be “Swapped back.”
- [[##rule 438.7.a|438.7.a.]] “Swapping Back” is an extension of the Replace action.
- [[##rule 652.2.a|652.2.a.]] If it was in use, Replace it with a token battleﬁeld with no abilities.
- [[##rule 652.2.b|652.2.b.]] Any units or hidden cards there do not move and are otherwise unaffected by this process. See rule 438. Replace for more information.
- [[##rule 725.1|725.1.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Attaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Attaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Attaches.
- [[##rule 725.2|725.2.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Detaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Detaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Detaches.

####  replacement effect

**Replacement Effect**

- [[##rule 157.2|157.2.]] If a later part of a spell applies a Replacement Effect that alters earlier parts of the spell, apply those replacement effects as appropriate. Example: A spell says "Choose a unit. Kill it the next time it takes damage this turn." and "[Legion] — Kill it now instead. (Get the effect if you've played another card this turn.)" If the Legion condition is satisﬁed, the unit is killed immediately and the instruction to kill it the next time it takes damage is ignored, even if the unit remains on the board somehow. See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information.
- [[##rule 361.1|361.1.]] An Ability has multiple structures.  -Passive Abilities  -Replacement Effects  -Activated Abilities  -Triggered Abilities  -Delayed Abilities
- [[##rule 368.1|368.1.]] Passive Abilities can be Replacement Effects.
- [[##rule 369|369.]] Replacement Effects intercede during the execution of a Game Effect and alter its execution.
- [[##rule 369.1|369.1.]] A Replacement Effect can usually be identiﬁed by the presence of the terms “would” or "instead."  Example: Zhonya's Hourglass reads "The next time a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Heal that unit, exhaust it, and recall it." This is a replacement effect that alters the execution of any Game Effect that would kill a friendly unit.
- [[##rule 369.2|369.2.]] Some Game Actions are themselves Replacement Effects. Example: Burning Out is a replacement effect. Example: Preventing Damage is a replacement effect.
- [[##rule 370|370.]] A Replacement Effect can alter the typical flow of play, including other cards' executions.
- [[##rule 370.1|370.1.]] Replacement Effects apply to any event or instruction that qualiﬁes for their application. A Replacement Effect will specify the circumstances by which an event or instruction will qualify to be replaced.
- [[##rule 370.1.a|370.1.a.]] When a Replacement Effect applies, it replaces the qualifying event with one or more Game Actions or events, or the qualifying instruction with another instruction.
- [[##rule 370.2|370.2.]] A Replacement Effect can only be applied once to an event, or to any Game Actions or events that replace that event. Example: A player plays a spell that reads “gear you control become 1 [M] gear units this turn.” They control two copies of Zhonya’s Hourglass when the spell resolves. If one of those copies is killed, both of their Replacement Effects will be applied. Whichever is applied ﬁrst, that Replacement Effect can’t be applied again. When it is applied, it kills its source, which creates an event the other can apply its Replacement Effect to. Once they’ve both applied their Replacement Effect to the original death event and the event that replaced it, they cannot go any further. At that point, whichever Zhonya’s Hourglass applied its Replacement Effect last will die.
- [[##rule 370.3|370.3.]] If a Game Object has a Replacement Effect that is active in a speciﬁc zone, it is evaluated and subsequently applied if it enters that zone before an event occurs that it could replace.  Example: A unit that reads “if a unit you control would die, you may banish me from your trash instead. If you do, heal that unit, exhaust it and recall it.” The ﬁrst unit dies simultaneously with a 1 [M] Recruit token. It does not enter the trash before the Recruit dies, so it will not be able to replace its death.
- [[##rule 371|371.]] Some Replacement Effects will begin with “once each turn.”
- [[##rule 371.1|371.1.]] When an event the Replacement Effect could apply to occurs, the player who controls the Replacement Effect may choose to apply it to the event.
- [[##rule 372|372.]] If more than one Replacement Effect applies to the same event being executed, then the owner of the object being acted on determines the order the Replacement Effects will apply.
- [[##rule 372.1|372.1.]] If it is a player being acted on, that player decides the order the Replacement Effects will apply.
- [[##rule 372.2|372.2.]] If the affected object is an Uncontrolled Battleﬁeld then the Current Turn Player decides the order the Replacement Effects will apply.
- [[##rule 373|373.]] If more than one event occurs simultaneously that Replacement Effects could apply to, each event is treated separately and individually for the purposes of Replacement Effects, and Replacement Effects with the same controller are applied in the order of their controller’s choosing. Example: Two units controlled by the same player die in the same cleanup. That player also controls Zhonya’s Hourglass. They must decide which event to apply Zhonya’s Hourglass to ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 373.1|373.1.]] Although these events are simultaneous, the applied Replacement Effects are ordered. If multiple applied Replacement Effects with different controllers would execute simultaneously, they execute in turn order.
- [[##rule 374|374.]] A Replacement Effect’s controller is the player that controls the source of the Replacement Effect.
- [[##rule 375|375.]] If an event that a Replacement Effect applies to would be modiﬁed by a Game Effect, or the results of that event would be modiﬁed by a Game Action, the Replacement Effect will inherit those modiﬁcations. Example: Treasure Hunter reads “When I move, play a Gold gear token exhausted.” A Replacement Effect that says “if you would play a token gear, play that token and an additional copy instead” is applied to the event of the Gold gear token being played. The additional copy will also be exhausted, as it inherits the “exhausted” modiﬁcation. Example: Another Replacement Effect says “if you would play a token, draw 1 instead.” The modiﬁcation cannot apply, so we ignore it. Example: A spell reads “play a ready 3 [M] Mech token. Then do this: Give it Temporary.” A Replacement Effect that says “if you would play a unit token, play that token and a 1 [M] Recruit token instead” is applied to the event of the Mech token being made. The Recruit token enters ready and is given Temporary.
- [[##rule 390.3|390.3.]] Delayed Replacements are Replacement Effects that can be recognized by specifying the effect they are replacing at a speciﬁc time, or “the [Nth] time” in the description of the effect as it resolves.
- [[##rule 431.5|431.5.]] Burning Out is a Replacement Effect.  See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information.
- [[##rule 437.7|437.7.]] Prevent is a Delayed Replacement Effect. See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information. See rule 389. Delayed Abilities for more information.

####  resolution

**Resolution**

- [[##rule 321.1|321.1.]] If an event occurs during the Resolution of a Chain Item that qualiﬁes for a Cleanup, that Cleanup will be made an Outstanding Task.
- [[##rule 324.1|324.1.]] When a Special Cleanup is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a Combat Cleanup is invoked, the Combat section deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 461. The Resolution Step for more information. Example: When an End of Turn Cleanup is invoked, the End of Turn Phase subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 317. The Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 460.3|460.3.]] 2. Skip the FEPR process and proceed to the Resolution Step.

####  resolving

**Resolving**

- [[##rule 157|157.]] When a spell is successfully played, a player executes the rules text of the spell. This is called Resolving the spell.
- [[##rule 157.1|157.1.]] Spells have their rules text executed from top to bottom when they are Resolved.
- [[##rule 157.3|157.3.]] While a spell or ability on the chain is Resolving, no other spells or abilities can be ﬁnalized on the chain or resolved, including triggered abilities or game effects that would occur as a result of the execution of the spell.
- [[##rule 320|320.]] While a Cleanup is occurring, Chain Items cannot be Resolved.
- [[##rule 321|321.]] Similarly, while Chain Items are Resolving, a Cleanup cannot occur.

####  responsibility

**Responsibility**

- [[##rule 411|411.]] Responsibility

####  reveal

**Reveal**

- [[##rule 424|424.]] Reveal
- [[##rule 424.1|424.1.]] Revealing is the act of presenting a card to all players from a zone that one or more players do not have access to the information of.
- [[##rule 424.1.a|424.1.a.]] Revealed is a temporary state and is not a zone.
- [[##rule 424.1.a.1|424.1.a.1.]] Other cards, including the card being revealed, can  the act of being Revealed.
- [[##rule 424.1.a.2|424.1.a.2.]] Cards remain in the zone they are being Revealed from. Example: If a card is being Revealed from the top of a player's Main Deck, it is still the top card of that player's Main Deck.
- [[##rule 424.1.b|424.1.b.]] Unless otherwise described, Revealed cards do nothing else beyond become temporarily known information to all players.
- [[##rule 424.2|424.2.]] Revealing is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 424.2.a|424.2.a.]] Players may only Reveal cards from Private or Secret zones when instructed to do so by Game Effects.
- [[##rule 424.4|424.4.]] Game Effects can manipulate or modify the cards Revealed while they are Revealed
- [[##rule 424.4.a|424.4.a.]] While cards are Revealed, those cards can be further manipulated, or accessed. They can even have their destination modiﬁed for when the Reveal ends.  Example: "Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck. Put one into your hand and Recycle the other" would be executed by taking the top two cards from your Main Deck to the table, and once every player present has had a chance to understand them you would make the selection of one of them to add to your hand. The one you did not select would then be Recycled to the bottom of the Main Deck.
- [[##rule 431.1.c|431.1.c.]] If an instruction directs a player to look at or reveal cards in excess to the number of cards in a player’s Main Deck, that player looks at or Reveals as many as possible, but does not Burn Out, then proceeds with the rest of the instruction.
- [[##rule 484.8.e.1|484.8.e.1.]] Revealing Cards is still a game action and cannot be done unless instructed.  See rule 424. Reveal for more information.

####  revealing cards

**Revealing Cards**

- [[##rule 484.8.e.1|484.8.e.1.]] Revealing Cards is still a game action and cannot be done unless instructed.  See rule 424. Reveal for more information.

####  riftbound

**Riftbound**

- [[##rule 129.1|129.1.]] The back side of a card is the side with the Riftbound logo.
- [[##rule 178|178.]] Tokens can be represented by anything. Printed tokens are included in Riftbound booster packs, but they are not required to play a token.
- [[##rule 424.2.b|424.2.b.]] During the course of a game of Riftbound, a player may choose to show Private information to one or more other players. This does not count as revealing and does not trigger any effects that trigger when cards are revealed.
- [[##rule 477|477.]] There are multiple methods of playing Riftbound.
- [[##rule 702.1|702.1.]] Buffs can be tracked with a buff reminder card from a Riftbound booster pack or with any spare object in your surroundings.

####  rules text

**Rules Text**

- [[##rule 135|135.]] Rules Text
- [[##rule 135.1|135.1.]] All cards have a section that describes how they affect the game. This section is known as the Rules Text of the card.
- [[##rule 135.4|135.4.]] A card’s printed Rules Text is Inactive while that card is Attached to another card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 135.4.a|135.4.a.]] The presence of text, rules, Keywords, and other effects can still be d and detected by other game effects, even while Rules Text is Inactive.
- [[##rule 135.4.b|135.4.b.]] Any granted or appended Rules Text on a card is still Active even if that card is Attached to another card.
- [[##rule 136.1|136.1.]] Some cards have a separate section of text below the Rules Text. This is referred to as the Effect Text.
- [[##rule 136.2.c|136.2.c.]] The abilities in the Effect Text section of a card are appended to the Rules Text of the card to which the card with the Effect Text is Attached.
- [[##rule 434.1.c|434.1.c.]] The Top-Most card has all Effect Text of all cards Attached to it appended to its Rules Text.
- [[##rule 434.1.e|434.1.e.]] Attaching one or more cards will cause those cards’ Rules Text to become Inactive for as long as they remain Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 435.1.c|435.1.c.]] The card being Detached has its Effect Text become Inactive and its Rules Text cease being Inactive.
- [[##rule 435.1.d|435.1.d.]] The Top-Most Card ceases to have the Effect Text of the card being Detached appended to its Rules Text.
- [[##rule 475.2|475.2.]] When Rules Text becomes Inactive for any reason, it loses its Timestamp. When it ceases to be Inactive, a new Timestamp is established.
- [[##rule 718.2|718.2.]] While in this state, the card’s printed Rules Text is Inactive. See rule 720. Inactive for more information.
- [[##rule 718.3|718.3.]] While in this state, Abilities in the card’s Effect Text are appended to the Rules Text of the Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 718.5.g|718.5.g.]] An Attached card still appends the abilities in its Effect Text to the Rules Text of the Top-Most card and modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by its Might Bonus.
- [[##rule 719.1|719.1.]] The Effect Text of all cards Attached to this card are appended to the Rules Text of this card for as long as they remain Attached.
- [[##rule 723|723.]] Rules Text is never Inactive by default.
- [[##rule 818.5.a|818.5.a.]] Whether or not a Gear has Equip may be d even if the Rules Text of the Gear is Inactive. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 821.1.c|821.1.c.]] Weaponmaster is functionally short for: “When you play me, you may choose a Card you control with the Equipment tag. Necessary portions of its Rules Text are no longer Inactive if they are currently Inactive. Pay the cost of its Equip ability, reduced by [A], to attach it to this unit.” See rule 716. Attachment for more information.

####  rune

**Rune**

- [[##rule 103.3.a|103.3.a.]] 12 Rune Cards
- [[##rule 107.1.c|107.1.c.]] Permanents and Runes controlled by a player reside in that player's Base.
- [[##rule 107.1.d|107.1.d.]] Permanents and Runes in Bases are Public Information.
- [[##rule 133.5.a|133.5.a.]] Runes
- [[##rule 159|159.]] Runes
- [[##rule 160|160.]] Rune is a Card Type.
- [[##rule 160.1|160.1.]] A Rune is not a Main Deck card.
- [[##rule 160.2|160.2.]] Runes are kept in the Rune Deck.
- [[##rule 160.2.a|160.2.a.]] Exactly 12 Rune cards chosen during Deck Construction.  See rule 103.3. Rune Deck for more information.
- [[##rule 160.2.b|160.2.b.]] When a Rune is Recycled it is returned to the Rune Deck, not the Main Deck.  See rule 416. Recycle for more information.
- [[##rule 161|161.]] Runes produce the resources needed to pay costs.
- [[##rule 162|162.]] Runes produce Energy and Power.
- [[##rule 162.2.a.1|162.2.a.1.]] Power's Domain usually corresponds to the Domain of the Rune that produced it.
- [[##rule 163.2.b.1|163.2.b.1.]] The Power added this way corresponds to the Domain of the Rune that is being Recycled.
- [[##rule 188.3|188.3.]] For Permanents and Runes, when they Enter the Board, that player is assigned as that Game Object's Controller.
- [[##rule 323.7|323.7.]] 5. Recall all Unattached non-Unit Gear at Battleﬁelds, and all Permanents and Runes in Bases other than their controller’s. Remove all Hidden cards from all Battleﬁelds that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's Trash.
- [[##rule 335|335.]] Whenever a Player takes one or more actions that incur Tasks they should refer to the process of HOT FEPR: Handle Outstanding Tasks; then Finalize, Execute, Pass, Resolve.
- [[##rule 416.1.b|416.1.b.]] Runes are Recycled to the Rune Deck.
- [[##rule 430.1|430.1.]] Channeling is the action of taking one or more Runes from the top of a player's Rune Deck and putting them on the board.

####  rune deck

**Rune Deck**

- [[##rule 103.3|103.3.]] Rune Deck
- [[##rule 108.5|108.5.]] Rune Deck Zones
- [[##rule 108.5.a|108.5.a.]] Each player has their own Rune Deck Zone.
- [[##rule 108.5.b|108.5.b.]] The space for the player's Rune Deck.
- [[##rule 115.2|115.2.]] The Rune Deck is placed in the Rune Deck Zone.
- [[##rule 127.1|127.1.]] For gameplay purposes, a card's Owner is the player who brought it into the game, either as their Champion Legend, one of their Battleﬁelds, or part of their Main Deck or Rune Deck. The legal owner of a card doesn't matter during gameplay.  Example: Bo didn't bring a deck, so Alice loans him a deck. During the game, Bo is considered the owner of those cards, even though legally they belong to Alice.
- [[##rule 129.2|129.2.]] There is a unique pattern of back side for each of the three categories of card: Main Deck cards, Rune Deck cards, and Battleﬁelds and Champion Legends.
- [[##rule 133.5|133.5.]] Rune Deck Cards begin the game in the Rune Deck.
- [[##rule 160.2|160.2.]] Runes are kept in the Rune Deck.
- [[##rule 160.2.a|160.2.a.]] Exactly 12 Rune cards chosen during Deck Construction.  See rule 103.3. Rune Deck for more information.
- [[##rule 160.2.b|160.2.b.]] When a Rune is Recycled it is returned to the Rune Deck, not the Main Deck.  See rule 416. Recycle for more information.
- [[##rule 315.3.b|315.3.b.]] 1. The Turn Player channels 2 runes from their Rune Deck.  See rule 430. Channel for more information.
- [[##rule 315.3.b.1|315.3.b.1.]] If there are fewer than 2 runes in the Rune Deck, they channel as many as possible.
- [[##rule 416.1.b|416.1.b.]] Runes are Recycled to the Rune Deck.
- [[##rule 416.1.c|416.1.c.]] Each player Recycles cards to their own Main Deck and Rune Deck, regardless of which player is instructed to perform the Recycle action.
- [[##rule 416.5.a|416.5.a.]] If 2 or more cards are Recycled to the Rune Deck simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in the order of their owner's choosing.
- [[##rule 430.1|430.1.]] Channeling is the action of taking one or more Runes from the top of a player's Rune Deck and putting them on the board.

####  rune pool

**Rune Pool**

- [[##rule 131.1|131.1.]] Main Deck cards have a Cost, listed in the upper left corner of the front face of the card. See rule 164. Rune Pools for more information.
- [[##rule 135.2.e.5.b|135.2.e.5.b.]] When Added to a player’s Rune Pool, [A] can be spent to pay a Power cost of any Domain.
- [[##rule 165|165.]] The Rune Pool is a conceptual collection of a player's available Energy and Power available to pay Costs.
- [[##rule 165.1|165.1.]] When a card adds Energy or Power, it is added to the controlling player's Rune Pool.
- [[##rule 165.2|165.2.]] Players must ﬁrst add Energy and Power to their Rune Pool in order to be able to spend it to play cards or pay for Abilities with costs.
- [[##rule 166|166.]] Every player's Rune Pool empties at the end of each player's draw phase and the end of each player's turn.
- [[##rule 167|167.]] All Abilities that include the action "Add" are abilities that are adding Energy or Power to the Rune Pool. See rule 429. Add for more information.
- [[##rule 315.4.d|315.4.d.]] 1. Each player's Rune Pool empties. Any unspent Energy and Power are lost. See rule 164. Rune Pools for more information.
- [[##rule 317.2.d|317.2.d.]] Insert “2e. Each player’s Rune Pool empties. Any unspent Energy and Power are lost.”
- [[##rule 357.1.a|357.1.a.]] During this step, the card's controller can use activated abilities with the Reaction tag that Add resources to add Energy and Power to pay the card's costs.  See rule 164. Rune Pools and rule 429. Add for more information.
- [[##rule 429.1|429.1.]] Adding is the action of putting resources into a player's Rune Pool.

###  group S

####  same layer

**Same Layer**

- [[##rule 473|473.]] If more than one effect applies to the same Game Object in the Same Layer, or to each other in the same layer, then both effects will apply but their order may be determined by Dependency.

####  sand soldier token

**Sand Soldier Token**

- [[##rule 184.3|184.3.]] A 2 [M] Sand Soldier token is a domainless unit token with 2 Might and the Shurima tag.

####  score abilities

**Score Abilities**

- [[##rule 466.2|466.2.]] Trigger Score abilities at the Battleﬁeld that Scored.

####  scoring

**Scoring**

- [[##rule 315.2.b.2|315.2.b.2.]] 1. The Turn Player Holds all Battleﬁelds they Control. See rule 462. Scoring for more information.
- [[##rule 462|462.]] Scoring
- [[##rule 463|463.]] Scoring is the act of a Player gaining a point through the process of seizing or maintaining control over Battleﬁelds.
- [[##rule 463.1|463.1.]] Every instance of Scoring is also an instance of Gaining points
- [[##rule 464|464.]] A player Scores in one of two ways:
- [[##rule 464.1|464.1.]] Conquer: A player gains Control of a Battleﬁeld they did not yet Score this turn.
- [[##rule 464.1.a|464.1.a.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds under the Control of a teammate during the Beginning Phase are also disqualiﬁed from being Scored through Conquer by any means.
- [[##rule 465|465.]] A player may only Score, from either method, once per Battleﬁeld per turn.
- [[##rule 466|466.]] When a player Scores, two things occur:
- [[##rule 466.1.b|466.1.b.]] When a player tries to Gain a Point through a Score, and their current Point Total is 1 point from the Victory Score of the Mode of Play or higher, the following occurs:
- [[##rule 466.1.b.1|466.1.b.1.]] If the player has Scored through Hold, that player Gains the Winning Point.
- [[##rule 466.1.b.2|466.1.b.2.]] If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has Scored every Battleﬁeld through either method this turn, that player Gains the Winning Point. If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has not Scored every Battleﬁeld this turn, that player draws a card.
- [[##rule 466.2|466.2.]] Trigger Score abilities at the Battleﬁeld that Scored.
- [[##rule 466.2.c|466.2.c.]] These will only trigger when the Battleﬁeld is Scored; I.E. These cannot be triggered more than once per turn for a player.
- [[##rule 484.8.f.1|484.8.f.1.]] When scoring the Final Point from Conquer, a player must Score each Battleﬁeld in the same turn, excepting any that were occupied by their ally during that turn’s Beginning Phase.

####  seating

**Seating**

- [[##rule 116.1.b|116.1.b.]] If not otherwise speciﬁed, Seating then determines the sequence, play proceeding clockwise from the First Player.

####  secret

**Secret**

- [[##rule 128.3|128.3.]] Secret: This level of Privacy indicates that no player may read or look at the face of the card.
- [[##rule 129.3|129.3.]] The back side of a card is presented to conceal information for Private and Secret information cards. For example, cards in the Main Deck and cards in hand have their back side presented.
- [[##rule 424.2.a|424.2.a.]] Players may only Reveal cards from Private or Secret zones when instructed to do so by Game Effects.

####  secret information

**Secret Information**

- [[##rule 103.2.e|103.2.e.]] During Gameplay, the Main Deck is Secret Information.
- [[##rule 108.4.d|108.4.d.]] The order of cards in the deck is Secret Information during the course of play.  See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 108.5.d|108.5.d.]] The order of runes in the deck is Secret Information during the course of play.  See rule 128. Privacy for more information.

####  setup

**Setup**

- [[##rule 104|104.]] Setup
- [[##rule 128.1|128.1.]] A card will always exist in one of the many Zones described during Setup.
- [[##rule 478.5|478.5.]] Setup: Any changes to initial setup required for this mode.
- [[##rule 480.5|480.5.]] Setup: Each player randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously in the Battleﬁeld Zone.
- [[##rule 481.5|481.5.]] Setup: Each player selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are set aside and will not be used for this round of play. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously in the Battleﬁeld Zone. After this game, the Battleﬁelds that were used are to be removed and not selected again for this Match. One of the remaining Battleﬁelds that were set aside must be chosen instead.
- [[##rule 482.5|482.5.]] Setup: Each player randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are discarded and will not be used for this game. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously between the three Players before play and will be used for this game.
- [[##rule 483.5|483.5.]] Setup: Each player who is not going ﬁrst randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battleﬁelds. The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected Battleﬁelds are placed simultaneously between the players before play and will be used for this game.
- [[##rule 484.5|484.5.]] Setup:

####  shield

**Shield**

- [[##rule 814|814.]] Shield

####  showdown

**Showdown**

- [[##rule 144.1.c|144.1.c.]] This action cannot be performed during a Showdown or Combat.
- [[##rule 145.2|145.2.]] The Activated Ability of Units may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 150.2|150.2.]] The Activated Ability of Gear may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 154|154.]] A spell can be played during an Open State outside of Showdowns on its controller's turn.
- [[##rule 158.2.a.1|158.2.a.1.]] This indicates that, in addition to being able to be played during an Open State, this spell may also be played during Open States during Showdowns. See rule 806. Action for more information.
- [[##rule 187.4.b|187.4.b.]] While a Combat or Showdown is ongoing at a Battleﬁeld, Control of that Battleﬁeld cannot change until instructed by steps of the Combat or Showdown.
- [[##rule 187.4.c|187.4.c.]] If a player has no Units at a Battleﬁeld and the turn is in an Open state, they lose Control of that Battleﬁeld in the following cleanup, unless there is a Combat or Showdown ongoing there.
- [[##rule 308|308.]] At any given time, the turn is in either a Neutral State or a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 308.1|308.1.]] If a Showdown or Combat is in progress, the turn is in a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 308.1.a|308.1.a.]] Only cards and abilities with the Action or Reaction keywords can be played or activated in a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 308.2|308.2.]] If no Showdown or Combat is in progress, the turn is in a Neutral State.
- [[##rule 310.1|310.1.]] Neutral Open: There is no Showdown or Combat in progress and no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.2|310.2.]] Neutral Closed: There is no Showdown or Combat in progress and a Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.3|310.3.]] Showdown Open: A Showdown or Combat is in progress and no Chain exists.
- [[##rule 310.4|310.4.]] Showdown Closed: A Showdown or Combat is in progress and a Chain exists.
- [[##rule 312.2.b|312.2.b.]] When the turn is in a Showdown State and they gain Focus.
- [[##rule 316.4.f|316.4.f.]] Combat will also include a Showdown.
- [[##rule 316.5|316.5.]] Showdowns
- [[##rule 316.5.a|316.5.a.]] A Showdown occurs when a Combat occurs.
- [[##rule 316.5.b|316.5.b.]] A Showdown is marked as Staged at a Battleﬁeld when the Contested status is applied to a Battleﬁeld with no current controller.
- [[##rule 316.5.b.1.a|316.5.b.1.a.]] These Showdowns are called Non-Combat Showdowns. During the proceedings of a Non-Combat Showdown, units controlled by a different player may become present at the Battleﬁeld where the Showdown is ongoing. This will cause the Showdown to become a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 316.5.c|316.5.c.]] A Showdown is a structured Window of Opportunity where Players may play cards and activate abilities with Action or Reaction. See rule 341. Showdowns for more information.
- [[##rule 323.6|323.6.]] 4. If the turn is in an Open State, Battleﬁelds with no Units occupying them and no Showdown or Combat ongoing become Uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 323.8|323.8.]] 6. Mark a Showdown as Staged at each Battleﬁeld that Contested was applied to.
- [[##rule 323.8.a|323.8.a.]] The Showdown remains Staged at each Battleﬁeld that is Contested and has units present controlled by the player that applied Contested.
- [[##rule 323.11|323.11.]] 8. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and one or more Showdowns are Staged, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. A Showdown begins there.
- [[##rule 323.12|323.12.]] 8a. If a Showdown and Combat are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player chooses to initiate the Showdown there, the Showdown will open as a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 323.14|323.14.]] 9a. If the current state is Showdown Open State and Combat is Staged at a Battleﬁeld where there is a Non-Combat Showdown ongoing, that Showdown becomes a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 326.2|326.2.]] During a Showdown
- [[##rule 337.1.c.1.a|337.1.c.1.a.]] If this occurs during a Showdown, the next player in turn order gains Focus.
- [[##rule 340.2.a|340.2.a.]] If this occurs during a Showdown, focus passes to the next player in turn order.
- [[##rule 341|341.]] Showdowns
- [[##rule 342|342.]] A Showdown is a Window of Opportunity in which Players have an Open State in which they may play Spells in an alternating fashion.
- [[##rule 343|343.]] The State of the turn is partially determined by whether or not a Showdown or Combat is in progress.
- [[##rule 343.1|343.1.]] The turn is said to be in a Showdown State if a Showdown or Combat is in progress.
- [[##rule 343.1.a|343.1.a.]] Cards of all Categories, by default, cannot be played during a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 343.1.b|343.1.b.]] Card abilities, by default, cannot be played during a Showdown State.
- [[##rule 343.2|343.2.]] The turn is said to be in a Neutral State if no Showdown or Combat is in progress.
- [[##rule 344|344.]] A Showdown begins when Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the turn is in a Neutral Open State.
- [[##rule 344.1|344.1.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested between two players, then a Showdown will be opened as the ﬁrst step of Combat.  See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 344.2|344.2.]] If Control of a Battleﬁeld is Contested and the Battleﬁeld in question is uncontrolled when it becomes Contested, a Showdown is opened during the Cleanup at the end of the action that caused the Battleﬁeld to become Contested.
- [[##rule 345|345.]] As a Showdown begins, the player who applied Contested status to the Battleﬁeld gains Focus.
- [[##rule 346|346.]] When the last item on the chain resolves and the turn returns to an Open State during a Showdown, Focus passes, and the next Player gains both Focus and Priority.
- [[##rule 347|347.]] During a Showdown, the player with Focus may do one of the following:
- [[##rule 347.3.a|347.3.a.]] If all Players have passed once in sequence, the Showdown ends.
- [[##rule 348|348.]] If all players pass Focus without playing a spell or activating an ability, then the Showdown Closes.
- [[##rule 446|446.]] Units may cause a Showdown without a Combat when they Move.
- [[##rule 446.1|446.1.]] A Showdown is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested while it has no Units present from any player other than those that just moved.
- [[##rule 447.1|447.1.]] A Combat is opened when a Move causes a Battleﬁeld to become Contested and Units controlled by opposing players, or when a Move causes Units controlled by opposing players to become present in the same Battleﬁeld where a Showdown is ongoing. See rule 454. Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 455|455.]] A Combat occurs when a Cleanup occurs, there are no items on the Chain, there is a staged Combat at a Battleﬁeld, and no Showdown or Combat is ongoing at any other Battleﬁeld. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
