- [[##rule 455.1|455.1.]] If there is an ongoing Showdown at the Battleﬁeld where the Combat is staged, that Showdown will become a Combat Showdown and a Combat will be initiated there.
- [[##rule 456.3|456.3.]] If a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown, it will open as a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 459.1|459.1.]] Combat will open in one of two ways: when a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown; or when the turn is in a Showdown Open State and a Combat is staged at the Battleﬁeld where the current Showdown is ongoing. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 460.2|460.2.]] 1. When the Showdown closes, Attackers and Defenders resolve Combat Damage at the Battleﬁeld that was attacked, using their current Might.
- [[##rule 652.5.b.1|652.5.b.1.]] If the removed player had Focus in a Showdown, the next Player in order receives Focus.
- [[##rule 652.5.b.2|652.5.b.2.]] If the player being removed creates a state where all Players have Passed their Focus, the Showdown ends and play proceeds as necessary, E.G. Combat is resolved or a Cleanup is completed.
- [[##rule 806.1.b|806.1.b.]] Action grants the corresponding card or effect permission to be played or activated during Showdowns, even when it is not the Controlling player's turn.
- [[##rule 813.2|813.2.]] The corresponding card or effect with this keyword is not restricted to Closed States or Showdowns. This permission is inclusive of all other timings and options available to the ability as written, Action's permissions, or by default.

####  showdown closed

**Showdown Closed**

- [[##rule 310.4|310.4.]] Showdown Closed: A Showdown or Combat is in progress and a Chain exists.

####  showdown open state

**Showdown Open State**

- [[##rule 313.1|313.1.]] Focus is the permission to take appropriately timed Discretionary Actions when the turn is in a Showdown Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 323.14|323.14.]] 9a. If the current state is Showdown Open State and Combat is Staged at a Battleﬁeld where there is a Non-Combat Showdown ongoing, that Showdown becomes a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 459.1|459.1.]] Combat will open in one of two ways: when a Combat and Showdown are staged at the same Battleﬁeld and the turn player initiates the Showdown; or when the turn is in a Showdown Open State and a Combat is staged at the Battleﬁeld where the current Showdown is ongoing. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.

####  signature

**Signature**

- [[##rule 103.2.d|103.2.d.]] Your deck may only contain 3 total Signature cards that have the same Champion tag as your Champion Legend.
- [[##rule 133.7.b|133.7.b.]] Signature is a supertype that may apply to game objects of any card type. It impacts the rules for deckbuilding. See rule 103.2.d.for more information about Signature cards.
- [[##rule 133.8.b|133.8.b.]] Tags used to link Legends, Champion Units, and Signature cards are known as Champion Tags.
- [[##rule 825.2.b|825.2.b.]] If a card is a Signature card and is also Unique, then that Deck can contain any combination of three Signature cards, but still only one of each named Unique card.

####  silver rule

**Silver Rule**

- [[##rule 050|050.]] Silver Rule

####  simultaneously

**Simultaneously**

- [[##rule 144.3.c|144.3.c.]] The Costs of Exhausting the Units are also paid Simultaneously.

####  special cleanup

**Special Cleanup**

- [[##rule 317.2.a|317.2.a.]] Invoke an Ending Special Cleanup.  See rule 318. Cleanups for more information.
- [[##rule 324|324.]] Special Cleanups are Cleanup steps invoked at speciﬁc times that have additional steps not present in a normal Cleanup.
- [[##rule 324.1|324.1.]] When a Special Cleanup is invoked, the unique steps added will be inserted and deﬁned by the sub-section that invokes it.  Example: When a Combat Cleanup is invoked, the Combat section deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 461. The Resolution Step for more information. Example: When an End of Turn Cleanup is invoked, the End of Turn Phase subsection deﬁnes what steps are added to the Cleanup. See rule 317. The Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 324.2|324.2.]] If events during a Special Cleanup require another Cleanup, a normal Cleanup is invoked, not another iteration of the Special Cleanup.

####  special cleanup require

**Special Cleanup Require**

- [[##rule 324.2|324.2.]] If events during a Special Cleanup require another Cleanup, a normal Cleanup is invoked, not another iteration of the Special Cleanup.

####  special terms

**Special Terms**

- [[##rule 739|739.]] Special Terms

####  spells

**Spells**

- [[##rule 133.4.b|133.4.b.]] Spells
- [[##rule 152|152.]] Spells
- [[##rule 188.2|188.2.]] For Spells, they are the Spell's Controller.
- [[##rule 316.4.b|316.4.b.]] This could be the result of a Standard Move Standard Action, a Spell, or other Game Effect.
- [[##rule 342|342.]] A Showdown is a Window of Opportunity in which Players have an Open State in which they may play Spells in an alternating fashion.
- [[##rule 351.2|351.2.]] Spells create game effects that are executed, then the card is placed in the trash when Played.
- [[##rule 355.3|355.3.]] For Spells and Abilities with a bulleted list of modes to choose from, make the appropriate choices now.
- [[##rule 355.4|355.4.]] For Spells and Abilities that Move one or more Units, choose a valid Location as the Move Destination for each Move that will be performed.
- [[##rule 359.3|359.3.]] A Spell lingers on the Chain.
- [[##rule 361|361.]] An Ability is the structured rules and capabilities of Game Objects or Spells.
- [[##rule 379|379.]] Activated abilities are present on Game Objects and some Spells.
- [[##rule 383.3.b.2|383.3.b.2.]] Costs within instructions for Triggered Abilities are not paid on resolution, unlike costs within instructions for Spells.
- [[##rule 392|392.]] Delayed Abilities are not associated with Units or Gear; they are created by other Abilities or Spells. As such they are executed when their condition and/or speciﬁed time occurs regardless of whether the source of the Delayed Ability is still on the board or not.
- [[##rule 400.1|400.1.]] When an Ability ﬁnishes the steps of playing it becomes a Chain Item just like a Spell.
- [[##rule 406.5|406.5.]] Otherwise, execute the Ability just like a Spell, then clear the Chain Item from the Chain.
- [[##rule 444|444.]] Spells, Abilities, or other effects may cause a Move to occur.
- [[##rule 806.5.b|806.5.b.]] Whether or not a Spell has Action is a characteristic of that Spell and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 813.5.b|813.5.b.]] Whether or not a Spell has Reaction is a characteristic of that Spell and may be checked or d by other Game Effects.
- [[##rule 820.1.a|820.1.a.]] Repeat is present on Spells.

####  spend xp

**Spend Xp**

- [[##rule 730.2|730.2.]] To Spend XP, reduce the value of XP marked on the Player spending it.

####  spending

**Spending**

- [[##rule 702.2.b|702.2.b.]] Spending a Buff removes a single Buff counter from a Unit.
- [[##rule 730|730.]] XP can be Gained and Spent.

####  splitting

**Splitting**

- [[##rule 355.14|355.14.]] Splitting
- [[##rule 715.3|715.3.]] If the Deal action Splits damage, then the Bonus Damage applies to the amount of Damage that will be Split. This can alter the number of targets eligible to be chosen.  Example: Volibear, Furious is a unit that says in part “When I attack, deal 5 damage split among any number of enemy units here.” A player attacks with Volibear, Furious while they also control Annie, Fiery, a unit that says “Your spells and abilities deal 1 Bonus Damage.” Volibear, Furious now deals 6 damage split among any number of enemy units at its location, and can choose to split that damage among up to 6 units rather than the usual 5.

####  sprite token with temporary

**Sprite Token With Temporary**

- [[##rule 184.2|184.2.]] A 3 [M] Sprite token with Temporary is a domainless unit token with 3 Might, the Fae tag, and the Temporary keyword. See rule 816. Temporary for more information.

####  staged combats

**Staged Combats**

- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 456.2|456.2.]] If Staged Combats stop being Staged before the Steps of Combat are initiated, they are not resolved or executed.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.
- [[##rule 457.2|457.2.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid to be chosen as a location to play one or more Units by a player not involved in that Combat by any means,
- [[##rule 457.2.a|457.2.a.]] If an effect would require a Unit be played to a Battleﬁeld with a Staged Combat or a Combat in Progress, where the controller of the played unit is not a participant, instead the Unit is played to its controller's Base.

####  standard move

**Standard Move**

- [[##rule 144|144.]] Units have the Inherent Ability to perform a Standard Move.
- [[##rule 144.4|144.4.]] The Destinations where Units can Move to with their Standard Move are restricted:
- [[##rule 144.4.c|144.4.c.]] Ganking is a unique ability that affects a Unit's Standard Move
- [[##rule 144.4.c.1|144.4.c.1.]] Units with Ganking may use their Standard Move to Move from Battleﬁeld to Battleﬁeld.  See rule 810. Ganking for more information.
- [[##rule 420.2.b|420.2.b.]] The Standard Move inherent to Units may also cause Movement.  See rule 144.for more information on the Standard Move.
- [[##rule 420.3|420.3.]] The Standard Move inherent to Units is a Discretionary Action.
- [[##rule 442.2.a|442.2.a.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have permanents at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 442.2.b|442.2.b.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, Battleﬁelds Controlled by a player’s teammates are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units that player controls.
- [[##rule 443|443.]] Players may choose to move their Units with the Standard Move. See rule 144.for more information on the Standard Move.
- [[##rule 457.1|457.1.]] In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battleﬁelds with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds (Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players not involved in those Combats or who don't already have Units at that Battleﬁeld.  See rule 442.2.a.for more information on Invalid Destinations.
- [[##rule 484.8.c.2|484.8.c.2.]] Players may not issue Standard Movement to their Teammate's Units.

####  standard move standard action

**Standard Move Standard Action**

- [[##rule 316.4.b|316.4.b.]] This could be the result of a Standard Move Standard Action, a Spell, or other Game Effect.

####  start of turn

**Start Of Turn**

- [[##rule 315|315.]] Start of Turn
- [[##rule 316.1|316.1.]] When all steps of the Start of Turn have been completed, the Main Phase begins.
- [[##rule 334.1|334.1.]] Tasks include, but are not limited to: Cleanups, the actions performed during the Start of Turn Process, throughout Combat in its various steps, and the actions performed during the End of Turn  Process. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information on Cleanups See rule 315. Start of Turn for more information on the Start of Turn process See rule 454. Combat for more information on the steps of Combat See rule 317. Ending Phase for more information.

See rule 318. Cleanups for more information on Cleanups See rule 315. Start of Turn for more information on the Start of Turn process See rule 454. Combat for more information on the steps of Combat See rule 317. Ending Phase for more information.

####  started

- [[##rule 338.1.a.5|338.1.a.5.]] This can be an additional card to the item that Started the Chain in the case of the ﬁrst player with Priority after creating the Chain.

####  state

**State**

- [[##rule 109.2|109.2.]] The State of all Game Objects in the Play Area is also Public Information.  Examples:   If a Unit is Buffed  If a Gear is Exhausted  Etc.
- [[##rule 316.5.b|316.5.b.]] A Showdown is marked as Staged at a Battleﬁeld when the Contested status is applied to a Battleﬁeld with no current controller.
- [[##rule 323.8|323.8.]] 6. Mark a Showdown as Staged at each Battleﬁeld that Contested was applied to.
- [[##rule 323.8.a|323.8.a.]] The Showdown remains Staged at each Battleﬁeld that is Contested and has units present controlled by the player that applied Contested.
- [[##rule 323.9|323.9.]] 7. Mark a Combat as Staged at each Battleﬁeld that Contested was applied to that have Units present controlled by opposing players.
- [[##rule 323.9.a|323.9.a.]] The Combat remains Staged at that Battleﬁeld as long as there are Units present from two opposing players there.
- [[##rule 323.10|323.10.]] 7a. If Units of two opposing players are no longer present at a Battleﬁeld that has a Combat Staged before it has opened, the Combat will cease being Staged
- [[##rule 323.11|323.11.]] 8. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and one or more Showdowns are Staged, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. A Showdown begins there.
- [[##rule 323.13|323.13.]] 9. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and Combat is Staged at one or more Battleﬁelds, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. Combat begins there.
- [[##rule 323.14|323.14.]] 9a. If the current state is Showdown Open State and Combat is Staged at a Battleﬁeld where there is a Non-Combat Showdown ongoing, that Showdown becomes a Combat Showdown.
- [[##rule 331|331.]] The State of the Turn is partially determined by whether or not the Chain currently exists.
- [[##rule 343|343.]] The State of the turn is partially determined by whether or not a Showdown or Combat is in progress.
- [[##rule 423|423.]] Stun
- [[##rule 442.2.c|442.2.c.]] If an action would require a Move that would cause a Unit to become present in a Location where it cannot move for any reason, such as a Battleﬁeld with two players that are not the controller of the Unit performing this Move action are in a Combat or such a Combat is Staged, it instead Recalls. See rule 449. Recalls for more information.
- [[##rule 456|456.]] Combat is considered Staged if there are units controlled by two opposing players at a Battleﬁeld but the Steps of Combat have not been initiated.
- [[##rule 456.2|456.2.]] If Staged Combats stop being Staged before the Steps of Combat are initiated, they are not resolved or executed.
- [[##rule 459.2.e.1|459.2.e.1.]] Otherwise the Combat Showdown continues, with the State Open as normal.

####  state closes

**State Closes**

- [[##rule 459.2.e|459.2.e.]] The State Closes if a Combat Chain was created.

####  statements of fact

**Statements Of Fact**

- [[##rule 364.2|364.2.]] They can be recognized by being statements of fact.

####  states of the turn

**States Of The Turn**

- [[##rule 313.1|313.1.]] Focus is the permission to take appropriately timed Discretionary Actions when the turn is in a Showdown Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 316.2.b|316.2.b.]] This is denoted as a Neutral Open State, and only the Turn Player has the ability to play spells or activate abilities.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 354.1|354.1.]] This Closes the State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 410.1.a|410.1.a.]] A Discretionary Action is a Game Action that may be performed at any time during a player's turn during a Neutral Open State.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.

####  step 1: finalize

**Step 1: Finalize**

- [[##rule 337|337.]] Step 1: Finalize

####  step 1: the combat showdown step

**Step 1: The Combat Showdown Step**

- [[##rule 459|459.]] Step 1: The Combat Showdown Step

####  step 2

**Step 2**

- [[##rule 356.2.b.1|356.2.b.1.]] Some Optional Costs speciﬁed by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Non-Mandatory, and must be paid only if the player made the choice to pay them in step 2. They use the phrase "as an additional cost" and the word "may."  Example: A unit has the ability "As you play me, you may discard 1 as an additional cost. If you do, reduce my cost by [2]." While playing the unit, its controller declares their intention to pay the additional cost in step 2, applies that additional cost in rule 356.2, applies the discount granted by paying that cost in rule 356.4, and discards a card to pay that additional cost in rule 357.2.See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.

####  step 2: execute

**Step 2: Execute**

- [[##rule 338|338.]] Step 2: Execute

####  step 2: the combat damage step

**Step 2: The Combat Damage Step**

- [[##rule 460|460.]] Step 2: The Combat Damage Step

####  step 3: pass

**Step 3: Pass**

- [[##rule 339|339.]] Step 3: Pass
- [[##rule 357.2|357.2.]] In addition, pay any non-standard Cost summed in step 3 in any order.
- [[##rule 357.2.a|357.2.a.]] Costs that are replaced with other events by replacement effects are still considered paid.  Example: A player plays Cruel Patron, which says "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." They also control Zhonya’s Hourglass, which says “If a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Heal that unit, exhaust it, and recall it.” They choose to kill a friendly unit during step 3, but as they pay the cost in step 4, Zhonya’s Hourglass replaces that unit’s death. The cost is considered paid, and the player can continue playing Cruel Patron.

####  step 3: the resolution step

**Step 3: The Resolution Step**

- [[##rule 461|461.]] Step 3: The Resolution Step

####  step 4

**Step 4**

- [[##rule 357.2.a|357.2.a.]] Costs that are replaced with other events by replacement effects are still considered paid.  Example: A player plays Cruel Patron, which says "As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit." They also control Zhonya’s Hourglass, which says “If a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Heal that unit, exhaust it, and recall it.” They choose to kill a friendly unit during step 3, but as they pay the cost in step 4, Zhonya’s Hourglass replaces that unit’s death. The cost is considered paid, and the player can continue playing Cruel Patron.

####  step 4: resolve

**Step 4: Resolve**

- [[##rule 340|340.]] Step 4: Resolve

####  steps of combat

**Steps Of Combat**

- [[##rule 316.4.e|316.4.e.]] Play proceeds following the steps of combat.  See rule 458. The Steps of Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 348.1|348.1.]] If it is a Combat Showdown, proceed with the remaining steps of Combat to resolve the phase.  See rule 458. The Steps of Combat for more information.
- [[##rule 456|456.]] Combat is considered Staged if there are units controlled by two opposing players at a Battleﬁeld but the Steps of Combat have not been initiated.
- [[##rule 456.2|456.2.]] If Staged Combats stop being Staged before the Steps of Combat are initiated, they are not resolved or executed.
- [[##rule 458|458.]] The Steps of Combat

####  stun units

**Stun Units**

- [[##rule 423.2.a|423.2.a.]] Players may only Stun Units when directed to by Game Effects.

####  stunned unit

**Stunned Unit**

- [[##rule 423.1.a.1|423.1.a.1.]] A Stunned Unit can not be Stunned again.  Example: Eclipse Herald has the ability "When you stun an enemy unit, ready me and give me +1 [M] this turn." Its controller plays a spell that reads "Stun a unit." They may choose a unit that's already stunned, but if they do, Eclipse Herald will not trigger.
- [[##rule 423.1.a.2|423.1.a.2.]] Stunned Units lose the Stunned status at the beginning of the next Ending Step.
- [[##rule 423.1.b|423.1.b.]] A Stunned Unit does not contribute its might to damage in the combat damage step. See rule 460. The Combat Damage Step for more information.
- [[##rule 423.1.c|423.1.c.]] A Stunned Unit must still have damage applied to it equal to, or greater than, its full might value to be killed.

####  stunning

**Stunning**

- [[##rule 423.1|423.1.]] Stunning is the act of selecting one or more Units on the Board and rendering them Stunned.
- [[##rule 423.1.a|423.1.a.]] Stunned is a binary state. A Unit is Stunned or it isn't.
- [[##rule 423.2|423.2.]] Stunning is a Limited Action.

####  sub-categories

**Sub-categories**

- [[##rule 133.1|133.1.]] A card can have one or more Categories and Sub-Categories based on the properties of its front and back sides.
- [[##rule 133.2|133.2.]] These Categories and Sub-Categories dictate the behaviors of the card during play.

####  sub-phase

**Sub-phase**

- [[##rule 316.5.a.1|316.5.a.1.]] Showdowns that occur as a result of Combat are a Sub-Phase of Combat.

####  supertypes

**Supertypes**

- [[##rule 133.7|133.7.]] Supertypes are Categories that may apply to game objects of multiple types. They are listed before a card’s type.

####  swap

**Swap**

- [[##rule 433|433.]] Swap
- [[##rule 433.1|433.1.]] Swapping is the act of increasing one numeric value and decreasing another numeric value on some number of Game Objects such that their values are reversed.
- [[##rule 433.1.a|433.1.a.]] Swapping creates two different effects that apply to each attribute. One that Increases one value and one that Decreases the other.
- [[##rule 433.1.c|433.1.c.]] If both attributes are the same numeric value, Swapping has no effect.
- [[##rule 433.2|433.2.]] Swapping is a Limited Action.
- [[##rule 438.7.b|438.7.b.]] To Swap Back, the token stops existing and the original card is returned to the space that the token just occupied, inheriting all current effects and statuses.

####  symbols

**Symbols**

- [[##rule 135.2.e|135.2.e.]] Symbols

###  group T

####  tags

**Tags**

- [[##rule 133.8|133.8.]] Tags are Categories that may apply to game objects of multiple types. They are listed after a card’s type.
- [[##rule 133.8.a|133.8.a.]] Tags have no innate rules meaning, but may be d by game rules and card effects.
- [[##rule 133.8.b|133.8.b.]] Tags used to link Legends, Champion Units, and Signature cards are known as Champion Tags.
- [[##rule 143.1|143.1.]] Tag: A Unit has zero or more Tags representing one or more champions, regions, factions, or species it belongs to.
- [[##rule 182.1.c|182.1.c.]] Tokens may have one or more tags.
- [[##rule 335|335.]] Whenever a Player takes one or more actions that incur Tasks they should refer to the process of HOT FEPR: Handle Outstanding Tasks; then Finalize, Execute, Pass, Resolve.
- [[##rule 718.5.a|718.5.a.]] Attached cards still have all Types and Tags while Attached.

####  tank

**Tank**

- [[##rule 460.2.c.5|460.2.c.5.]] A player must obey all requirements and restrictions on damage assignment if able.  Example: A player is assigning damage to the following units: a unit with Tank ("I must be assigned combat damage ﬁrst."); Caitlyn, Patrolling ("I must be assigned combat damage last."); and another unit without any abilities. That player must assign combat damage ﬁrst to the unit with Tank, then to the unit with no abilities, then to Caitlyn.
- [[##rule 460.2.c.6|460.2.c.6.]] If multiple Units have abilities or effects that require a player to assign them damage with the same priority, that player may assign damage to those units in any order.  Example: A player is assigning damage to the following units: two units with Tank ("I must be assigned combat damage ﬁrst.") and one unit with no abilities. That player chooses one of the units with Tank and assigns combat damage to it. Then they must assign any remaining damage ﬁrst to the other unit with Tank, then to the unit with no abilities.
- [[##rule 815|815.]] Tank

####  targeting

**Targeting**

- [[##rule 355.6|355.6.]] Targeting
- [[##rule 355.7|355.7.]] When a card Chooses one or more speciﬁc Game Objects to affect, it is Targeted unless indicated otherwise by the rules in this section.
- [[##rule 355.11|355.11.]] Some cards identify a group of Targets with Targeting Requirements that must be met by the group as a whole.
- [[##rule 355.14.a|355.14.a.]] If a card speciﬁes that an amount of damage may be split among some number of Units, then each Unit chosen is Targeted.
- [[##rule 355.14.b|355.14.b.]] The Targets are chosen when the spell or ability is ﬁnalized on the chain.
- [[##rule 355.14.c|355.14.c.]] A number of Targets can only be chosen up to, and not exceeding, the initial amount of damage available when the spell is played. Example: A player playing a spell that instructs them to "Split 5 damage" may only choose up to 5 units, but may choose fewer.
- [[##rule 355.14.d|355.14.d.]] Each Target is valid, and contributes to Chosen triggers individually.
- [[##rule 355.14.f|355.14.f.]] Each Target must receive a valid amount of damage.
- [[##rule 355.14.h|355.14.h.]] If, at resolution of the spell or effect, there are more Targets than available damage to divide, then the player who controls the effect dealing damage determines which Targets cease being Targets.
- [[##rule 355.14.i|355.14.i.]] Any costs that were paid, or effects that were triggered as a result of those Game Objects being chosen as Targets remain in effect, paid, or otherwise triggered.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.7|359.3.e.7.]] If all of an instruction's Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is ﬁnished being played, that instruction will not execute.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.8|359.3.e.8.]] If an instruction has more than one Target and fewer than all of the Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is ﬁnished being played, the instruction will execute, with only the Targets available and valid being operated on.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.3|383.4.b.3.]] Although these abilities say “choose” in their Condition, they trigger speciﬁcally when an appropriate Game Object is Targeted. See rule 355.6. Targeting for more information on what counts as Targeting.
- [[##rule 457.2.b|457.2.b.]] Any subsequent  to "here" in the corresponding effect is reassigned to the Controller's Base, where the Unit was played. Any further effects that may be invalidated are invalidated as if the effect was mistargeted. See rule 355.6. Targeting for more information on Mistargeting.
- [[##rule 811.1.d|811.1.d.]] Some choices made while playing a card from Hidden are restricted to the battleﬁeld where it was hidden. A card cannot be played from Hidden if it is a spell with no valid targets under these restrictions.  See rule 355.6. Targeting for more information.
- [[##rule 818.1.b.1|818.1.b.1.]] Equip’s choice is a Target.

####  targeting effects

**Targeting Effects**

- [[##rule 383.4.b|383.4.b.]] Targeting Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that a Game Object becomes targeted.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.4|383.4.b.4.]] These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Targeting Effects.

####  targeting requirements

**Targeting Requirements**

- [[##rule 355.11|355.11.]] Some cards identify a group of Targets with Targeting Requirements that must be met by the group as a whole.

####  task

**Task**

- [[##rule 315.1.a|315.1.a.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:
- [[##rule 315.2.b.1|315.2.b.1.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:
- [[##rule 315.3.a|315.3.a.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:
- [[##rule 315.4.a|315.4.a.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:
- [[##rule 315.4.c|315.4.c.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:
- [[##rule 317.2.e|317.2.e.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:
- [[##rule 323|323.]] When a Cleanup occurs, the following Tasks become Outstanding in the order described:
- [[##rule 334|334.]] A Task is one or more steps or processes that one or more Players must perform before continuing with any other actions.
- [[##rule 334.1|334.1.]] Tasks include, but are not limited to: Cleanups, the actions performed during the Start of Turn Process, throughout Combat in its various steps, and the actions performed during the End of Turn  Process. See rule 318. Cleanups for more information on Cleanups See rule 315. Start of Turn for more information on the Start of Turn process See rule 454. Combat for more information on the steps of Combat See rule 317. Ending Phase for more information.
- [[##rule 335|335.]] Whenever a Player takes one or more actions that incur Tasks they should refer to the process of HOT FEPR: Handle Outstanding Tasks; then Finalize, Execute, Pass, Resolve.
- [[##rule 335.1|335.1.]] In the course of Handling Outstanding Tasks, Chain Items may be added to the Chain. They will remain there until the Tasks are complete.
- [[##rule 335.2|335.2.]] When all Outstanding Tasks are completed, all pending Chain Items will subsequently be processed by the FEPR process.
- [[##rule 335.3|335.3.]] If there are no Outstanding Tasks, no pending Chain Items, and it is the Main Phase, the Turn Player receives priority. If there are no Outstanding Tasks, no pending items, and it is any other phase of the turn, proceed to the next substep, step, phase, or turn.
- [[##rule 336|336.]] When there are no outstanding Tasks and there are pending Chain Items on the Chain, players should refer to the FEPR process to proceed.
- [[##rule 459.2.a|459.2.a.]] The following Tasks become Outstanding, in the order described:
- [[##rule 460.1|460.1.]] If both Attacking and Defending units remain at this battleﬁeld, the following Tasks become Outstanding, in the speciﬁed order:
- [[##rule 461.2|461.2.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:
- [[##rule 461.4|461.4.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:
- [[##rule 461.6|461.6.]] The following Task becomes Outstanding:

####  teams

**Teams**

- [[##rule 315.2.b.3|315.2.b.3.]] Reminder: In Modes of Play with Teams, Battleﬁelds held by a Teammate of the Turn Player during this phase are disqualiﬁed from being scored this turn by the Turn Player.
- [[##rule 484.8.a|484.8.a.]] Players may play spells or activate abilities during their Teammate's Turn.In order to do so, their Teammate will invite them to play a spell or activate an ability using their own Priority.
- [[##rule 651.4|651.4.]] If the player has Teammates due to the Mode of Play, that player’s Teammates also lose and are removed from the game.
- [[##rule 732|732.]] XP is not shared between Allies in Game Modes with Teammates.

####  temporary

**Temporary**

- [[##rule 184.2|184.2.]] A 3 [M] Sprite token with Temporary is a domainless unit token with 3 Might, the Fae tag, and the Temporary keyword. See rule 816. Temporary for more information.
- [[##rule 816|816.]] Temporary

####  temporary modiﬁcations

**Temporary Modiﬁcations**

- [[##rule 110|110.]] Whenever a Game Object changes zones to or from a Non-Board Zone, all Temporary Modiﬁcations of all kinds cease to be tracked on it in all capacities.  Examples:  Damage is cleared.  Buffs are removed.  Granted Keywords are no longer granted.

####  timestamp

**Timestamp**

- [[##rule 475|475.]] If more than one effect applies in the same layer but no dependency is established, then Timestamp order is applied to the effects within that layer and sublayer
- [[##rule 475.1|475.1.]] When an effect begins applying, it establishes a time for which it is compared against other Game Effects for purposes of resolving Layered effects as its Timestamp.
- [[##rule 475.1.a|475.1.a.]] Timestamps are not rote values.
- [[##rule 475.1.b|475.1.b.]] Timestamps are relative comparisons between effects and when they began applying to the game.
- [[##rule 475.1.c|475.1.c.]] Timestamps are not d by Game Effects in any way. They are only used to ﬁnalize layered effects.
- [[##rule 475.2|475.2.]] When Rules Text becomes Inactive for any reason, it loses its Timestamp. When it ceases to be Inactive, a new Timestamp is established.
- [[##rule 475.3|475.3.]] Effects are applied such that the earliest Timestamp within each Layer and Sublayer applies ﬁrst, followed by other Effects in that Layer and Sublayer in chronological order.
- [[##rule 727.1.a.1|727.1.a.1.]] This Condition may also have a determined Duration, Time, or Limitation as part of its deﬁnition. EXAMPLE: Legion speciﬁes the duration of its condition: “if you have played another card this turn.” This turn is the duration. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “Until you have spent [3] this turn” would include a limitation on its condition. EXAMPLE: A dependent keyword that is short for “After you’ve become an attacker this turn” would include a time after which the condition is active.

####  token

**Token**

- [[##rule 133.7.c|133.7.c.]] Token is a supertype applied to temporary game objects of any card type. See rule 176. Tokens for more information.
- [[##rule 176|176.]] Tokens
- [[##rule 177|177.]] Tokens are Game Objects created by spells and abilities during play.
- [[##rule 350.2|350.2.]] Tokens are not cards, but can still be Played.  See rule 176. Tokens for more information.
- [[##rule 439.3.a|439.3.a.]] If the Game Object is a token, it will follow the normal rules for tokens. See rule 176. Tokens for more information.

####  top-most card

**Top-most Card**

- [[##rule 434.1|434.1.]] Attaching is the act of linking two cards on the board together to combine their effects in some way. This causes one or more cards to become Attached and at least one card to become a Top-Most Card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.
- [[##rule 434.1.a.1|434.1.a.1.]] One card will be designated as the one being Attached, and thus become Attached. The other will become the Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 434.1.b|434.1.b.]] This is represented by physically laying the Top-Most card on top of the other or others such that all Effect Texts and Might Bonuses are showing, but nothing else from the card or cards Attached.
- [[##rule 434.1.b.1|434.1.b.1.]] In the situation where there is more than one card attached to the Top-Most card, they should be stacked in such a way that all Effect Text boxes and Might Bonuses are readable. The order of the Attached cards has no bearing on the application of effects.
- [[##rule 434.1.c|434.1.c.]] The Top-Most card has all Effect Text of all cards Attached to it appended to its Rules Text.
- [[##rule 434.1.d|434.1.d.]] The Top-Most Card has its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of all cards Attached to it.
- [[##rule 434.1.f|434.1.f.]] Attaching a card to a new Top-Most Card will cause it to Detach from the card to which it is currently Attached.
- [[##rule 434.1.g|434.1.g.]] Attaching a card to its current Top-Most Card  will not have any effect.
- [[##rule 434.1.h|434.1.h.]] If a Game Effect instructs a player to Attach a card to its current Top-Most Card, nothing additional happens.
- [[##rule 434.4|434.4.]] When a card Attaches to a card, its location becomes the same as the new Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 435.1|435.1.]] Detaching is the act of unlinking two cards that are currently linked through the act of Attaching. This causes one to cease being Attached, and potentially causes the other to cease being a Top-Most card.
- [[##rule 435.1.b.1|435.1.b.1.]] To represent this, these cards should no longer be placed under the card they were previously placed under as Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 435.1.b.2|435.1.b.2.]] If the Top-Most Card no longer has any cards Attached to it after this, it is no longer a Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 435.1.d|435.1.d.]] The Top-Most Card ceases to have the Effect Text of the card being Detached appended to its Rules Text.
- [[##rule 435.1.e|435.1.e.]] The Top-Most Card ceases to have its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of the card being Detached.
- [[##rule 435.4|435.4.]] When a card Detaches from a Top-Most Card, its location is the same as the Top-Most Card from which it Detached.
- [[##rule 435.4.b|435.4.b.]] If the Attached card was Detached because the Top-Most Card changed zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, then the location that the Attached Card will Detach to is the last location the Top-Most Card was at before changing from a board zone to a non-board zone.
- [[##rule 718.3|718.3.]] While in this state, Abilities in the card’s Effect Text are appended to the Rules Text of the Top-Most Card.
- [[##rule 718.4|718.4.]] While in this state, the card’s Might Bonus modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by the value listed.
- [[##rule 718.5.c|718.5.c.]] Attached cards cannot be moved separately from the Top-Most Card they are Attached to.
- [[##rule 718.5.d|718.5.d.]] A card may be Attached only to a single Top-Most card at a time.
- [[##rule 718.5.e|718.5.e.]] Attached cards may have different Controllers from their Top-Most card.
- [[##rule 718.5.f|718.5.f.]] Changes in Control of the Top-Most card do not impact Control of Attached cards and vice versa.
- [[##rule 718.5.g|718.5.g.]] An Attached card still appends the abilities in its Effect Text to the Rules Text of the Top-Most card and modulates the Top-Most Card’s Might by its Might Bonus.
- [[##rule 719|719.]] A Top-Most Card is a card that has one or more cards linked to it through the process of Attaching.
- [[##rule 719.2|719.2.]] This card ceases being a Top-Most Card when there are no longer any cards Attached to it.
- [[##rule 719.3|719.3.]] A Top-Most Card and all cards Attached to it are at the same location.
- [[##rule 719.3.a|719.3.a.]] When the Top-Most Card moves, all Attached cards move with it.
- [[##rule 719.4|719.4.]] The Exhausted and Ready state of the Top-Most card does not affect nor change the status of the Attached cards and vice versa.
- [[##rule 719.5|719.5.]] When a Top-Most Card changes zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, all Attached cards Detach from it, remaining in their current zones.
- [[##rule 719.5.a|719.5.a.]] The player that controls the Top-Most Card that changed zones decides the order these cards Detach in, and thus the order of any relevant effects that occur due to the Detach occurring.
- [[##rule 818.1.b.2|818.1.b.2.]] The chosen Unit will become the Top-Most Card for the Attach action.
- [[##rule 818.3|818.3.]] Equipped is the state of a Top-Most Card being Attached by one or more cards that are Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.3.b|818.3.b.]] A Top-Most Card is Equipped as long as one or more of its Attached cards are Equipment.
- [[##rule 818.3.c|818.3.c.]] The state of being Equipped corresponds to a Top-Most card having a card with Equip that is Attached to it.
- [[##rule 821.1.c.5|821.1.c.5.]] If the chosen card’s Equip cost can’t be paid, if it can’t be detached from its current Top-Most card, or if it can’t be attached to the unit with the Weaponmaster ability, it stays in its current location, Attached to anything it was already Attached to.

####  total cost

**Total Cost**

- [[##rule 356.1.b.3|356.1.b.3.]] Further additional costs and/or cost increases applied in subsequent steps may raise the card's Total Cost above zero.  Example: Legion Rearguard is a Fury unit that costs 2 Energy and 0 Power and has Accelerate. A player plays Legion Rearguard and is instructed to ignore its costs, but chooses to pay the Accelerate cost. They ignore Legion Rearguard's Base Cost of 2 Energy, but the optional additional cost of 1 Energy and 1 Fury Power is added to its Total Cost and must be paid.

####  trashes

**Trashes**

- [[##rule 108.2|108.2.]] Trashes
- [[##rule 108.2.a|108.2.a.]] Each player has their own Trash.
- [[##rule 108.2.c|108.2.c.]] Cards in each player’s Trash are unordered. Their sequence does not matter, and they may be reorganized.
- [[##rule 108.2.d|108.2.d.]] Cards in a player's Trash are Public Information. See rule 128. Privacy for more information.
- [[##rule 141.1.b|141.1.b.]] While in the Trash:
- [[##rule 141.1.b.3|141.1.b.3.]] Units can be affected by spells and game effects that target Units in the Trash.
- [[##rule 148.1.b|148.1.b.]] While in the Trash
- [[##rule 148.1.b.3|148.1.b.3.]] Gear can be affected by spells and game effects that affect Gear in the Trash.
- [[##rule 156|156.]] A spell creates a game effect according to its instructions and is then placed in the Trash of the player who owns it.
- [[##rule 323.5|323.5.]] 3b. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might are killed and placed in their owners' Trash.
- [[##rule 323.7|323.7.]] 5. Recall all Unattached non-Unit Gear at Battleﬁelds, and all Permanents and Runes in Bases other than their controller’s. Remove all Hidden cards from all Battleﬁelds that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's Trash.
- [[##rule 359.3.d|359.3.d.]] Otherwise, execute the game effect of the spell, from top to bottom of the rules text of the card and then place the card in the Trash of the owning player.
- [[##rule 422.1.a|422.1.a.]] The player who is performing the action chooses which cards to send to their Trash, and may use Private Information to do so.
- [[##rule 428.1.a.1.b|428.1.a.1.b.]] When a unit with a Deathknell  is to be put in the Trash due to a Kill Instruction, it ﬁrst has its Deathknell added to the chain as a Pending Item. Note the unit’s location, attributes, and other relevant information to process its Deathknell when ﬁnalized before completing this Kill Instruction.
- [[##rule 431.1.b|431.1.b.]] If a player must put one or more cards from their Main Deck in any other zone, such as the Trash, in excess of the number of cards in their deck they will do so as much as possible, perform this action, and then complete the remaining number required by the instruction.
- [[##rule 808.1.d|808.1.d.]] The Trigger for this effect is the Permanent being Killed and sent to the Trash.
- [[##rule 808.1.d.1|808.1.d.1.]] If the Permanent with the effect is not sent to the Trash, for example because its "killed" event was replaced with a recall, the Deathknell will not occur.
- [[##rule 808.1.d.3|808.1.d.3.]] Before the card with Deathknell is moved to the Trash, note its location, its attributes, and any other details related to the effect of its Deathknell to process the trigger after it has been Finalized.

####  trigger

**Trigger**

- [[##rule 383.2.c|383.2.c.]] The Condition of a Trigger is evaluated after a potentially inciting event has been processed.
- [[##rule 383.2.c.1|383.2.c.1.]] If a Game Object with a Triggered Ability that is active in a speciﬁc zone, it is evaluated and subsequently triggered if it enters that zone at the same time that its Trigger’s condition is met.  Example: Immortal Phoenix says “When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.” This ability triggers if Immortal Phoenix is in your trash immediately after you kill a unit with a spell, even if the unit you killed with a spell was that Immortal Phoenix.
- [[##rule 383.2.c.2|383.2.c.2.]] A Game Object will not be able to successfully be able to evaluate its Trigger Condition, however, if it leaves the zone that its Trigger is active from at the same time that its Trigger is satisﬁed.  Example: Viktor, Leader says “When another non-Recruit unit you control dies, play a 1 [M] Recruit unit token into your base.” This ability triggers if Viktor is on the board immediately after another non-Recruit unit you control dies. It does not trigger if Viktor and another non-Recruit unit you control die during the same game action (for instance, if they are both killed in the same Cleanup due to the damage dealt by Unchecked Power).
- [[##rule 383.3.d|383.3.d.]] If more than one Triggered Ability is Triggered simultaneously, then the player that controls the Abilities selects the order to place them on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.d.1|383.3.d.1.]] If multiple players separately control Triggered Abilities that are Triggered simultaneously, then starting with the Turn Player and proceeding in Turn Order, each player orders their Triggered Abilities on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.f.2|383.3.f.2.]] If they do not, it has not Triggered this turn.
- [[##rule 402.3.b|402.3.b.]] If there are legal options to choose, the ability’s controller must choose them. They may not decline this stage of playing a Trigger.
- [[##rule 725.1|725.1.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Attaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Attaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Attaches.
- [[##rule 725.2|725.2.]] If an Attached card has a Passive or Replacement ability that applies during the process of Detaching or a Triggered ability that triggers off of Detaching, that text exists and can be processed as it Detaches.
- [[##rule 808.2.a|808.2.a.]] The controller will choose the order to add these Triggers to the chain.

####  trigger condition

**Trigger Condition**

- [[##rule 383.2.c.2|383.2.c.2.]] A Game Object will not be able to successfully be able to evaluate its Trigger Condition, however, if it leaves the zone that its Trigger is active from at the same time that its Trigger is satisﬁed.  Example: Viktor, Leader says “When another non-Recruit unit you control dies, play a 1 [M] Recruit unit token into your base.” This ability triggers if Viktor is on the board immediately after another non-Recruit unit you control dies. It does not trigger if Viktor and another non-Recruit unit you control die during the same game action (for instance, if they are both killed in the same Cleanup due to the damage dealt by Unchecked Power).

####  triggered abilities

**Triggered Abilities**

- [[##rule 169.9|169.9.]] Battleﬁelds can have Triggered Abilities. See rule 382. Triggered Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 173.7|173.7.]] Legends can have Triggered Abilities. See rule 382. Triggered Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 303.2.a|303.2.a.]] If one or more game actions, game effects, or Triggered Abilities are activated simultaneously, then Turn Order is d to organize the sequence of actions.  See rule 382. Triggered Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 355.5.b|355.5.b.]] This does not include making choices for Triggered Abilities of permanents, even if those abilities trigger when the permanent is played.  Example: A unit with a triggered ability that says "When I'm played, kill a unit" does not require you to choose a target as it's played. The target will be chosen when the ability triggers.  See rule 382. Triggered Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 361.1|361.1.]] An Ability has multiple structures.  -Passive Abilities  -Replacement Effects  -Activated Abilities  -Triggered Abilities  -Delayed Abilities
- [[##rule 383|383.]] Triggered Abilities are repeatable effects that happen when a Condition is met.
- [[##rule 383.1|383.1.]] Triggered Abilities can usually be recognized by the word "when" followed by a game action or event; the word "at" followed by a point in time during the turn sequence; or the phrase “the [Nth] time” followed by a game action or event.  Examples:  "When you conquer here, you may spend a buff to draw 1."  "At the end of your turn, ready 2 runes."  “The ﬁrst time I move each turn, you may ready something else that's exhausted.”
- [[##rule 383.2|383.2.]] Triggered Abilities have a Condition and an Effect.
- [[##rule 383.2.c.1|383.2.c.1.]] If a Game Object with a Triggered Ability that is active in a speciﬁc zone, it is evaluated and subsequently triggered if it enters that zone at the same time that its Trigger’s condition is met.  Example: Immortal Phoenix says “When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.” This ability triggers if Immortal Phoenix is in your trash immediately after you kill a unit with a spell, even if the unit you killed with a spell was that Immortal Phoenix.
- [[##rule 383.3|383.3.]] When a Condition is met, a Triggered Ability behaves like an Activated Ability and is placed on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.a|383.3.a.]] If a Triggered Ability says “you may” as the ﬁrst part of its Effect, the controller of its source will choose whether or not to place the Triggered Ability on the chain when its trigger Condition is fulﬁlled.
- [[##rule 383.3.b|383.3.b.]] If a Triggered Ability contains a cost within instructions, that cost is treated as the base cost of the Triggered Ability.
- [[##rule 383.3.b.1|383.3.b.1.]] The cost must be paid in order to ﬁnalize the Triggered Ability to the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.b.2|383.3.b.2.]] Costs within instructions for Triggered Abilities are not paid on resolution, unlike costs within instructions for Spells.
- [[##rule 383.3.c|383.3.c.]] Triggered Abilities can be put on the Chain during Closed States or Open States on any player's turn.
- [[##rule 383.3.d|383.3.d.]] If more than one Triggered Ability is Triggered simultaneously, then the player that controls the Abilities selects the order to place them on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.d.1|383.3.d.1.]] If multiple players separately control Triggered Abilities that are Triggered simultaneously, then starting with the Turn Player and proceeding in Turn Order, each player orders their Triggered Abilities on the Chain.
- [[##rule 383.3.f|383.3.f.]] Some Triggered Abilities will trigger “once each turn.”
- [[##rule 383.3.f.1|383.3.f.1.]] When the Condition is fulﬁlled, the player who controls the source of the Triggered Ability may choose to place it on the chain.
- [[##rule 383.4.a|383.4.a.]] Play Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that the Permanent that has the Play Effect being played to the board.
- [[##rule 383.4.a.2|383.4.a.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Permanent these effects correspond to is ﬁnalized and enters the board.
- [[##rule 383.4.a.3|383.4.a.3.]] These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Play Effects.
- [[##rule 383.4.b|383.4.b.]] Targeting Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that a Game Object becomes targeted.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.2|383.4.b.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after a spell or ability that targets an appropriate Game Object is Finalized.
- [[##rule 383.4.b.4|383.4.b.4.]] These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Targeting Effects.
- [[##rule 383.4.c|383.4.c.]] Conquer Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit participating in, and successfully Conquering a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2|383.4.c.2.]] This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Conquer action, or Abilities that  the player that performed the Conquer action.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.3|383.4.c.3.]] These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Conquer Effects.
- [[##rule 383.4.d|383.4.d.]] Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battleﬁeld during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2|383.4.d.2.]] This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Hold action, or Abilities that  the player that performed the Hold action.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.3|383.4.d.3.]] These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Hold Effects.
- [[##rule 383.4.e|383.4.e.]] Attack Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Attacker designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2|383.4.e.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Attacker designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.3|383.4.e.3.]] These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Attack Triggers.
- [[##rule 383.4.f|383.4.f.]] Defend Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Defender designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2|383.4.f.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Defender designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.3|383.4.f.3.]] These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Defend Triggers.
- [[##rule 384.2|384.2.]] Triggered Abilities of Permanents are only able to have their Conditions evaluated while on the Board.
- [[##rule 385.1|385.1.]] Triggered Abilities on cards outside of the Board rely on the Information Level of the zone they are in.
- [[##rule 385.2|385.2.]] Triggered Abilities outside of the Board will self-describe their context.  Example: The triggered ability "When you conquer, you may discard 1 to return this from your trash to your hand." triggers while the card it's on is in the trash, and not anywhere else.
- [[##rule 387|387.]] Reflexive Triggers are a type of Triggered Ability that create one or more Chain Items when their condition is met.
- [[##rule 387.3|387.3.]] If present, the Condition of a Reflexive Trigger will follow the same format as a Triggered Ability.
- [[##rule 390.2|390.2.]] Delayed Triggers are Triggered Abilities that can be recognized by describing a speciﬁc time of the turn, or by structuring a Triggered Ability with a speciﬁc frame of time as a restriction.
- [[##rule 402.3|402.3.]] If there are not enough options to make legal choices for a Triggered Ability that has been put on the chain, remove it from the Chain now. It ceases to be a Pending Item but never becomes a Chain Item.
- [[##rule 403.1.b|403.1.b.]] Triggered Abilities will typically not have a base cost associated with them when placed on the chain due to their conditions.
- [[##rule 403.1.b.1|403.1.b.1.]] If a Triggered Ability has a cost within instructions (e.g. “[do X] to [do Y]”), the cost is taken as the base cost. See rule 742.1.for more information on costs within instructions.
- [[##rule 404.2|404.2.]] At this stage, players may decline to pay for Triggered Abilities that have incurred a cost. If they do, the ability will cease being a Pending Item and be removed from the Chain. It never becomes a Chain Item.
- [[##rule 422.1.b|422.1.b.]] “When I am discarded” abilities or other Triggered Abilities that trigger on discarding are executed after discarding has occurred.
- [[##rule 451.1|451.1.]] They do not cause Triggered Abilities to trigger that are triggered by Move actions.
- [[##rule 459.2.d|459.2.d.]] 3. Add items to the Combat Chain if establishing Attacker and Defender has caused Triggered Abilities to become Pending.
- [[##rule 459.2.d.1|459.2.d.1.]] The Attacking player, who has Focus, places Triggered Abilities on the Chain ﬁrst, followed by all non-Defender players in Turn Order, followed by the Defending Player.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.1|727.1.c.1.]] Triggered Abilities of Dependent Keywords must be Active for their trigger to be evaluated.
- [[##rule 727.1.c.1.a|727.1.c.1.a.]] If a Triggered Ability becomes active at the same time as its trigger condition would be fulﬁlled, it triggers.
- [[##rule 808.1|808.1.]] Deathknell is a Triggered Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 816.1|816.1.]] Temporary is a Triggered Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 817.1|817.1.]] Vision is a Triggered Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 818.2.a|818.2.a.]] This is an event other Game Effects and Triggered Abilities can .
- [[##rule 819.1|819.1.]] Quick-Draw is a Triggered Ability keyword. It is also a Permissive keyword.
- [[##rule 821.1|821.1.]] Weaponmaster is a Triggered Ability keyword.
- [[##rule 823.1|823.1.]] Hunt is a Triggered Ability keyword.

####  turn order

**Turn Order**

- [[##rule 116|116.]] Determine Turn Order using any fair random method agreed on by all players.
- [[##rule 116.1|116.1.]] Turn Order is established as a repeating set of the players.
- [[##rule 116.1.c|116.1.c.]] The Turn Order generates a looping queue of turns, starting with the First Player and repeating until the game ends.
- [[##rule 301|301.]] The Turn
- [[##rule 303.2.a|303.2.a.]] If one or more game actions, game effects, or Triggered Abilities are activated simultaneously, then Turn Order is d to organize the sequence of actions.  See rule 382. Triggered Abilities for more information.
- [[##rule 306|306.]] The Turn Player changes when the current Turn Player reaches the End of all of the Phases of their Turn.
- [[##rule 312.2.d|312.2.d.]] When the turn is in a Closed State, they are the next Player in Turn Order, and the player with Priority passes.
- [[##rule 317.3|317.3.]] The next player with their Turn queued becomes the Turn Player.
- [[##rule 331|331.]] The State of the Turn is partially determined by whether or not the Chain currently exists.
- [[##rule 338.1.c.1|338.1.c.1.]] The player with Priority passes Priority to the next Player in Turn Order. Proceed to Step 3: Pass.
- [[##rule 339.2|339.2.]] Otherwise, the player with Priority passes Priority to the next Player in Turn Order. Return to Step 3: Execute.
- [[##rule 347.4|347.4.]] Otherwise, Focus passes to the next Player in Turn Order.
- [[##rule 383.3.d.1|383.3.d.1.]] If multiple players separately control Triggered Abilities that are Triggered simultaneously, then starting with the Turn Player and proceeding in Turn Order, each player orders their Triggered Abilities on the Chain.
- [[##rule 459.2.d.1|459.2.d.1.]] The Attacking player, who has Focus, places Triggered Abilities on the Chain ﬁrst, followed by all non-Defender players in Turn Order, followed by the Defending Player.
- [[##rule 484.8.a|484.8.a.]] Players may play spells or activate abilities during their Teammate's Turn.In order to do so, their Teammate will invite them to play a spell or activate an ability using their own Priority.
- [[##rule 652.5.a.1|652.5.a.1.]] If the removed player was the Turn Player, play proceeds in Turn Order to the next available player in order.
- [[##rule 737|737.]] When an Additional Turn is inserted into this queue, it does not change the Turn Order of the game. The owner of the Additional Turn just has the next queued turn. After that turn is completed, it will be removed and the queue will proceed with its previously queued turns.

####  turn player

**Turn Player**

- [[##rule 116.1.b.1|116.1.b.1.]] The First Player is the player who becomes the Turn Player ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 187.6.b|187.6.b.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Uncontrolled, its Abilities are also Uncontrolled. The Turn Player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed, and is treated as their Controller if any game rule or effect requires one. Example: The Arena’s Greatest is a battleﬁeld that reads “At the start of each player's ﬁrst Beginning Phase, that player gains 1 point.” This ability will usually trigger while the battleﬁeld has no controller. If it does, the Turn Player goes through the steps of adding the ability to the chain and receives priority after doing so, exactly as if they controlled the ability.
- [[##rule 304|304.]] The Turn Player is the player taking the current turn.
- [[##rule 305|305.]] When there are no items on the Chain and the Turn Player cannot or chooses not to perform any Discretionary Actions, the current phase or step of the turn ends and the next phase, step, or turn begins.
- [[##rule 306|306.]] The Turn Player changes when the current Turn Player reaches the End of all of the Phases of their Turn.
- [[##rule 315.1.b|315.1.b.]] 1. The Turn Player readies all Game Objects they control that are able to be readied.  See rule 415. Ready for more information.
- [[##rule 315.2.b.2|315.2.b.2.]] 1. The Turn Player Holds all Battleﬁelds they Control. See rule 462. Scoring for more information.
- [[##rule 315.2.b.3|315.2.b.3.]] Reminder: In Modes of Play with Teams, Battleﬁelds held by a Teammate of the Turn Player during this phase are disqualiﬁed from being scored this turn by the Turn Player.
- [[##rule 315.3.b|315.3.b.]] 1. The Turn Player channels 2 runes from their Rune Deck.  See rule 430. Channel for more information.
- [[##rule 315.4.b|315.4.b.]] 1. The Turn Player draws 1.
- [[##rule 315.4.b.1|315.4.b.1.]] If there are no cards remaining in their Main Deck to draw, the Turn Player has been Burned Out.  See rule 431. Burn Out for more information.
- [[##rule 315.4.b.2|315.4.b.2.]] After completing the Burn Out the Turn Player still Draws 1.
- [[##rule 316.2.b|316.2.b.]] This is denoted as a Neutral Open State, and only the Turn Player has the ability to play spells or activate abilities.  See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.
- [[##rule 316.2.b.1|316.2.b.1.]] In Modes of Play with teammates, the Turn Player's teammates may play spells and activate abilities, including ones without Action or Reaction. They can only do so when the Turn Player invites them to do so with their own Priority.
- [[##rule 317.3|317.3.]] The next player with their Turn queued becomes the Turn Player.
- [[##rule 323.11|323.11.]] 8. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and one or more Showdowns are Staged, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. A Showdown begins there.
- [[##rule 323.13|323.13.]] 9. If the current state is a Neutral Open State and Combat is Staged at one or more Battleﬁelds, the Turn Player chooses one of those Battleﬁelds. Combat begins there.
- [[##rule 335.3|335.3.]] If there are no Outstanding Tasks, no pending Chain Items, and it is the Main Phase, the Turn Player receives priority. If there are no Outstanding Tasks, no pending items, and it is any other phase of the turn, proceed to the next substep, step, phase, or turn.
- [[##rule 383.3.d.1|383.3.d.1.]] If multiple players separately control Triggered Abilities that are Triggered simultaneously, then starting with the Turn Player and proceeding in Turn Order, each player orders their Triggered Abilities on the Chain.
- [[##rule 456.1|456.1.]] If more than one Battleﬁeld has Units controlled by opposing players at it at the same time, the Turn Player decides which Combat to resolve ﬁrst.
- [[##rule 652.5.a.1|652.5.a.1.]] If the removed player was the Turn Player, play proceeds in Turn Order to the next available player in order.

####  two game wins

**Two Game Wins**

- [[##rule 481.6|481.6.]] Format: Best of 3. The ﬁrst player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the game. The winner of that game earns One Game Win. Players then reset the game state, remove the Battleﬁelds in play from the game, choose new Battleﬁelds from those set aside, and play again. The ﬁrst player to earn Two Game Wins wins the match.

####  type

**Type**

- [[##rule 182.1.d|182.1.d.]] Tokens have a type. They follow all rules for their type unless otherwise speciﬁed. Example: A token unit is a unit. It enters exhausted, can take the standard move action, deals damage equal to its Might in combat, is destroyed if it takes damage equal to or greater than its might, can be chosen or otherwise affected by spells or abilities that choose or affect units, etc.
- [[##rule 718.5.a|718.5.a.]] Attached cards still have all Types and Tags while Attached.

###  group U

####  unattached

**Unattached**

- [[##rule 323.7|323.7.]] 5. Recall all Unattached non-Unit Gear at Battleﬁelds, and all Permanents and Runes in Bases other than their controller’s. Remove all Hidden cards from all Battleﬁelds that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's Trash.

####  unavailable

**Unavailable**

- [[##rule 359.3.e.7|359.3.e.7.]] If all of an instruction's Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is ﬁnished being played, that instruction will not execute.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.8|359.3.e.8.]] If an instruction has more than one Target and fewer than all of the Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is ﬁnished being played, the instruction will execute, with only the Targets available and valid being operated on.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.9|359.3.e.9.]] The process for a card's choice becoming Invalid or Unavailable is referred to as mistargeting.  Example: A spell has the instruction "Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld." Before that instruction can execute, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The instruction will not be executed, because it speciﬁes that the unit it chooses must be at a Battleﬁeld, and by the time it attempted to execute, the unit was no longer valid as a choice.
- [[##rule 359.3.e.10|359.3.e.10.]] It is possible for none of a spell's instructions to be executed as it resolves, due to all of them requiring targets to act on and all of those targets becoming Invalid or Unavailable. In this case, the spell has no effect but is still considered played.  Example: A player plays a spell that reads "Deal 2 to a unit at a battleﬁeld" with no other instructions, and chooses an enemy unit at a battleﬁeld. They also control a unit with the ability "When you play a spell, give me +1 [M] this turn." Before the spell resolves, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The spell resolves and its only instruction cannot be executed, but the unit's ability still triggers as the spell resolves and gives it +1 [M].

####  uncontrolled

**Uncontrolled**

- [[##rule 187.2.a|187.2.a.]] A Battleﬁeld is Controlled or Uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 187.6.b|187.6.b.]] While a Battleﬁeld is Uncontrolled, its Abilities are also Uncontrolled. The Turn Player takes responsibility for adding them to the Chain if applicable, makes all choices required by them unless otherwise speciﬁed, and is treated as their Controller if any game rule or effect requires one. Example: The Arena’s Greatest is a battleﬁeld that reads “At the start of each player's ﬁrst Beginning Phase, that player gains 1 point.” This ability will usually trigger while the battleﬁeld has no controller. If it does, the Turn Player goes through the steps of adding the ability to the chain and receives priority after doing so, exactly as if they controlled the ability.
- [[##rule 323.6|323.6.]] 4. If the turn is in an Open State, Battleﬁelds with no Units occupying them and no Showdown or Combat ongoing become Uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 461.5.b|461.5.b.]] If there are no Units remaining here controlled by any player, the Battleﬁeld becomes Uncontrolled.

####  uncontrolled battleﬁeld

**Uncontrolled Battleﬁeld**

- [[##rule 372.2|372.2.]] If the affected object is an Uncontrolled Battleﬁeld then the Current Turn Player decides the order the Replacement Effects will apply.

####  unique abilities

**Unique Abilities**

- [[##rule 188.3.b|188.3.b.]] That player may make decisions about the Game Object's Unique Abilities.

####  unique rules

**Unique Rules**

- [[##rule 478.8|478.8.]] Unique Rules
- [[##rule 484.8|484.8.]] Unique Rules

####  unit

**Unit**

- [[##rule 109.2|109.2.]] The State of all Game Objects in the Play Area is also Public Information.  Examples:   If a Unit is Buffed  If a Gear is Exhausted  Etc.
- [[##rule 133.4.a.2|133.4.a.2.]] Unit and Gear are permanent types.
- [[##rule 140|140.]] Units
- [[##rule 141|141.]] Unit is:
- [[##rule 141.1.a.1|141.1.a.1.]] Units are at one of several Locations while on the Board: a Battleﬁeld or their Base.
- [[##rule 141.1.a.2|141.1.a.2.]] Units and their details are Public Information while on the Board.
- [[##rule 141.1.a.3|141.1.a.3.]] Units can be chosen, affected, or manipulated by spells, affects, or game actions that specify Units.
- [[##rule 141.1.a.4|141.1.a.4.]] Units can be Killed.  See rule 428. Kill for more information.
- [[##rule 141.1.b.1|141.1.b.1.]] Units are treated as Cards, similar to when in the Hand.
- [[##rule 141.1.b.2|141.1.b.2.]] They retain the properties of being a Unit, but are not on the Board and thus cannot take actions or be affected by spells, abilities, or game actions that target Units on the Board.
- [[##rule 141.1.b.3|141.1.b.3.]] Units can be affected by spells and game effects that target Units in the Trash.
- [[##rule 142|142.]] Damage is a marked value that is applied to Units.
- [[##rule 142.3|142.3.]] Damage tracks how close a Unit is to being Killed.  See rule 428. Kill for more information.
- [[##rule 143|143.]] Units have multiple Intrinsic Properties unique to them:
- [[##rule 143.1|143.1.]] Tag: A Unit has zero or more Tags representing one or more champions, regions, factions, or species it belongs to.
- [[##rule 143.2|143.2.]] Might: The combat statistic of a Unit. Used to determine a Unit's contribution to Combat, as well as when it is Killed by damaging effects.
- [[##rule 143.2.a|143.2.a.]] If a Unit ever has nonzero damage marked on it equalling or exceeding its Might, it is Killed.
- [[##rule 143.3|143.3.]] Units can have damage marked on them.
- [[##rule 143.3.a|143.3.a.]] When spells, abilities, or other game effects deal damage, Units mark that damage on them temporarily. This can be tracked with coins, dice, or other markers, or by memory.
- [[##rule 143.3.b|143.3.b.]] Damage is Healed from Units at two speciﬁc times:
- [[##rule 143.4|143.4.]] Units enter the Board exhausted.
- [[##rule 144|144.]] Units have the Inherent Ability to perform a Standard Move.
- [[##rule 144.2|144.2.]] Exhausting the Unit is the Cost for this action.
- [[##rule 144.3|144.3.]] Players may perform multiple Units' standard move simultaneously.
- [[##rule 144.3.c|144.3.c.]] The Costs of Exhausting the Units are also paid Simultaneously.
- [[##rule 144.4|144.4.]] The Destinations where Units can Move to with their Standard Move are restricted:
- [[##rule 144.4.a|144.4.a.]] Units may move from their Base to a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 144.4.b|144.4.b.]] Units may move from a Battleﬁeld to their Base.
- [[##rule 144.4.c|144.4.c.]] Ganking is a unique ability that affects a Unit's Standard Move
- [[##rule 144.4.c.1|144.4.c.1.]] Units with Ganking may use their Standard Move to Move from Battleﬁeld to Battleﬁeld.  See rule 810. Ganking for more information.
- [[##rule 145|145.]] Units may have Activated Abilities.
- [[##rule 145.2|145.2.]] The Activated Ability of Units may be executed at any time during the controlling player's Main Phase during an Open State, and not during a Showdown.
- [[##rule 146|146.]] Units have a Location.
- [[##rule 162.2.b|162.2.b.]] Some Power is Universal and can be used to pay for costs of any Domain.
- [[##rule 169.6|169.6.]] Any number of Units can be present at a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 169.10.a|169.10.a.]] Battleﬁelds can be “occupied.” This means they have a Unit present.
- [[##rule 187.3.a|187.3.a.]] Contested is a temporary status applied to the battleﬁeld when a Unit controlled by a Player who does not currently Control that Battleﬁeld Moves or otherwise becomes present there.
- [[##rule 187.3.a.1|187.3.a.1.]] Units moving to or being played to a battleﬁeld apply Contested status if that battleﬁeld is not already contested and that Unit’s controller does not already control that battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 187.4|187.4.]] Control is established by having Units at a Battleﬁeld at the end of a Showdown or Combat after applying the contested status.
- [[##rule 187.4.a|187.4.a.]] If a player controls Units at a Battleﬁeld, outside of Combat, they maintain Control of that Battleﬁeld for as long as they have Units at that Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 187.4.c|187.4.c.]] If a player has no Units at a Battleﬁeld and the turn is in an Open state, they lose Control of that Battleﬁeld in the following cleanup, unless there is a Combat or Showdown ongoing there.
- [[##rule 316.4.a|316.4.a.]] A Combat occurs as a result of Units controlled by opposing players being present at the same Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 317.2.b|317.2.b.]] Insert “2c. Heal all Units.”
- [[##rule 323.2|323.2.]] 2. Assign or Remove the Attacker or Defender designation from Units as needed if there is a Combat in progress
- [[##rule 323.2.a|323.2.a.]] If there are Units present at the Battleﬁeld the Combat is taking place at, but do not have a designation, they gain the same designation as their Controller now
- [[##rule 323.2.b|323.2.b.]] If there are Units present at the Battleﬁeld the Combat is taking place at, but have the opposite designation of their controller, they lose that designation, and gain the same designation as their controller now
- [[##rule 323.2.c|323.2.c.]] If there are Units at locations other than the Battleﬁeld that the Combat is taking place at, but have either Attacker or Defender designations, they lose those designations now
- [[##rule 323.4|323.4.]] 3a. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might that have Deathknell abilities will trigger their Deathknell ability now, making note of their current location, attributes, and other information relevant to add the trigger as a Pending Item See rule 808 Deathknell for more information.
- [[##rule 323.5|323.5.]] 3b. All Units that have non-zero Damage marked on them equalling or exceeding their Might are killed and placed in their owners' Trash.
- [[##rule 323.6|323.6.]] 4. If the turn is in an Open State, Battleﬁelds with no Units occupying them and no Showdown or Combat ongoing become Uncontrolled.
- [[##rule 323.7|323.7.]] 5. Recall all Unattached non-Unit Gear at Battleﬁelds, and all Permanents and Runes in Bases other than their controller’s. Remove all Hidden cards from all Battleﬁelds that are not controlled by the same player and place them in their owner's Trash.
- [[##rule 323.9.a|323.9.a.]] The Combat remains Staged at that Battleﬁeld as long as there are Units present from two opposing players there.
- [[##rule 355.2|355.2.]] For Units, choose a valid Location where that Unit will be placed upon being Played.
- [[##rule 355.2.b|355.2.b.]] Some Game Effects may grant players permission to play Units to locations that are not normally Valid. Such locations become Valid for the purposes of Playing the Unit.
- [[##rule 355.4|355.4.]] For Spells and Abilities that Move one or more Units, choose a valid Location as the Move Destination for each Move that will be performed.
- [[##rule 355.4.a|355.4.a.]] A valid Location is one other than the Units’ current Location where they are allowed to be present.
- [[##rule 355.14.a|355.14.a.]] If a card speciﬁes that an amount of damage may be split among some number of Units, then each Unit chosen is Targeted.
- [[##rule 358.2|358.2.]] Ensure that the outcome of the effect of this card being played would not create an illegal state.  Example: Check that a spell's execution does not create a state where a Battleﬁeld has Units controlled by 3 different players.
- [[##rule 359.2.c|359.2.c.]] If it is a Unit, it enters the Board exhausted at the Location that was chosen.
- [[##rule 383.4.a.1|383.4.a.1.]] These are commonly structured as “When you play me…” for Units and “When you play this…” for Gear.
- [[##rule 383.4.c|383.4.c.]] Conquer Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit participating in, and successfully Conquering a Battleﬁeld.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2|383.4.c.2.]] This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Conquer action, or Abilities that  the player that performed the Conquer action.
- [[##rule 383.4.c.2.a|383.4.c.2.a.]] The Conquer Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit(s) these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from Conquering.
- [[##rule 383.4.d|383.4.d.]] Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battleﬁeld during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2|383.4.d.2.]] This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Hold action, or Abilities that  the player that performed the Hold action.
- [[##rule 383.4.d.2.a|383.4.d.2.a.]] The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battleﬁeld when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.
- [[##rule 383.4.e|383.4.e.]] Attack Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Attacker designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2|383.4.e.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Attacker designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.e.2.a|383.4.e.2.a.]] These triggers will only have their condition checked once per combat, despite a Unit being able to gain and lose the Attacker designation multiple times in the same combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f|383.4.f.]] Defend Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Defender designation for the ﬁrst time during a combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2|383.4.f.2.]] These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Defender designation during Combat.
- [[##rule 383.4.f.2.a|383.4.f.2.a.]] These triggers will only have their condition checked once per combat, despite a Unit being able to gain and lose the Defender designation multiple times in the same combat.
- [[##rule 392|392.]] Delayed Abilities are not associated with Units or Gear; they are created by other Abilities or Spells. As such they are executed when their condition and/or speciﬁed time occurs regardless of whether the source of the Delayed Ability is still on the board or not.
- [[##rule 400.2|400.2.]] When an Ability with the [Add] action is ﬁnalized it resolves immediately instead of becoming a Chain Item, like a Unit or Gear.
- [[##rule 410.1.b.3|410.1.b.3.]] As long as it does not result in any forbidden action being taken or game state being created.  Example: A player can't use the Standard Move discretionary action to move a unit to a Battleﬁeld that's already occupied by Units controlled by two other players.
- [[##rule 414.1.b|414.1.b.]] A Unit that is already Exhausted cannot be Exhausted again.
- [[##rule 414.1.c|414.1.c.]] If a Unit is instructed to be Exhausted while it is already Exhausted, nothing additional happens.
- [[##rule 415.1.b|415.1.b.]] A Unit that is already Ready cannot be Readied again.
- [[##rule 415.1.c|415.1.c.]] If a Unit is instructed to be Readied while it is already Ready, nothing additional happens.
- [[##rule 417.1.b|417.1.b.]] To Deal Damage to Units, mark the speciﬁed amount of Damage on the Unit.
- [[##rule 417.1.d|417.1.d.]] Damage can be Dealt to more than one Unit at the same time.
- [[##rule 417.6.c|417.6.c.]] Damage Dealt as a result of being assigned during Combat has the Units as its source.
- [[##rule 418.1|418.1.]] Damage being cleared from Units is Healing.
- [[##rule 418.2|418.2.]] More than one Unit can be Healed at the same time.
- [[##rule 420.2.b|420.2.b.]] The Standard Move inherent to Units may also cause Movement.  See rule 144.for more information on the Standard Move.
- [[##rule 420.3|420.3.]] The Standard Move inherent to Units is a Discretionary Action.
- [[##rule 420.3.a|420.3.a.]] The Cost is Exhausting one or more Units.
- [[##rule 420.3.b|420.3.b.]] The Effect is Moving those Unit.
